O vos, tres chiers filz, je vos ai acomplit cest livre qui est li derriens de la science de medicine ensamble l’emplissement de lui, et ai fait la fin per ses expositions et par ses declarations.	To you, dear sons, I have completed this book which is the latter part of the science of medicine combined with its completeness. And I have done the end through its demonstrations and by its statements.
Et m’est venu en vision que je le vos acomplisse avec cest traitier, qui est partie de l’uevre de mains, c’est a savoir «cyrurgie».	And it came to my mind that I should complete this book with this treatise, which is a part of the work of hands, namely "surgery".
Et por ceu que l’uevre de mains est fortraite en nostre region et est etraingie dou tout en tout, si est perie li science et decopee, et n’est riens demorez de li fuers que les petites descriptions en livres des anciens que les mains ont muees.	And because the art of hands is practiced in our region and is unknown everywhere, it has been lost and discarded, and nothing remains from it except for small descriptions in books by the ancients that have been performed by hand.
Et de ceu est venue li error et li vanitez, et sont closes les ententions et est aloignie li science.	And because of this, errors and vanity have come about, and minds are closed, and knowledge has become distant.
Or me semble que je la vuel vivifier ensamble l’ordination de cest traitier selonc la voie d’exposition et de declaration et de l’abreviation; et venrai ensamble les formes des ferremens de cautere, et des autres estrumens de l’uevre avec l’ajostement de la declaration et de preparation de li, sicom il est mestier.	It seems that I will revive this treatise in its entirety according to the path of exposition and declaration and abbreviation; and will come together with the forms of the cautery instruments, and other tools of work alongside their declaration and preparation, just as it is necessary.
Et por la raison de ceu que nuls boins maistres de mains n’est trovez en nostre tens, est li ars de medicine eslongié.	And because no good masters are found in our time, the art of medicine has been extended.
Et covient celui qui s’en entremet sormonter en la science d’anathomie, si com Galiens dit, tant qu’il saiche la juement des menbres, et les formes et les conjunctions et les separations d’aus, et aient connissance des osses et des nerf et des brais et le nombre d’ous, et le demenement et des voines movans et des reposans, et dou leu de lor issue.	And it is necessary for the one who intervenes to master in the art of anatomy, as Galen says, as long as he knows the measurement of the limbs, and their forms and connections and separations, and have knowledge of bones and nerves and tendons, and the number of bones, and their movement and mobile and stationary veins, and the location of their exit.
Et por ceu dist Ypocras que li nons avec le non est mout, et avec l’uevre est poc; et meismement en l’art de main.	And so says Ipython that with speech we are many, and with action we are few; indeed in the art of hands.
Nos vos disons en l’introite de cest livre que qui n’est conissans des choses devant dites, si se gart qu’il ne chiece en error et qu’il n’ocie les homes; ensi que j’ai veut maintes fois plusors de ces qui s’entremettent de ceste science et si s’abandonent sen science et sens experiment.	We tell you at the beginning of this book that if someone doesn't know the things we have spoken, they may go wrong and mislead people; thus I have seen many times more than others who interfere in this science and abandon their knowledge and experience.
Car je vis un fol mire qui copa .i. apostume de scrophules ou col d’une femme, et copa les arteres dou col; por coi tant de sanc issit hors que li femme cheit morte entre ses mains.	And I saw a foolish man treat an abscess on a woman's neck, and cut the arteries beneath it. Because so much blood flowed out that the woman died in her death throes between his hands.
Et vis .i. autre mire qui traït une piere d’un home d’eaige, et li piere estoit grans; si emporta avec li une piece de la vessie, et fut mors li hons dedens .iij. jors.	And I saw another physician who treated a stone in an elderly man's bladder, and the stone was large; he removed part of the bladder with it, and killed the man within three days.
Et je i avoie ja esteit apelez por lou traire, et vis la disposition dou malaide et la grandor de la piere, et soi bien s’on lou tailloit il en morroit.	And I have already been summoned to extract, and saw the location of the disease and the size of the stone, and if they were well cut it would kill him.
Et vis .i. autre mire qui prist en cure .i. duc de nostre terre qui avoit la jambe brisie, et avec la briseure ot plaie; et li mires plains d’ignorance estraint la brisure sus la plaie as esteles par fort lieure, et ne lassa a la plaie point de xalain, et le lassa ensi .i. termine; et li comanda qu’il ne la desliast mie; et demora ensi que li jambe fut toute enflee et li piez et vint a perdition.	And saw another case where he was called to treat the leg of one of our country's Duke who had broken his leg, and had an injury as well due to the break. The patients were full of ignorance, forcing the break onto the wound in various places using strong force, not allowing any healing for the wound, making it so until the second month; he was instructed not to disintegrate the break; stayed this way until the leg swelled up completely and the foot, leading to his downfall.
Je fuis apelez por venir a lui, et me hastai por venir deslier la jambe; et quant je l’oi desloie si fut em pais et ne sentit point de dolor.	I was summoned to come to him, and I quickly went to relieve his leg; and when I heard it being dislocated so smoothly that he felt no pain.
Mais toute voie li corruptions estoit ja confermee ou membre, et ne la poi saner; et ne cessa li corrution d’aler par le membre tant que li membres fut dou tout perdus.	But every pathway of corruption had already been confirmed throughout the body or member, and it could not be healed; and the process of decay continued to spread within the limb until the entire member was lost.
Et vis .i. autre mire qui effondra .i. apostume enchancreit, et puis enflama per le malice de sa signorie.	And as for another instance where one abscess weakened another intertwined abscess, and then it inflamed due to the wickedness of its lordship.
Car chancre, quant il est purs d’umor melancolique, ne covient mie qu’on i(l) touche de fer s’il n’est en teil leu c’on puisse toute oster ce que est corrumpus.	For the ulcer, when it is pure of melancholic humours, does not allow one to touch it with iron if it isn't in its entirety within what can be removed all that which has been corrupted.
Et por ceu, treschier filz, vos est besoig que vos sachiez que oevre de mains est devisee en .ij. divisions: c’est asavoir, huevre ou il a peril en plusors dispositions; et je mostrerai en chescun leu de cest livre ou il a paour et peril.	And because of this, skilled children, you are required to know that the work of hands is divided into two parts: meaning, an area where there is danger in multiple positions; and I will show in each section of this book where it has strength and danger.
Por coi il est besoig que vos vos en gardez, si que li fol mire ne puissent mal parler de vos Si prenez vos armes en cusenson, et entreprenez vos malaides legierement et fermement, et usez de la millor voie si que per la graice de Deu vos venez a salut et soiez loez; et lassiez les maladies espoantables de grief saniteit; et ostez vos armes de ceu que vos fait douter, et aiez foit en vos si que vos puissiez venir de cestui monde a l’autre de gloire.	Because you must be prepared for this, so that the foolish may not speak ill of you. Take up your weapons with caution and firmly, use the best way possible, that by grace of God you come to salvation and stay safe; and leave unendurable diseases in despair of health; remove from those who cause doubt about you, trust only in yourselves that you may pass from this world to glory.
Galiens dist en aucuns de ses amonestemens: «Ne prenez mie en cure male maladie, que vos ne soiez apelez fol mire.	Galiens states in all of his admonishments: "Do not treat any illness incorrectly, lest you be called a foolish physician.
» J’ai deviseit cest traitier selonc III chapitres.	I have composed this treatise according to three chapters.
Li premiers chapitres est des cauteres de feu et dé cauteres de medicine ague, et est li chapitres ordenez de lou chief jusques as piez; et des formes des estrumens, et des ferremens de cautere, et de tout ceu qui est necessaire en l’ueuvre.	The first chapters discuss fire cauterization and medical cauterizations, and organize chapters up to the joints; and descriptions of instruments, metal tools for cauterization, and all that is necessary for the operation.
Li secons chapitres si est de taillier et de percier, et des ventouses et des plaies, et des estractions des saiettes, et des semblans choses; et est li chapitres ordenez et les formes des estrumens.	The second chapters deal with cutting and piercing, as well as suction cups and wounds, and the extraction of arrows, among similar matters; and organizes chapters along with descriptions of instruments.
Li tiers chapitres est de restorer les dislocations et des torcions, et des semblans choses; et est ordeneiz des lou chief jusc’as piez, et des formes des estrumens.	The third chapters are about restoring dislocations and twists, and similar matters; it organizes up to the joints from the head onwards, along with descriptions of instruments.
Ainsois que nos nos remembriens de l’uevre, il covient que je die la qualiteit de l’aide et dou nuisement de chescune complexion.	Just as we recall our work, it is fitting that I explain the quality of each aid and the harm of each constitution.
Je dis que li qualiteis de l’aide, et dou nuisement, est li plus longe parole et subtilz science et li secrez reponus; et de ceu parlerent li plusors des saiges, et s’acorderent a ceu; et me soffisent poc lor paroles, car je redous la longesce.	I say that the qualities of help, and harm, are the longest word and subtlest science and the secrets answer to it; and many wise people spoke about this, agreeing with it. And they suffice me with their words, for I fear its length.
Je dis que cautere aide universement a toute complexion ou il a matiere, fuer que .ij. complexions: c’est a savoir complexion chaude sens matere, et complexion seche sens matere.	I say that the fire cautery universally helps with all types of body composition where there is substance, for it deals with two compositions: these are known as hot body with substance and dry body with substance.
En complexion chaude et seche ensamble matiere, deviserent aucun et dirent que cautere i est grans aide; et li autre dirent le contraire: que cautere ne vaut a maladie que vient de chalor et de sechour.	In the composition of a hot and dry body combined with substance, there was no agreement and they said that fire cautery is a great help. And another group said the opposite: that fire cautery only benefits diseases that come from heat and dryness.
Car li nature dou feu si est chaude, et ne doit mie estre cureiz de chaude maladie par chalor, ne per sechour; et dist cil qui dist lou contraire que cautere fait grant aide a maladie chaude et seche que vient en cors des homes.	For the nature of fire is so hot, and should never be treated with diseases of heat or drying; and it is said who says otherwise that the cautery provides great help for hot and dry illnesses that come into the body.
Car quant tu comperes le cors de l’ome et sa moistor a la complexion dou feu, tu trueves le cors froit.	For when you compare the body of the person and their moisture to the constitution of fire, you find that the body is cold.
Et je m’acorde a ceste parole.	And I agree with this word.
Car je l’ai troveit aucune fois per experiment.	For I have found it true on every occasion through experimentation.
Et toute voie, ne s’en entremette mie fuers que cil qui l’a esproveit, et qui conoit par lonc usaige le chapistre des cauteres, et la diversiteit des complexions des homes, et les dispositions et les causes de lor maladies, et les sorvenues et l’espaice dou tens; des autres complexions n’avons nos mie paour, meismement em maladies froides et moistes.	And with any passage, do not interfere beyond him who has proven it, and who knows through long usage the chapter of cauteries, and the variety of skin types in men, and their dispositions and causes of illnesses, and the occurrences and space during treatment; we have no fear for other skin types, especially for cold and moist diseases.
Et tuit li mire s’asemblerent et s’acorderent au cautere.	And all these matched and agreed with the cautery.
Et sachiez, filz, que cautere ensamble feu si est des secrez des cures, et de plus grant bonteit que cautere de medicine ardant.	And know, children, that when assembled in fire, a cautery has secrets of healing arts, and it offers more benefit than a hot medical treatment.
Car li feus est simples, et ne vient mie fuers que au membre qui est cuis, et ne nuit a autre membre se poc nom.	For fire is simple, and does not come out except at the body part that is heated, and does not harm other parts if you do not name it.
Les medicines ardans vienent de membre a autre en aloignant, et font venir au membre maladies de grief sanation; et par aventure ocit lou malaide Li feus por sa hautece et por la bonteit de sa substance ne fait mie ceu, s’il n’i a superfluiteit.	The active medicines move from one part to another, causing diseases due to lack of health; and sometimes the patient feels the discomfort of illness. The fire medicine, because of its strength and the goodness of its composition, does not cause this unless there is excess.
Et ceu vos ai je troveit par experiment et par la longesce dou servise et de l’estude que j’ai mis en l’art, et esteit sus la verteit des choses; et por ceu je m’escuse de la longesce de la parole, car il ne me plait mie que je vos oste le secreit qui est reponus ou feu, et la qualiteit de l’uevre, coment il deboute les maladies des cors, si com li philosophe le dit en demostrant; or le recevez en vos pensees.	And I have found this through experimentation and the length of service and study that I have put into the art, which corresponds to the truth of things; and for this reason, I apologize for the length of my words, because I do not want to withhold from you the secret of fire and its quality, how it removes diseases from bodies, as the philosopher demonstrates in his demonstration. Now accept this knowledge in your thoughts.
Et sachiez, fil, que il s’acorderent en quel tens doient estre faites les cauteres, et eslirent prientens.	And know, son, that they decided on what times the cauterizations should be performed, and prescribed them carefully.
Et je dis que cautere est covenable en tous tens, por ceu que li nuisemens sorvenans est desoz mis par l’aide dou cautere; et meismement se li cauteres est por dolors necessaires fors et hastans que ne puent atendre le tens que plus grans malice ne veigne au membre.	And I say that cauterization is suitable in all times, because the damages occurring are alleviated by the aid of the cautery; and likewise if the cauterizations are for necessary pains that cannot wait until larger harm befalls to the limb.
Et n’i pensez onques, chier fil, si com font li fol mire; car a la maladie qui est sanee par cautere n’a point de revenue; et il le dient ensi; mais il n’est mie si com il cuident, por ce que cauteres nen est que medicine qui mue la complexion, et seche les humors que sont cause de la dolor, et vaut mues que medicine por le hastement de sa valor, et por la vertut de son oevre et de sa signorie.	And never think like those who are fools, my dear child; for a disease cured by cauterization does not have a return. And they say it this way; but it is not as they believe, because cauterizations are just medicine that changes the complexion and dries out the fluids that cause pain, and works better than medicine for hastening its power, and through the virtue of its work and its authority.
Et possans chose est que li maladie viegne aucune fois selonc la complexion dou malaide et lou leu de la maladie et sa vertut; et sont assemblees en lui les superfluitez par l’aquisition des viandes et des semblans choses, se ce n’est cauteres administrez em leu ou il ait poc de superfluitez et de moistor, si com cauteres de dens por la dolor, et les semblans choses, et teil dolor ne revient mie; mais ce avient poc.	And the possibility is that diseases come about in any way according to the disposition of the sick person and the location of the disease and its virtue; and they accumulate in him unnecessary things through the acquisition of meats and similar matters. If only cauterizations are given where there is little excess matter and moisture, as with cauterizations for pain, and similar things, then such pain does not recur; but this happens seldom.
Et mout de gens n’entendent mie por coi cauteres est apelez li derriens de medecine, et c’est voir; mais il ne croient mie que cauteres vaille aprés medicine, mais lor ententions est fause, et est cauteres li derriens de medicine por ceu que quant nos aministrons manieres de cures en aucune maladie et elles ne valent, adonc administrons nos le cautere, et il vaut.	And no one understands why cauteries are called the ends of medicine, and this is seen; but they do not believe that cauteries can follow medicine, but their understanding is false, and it is said that cauteries are at the end of medicine because when we administer methods for cures in any disease and they don't work, then we administer our cautery, and it works.
Adonques apert bien que cauteres est li derriens de medicine, ne mie selonc l’entention des folz mires.	Therefore, it is true that cauteries are at the end of medicine, not according to the understanding of those who misunderstand.
Li ancien dirent que cauteres d’estrument d’or est muedres que de fer, et ne dirent ceu fuers que por la qualiteit de l’or et por la hautece de sa substance; et dirent que li leus de cautere ne fait mie porriture, mais ceu n’est mie voir car je l’ai esprovei, et ai troveit que c’est voir en aucuns homes; et cauteres d’or vaut mues que de fer, si com il lou dirent.	The old ones said that gold cauteries are melted better than iron ones, and they mentioned this only because of the quality of gold and the purity of its substance; and they stated that the metal parts of a cautery do not cause rotting, but this is not visible as I have proven it and found out that some people do experience this. And gold cauteries are more melted than iron ones, just as they said.
Et toutevoie quant tu chaufes estrument d’or, tu ne seis mie quant il est chaus par la color de l’or, et s’est tantost refroidiez; et s’on le chaufe trop; si font au feu; et ensi i a assez d’empechement.	And yet, when you heat the gold instrument, you do not know immediately by the color of the gold when it is heated, and it quickly cools down; and if it is heated too much; it gets too hot to use; and thus there is enough prevention.
Et por ce usons nos de cautere de feir que nos l’avons mues apparilliet a nostre oevre.	And for this reason, we use our fire cautery that has been prepared for our work.
Or vos ai ordeneit cest chapitre des lou chief jusc’a piez, por ceu que li voie soit plus legiere a trover.	So I have ordered this chapter on how to find the shoulder joint until this point, because it makes the search for it lighter.
dou cautere olivaire	with the olive cautery
Cist cauteres vaut a moistor et a froidor sus lou cerveil, et en i a dous c’on fait par la cause d’une maladie qui est apelee «soda», et par la cause de maintes humors qui dessendent dou chief as eulz, et as oreilles, et por multitude de songes et dolor de dens et dolor de gorge, et meismement a toutes maladies qui vienent de froidor si com paralisie et sode et apoplexie et semblans maladies.	The use of cautery is appropriate in cases of moisture and cold within the brain. There are two kinds done by reason of an illness called 'soda', and due to various humors descending from head to eyes, and ears, as well as from numerous dreams and toothache, and throat pain, and especially for all diseases coming from cold such as paralysis, soda (a type of stroke), apoplexy, and similar illnesses.
Li forme de cest cautere si est que li malaides soit espurgiez par medicine solutive mondifiant le chief .iij. nuis ou .iiij., selonc ceu que li vertus et li eaige et li acostumance dou malaide le puet soffrir; et puis fai rere lou chief dou malaide.	The form of this cautery involves purging the patient with a solutary medicine to transform their body for three or four weeks, depending on how well the disease, its intensity and regularity suit the body. Then it allows the recovery of the diseased part afterwards.
Et puis le fai seoir croisiet entre tes mains, et mettre ses mains sor som peis; aprés met la racine de ta palme sus la racine de son neis entre ses .ij. eulz; et lai ou venra tes dois moiens, si saigne d’enche puis eschaufe le cautere qui est apelé «olivare», de coi ci est li forme:	And then hold their hands together in your palms and place their hands on the bridge of their nose. Afterwards, put the root of your palm against the root of their nose between their two nostrils; let them breathe as you move your middle fingers to where they bleed, then heat up the cautery which is called 'olivare', this is its form:
Et le met sor le leu signiet d’encre, et fai en dessendant et en estraignant ta main poc et poc en trestornant; puis lieve ta main isnelement, et rewarde le leu se tu vois l’os .i. sol petit; et se tu ne lou vois, si rencomence le cautere tant que tu voies l’os si com je lou t’ai dit; aprés pren .i. poc de seil, et met en awe et molle coton dedens, et met sor le leu, et li laisse .iij. jors; aprés met sus cotun moilliet en burre; et laisse sus tant que li eschaudure soit ostee; aprés cure la plaie de l’oignement qui est apelez «tetrafarmaçon», tant qu’il soit sanez.	And place it in its natural position with ink, and move your hand down gradually while pushing lightly against it; then raise your hand alone, and if you see the bone .i. a small dot; and if you do not see it, continue using the cautery until you see the bone as I've instructed. After this, take .i. pinch of sulfur, put it in oil and wet cotton inside, and place it on the bone, letting it stay there for three days. Afterwards, apply buttered oil on the skin; let it remain until the scab falls off; then treat the wound with balm known as 'tetrafarmaçon', until it heals over.
Et se dirent li ancien, que quant plus demoure overte li plaie, plus s’espurge; et por ce si aide mues.	And they said that the more an open wound stays exposed, the more it purges out impurities; and because of this help, movements occur.
Et dirent aucun de ces que on doit tant lassier le cautere que partie de l’os soit arse, et puis rese on ceu qui est ars de l’os, et soit curez.	And it was said that one should leave the cauterization for so long that part of the bone gets burned, and then remove that which is burned from the bone, and treat it.
Et dient li autre c’on doit le cautere tant lassier sus, et bouter si fort c’on abaite de l’os ausi large comme .i. vertoil que les femmes mettent en lor fusez por ceu que les humors issent mues hors; et doit on lassier la plaie longement overte; aprés le doit on curer et sodeir.	And it is said that the cautery should be left in place for as long as necessary, pressing so strongly that one lifts up to the bone as wide as a thumb that women insert into their fuses when they are menstruating because the body's fluids can then escape; and should the wound remain widely open after this? Afterward, it must be treated and sewn.
Et ces .ij. manieres de cauteres ne me semblent mie estre bones dou tout en tout, fuers qu’en aucuns homes ou il ait voie de paor; et mues me semble que je lou doie laissier; car li chiés li est afoiblis par les solutions continuees de nature, si com nos le tesmoignons ens autres membres; et meisme quant li chiés dou malaide est foibles par nature, et li premiere semblance de cautere est plus salve et muedre por moi, et de celi use je oevre en donques emsamble salut.	And these two ways of applying the cautery do not seem to me to be entirely good for everything, except where there is a channel for fear; and I think that I should leave them like this. For the joints weaken through continuous exposure to nature, as we attest in other limbs; even when the joint of illness is weak due to nature, and my first application of cautery feels more soothing and less painful to me, so from this usage, I work thus together for their benefit.
de l’anciainne dolor dou chief	from the old pain in the head
Quant en tout le chief vient dolor croniques, et dure longement, si doit user li malaides yeris et pilules qui sont apelees «cochie», et d’espurgement de chief et d’oiles et d’emplastres; et s’on li fait le cautere que nos avons devant dit, et il ne vaut.	When throughout the head comes chronic pain and lasts for a long time, one should use the patient's elbows and pills that are called 'cochies', and treatments of chief [possibly referring to herbs] and ears and bandages; and if one applies the cautery as we have previously said, it may prove effective.
Pren warde se li chiés dou malade est de fort nature, et qu’il ne soit trop froit; adonques le cauterize desoz celui cautere un poc que nos avons dit desus.	Take care that the shoulder of the sick person is not too cold and robust in nature; therefore, apply the cautery under the fire for a bit as we have spoken about.
Aprés fai cautere sus chescune corne dou chief jusc’a l’os, si com devant avons dit, et fai .i. cautere ou leu qui est apelez «vasselz»; et est .i. leus en coi on met ventouses; et alige ta main si que tu ne voises mie jusc’a l’os: li malaides sent trop plus grant dolor en cest cautere que as autres, et je em parlerai aillors; et covient que li cauteres des cornes soient plus subtis que cil dont on cautere la moieneteit dou chief, et c’est li forme:	After you perform the cautery on each part of the shoulder until it reaches the bone, as we have said previously, do one more cautery where your hand is called "vassel"; and make two others in which suction cups are placed; and lift your hand so that you do not reach the bone: patients feel much greater pain with this cautery than with others, and I will speak further about it elsewhere; and it must be known that the cauterizations of the shoulder parts should be more precise than when one cauterizes the middle part of the head, and this is the form:
dou cautere dou chief	For the fire cautery,
Quant en une partie dou chief vient dolor sodaine, et est estendue li maladie jusc’a l’oil, et li chiés est espurgiez par medicines mondifians, et on a fait les autres cures que j’ai dit en la division des maladies, et tout ceu ne profite mie: adonques li fai cauteres selonc .ij. manieres, c’est a savoir de medicine ague et de feir.	When suddenly in part of the head comes an intense pain,
Li cauteres de medicine ague si est que tu preignes une doce d’alz, et oste l’escorce et le recope .i. poc as .ij. chiés, et puis fent la temple ou li dolor tient en teil maniere que tu puisses reponre la doce d’alz desoz le cuir; et quant elle sera reponuee si le lie et l’estraint bien et le laisse ensi .xij. houres; et puis le deslie et trait fuers la doce d’ail, et laisse la plaie ensi .ij. jors ou .iij.; puis met sus cotun plongiet en burre tant que porreture en isse.	The cauteries of fever require you to soak a piece of wool in sweet alcohol, then apply the peel and cover it with one band around each shoulder, positioning them so that the alcohol can reach the skin. Then secure it well for 12 hours; afterwards remove it and let it out on its own for two days or three.
Aprés le cure d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez; et se tu vues si fai ceu d’aucunes medicines comburans que j’ai escrites ou dozime traitier des medicines comburans.	After the oil treatment as long as it is clean; and if you see that you are doing with some burning medicines that I have written or the tenth treatise on burning medicines.
Li cautere de fer si est selonc ceste meniere.	The iron cautery operates in this manner.
Chaufe le cautere de coi ci est li forme:	Heat the cautery which is as follows:
Et est apelez «clos» por ceu que li chief est fait a la forme d’un clo ou il ait .i. poc de corbeure, et em mileu a une petite apparance; et le met sor le leu dolorous, et tien ta main et trestorne le feir un poc legierement, tant que li moitiez de l’espés dou keur soit arse; et lieve ta main que li artere n’arde, que est defuers, et decorre habundance de sanc.	And call it "closed" because its head is made in the shape of a bell where there is .i. point of curvature, and in the middle it has a small appearance; and place it on the painful area, and hold your hand and gently turn the iron until half of the thickness of the skin is burned; then lift your hand so that the artery doesn't burn, when it is done, let out an abundance of blood.
Aprés met coton en awe de seil, et met sor le leu par .iij. jors; puis i met coton moilliet em burre, et puis cure le leu d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez; et se tu vuelz cauterize ceste emigraine avec le cautere qui est apelez «cultellare», a tout la pointe, et te garde de coper l’artere en ceste emigraine qui n’est mie anciaine.	After that, put cotton in a sailcloth, and apply it on the wound for three days; then change to damp cotton soaked in butter, and continue treating the wound with oil as long as it remains clean; if you wish to cauterize this headache with the iron cautery ("cultellare"), do so at its tip, but be careful not to cover the artery in this headache that is not old.
de emigraine	Regarding the use of a fire cautery, instruct the patient to allow their hair to grow long and evenly; if they are pricking at their base, hold them steady so they don't move until they fully grow.
Quant tu cures emigraine si com nos avons devant dit en divisions des maladies, et ne profite mie, et vois que li cauteres devant dis de la medicine et dou fer ne li soffit mie, adonques covient il que tu eschaufes le cautere qui est apelez «cultellare» tant qu’il soit blans; et seigne ainsois sor le leu doillant une ligne de demi doi de lonc, et oste ta main une fois, et l’estrain que tu ne coper l’artere et que ne viegnes jusc’a l’os; et te warde de la mandibule que muet quant on menjut, et li ners n’ait regart que la muet et que spasmus ne veigne a malaide, et te warde de decorrement de sanc de l’artere quant elle sera copee, ou copement ait grant paour et meismement a celui que ne s’i conoit, et qui n’est estudians et esprovez; et laisse l’uevre em mi voie; mais je vos dirai coment on restainche sanc quant li artere est copee, et je vos mostrerai a leu ou il afiert en cest livre.	When you are treating migraines as we have discussed in the divisions of diseases previously, if it does not benefit and you find that none of the cauterizations mentioned from the medicine and iron do not apply, then it is necessary for you to heat up the cautery which is called 'cultellare' until it's white; and do this on the part of the body where there's a line approximately half an inch long, and use your hand once, making sure that you don't cut into the artery and stop before reaching the bone; and guard against the jaw clenching when eating, ensuring only the jaw is moving and not any spasm affecting the patient, and guard against blood drainage from the artery if it's been cut, or sudden fear even in someone who doesn't know this procedure and hasn't experienced it; and leave your work for me to finish; but I will tell you how to stop bleeding when the artery has been cut, and show you where it is done in this book.
Et se tu vois que cist cauteres ne soffise mie a la maladie, et li malaides est soffrans, cauterize le enmi le chief ausi com nos avons dit, et cure la plaie tant qu’elle soit sanee; et se tu vues, aministre le cautere que nos avons dit ou chapistre de l’estraction de l’artere, avec le cautere qui ait .ij. coutelz; et est cist cauteres millors de celui et plus aidans.	And if you find that this cautery does not work for the disease and the patients are suffering, use it on the head as we have said before, and treat the wound until it has healed; and if you observe to administer the cautery that we have said in the chapter about extracting the artery, with a two-bladed knife; and these cauterizations are better than others and more helpful.
de la dolor des oreilles de part froidor	The pain of the ear from both cold and heat
Quant en l’oreille vient dolor de froit, et on i a ovreit de medicines solutives et des autres cures que nos avons dit en la division, et li dolors ne se muet, adonques eschaufe cest cautere qui est apelez «poins», de coi ci est li forme:	When pain comes from cold in the ear, and we have applied solutive medicines and other treatments that we mentioned under division, and if the pains do not subside, then heat this cautery called "points", according to its form.
Aprés pointoie tout entor l’oreille malaide, ou entor les .ij. se la dolor tient en ambedous, et t’esloigne un poc ensus de la racine de l’oreille puis que tu as signiet le leu d’enche; et ait .x. poins entor chescune oreille; aprés cure le leu tant qu’il soit sanez.	After applying points all around the ear, or around both if pain is in both ears, and after removing somewhat from the root of the ear right where you have marked its edge; place ten points around each ear. After that, treat the area until it becomes healed.
de la torture de la bouche	Of the torment of the mouth
Torture qui doit estre curee par cautere nen est fuers que de celles que muevent de fleume, si com nos avons dit en divisions des maladie; et ne faire point de cautere as semblances que vienent de sechor et de spame de ners.	Treatments that need to be healed by the fire cautery are only those that move from pus, as we have explained in sections of diseases; and no cautering should be done on symptoms that come from scarring and rash of nerves.
Quant tu cures ceste semblance de torture qui muet de fleume d’ydres et d’espurgemens de chief et de gargarisme, et ceu ne vaut, adonc covient que tu cauterizes le malaide de .iij. cauteres: l’une en la racine de l’oreille, et l’autre un poc defuers la temple, et le tier en l’ajostement des .ij. levres; et met le cautere en la partie qui apert saine, et li fai cautere endroit le chief de l’oreille desus un poc desoz la corne dou chief, et un autre en la temple ausi longe com uns poce; et laisse le cautere tant sus que li moitiez dou keur soit arse; et c’est li forme dou cautere:	When you treat this sign of torture that moves from pus in the ears and from discharges from the nose and gargling, if it is not effective, then it is necessary for you to cauterize the hair with three cauteries: one at the root of the ear, and another a little beyond the temple, and the third on the junction of the two lips; and place the cautery where the healthy part opens, and make it cauterize the head of the ear above slightly below the nose horn, and another in the temple as long as an inch; and leave the cautery burning until half of the skin is burned; and this is the shape of the cautery:
Et est li semblance dou cutellaire que nos avons mise devant, mais il est un poc plus subtilz et covient que li coutelz soit un poc plus gros; aprés cure lou leu si com j’ai devant dit, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And as for the sign of the knife wound that we have described earlier, but it is a bit more subtle; so it needs that the knives be a little thicker. After treating the wound as I have said before, until it heals properly.
Quant apoplexie est ancieinne et tu la cures ensi com nos avons dit, et il ne profite mie, et li malaides n’ait fievre, adonques li fai .iiij. cauteres: .ij. sus les .ij. cornes dou chief, et .i. emmi le chief, et .i. ou leu qui est apelez «vasselz» si com nos avons devant dit, et lou derrien cautere sus la bouche de l’estomac; et soit curez si com nos avons dit devant.	When dealing with an old apoplexy and you're treating it as we have described, and if the patient doesn't improve, and the sick person has a fever, then do this: four cauterizations. Two of them on the two tips of their head, one around the head, and one where the neck is called 'vessel' as we previously mentioned, and the final one on the mouth of the stomach; and treat it just as we have described before.
de litargie	Of Liturgy
A cest maladie covient doner au malaide yeres grans et pilules mondifians le cerveil; aprés reis lou chief dou malaide tout, et li met sus l’occipite l’emplaustre de sinapi qui est escrit ou traitier des emplastres; et c’est li maniere dou cautere: si lou fai si com j’ai dit.	For this illness, you should give the patient large berries and pills that lighten the brain; after that, you examine the head of the sick person thoroughly, and then place the strappado made of tamarisk on their occipital region. And this is how to use a cautery: do it as I have said.
S’il est sanez ensi, boin est; et s’il ne l’est, se li fai .iij. cauteres des emmi le chief en dessendant jusc’a col, et ait d’espaice entre chescun cautere .i. doi de gros; et le cure si com les autres, et se tu i vues ajoster, et li malaides est soffrans, se li fai .i. cautere en mileu; et se mestiers est, .ij. autres sus les .ij. cornes, et le cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et soit li cauteres qui est apelez «olivare», si com j’ai devant dit.	If it's healing like this, well done; and if not, you should do the following: apply three fire cauteries down to the neck while descending, leaving an interval of one thumb between each one. Treat as with the others, and if you see them adjusting, and the patient is suffering, then apply another cautery in the middle; and if necessary, two more above the two horns, and treat until it heals. And use the cauteries known as 'olivare', as I have said previously.
de la froidor dou chief	from the cold of the head
Il covient que li chief soit mundifiez de yeres et de ceu que nos avons devant dit; aprés reis le chief dou malaide, puis li fai cautere emmi le chief et sus chescune corne, et .i. derrier et .iij. sus l’espinee dou col; et se tu en as plus mestier, et li cors est moiste et li malaides est soffrans, et li maladie est fors, se li fai .iiij. cauteres sus l’espinee dou dos; et li laisse tant que li plus dou keur soit ars, et lieve ta main; aprés le cure tant qu’il soit sanez, et soit li cauteres qui est apelez «olivare» que nos avons devant dit.	It is necessary to cleanse the head of warts and what we have previously discussed; after treating the head with a cautery, then apply it to the patient, on each horn of the head and one at the base and three on the spine of the neck; and if you need more, and the horns are moist and the patient is suffering, and the disease has spread, then apply four more cauterizations on the spine of the back; and leave until the most sensitive area is completely dry, then lift your hand; afterwards treat until it heals, and use the cauteries known as 'olivare' that we have previously mentioned.
de l’epilempsie	Regarding the application of a cautery with fire, instruct the afflicted to allow hair growth until it is long and even; and if they poke at their origins, restrain the eyes so that they do not move until they grow.
Li epilentiques ne doit useir de cautere fuers que cil qui est fleumatique, et covient premier mondifier le cerveil de yeres et d’autres cures que nos avons dites en la division quant li malaides est grans et soffrans de penre medicine.	The epileptics should only use fire cautery if they are of the phlegmatic type, and it is necessary to first modify their diet with years' worth and other treatments that we have mentioned in the division where the diseases are large and suffer from medicine.
Et se c’est uns enfes qui ne lou puisse soffrir, se li fai gargarisme et mastication mondifiant le cerveil sovent avec bones viandes; aprés li reis lou chief em mileu, et i fai .i. cautere selonc ce que nos avons dit devant, et .i. cautere sus lou vassel, et sus chescune corne; et se li malaides est fors et soffrans, se li fai cauteres si com j’ai dit a celui qui ait paralisie et mollification de cors, sus l’espinee dou dos et dou col, et soit li cauteres olivier selonc la maniere que j’ai dit.	And if it's a child who can't bear the discomfort, make them gargle and chew frequently with good meats; after that, they should have their head in the middle, and I do one fire according to what we said before, and one fire on the vessel, and on each horn; and if the disease is strong and causing suffering, make fires as I said for those who are paralyzed and have softening of muscles, over the spine at the back and neck, and apply olive wood fires in the manner that I have described.
Se li malaides est enfes, se li fai .i. cautere subtil selonc ceste maniere:	If the patient is young, make him a fine fire cautery according to this method:
Quant par la cause de melancolie sunt les superfluitez ou les moistors corrumpues et fleume grosse, adonques lou cauterize de teils cauteres com nos avons dit a celui qui ait paralisie.	When it is due to melancholy that the excesses or moisture are corrupted and blood is thickened, then apply the cautery of partial cauteries as we have said for the one who has paralysis.
Et se par la cause de melancolie est li superfluitez declinans a melancolie, et est li cors dou malaide moistes, adonc li done a boivre chose par coi li cervelz soit mundifiez, selonc ceu qu’il est devant en la division.	And if it is due to the cause of melancholy that the excesses decline towards melancholy, and there are symptoms in the body of moist maladies, then let them drink something that purifies the brain according to what was stated previously in this section.
Aprés reis lou chief dou malaide; aprés fai .i. torteil de lin bien fait, ausi com .i. cercle, si le met emmi le chief; et li malaides sié croisiez, et soit bien tenus de toutes pars; aprés presente le linement, et vaut mues de burre de berbis ancien; et lou chaufe a feu tempreement, si que li dois s’on li boute le puisse soffrir; aprés vuide le cercle par dedens emmi le chief, et lou laisse refroidier; et fai ce a malaide chescune semaine une fois avec autre governement boin, tant qu’il soit sanez.	After the king of the patient's ailment; after make two thread from well-made linen, as one circle, if put it into the head; and the patient sit upright, and must be held in all directions; after present the treatment, and rub with old bee wax; and heat the fire moderately so it can be applied without causing pain; afterwards empty the circle through the head, and let it cool down; and do this to the patient once a week for another procedure, until they are well.
Ou se tu vues cauterize lou en faisant poins plusors a tot le cautere.	Or, if you see that it has been burned by making marks on almost the entire cautery.
Ceste maniere de cautere amoistit le cerveil igaument; et puis met sus coton moilliet en burre et en graisse de geline.	This method of cautery moistens the brain greatly; and then place a wet cotton in butter and lard oil.
de l’awe des eulz	regarding the wisdom of the eyes
Quant awe vient premierement as eulz par les signes que j’ai dit en la division, adonques encomence et done boivre au malaide chose mundifiant le chief, et le warde de toutes moistors, et lou fai suer ou bain plusors fois a jeun.	When the eyes first come by means of the signs that I have described in division, then you should start and continue to provide the patient with things that cleanse the head, and protect it from all moisture. Make them sweat or take several baths fasting.
Aprés li comande a rere son chief, et li fai cautere emmi le chief, et li fai .ij. cauteres sus les .ij. temples se li dessendemens de l’awe est as .ij. eulz ensamble, ou en .i. se li dessendemens est en .i.; et cope a tout le cautere toutes les voines et les arteres que sont desoz le keur, et soient li cautere lonc selon lou large de la temple; et te warde de decorrement de sanc, et se tu vois trop de sanc issir, si li estainche de teil pooir com tu as.	After commanding him to move his head and have the fire cautery applied around the head, then apply two cauterizations on each temple when both eyes are descending or when one eye is descending while the other remains still. And for every cautery, take care of all veins and arteries that are near the brain; and apply the cautery long according to the width of the temples; and guard against bleeding out; if you see too much blood coming out, stop it with something as you know how to do so.
Et je t’enseignerai en l’estraction des arteres et a l’incision la cautele coment tu l’estencheras; et aucune fois fait on cautere ou hatereil desoz les .ij. os derrier.	And I will teach you about the extraction of arteries and incisions in how to apply the cautery; and every time, do not cauterize or burn anywhere near the two bones behind.
dou cors des larmes	of the tears' boughs
Quant les larmes des eulz sont ancienes et acostumees et sont sus les voines, ou delez les arteres que sont en l’aparance dou chief defors; et on voit que c’est des superfluitez froides fleumatiques, adonques li fai le cautere que j’ai dit en l’encomencement de l’awe dessendant as eulz: .i. cautere emmi le chief, et .ij. cauteres sus les .ij. temples, et .ij. cauteres ou haiterel desoz les .ij. os; et s’il i a besoigne plus, si le cauterize saigement desus le sorcil a tout .i. petit cautere.	When the tears of the eyes are old and accustomed, and present on the veins, or out from the arteries that are at the apparent backside of the head; and it's seen that they're excesses of cold humors, then I make them to be treated with cautery as I said at the beginning: first. apply fire to the head, and secondly. two cauteries on each of the four temples, and thirdly. two more cauteries under each of the four bones; and if it needs more care, carefully cauterize above the eyebrow, with one small cautery in total.
dou cors des larmes par dedens les eulz	of the tears' paths within the eyes
Quant tu le medicines selonc ceu que nos avons dit en la division, et il ne profite mie, adonques done a boivre a malaide .iij. nuis cochies; aprés li reis le chief, et li fai cautere ou mileu dou cautere olivaire; et fai .ij. cauteres dou cautere qui est apelez «clavilis» sus les .ij. sorcis, un poc desoz les chevous; et te warde de l’artere que tu ne la coper.	When you administer the medicines according to what we have said in the division, and if it does not benefit, then try giving the patient three bad eggs; after that, rub the head, and apply a cautery right in the middle of the olive oil cautery; and make two cauteries using the 'claw' type cautery on each eyebrow, slightly above the hairline; and beware to avoid touching the artery so you don't cut it.
Et c’est li forme dou cautere qui est apelez «clavilis»:	And this is the shape of the cautery which is called "claw":
Quant li papiere de l’oil est mollifie de maladie et de moistor, adonques la cautarize de cest cautere qui est apelez «olivare».	When the paper of the oil is softened by disease and moisture, then cauterize with this cautery which is called "olive".
de coi ci est li forme:	Of which the form is:
Et se tu vues si fai .ij. cauteres sus les .ij. sorcis ausi lons com li sorcilz sont; et n’i lassiez mie la main fors que tant que li tierce partie de la papiere soit arse, selonc la maniere que j’ai dit.	And if you see to apply two cauteries on the two ears as long as they are; and do not let your hand rest until that third part of the paper is burned, according to the manner I have said.
dou poil qui point l’oil	of the hair which points the ear
Aucune fois avient que li poil des oilz sont convertit au pardedens, et poignent l’oil, et i fait on cauteres selonc .ij. manieres: c’est a savoir de feu, ou de medicine ardant.	No time has there been when the hair of the ear turns into wax and touches the ear, and in this case one uses cautery according to two ways: that is to say by fire, or with burning medicine.
Ou cautere de feu comande au malaide qu’il laisse les poilz tant qu’il soient lons et igals; et s’il le poignent a lor nassance, se li estraint les eulz qu’il ne se muevent tant qu’il naissent.	For the fire cautery, instruct the patient to let the hairs grow long and even; and if they prick at their base, hold the eyes steady so they do not move until they grow.
Quant il naissent et i sont igalz, adonques met le malaide en ton sain; aprés seigne sus la papiere des eulz une figure que soit ausi com li fuelle dou mirte, et soit li comencemens dou signe delez les poilz; puis i met coton moilliet en glaire d’uef et muscillaige de persillion sus l’oil, puis eschaufe le cautere de coi ci est li forme:	When they have grown and are even, then heal the patient; afterwards draw on the paper of the eyes a figure that looks like a leaf of myrtle, and mark its beginning under the sign opposite the hairs; then apply moist cotton dipped in egg white and garlic paste to the eye, then heat the cautery according to this shape:
Aprés cauterize sus la figure que tu as signiet poc et poc mout de fois, que li keurs soit ars lai endroit; et li signes de la santeit de l’uevre est que tu voies la papiere retraite, et les poilz levez a la pointure de l’oil; adonques lieve ta main, et laisse ensi .iij. jors, puis i met coton moilliet en burre tant que li eschaudure soit ostee; aprés le cure d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez.	After applying the cautery to the area you've marked, do so gradually a little bit at a time, until the skin is burned in that spot; and signs of healthy healing are when you see the paper retreat, and the hairs stand up at the eye's edge; then lift your hand, and leave it like that for three days. Next, place wet cotton in butter until the scab is removed; afterwards apply ointment until it becomes clean.
Et se aprés ceu vienent li poilz, et li papiere est mollifie adonques rencomence le cautere sus cel leu meisme, si com tu as fait premiers; et se li poil sont defuer, si le cauterize tant que li papiere soit levee a son leu natureil, et soit igals, et ne poignent mie li poil l’oil.	And when hairs and paper start to soften after this, then resume the cautery on that same area as you did first. If hairs have fallen out, apply the cautery until the paper rises back up to its natural position in a uniform way, ensuring it doesn't pinch or irritate the eye.
Li cauteres de medicine ardant est que tu comandes au malaide qu’il laisse les poilz tant qu’il soient grans et igalz, puis fai de parchemin la forme de la foille de mirte; puis pren de savon fransois et de vive chalz, de chescun une .З., et broie ensamble bien; et le fai hastanment, si qu’il ne refroide, puis en espant sus la forme que tu es fait sicom la foille dou mirte, et met sus la papiere des eulz; et se li maladie tient en .i. oil soulement, si doit on ovrer en .i., et se en ambedous ausi; et met desoz l’oil coton moilliet en abin d’uef; et li chiés dou malaide soit en ton sain et met ton doi mostrant sus la medicine, et presse .i. poc et lou muef toutes les fois que li malaide sent mordication de la medicine, car il sent mordication ausi com de feu.	The instructions for the hot cautery are to guide the patient on letting hairs grow until they are large and uniform. Then create a shape of parchment resembling a bay leaf. Next, take French soap and live charcoal; each will require one-third, and grind them well together. Grind it quickly so that it doesn't cool down. Then apply this mixture according to the shape of a bay leaf on paper covering the affected area. If the ailment lasts for only an eye's span, you must cut into it within an eye's span. And if in both eyes; then stuff cotton moistened with egg white beneath each eye. Ensure the patient's side is toward your body and place your elbow while applying the medicine. Press one-third of a spoonful of the mixture along with some saliva every time the patient feels irritation from the medicine, for it feels irritation like fire.
Quant tu as ceu fait longement, si oste la medicine a ton doit.	When you have done this for a long time, if the medicine prescribed to you is needed.
Et quant li mordication sera passee, si leve le leu d’awe, et rewarde se tu vois la papiere levee ausi com s’ele estoit levee par constraignement de feu ou par incision; et s’il est ensi, si est bien.	And when the incision is past, if you lift up the elbow and reward it so that you see the paper lifted in the same way as it would be lifted by the constraint of fire or by incision; and if it is like this, then it is well.
Se ceu non, si remet encor de la medicine sus lou leu ou li medicine n’ait ovreit, tant que tes ovraiges soit igalz, et tes eulz mis a point; puis met sus coton moilliet en burre tant que li keurs ars soit cheus, aprés cure le leu de l’oignement qui est apelez «dyafenis» et d’autre, tant qu’il soit sanez.	If not, it still awaits the medicine on its place or until the medicine has acted, as long as your operations are equal, and your eyes are focused; then put moist cotton in butter until the burned areas are covered, after treating the place with ointment called 'dyafenis' and others, until it becomes clean.
Et se t’est mestier que tu te warde bien a ton ovraige par grant warde qu’il ne chiece point de la medicine as eulz.	And if it's your business that you must guard well to your operation by great care so that no medicine leaks out from the eyes.
Et se li papiere devient mole aprés, et li poil poignent en l’oil, si recomence la medicine sus celui leu qui est mollifiez de la papiere proprement, ensi com tu as fait devant; aprés le cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et c’est li forme de la fuelle dou mirte:	And if the paper becomes damp afterwards, and the hair grips in the eye, then restart the medicine on that part of the face which is softened by the clean paper as you did before. Afterward treat until it becomes clean; and this is like the form of a mint leaf:
Et saichés que li eul des homes sont divers en grandor et en petitece, et selonc ceu soit tes constraignemens; et ne soit mie reponue li droite voie a celui cui est li estude de cest art.	And know that the eyes of men vary in size and smallness, and according to this are your restrictions; and do not have the right path respond to him who studies this craft.
de la cure de fistule par cautere	Of treating fistulas by cautery
Quant tu cures fistule si com nos avons dit en divisions des maladies, et tes cures ne profitent mie, adonques covient il que tu li fais cautere selonc ceste maniere.	When you treat a fistula as we have explained in the sections on diseases and your treatments are not beneficial, then it is necessary for you to apply a cautery treatment according to this manner.
Comande au malaide qu’il mette son chief en ton sain; et teigne li menistres son chief entre tes mains en teil maniere qu’il ne se mueve, ne ne demoinne son chief; aprés met coton moilliet en abin d’uef ou en jus de persillion sus l’oil; aprés chaufe le cautere qui est teilz: et est chevez au chief si com li forme d’une penne de vouteul, ensamble la queil soit li cautere; se tu vues, si soit apointé des l’un chief dusc’a l’autre, et se tu vues, si soit ausi com une tente; mais toutevoie, cist qui est chevez vaut mues por ton ovraige.	Instruct the patient to place their head in your healthy position; and guide the surgeons' hands on their head between your palms so it does not move or slip from its place. After that, apply cotton soaked in egg juice or garlic juice to the eye; then heat up the cautery which is made: and place it close to the eye as if it were the shape of a goose feather, combine it with the point of the cautery touching it; if you see, make sure it points from one feather tip to the other, and if you can see, make it resemble a tent. But always remember that the position that works best for your operation is what truly matters.
Aprés presse la fistule s’ele est overte, et en trai la porriture, et la seche; et s’ele est close, si la oevre, et trai fuers la bowe; aprés met sus le cautere chaut forment, et tien ta main au cautere a la partie dou neif ensus de l’oil, que ta mains ne faice folie; et met le cautere en la graisse de l’oil, et la corromp.	After pressing the fistula when it has been opened, and treating the putrefaction, drying it out; if it is closed but still produces something, take it outside of the body; after this, place a cautery on it. Hold your hand at the part below the nose near the eye with the cautery, so that you don't lose control of your hand movements; and put the cautery in the grease around the eye, and allow it to decompose.
Se tu viens au comencement dou cautere jusc’a l’os, si serait bien.	If you come to the start of the cautery up to the bone, it would be well.
Se ceu non, si rencomence le cautere encor une fois, et autre se tu en as mestier, et le laisse III jors; aprés i met sus coton moilliet en burre, et lou cure de l’oignement desiccatif tant qu’il soit sanez, et se XL jors passent qu’il ne soit sanez, si met sus medicine ague corrosive tant que li os soit descovers; et lou reis selonc ceu que il venrait en son chapistre.	If not, restart the cautery one more time, and if you need it again, leave it for three days; after that, place wet cotton on butter, and apply an ointment dressing until healed. If forty days have passed without healing, apply corrosive mustard medicine until the bone is uncovered; then proceed according to what he had written in his chapter.
Et i a une maniere de cautere de fistule que aucun des anciens dirent.	And there is a way of cauterizing a fistula that none of the old ones mentioned.
Entens a fistule, et fens le leu; aprés met en la fendure I camahan subtil de coi ci est li forme:	Understand what a fistula is, and make the incision; afterwards place in the opening a thin camel bone cut to this shape:
et i font a la quantiteit d’une .З. de plonc; et tien ta main ou camahan fermement, et ne se mueve li malaides nes point, que li plons fondus ne corre a son oil; et covient c’on mette sus l’oil a malaide coton moilliet en abin d’uefz ou en awe: li plonc si art lou leu de fistule, et lou saine per mervillouse saniteit.	And they do it in the quantity of one and a half pints; hold your hand or cudgel tightly, and don't move the injured part until the heated metal has reached its oil; and one must place cotton soaked with moisture over the eye: the lead when applied to diseased tissue, and healthily heals diseased areas.
Et se li fistule est sanee per le cautere que nos avons dit, c’est boin.	And if the fistula is healed by the cautery as we have said, it is good.
Se ce non, si covient aministrer pertus au neif, et ramener la fistule au cors dou neif selonc ceu qu’il covient en som propre leu.	But if not, it is necessary to administer pertussis to the child and return the fistula to its proper place under the child's neck according to what is suitable in our own way.
des crevaices en levres	cuts in lips
Mout de fois avienent crevaices en levres que sont apelees «poil», et meismement en levres des enfans.	Rarely, there appear tears in lips which are called 'hair', and similarly in infants' lips.
Quant tu cures ces crevaices de ceu que nos avons dit en divisions, et li cure ne profite, adonques eschaufe .i. petit cautere cultellaire selonc ceste forme:	When you treat these tears as we have discussed in sections, and if the treatment doesn't help, then apply this: take a small surgical instrument for cauterization according to this form:
Et le met hastanment en celles crevaices tant qu’il viegne jusc’a font; aprés cure le leu de cerote tant qu’il soit sanez.	And immediately place it in those tears until you reach the base; afterwards, heal the wound with tallow until it is healthy.
de l’aposteme de la goule	from the abscess of the throat
Quant apostume vient en la racine de la goule ou en l’uve, ou ou palais, ou as racines des dens, aprés fait porriture et ront et est enveillis et devient fistule; et tu le cures si com nos avons dit en divisions, et il ne profite mie: adonques covient il que tu aies .i. cautere selonc la quantiteit de la fistule; aprés le bote ou pertus de la fistule, et tien ta main tant que li fer chaus viegne au font de li, et ou derrien leu; et fai ensi une fois ou .ij., aprés le cure de ce que nos avons dit en cures, tant qu’il soit sanez; et s’il est curez ensi, c’est boin; et se ceu non, si covient descovrir le leu et oster l’os corrumput, selonc ceu que vos le troverez en son chapistre.	When an abscess appears at the root of the throat or in the uterus, or on the palate, or under the roots of the teeth, after becoming putrid and swollen it becomes a fistula; and you treat it as we have said in divisions, but it fails to improve: therefore, it is necessary that you have one cautery according to the size of the fistula; after the removal or erosion of the fistula, hold your hand until the metal reaches the bottom of it, then any further; and do this once or twice, following the treatment we mentioned in treatments, while it remains healthy. If treated like this, it is good; and if not, you should expose its location and remove the infected bone as found in your chapter.
dou movement des dens	The shifting of teeth
Quant les gencives sont mollifies par moistor et les dens muevent, et tu le cures per medicines et ceu ne vaut, adonc met le chief dou malaide en ton sain; aprés eschaufe le cautere dont li forme venra ci aprés en teil maniere que tu mettes une cainne sor le dent; et met dedens le cautere chaut hastanment, et tien tant ta main que li malaides sente la chalor venant a la racine dou dent; aprés lieve ta main et rencomence le cautere selonc ta volenteit; aprés emplisse li malaides sa bouche d’awe salee, et la teigne une houre et raiche fuers.	When the gums soften due to moisture and teeth move, you treat it through medicines but if this fails, then place the head of the patient in a healthy position; afterward heat up the cautery as follows: take one stick next to the tooth. And place the end of the cautery immediately inside the tooth, while holding your hand so that the heat reaches the root of the tooth; after that lift your hand and start using the cautery according to your will; afterwards fill the infected area with salt water, let it sit for an hour and then remove it.
Et en teil maniere li dens qui estoit movans si est confermez, et li gencive mollifie restrainte, et li moistors corrumpue sechie.	And in this way, the teeth that were moving are stabilized, and the gums that were soft are made firm, and the moisture that was corrupt is dried.
de la dolor des dens	Of toothache
Quant dolor de dens vient por froidor, ou il i a froidor ou veir, et les cures de medicine ne valent, adonc i ait mestier de cautere selonc .ij. manieres: et cautere de burre et cautere de feu.	When toothache comes from coldness, or there is coldness or frostbite, and medical treatments don't help, then one must use cautery according to two ways: and butter cautery and fire cautery.
Cautere de burre si est telz que tu preignes burre de vaiche, et le bout en une cuillier de fer ou d’arain; aprés pren coton et envolope sus la pointe d’une tente, et la moille en burre bulit, et met sus le dent dolant hastanment et tien tant qu’il soit refroidiez; et ensi fai sovent tant que sa vertus viegne a la racine de la dent, et se tu vues si moille laine et coton en burre froit, et met sus le dent doillant, et met sus .i. fer chaut tant que li feus viegne au chevement dou dent.	Butter cautery if it is like this: you take butter from a cow, and use the tip of a iron or silver spoon; afterwards take cotton and wrap it on the tip of a needle, and immerse the wet end in the cold butter until it solidifies; then apply it quickly to the painful tooth and hold it until it has cooled down; and do this often until its effect reaches the root of the tooth, and if you see wet wool or cotton immersed in cold butter on the painful tooth, put them again on the aching tooth, and place a hot iron there until the heat reaches the pain in the tooth.
Li cauteres ensamble feu si est telz que tu preignes uns cainne de fer ou d’arain, et soit grosse si que li feus ne viegne a la bouche dou malaide; aprés chaufe le cautere, de coi li forme venra ci aprés, et le met sus le dent et tien ta main tant que li cauteres soit refroidiez; fai ceu sovent, car li dolor sera ostee celui jor meisme ou l’endemain.	The fire cautery should be like this that you prefer a piece of iron or tin, and make it large enough for the heat not to reach the mouth of the patient; after heating the cautery, from which the flame will come next, place it on the tooth and hold your hand until the cautery cools down; do this often because the pain will be relieved that day or the following day.
Et covient que li malaides emplisse sa bouche de boin burre en l’empressement de cel cautere, et puis le raiche fuer; et c’est li forme dou cautere:	And it is necessary that the patient fills their mouth with good butter in anticipation of this cautery, and then quickly pull it out; and this is the form of the cautery:
Et fai cautere dou queil chief que tu voudras, et selonc ceu que tu as pooir; et c’est li forme de la caine:	And perform the cautery at whatever you desire or are able to do; and this is the form of the iron:
des scrophules	Of scrofula
Quant les scrophules sont de fleume et de moistors froides, et ne sont obeissans a digestion par medicines, adonques eschaufe le cautere cheveit de coi ci aprés vient li forme, et ait II aovertures por les fumees a issir au cautere de l’autre partie; et met le cautere chaut sus l’apostume une fois, ou II se mestier est, tant qu’il viegne au font de l’apostume; et se li apostume est petis si met cautere selonc la quantiteit de l’apostume, et le laisse ensi III jors; et met sus coton moilliet em burre tant que li arsure soit ostee; aprés cure le leu d’oignemens et de tentes tant qu’il soit sanez.	When the scrophules are due to cold aqueous and moist substances, and do not respond to digestion by medicine, then heat up the cautery as described below, and open two openings for fumes to leave from it on the other side; and place the heated cautery against the abscess once or twice, according to how many times necessary, until it goes deep into the abscess. If the abscess is small, apply the cautery according to the size of the abscess and keep it there for three days. Then put moist cotton with butter on it until all pus has drained out; afterwards cleanse the area with ointments and bandages until it heals.
Li forme de la cainne:	The form of sugar:
Quant les moistors vainquent sus les chenals dou pormon, et meismement quant ce vient de froide complexion, adonc covient que li malaides soit voidiez premiers par medicines solutives; aprés li fai cautere a la racine de la gorge, et te garde que tu ne venir mie jusc’a la gorge, et n’ardre dou keur mais c’un poc.	When the moist substances conquer in the veins near the heart and especially when it comes from cold constitution, then it is necessary that the body be first cleansed by diuretic medicines; after that make a cautery at the root of the throat, and take care not to come all the way up to the throat, but just a little.
Aprés li fai I autre cautere a la jointure dou col au chief de l’espinee, et soit li cauteres qui est apelez «clavile» de coi nos avons la forme devant; et cure le leu si com nos avons devant dit tant qu’il soit sanez.	After this procedure, I perform another cauterization at the junction of the neck and the base of the spine. Let it be a cautery named 'clavicle', which we have demonstrated in front; then treat it as previously described until it is healthy.

Quant li chiés de l’ajutoire est desaloiez par cause de moistor, et on le remet a leu, et il n’i puet demorer ains revient adés et desalue par petit movement qui avient, si com nos avons esproveit, adonques covient il que tu ramoinnes la dislocation premierement. The treatment involves making three cuts across the liver, following this form, figure, and quantity, at the spot where the pain originates from the stomach; there should be an interval of about two fingers between each cut. dou cautere de pleuresin	of the weeping cautery

de la mice	Of mice

de ydropisie	Of cautery with fire, command the patient to let the hair grow long and even; and if they prick at their root, hold the eyes steady so they do not move until they grow.
Cautere ne vaut a ydropique, fors c’a la maniere qui est apelee «asclytes».	The cautery is not suitable for erysipelas, except in the way it is called "asclepiate".
Quant tu la cures selonc les manieres que nos avons dit en divisions, et ta cure ne profite mie, adonques covient il que tu li faices IIII cauteres entor la boude, et I sus l’estomac, et un sus le foie, et I sus la mice, et II derrier le dos sus l’espinee, et I endroit le pis; et soit li cauteres bien pres de l’espés dou keur. Aprés laisse le cautere aovert por giter porriture lonc tens, et ne lassier mie la cure dou malaide aprés le cautere; et sanation se hasterait, et seront ensamble les .ij. ententions avec l’aide de Deu.	After letting the cautery open for a long time to fumigate, do not stop the remedy from the patient after the cautery; and then healing would hasten, and both the two remedies would work together with God's help.
Li forme dou cautere por le ventre soit li clavile que nos avons devant mostreit; et cil por le dos soit olivaire, selonc ceu qu’il est ci devant mis.	The shape of the cautery for the belly should be like the illustration we showed before; and for that one used for the back it should be similar to an olive, as described earlier.

de la hainche	From the hip

de la dolor de la hainche	关于髋部的疼痛
Quant dolor vient en la boiste de la hainche, et c’est de froidor et de moistor, et li malaides est curez de ceu que nos avons dit en la division et li cure ne vaut, et li maladie est anciene: adonc covient il que tu purges le malaide des grosses humors de pilules fetides, ou autres pilules bones semblans.	When pain comes into the hip joint, and it's due to coldness and moisture, and patients are treated in accordance with what we have discussed about division and treatment for these conditions, but if the disease is old: then you should cleanse the patient of thick fluids using foul-smelling pills or other good pills that resemble them.
Aprés li fai cautere; et li maniere dou cautere si est selonc II manieres: c’est a savoir ensamble medicines ardans, et cautere de feu.	After you perform the cautery; and concerning the method of the cautery there are two ways: it means to combine heated medicines, and fire cautery.
Cautere de feu si est selonc mout de manieres, desquelz li uns est telz: que tu cauterize sus la boiste de la hainche III cauteres triangulalz selonc ceste forme, et i fai bone profunditeit et grant, et ait entre chaicun cautere d’espaice la groissece d’un doi, et soit li cauteres olivaire; aucune fois fait on cautere en mileu sus lou chief de la hainche, por coi il en i a IIII selonc ceste forme:	Fire cautery follows several methods. One of these is to apply three triangular cauterizations on the hip bone, following this form, and ensure they have a good depth and size, with each space between them as large as two fingers, and to make the cauterizations olive-like; there should be no cauterization in the middle of the highest part of the hip, for according to this form there are four.
Et se tu vues, si le cauterize au cautere dou cercle que nos avons devant dit en la dislocation de la hainche; mais fai en teil maniere que li cercles conteigne toute la hainche, et tous li espés dou keur soit ars.	And if you see fit, cauterize with a circular cautery as we have mentioned before in the dislocation of the hip joint; but do it so that the circles contain the entire hip joint, and all parts of the knee are burned.
Et c’est li maniere c’on fait en sciatique, quant li dolor tient en la hainche, et ne parvient mie jusc’a la cuisse ne jusc’a la jambe.	And this is the way it's done in sciatica, when pain stays in the hip and doesn't reach up to the thigh or down to the leg.
Et s’ele vient jusc’a la cuisse et la jambe, se li fai II cauteres lai ou li malaides dit que li dolor li tient, et I cautere desus la cheville IIII dois, a la partie senestre un poc; et soit li cauteres cutellaire, et soit arse li espesseté dou keur; et se li malaides sent que li dolor s’estende jusc’a dois dou piet ou pres d’enqui, se le cauterize la ou il sent la dolor III poins ou IIII au cautere qui est apelez «poins».	And if it comes up to the thigh and leg, apply two fire cauteries there where the illness says that the pain keeps them, and add three on top of the ankle above, four times, with a little in the left part; do these cutaneous cauterizations, and burn off any thickness on the knee; and if the illness feels that the pain spreads up to just two or slightly before the ankle bone, then apply the cautery where it senses the pain for three points or four at each point referred to as 'points'.
Et se mestiers est, se li en fai plus; et se il seit que li dolor soit desoz le genoil vers la cuisse, se li fais cautere au cautere cutellaire ou circulaire, et te done bien garde en tous tes cauteres que tu n’i lassier mie tant le cautere que tu brules les ners et les grans arteres, et que tu ne faices au malaide plus grant nuisance et contraction.	And if more work is needed, then proceed with it; and should the pain be spreading from the knee towards the thigh, apply cutlery or circular cauterization, and make sure to diligently carry out all your cauterizations without allowing them to stop short of burning nerves and major arteries, and do not cause the patient any greater harm or contraction.
Et je meisme ai veus plusors qui ont fait cautere sus la cheville dou piet, et li lasserent tant que li jambe fut toute enflee, et li piez ausi, et fut perciez et corrumpus toz li piez.	And I have seen several who applied the cautery on the ankle bone, and it was effective until their legs swelled completely and likewise their feet were pierced and corrupted in all of them.
Aprés une solution de ventre dont il ot la mort.	After an abdominal treatment that led to death.

Et soit eschaufez tant qu’il soit toz rouges et giete senteles, et puis le mette on sus la boiste de la hainche malaide, et soit tornez sus lou sain costeit; et lou cauterize une fois .i. cautere reont et lou laisse .iij. jors; et puis fai emplaustre de burre, et laisse la plaie aoverte lonc tens; aprés la cure d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez. ou il ait I petit pertuis defuer se que li pointe d’un raisor i puisse entreir; et met desor celui pot I autre pot bien plombeit, et met sus alcali et chalz et awe douce sus, tant qu’il en i ait I doi desus les poudres cant tu l’avras bien preingte a ta main; et le laisse ensi tant qu’il en dessende awe ague et chiece ou pot plombeit, puis pren toute cele awe, et la giete sus chalz et sus alcali si com devant. Et Galiens nos raconte une cure dont uns hons fut curez de la dolor de la hainche et de la voine sciatique, et lou loe mout, et dit que on n’i fist autre cure, et qu’il en fut sanez a une soule fois quant on ot fait ceste cure, et il se fut baigniez si com il l’enseigne ci aprés.	And Galen tells us of a remedy that was used for the pain in the hip and sciatic vein, and to a great extent. He says that no other treatment was done, and it worked miraculously on its first use when this cure was applied, and he took baths as is instructed below.
Et dist en teil maniere que tu preignes dou litargire vert fres et sec, et le broie mout avec I poc de graisse, et met sus la hainche et sus la cuisse et sus la jambe ou la dolor tient, et la lie; et li laisse III houres et par la quantiteit que li malaides ne sente plus l’arsure.	And it is said in this manner: take fresh and dried verdigris powder, grind it thoroughly with a little bit of fat, and apply it to the hip, thigh, and leg where the pain resides. And then make them enter into a warm bath until their body is slightly revived, and make them rest on a bed, and the pain will leave them completely and they will feel well.
Et saiches que nuls ne doit user de cautere de telz medicines, se ceu n’est aprés l’evacuation de cors.	And know that no one should use such medicines as the cautery, unless after the removal of the body.
