Prenez lainne et la beurez d’oile vielz, et metez sus la fossete qui est entre le pouce dou piez et l’autre qui est apelez foscile.	Take wool and soak it in old oil, and place it on the depression that is between the first toe of the foot and the other one called the foscile.
Aprés pren fiens de chievre sec, et l’empren a feu tant qu’il soit charbons, et lou met sus la laine, et le laisse tant qu’il soit estains; et refai encor ensi, et ne cesser de faire ensi tant que tu penses par sens qu’il viegne jusc’a la hainche, et que li dolor soit cessee; et cist manieres de cautere est apelez «cautere de chievre».	After taking dried donkey hair, hold it over the fire until it becomes charcoal, and place it on the wool, and let it burn out; and repeat this process again, without stopping until you think that it has reached up to the hip, and the pain is gone; and this method of cautery is called "donkey's hair cautery".
de la dolor dou dos	of the pain of the back
Quant dolor vient au dos, ou par cheoir ou de percussion ou par trop grant evacuation, ou par semblans de matiere espandue froide, a nule de ces semblances ne vaut cauteres, fuer que a celi qui vient de infusion de froide matiere.	When pain comes to the back, whether by falling or impact or from too much evacuation, or due to exposure to cold matter, none of these conditions warrant cauterization, for it is akin to what arises from the infusion of cold matter.
Il covient c’aprés ceu que li malaides est voidiez de pilules fetides ou d’autres semblans, que on li faice sus lou dos, lai ou li dolor tient, trois lignes signies d’enche, et en chescune ligne .v. cauteres ou plus selonc la vertut et la quantiteit que li malaides puet soffrir; et soit fait li cauteres selonc le cautere qui est apelez «poins»; et se tu vues, fai .iij. cauteres ou .iiij. au cautere clavile moien selonc ceste forme:	After the patient has been treated for bad pills or other similar conditions, one should apply this to their back where the pain is felt, marking three lines of length and applying burns at each line according to the size and quantity that the body can withstand; proceed with the burn technique as described for the "point" cautery. And if you see fit, do three or four burns around the median cautery following this form:
Maintes fois vient ceste maladie as petis enfans, et li signes de l’encomencement si est qu’il ont estroite alainne quant il se lievent, et paor; et tu trueves en la derriene espinee dou dos et en nous l’apparance qui vient sus les autres espinees.	This disease often affects small children, and at the onset it is characterized by a lack of strength when they stand up, followed by fear. You will find an inflammation in the last spinal nerve on the back and sometimes there appears a phenomenon on other nerves.
Quant tu vois ceu et tu le vues curer, si le cauterize au cautere de celcle selonc ceste forme.	When you see this and observe its cure, if you apply it with a hot iron in this manner on the body.
Si que li cautere porpreigne chescune partie de l’espinee egaument.	If the cautery burns each part of the spine equally.
Et se tu vues, si cauterize entor l’espinee au cautere poignant II lignes ou III, et soient li poins pres l’uns de l’autre.	And if you see it, apply the cautery to the spine along the line where the cauterization burns for two or three lines, and have the points close together.
Aprés cure le leu tant qu’il soit sanez selonc ceu que nos avons dit, et warde que tu n’amenistrer cautere en gilbositeit qui soit en spame de nerf.	After the cure as long as it is clean according to what we have said, and beware that you do not apply the cautery in a state of excitement near nerves.
de la dolor des jointes	of the pain in joints
Quant dolor de jointes sunt de moistors que sont espandues a chaicun membre dou cors, et quant dolor vient em piez, que li mire apelent «podagre» proprement, et quant elle est de froide cause et cures de medicines ne la puent curer, si est curez par cauteres en teil maniere: fai li mout de cauteres entor la jointure dou piet, et soit li cauteres olivaire selonc ceste forme:	When joint pain is due to moisture spread throughout each limb, and when pain comes in the foot, which they call "gout" properly, and when it is caused by cold and its treatment can be cured with medicines that cannot cure it, then it should be treated using cautery in this manner: make a series of iron cauterizations around the joint of the foot, and apply olive oil as follows:
Et s’il i a besoigne que tu poignes sus la faice dou piet, se li fai cautere a tot le cautere c’on claime «point».	And if there is need that you touch on the thigh by the foot, if it is cauterized with the entire cautery saying 'point'.
Et se les dolors viegnent jusc’a genous et as autres jointures, et ceu avient maintes fois, se li fai cautere sus chaicun genoil III cauteres ou IIII de chescunne partie, a tout le cautere olivaire; et se tu as mestier de plus, si en fai plus, mais n’i tenir mie ta main fuers que tant que li espés dou keur soit ars.	And if the pains extend up to the knees and other joints, and this happens many times, if you need to cauterize on each knee three or four at each part, with the entire olive oil cautery; and if you have the need for more, do more, but don't let your hand be out that until the skin where it's burned is cooked.
Et se les dolors dessendent jusc’a genoil et au dos, se li aministre le cautere que nos avons dit en son chapistre.	And if the pains descend as far as the thighs and back, then it is administered to them the cautery that we have said in our chapter.
Et se les dolors sunt as mains, si fai poins entor le foscile II lignes; et s’il remaint point de dolor as dois, si fai poins sus chescune jointe et sus lou poil de la main; et se les dolors vienent jusc’as coutes ou jusc’as espaules, si cauterize chescune partie, et fai boin governement au malaide et penre medicines.	And if the pains are in the hands, make points into lines II of the thigh; and if there remains no pain on the wrists, make points on each joint and on the hair of the hand; and if the pains come up to elbows or shoulders, cauterize each part, and well govern the patient and prescribe medicines.
Car se tu li fais boin governement et tu purges fleume, si sera saneis a l’aide de Deu.	And if you give them good governance and cleanse the humor, they will be helped by God to recover their health.
de la routure dou syfac	from the rupture of the uterus
Quant routure vient en angres, et li bouelz dessendent as coions et c’est novelement, si covient que quant tu lou vues curer, qu’il ne menjuce mie celui jor; et qu’il use choses qui laichent lou ventre, si que li fiens dessende de son ventre; aprés le fai seoir sus son dos entre tes mains, et li comande qu’il teigne son alaine tant que li boueil soient repairiet, et les ramoinne a tes dois, et seigne d’enche desoz la routure sus l’os dou poignil, et a tout un signe que soit semblans a la moitiet d’un cercle a desus dou cors; puis eschaufe le cautere de coi ci est li forme:	When rupture occurs in anger, and the bowels descend to the kidneys; it is something new. Therefore, when you are curing his eyes, do not let him drink during that time; and use things that calm the stomach so that the wind descends from his stomach. After that, make him sit on his back between your hands, and instruct him to scratch his armpit until the bowel has healed, then remove it with your fingers, and apply heat to the rupture over bone where the knife was used; ensure it resembles half of a circle above his chest. Then prepare the cautery as described here:
tant qu’il soit blans et qu’il giete senteles.	Until it is white and emits serents.
Puis ramoine les bouels a lor leu; et li ministres teigne sa main sus qu’il ne retornent arrier; et oevre bien les cuisses au malaide, et met desoz lui I cussin et I serjant sus les cuisses, et I autre sus lou pis qui li teigne les mains; puis met le cautere sus lou signe a tout ta main, et lou tien droit et lou tien tant que tu ateignes l’os, et se tu ne l’ateins la premiere fois, si le rencomence encor une autre tant que tu viegnes jusc’a l’os; et te warde subtilment que li boueil ne saille quant tu fais lou cautere; que tu ne le brulasses; et que par ceu li malaides ne muere, ou autre malz.	Then pull out the bowels from their place; and have the servants prick his hand so they do not turn back; and work well on the thighs with the patient, and place one cossin and one sergeant on the thighs, and another under his buttocks which pricks his hands; then apply the cautery to the sign on all your hand, and hold it straight and keep holding until you reach the bone; if you do not reach the bone the first time, try again a second time until you touch the bone; and watch carefully that the boil does not burst as you make the cautery; that you do not burn them; and so that the patient does not die or suffer any other ill.
Et saiches que quant tu ne viens jusc’a l’os au cautere, tes ovraiges ne vaut rien.	And know that when you do not come all the way to the bone with the cautery, your operations are worthless.
Et covient que li cauteres des enfans soit subtilz selonc la mesure d’ous, et des grans gens aussi grans selonc lor mesure; aprés III jors cure lou leu dou cautere de burre tant que li eschaudure soit ostee; aprés le cure d’autres oignemens tant qu’il soit sanez, et gise li malaides XL jors sus son dos tant que li plaie soit bien soudee; et covient que ses norrissemens soit lassatis longement, si que li boueil ne saillent quant il se preigdra d’aler en chambres.	And it must be that the cauteries for children are subtle according to their size, and also large people's as large according to their size; after three days treat with a balm on the skin by the fire iron until the scab comes off; afterwards apply other dressings until they heal well, and rest the patient forty days on their back so that the wound heals properly; and it must be that these instructions are followed for a long time, so that the pus doesn't spill when they wish to go into chambers.
Et aprés XL jors, quant il se voudra lever, se li amenistre une faixe bien faite, et la porse XL autres jors; et ait boin repos, qu’il se travaille poc et se warde de trop grant repletion de boivre et de mengier, et de trop haut braire; et quant il fait cest enseignement si est sanez entierement.	And after forty days, if they want to stand up, have them wear a well-made bandage and do this for another forty days; and ensure good rest, that they work little and guard against excessive drinking and eating, and too much shouting; and when they follow this advice, they will be completely healed.
Et je dirai ci aprés la cure de taillier en son chapistre.	And I will say after this chapter's treatment of tailoring.
de la routure dou ventre	regarding the rupture of the belly
Quant routures vienent en autres ventres et sont connisans, et tu vues qu’elles ne croissent plus, se li fai I cautere dou cautere reont selonc sa quantiteit, et soit ars li tiers dou keur; aprés le cure selonc ceu que nos avons dit; et aucun des anciens ont dit c’on le doit cauterizer au cautere a III angles selonc ceste forme:	When wounds occur in other bellies and are known, and you see that they no longer grow, I will apply the fire cautery according to its quantity, and let it be one-third of the coal; after treating according to what we have said; and none of the old ones said that one should cauterize at the fire in three angles according to this form:
mais signe premier le leu d’enche et fai une ligne per la largesce desus la routure, et une autre defuers, et main ta main emmi a tout le cautere clavile.	The first sign is the beginning of healing; draw a line across the width above the wound and another below it, and hold your hand with the fire tool all along.
Mais li premiers cauteres est plus legiers et muedres.	The first cauterizations are lighter and heal more easily.
de dolor anciene en aucun membre	from old pain in no limb
Quant dolor vient en aucun membre, ou de cheoir ou de ferir, et cele dolor tient lonc tens, et li cure de medicine n’i vaut, adonc covient qu’il soit cauterizeis au cautere qui est apelez «poins», et soit li cauteres selonc la longesce dou membre et la petitece et sa foibleteit et sa vertut et sa location de torcions et de sa dolor.	When pain comes to any limb, whether from falling or being hit, and the pain lasts for a long time, and medicine cure doesn't help it, then it should be cauterized with what is called "points" cautery, and the cauterizations must match the length of the member and its smallness and weakness and its function and location of twisting and its pain.
s’il est sanez dou premier cautere, c’est bien; se ceu nom, recomence I autre cautere sus celui, car teilz costume est qu’il se doit muer au membre que li est prochiens, por coi il covient que tu faices les cauteres tant que li malaides soit saneis.	If the patient has recovered from the first cautery, that's good; if not, start another cautery on it, for these practices require movement in a limb close to where they are performed, thus you must conduct the cauteries as long as the patient is healthy.
de meselerie	Regarding cautery from fire, instruct the patient to let the hairs grow long and even; and if they prick at their base, hold the eyes steady so they do not move until they grow.
Li meseil sont aidiet aucune fois par cautere par grant aide, et meismement li maladie que vient de la putrefaction de fleume et de melancolie.	The healings take place once every cautery with considerable assistance, and similarly the disease comes from the putrefaction of phlegm and melancholy.
Cant tu la vues cauterizer, pren warde se li maladie est au comencement, et s’ele est curee selonc ceu que nos avons dit en la division, et ne dessent ne ne demoure, et tu doutes que li corruption ne porpreigne tout le malaide, adonques li fai V cauteres sus lou chief: I emmi le chief a nouf, et l’autre vers lou front a la fin des chevous; et II sus les II cornes, et I derrierre sus le haiterel; et i laise tant ta main que li cauteres viegne jusc’a l’os, et tant que les escorces en issent fors si que les vapors des grosses humors s’en puissent issir; et le cauterize sus la mice selonc ce qu’il est devant.	Can't you see the cautery tool? Take care that if the disease is at its beginning, and it is treated according to what we have said in the division, without spreading or remaining, then you fear that corruption might spread throughout the body. Thus make V cauterizations on each side: I move the first one across from ear to chin, and the second one from the top of the head towards the back at the edge of the hair; and II cauterize both horns, and III cauterize behind on the spine; keep your hand as close as possible for the cautery to reach up to the bone, and until the scabs are expelled sufficiently so that the vapors from the excess fluids can escape; and cauterize lightly in the middle according to what was done beforehand.
Et se li meselerie est partout esparse; et elle pert manifestement, si covient que tu lou cauterizes de ces cauteres que nos avons dit ou chief, et .i. cautere en som lou neis, et .ij. cauteres sus l’espinee dou col, et .vj. cauteres sus l’espinee dou dos, et .i. grant sus la crupie et .i. autre delez, et .ij. sus les .ij. espaules; et .ij. sus les coutes, et .ij. sus les tendrons dou pis, et .i. sus chascune jointe des mains et des piez, et sus les fosses des mains; et te warde des ners que sunt sus lou derrien calcant, que tu ne les bruler; et aucune fois fait om cautere sus l’os dou poignil, et .i. autre sus l’os de l’estomac, et .i. autre sus lou foie.	And if the measles are everywhere scattered; and it is clearly missing, then it is necessary that you apply this cautery with these cauterizing methods to the head, and once on the nape of the neck, and seven cauterizations on the spine of the back, and one large near the chest and another below, and two near each shoulder blade; and two on the ribs, and two on the tendons of the foot, and one for each joint in hands and feet, and on the hollows of the hands; and be careful not to burn any nerves that are behind the heel, do not burn them. And never apply a cauterization near bone on the shinbone, and another on the bone of the stomach, and another on the liver.
Et saiches que quant plus i fais de cautere, plus li fais d’aide, et mues li profite; et saiches que li malaides ne sent point de dolor au cautere si com li sain le sentent, por ce que li cors est ja toz corrumpus.	And know that the more I apply the cautery, the more aid it provides, and profits him; and know that patients do not feel pain during cautery as healthy individuals would, because their bodies are already thoroughly corrupted.
Et covient ke li cautere soient grant et petit selonc les membres et les jointures, selonc ceu que vos lou troverez en manieres des fers.	And it is necessary that the cauterizing fires be large and small according to the limbs and joints, as you will find in the methods of metalworking.
Aprés cure lou leu de farine de veces avec miel et autres cures tant qu’il soit saneis.	After the treatment, use flour mixed with honey and other treatments until it becomes healthy again.
Quant enfleure vient en aucun membre et est curee par medicines et oiles et emplastres, et il n’est mie sanez, adonques li fai cauteres sus le membre selonc la grandour et la petitece dou membre; et soit li cauteres un poc entrans en l’espés dou keur; puis le cure d’oignemens tant qu’il soit sanez.	When inflammation occurs in any part of the body and is treated with medicines, oils, and plasters without improving, then you should apply cauterization to the limb according to its size; and let the cauterizations penetrate a bit into the red area of the wound; then treat it with dressings until it becomes healthy.
Et aucune fois fait on cautere et a la main et au piet et au dos, a l’issue dou nerf que muet le membre, et ensi si est ostee li enfleure; et toutevoie ne s’en entremette nuls s’il n’est conoissans des membres et des issues des ners movans lou cors.	And no time is there done cautery at the hand and foot and back, along the exit of the nerve that makes the limb moveless, and thus bones are removed; and all the while none interfere with it if one isn't acquainted with the limbs and workings of the moving nerves in the body.
de albaras	Of cauteries, instruct the patient to let their hair grow long and evenly; if they prick at their roots when young, hold them steady so they don't move until grown out.
Quant li maladie qui est apelee «albaras» est enveillie, et li engien de medicine n’i valent rien, adonques le cauterize d’un cautere un poc parfont, selonc la quantiteit de l’espés dou keur, tant que li blenchour soit ostee, et soit muee sa color; puis le cure de farine de veces et de lentilles avec oile roset et foilles de plantain, et sanc de colon et sanc d’alondre, de chescun une partie; et soit mellez tout ensamble, et soit liiez d’un drapel, et soit aers au leu tant qu’il soit sanez.	When the disease called "albaras" matures and medicine no longer helps, then one should use a small fire cautery according to the size of the spot, until the boil is removed and its color changes. Then apply cornmeal several times mixed with rose oil and plantain leaves, and blood from chicken and blood from duck, each in proportion. Mix all together, bind it with a cloth, and leave on the affected area until healed.
li cure de chancre par cautere	The treatment of a sore by cautery
Quant chancre vient au comencement, et tu lou vues arrester, si le cauterize au cautere qui semble I cercle, tout entor au tour dou chancre.	When gangrene begins, and you see it start to halt, if you notice it at the outset, apply a cautery instrument that appears like a circle, all around the circumference of the gangrene.
Et toutevoie li saige dirent que on faice cautere ausi au mileu dou chancre; et toutevoie ceu ne me semble mie boin, car je redous que il ne soit ulcerez et corrumpus, et je l’ai ja veut avenir aucune fois; et plus droituriere chose est qu’il soit cauteriés entor, au cautere qui est apelez «circule», si com nos avons dit en mout de cauteres.	And still, the wise ones advise that one should apply a cautery also at the center of the gangrene; and yet I do not think this is good, because I fear it might lead to erosion and corruption, and so I have decided never to do so; and more straightforwardly, the application should be made around the edge, with the type of cautery that we call "circular", as we described earlier in terms of cauteries.
de l’enfleure qui ne puet meurer	of swelling that cannot die
Quant aucuns ait une maladie qui est apelee «adubelati», et elle tarde de meurer ou por la superfluiteit qu’ele fait ou por l’eaige dou malaide quant il est decrepites (c’est a dire trop vielz) et il a poc de sanc, ou por lou tens; et tu la vues haster de meurer: adonques le cauterize entor de mout de petis cauteres en poignant; aprés le laisse ensi.	When someone has an illness called "adubelati", and it is delaying death or causing death due to overexertion or the old age disease when one grows too old (meaning being very elderly) and there is little blood, or due to tension; and you see it hastening towards death: then apply cautery repeatedly with small applications of fire; afterwards leave them in this condition.
Car elle se hastera de meureir.	For it will hasten to die.
Et se tu la vues percier a tout le cautere, si chaufe le cautere de coi ci est li forme:	And if you see it pierced through with all the cautery, heat the cautery as shown here:
Et met ta main en mileu de cele maladie qui est apellee «adubelati» tant que li cauteres ait perciet lou keur, et soit telz li cauteres que li malaides lou sente defuers en teil maniere que li cours de la porriture soit alegis.	And place your hand in the middle of this illness which is called "adubelati" as long as the fire points through its heart, and make such cauterizations that the patient feels it beyond in such a way that the course of corruption becomes easier.
Aprés le cure tant qu’il soit sanez parfaitement.	After the cure until it is completely healed.
li cure dou feu par fer	The fire cure by iron
Une autre maniere de maladie i a qui est apelee «corrodens», et n’est autre chose que une mengeson de membre, car ele menjut les membres ausi com li feus les leignes seches.	Another form of illness exists which is called 'corrodens', and this is nothing else but a member affection, as it burns the limbs just like you would dry wood.
Se tu vois ceste maladie en leu qui puisse soffrir cautere ensamble feu, adonques eschaufe les cauteres clavile mout petit et grant, selonc ceu qu’il covient au leu ou li maladie est; aprés le cauterize de toutes pars tant que tu erraiche toute la corruption, et nen remaigne rien de li, que tout ceu qui est corrumpus ne soit osteit.	If you see this disease in a place that can endure the fire cautery, then apply small and large fire cauteries together, according to what is needed for each part of the body or where the disease is. After applying the cautery everywhere until you've removed all the corruption, leave nothing behind; make sure that every corrupted part is completely gone.
Et puis le laisse III jors, et met sus les leus cauterizez soffre broiet avec oile tant que les eschaudures dou feu soient ostees, et toute li corruption.	And leave it for three days, and apply burning with oil on the burnt areas until the burned scabs have healed, and all the corruption has disappeared.
Aprés lou cure d’oignemens engendrans char.	After the treatment of ointments that generate pus.
Et se tu vois aprés III jors que chars saine ne naisse, c’est boin; et se ceu non, si rencomence le cautere sus ceu qui est demoreit des leus corrumpus.	And if after three days you see that the wound is healing properly, this is good; and if not, then restart the cauterization on the area where it has been stuck due to corruption.
Et ceste mengeson est aucune fois esteit curee de medicine ague en leu de cautere de feu; mais toutevoie cautere de feu est de plus grant aide, et j’ai ja dit la cure de la medicine ague en la division: pren la quant tu en as mestier.	And this remedy has not been cured by any medicine in lieu of a fire cauterization; but the fire cauterization is much more helpful, and I have already mentioned the treatment for that in medicine: take it when you need to.
des porrelz qui vienent as piez	Of the roots coming to stones
Mout de fois avient que as piez par defuers naist une maladie qui est apelee «clos» selonc nostre entencion, et est une grosse chose fautree qui blece lou piet.	Sometimes it happens that a disease arises through cracks in the skin which we call "cyst," according to our understanding, and it is a large lump that irritates the foot.
Et li cauteres de ceste maladie si est selonc II manieres.	And the cauterizations for this disease do so in two ways.
C’est a savoir cautere de feu, et cautere d’aigue chaude.	This means fire cautery and hot water cautery.
Cautere de feu si est que tu eschaufe I cautere cheveit ausi com est une penne de vouteul, et soit fait de boin fer a la mesure qu’il puisse porpenre le clou de toutes pars, et qu’il i ait subtilz marges; aprés le met tout chaut sus lou clou, et torne ta main tot entor le clou tant qu’il viegne au font dou clou; et lou laisse ensi III jors tant qu’il encomence giter porriture; puis li fai un emplaustre de malves savaiges broiies avec seil, et laisse l’emplaustre sus toute la nuit, et li clous cherra et sera desracinez de ses racines.	Fire cautery involves burning such that you sear the hair like a feather from a goose; make it out of well-made iron to a size where it can pierce all around and have thin edges. After warming it entirely on the tip, twist your hand completely round the tip as it reaches the end of the tip; and leave it thus for three days until the process begins to rot; then apply a plaster made from crushed wild mallow mixed with honey over him overnight, and let the plaster remain all night, and the tip will fall out and be removed from its roots.
Puis cure le leu d’oignement enjanrant char tant qu’il soit sanez.	Then treat the wound by cleaning it thoroughly until it is clean.
Et s’il sont convertit par defuers lou cors, et maintes fois avient et en mains et em piez, si covient que tu i amenistres cautere d’aigue chaude; et est en teil maniere: pren une cainne d’arain ou de fer, ou une penne de vouteul, et met sus lou clou et l’althelul, c’est asavoir porrelz verrues; et met la cainne sus si qu’ele porpreigne tout entor, puis i met un poc d’awe chaude, et retien bien ta main, et presse ta main en tornant si que li marge de la cainne viegne a la racine dou clou, et puisse trover l’aigue chaude voie parfonde jusc’a la racine; et soffre li malaides un poc la mordication de l’aigue chaude une houre; puis le laisse ensi, et il se derracinera tous a tout ses racines.	And if they are transformed through the back of the chest and it happens many times in hands and feet, you should apply a hot cautery. And do this way: take a reed from an arbor or iron or a goose feather, and place them on the tip and the base, that is to say for warts; then put the reed wherever its tip burns all around, then add a little of boiling water, and hold your hand well, and press your hand as you twist it until the edge of the reed reaches the root of the tip, and then find that the hot water penetrates deeply to the root; and let the patient endure for a while the bite of the hot water for an hour; then leave him like this, and all his roots will be uprooted.
Ensi fai un aprés autre, tant que tu esraiches toz ces qui sont au cors, puis les cure des oignemens qui engenrent char.	Start one after another, until you have treated all those inside the body, then treat the sores that produce pus.
li cure dou trembler	The treatment for shaking
Quant aucuns tremble de froidor de ners, ou de fievre quartaine ou d’autre, si covient que tu li faices .iiij. cauteres ou .iv. sus l’espinee dou dos, .i. cautere entre chescune espinee; et .i. cautere ou pez, et .i. sus l’estomac au cautere olivaire; si laissera lou trembler, et se hastera li santez de la maladie froide.	When some shake due to cold or nerves, or a quartan fever or otherwise, it is necessary that you apply four or five cauterizations on the spine of the back. And one cautery between each vertebra; and one on the skin, and one under the stomach with the olive cauterization; if this continues to cause shaking, hasten his recovery from the cold illness.
des pustules puans	puant sores
Aucune fois apperent par defuers le cors bathes, ou pustules puans, que vienent de grosses matieres corrumpues.	When any sign of disease becomes visible through the skin, or pus-filled ulcers appear, these come from large decayed materials.
si covient au premier quant eles apperent que on faice cautere sus chescun chief de la pustule: un cautere subtil de fust de mirte, de coi li pointe soit emprise au feu, ou de racine de aristologe longe, ou au cautere lenticulaire.	When they become visible that one must do to the first when they appear: a delicate cautery on each part of the pus-filled boil: a mirthorn stick cautery, where its tip is grasped by fire, or from the long root of aristologue, or with a lentil-shaped cautery.
Et aucune fois les cauterize on au comencement quant il aperent, selonc ceste maniere, et il ne puent croistre des enqui en avant, mais est desrompue li superfluitez dont il vienent, et sont sanez; mais il covient que ceu soit fait aprés l’evacuation de sanc.	And when they are cauterized at the beginning according to this manner, and do not grow more ulcers in front but release the excess from which they come, becoming healthy; but it should be done after bloodletting.
quant li artere est copee	When the artery has been cut
Maintes fois avient grans decorremens de sanc de l’artere qui est copee a la plaie que vient au pardefuers, ou a l’incision de l’aposteme, ou au cautere dou membre, et as semblans choses; et est mout grief chose d’estenchier.	Many times great variations of blood from the artery that has been cut at the wound come out towards the outside, or during incision of an abscess, or with the fire on the limb, and similar situations; it is a very vexing thing to stanch.
Et toutevoie quant ceu avient a aucun, si te haste de mettre ton doi indice sus la plaie de la voinne, et l’estrain mout tant que li sans soit apaisiez desoz ton doi, et que goute n’en isse plus; puis met au feu les cauteres olivaire plusors petis et grans tant qu’il soient tuit rouge; puis empren .i., ou grant ou petit selonc la plaie et lou leu en coi li artere est route, et met le cautere sus cele voine ou tu tiens ton doi, et tien le cautere tant sus que li sans soit restainchiez.	And yet when this happens to any of you, if you quickly place your index finger on the wound of the vein, and hold it very tightly until the pulse subsides under your finger, and no drop passes anymore; then light several small and large olive oil cauteries until they are all red. Then take .i., or large or small depending on the wound and the location where the artery is located, and place the cautery on that vein where you hold your finger, and hold the cautery there until the pulse is fully congealed.
Et s’il saut fuers quant tu lieves ton doi desus la voinne, et li cauteres estint, si pren hastivement .i. autre des cauteres qui sont au feu.	And if it jumps out when you remove your finger from the vein, and the cauteries are extinguished, take quickly another one of the cauteries that are at the fire.
Et ne cesser de faire ceu l’un aprés l’autre tant que li sans soit estenchiez; et warde que tu n’ardes lou nerf qui est delez, et que autre malice ne viegne sus lou malaide; et saiches que quant sans decourt de l’artere, c’on ne lou puet mie bien restenchier meismement quant li artere est grans, se ceu n’est par une des .iiij. manieres que nos avons dit: ou par cautere, ou par extraction quant ele n’est mie traite, ou par fort liement de fil, ou par medicines mises sus qui ont pooir de restenchier sanc; et soit liee et estrainte avennament.	And do not stop performing this one after the other until the stump is completely burnt; and beware that you don't burn the nerve underneath, and that no harm comes to the patient; and know that when bone leaves the artery, it can be hard to properly reattach it yourself even if the artery is large, as long as it isn't treated by one of these four methods: through cautery, or extraction when not yet treated, or with strong string tying, or using medicines applied that have power to stop bleeding; and bind and restrain it accordingly.
Qui i amenistrera restenchement de liier estroitement de drapelz ou de metre choses ardans sus, ou autres semblans choses, se n’i profite se poc non.	Who will administer the reattachment, by tightly binding with cloths or placing hot things on, or other similar actions, if it doesn't benefit them.

Ci encomence li secons livre des cures de taille	This begins the second book of treatments for amputations
Nos vos avons dit ou premier chapistre toute maladie en coi il covient cautere de feu, ou de medicine ardans, et les oquisons et les causes et les estrumens et les formes des cauteres; et ai mis celui chapistre des lou chief jusc’a piez, et je irai en cest chapistre par celi meisme voie por ceu c’on trueve plus legierement ceu c’on voura.	We have spoken in the first chapter about every disease where it is necessary to use a fire cautery, or medicine that burns, and we discussed their causes, tools, forms of the cauteries; and I placed that chapter up until here, and I will go through this chapter using the same path so that one finds them more easily than before.

dou chief plein d’aigue	the head filled with water
Saiches que ceste maladie vient mout de fois as enfans a l’enfanter, et quant li baille estraint trop fort le chief de l’enfant; et aucune fois vient ceu de cause reponue que on ne seit.	Know that this disease comes so often in infants at birth, and when the mother holds the head of the infant too tightly; and it happens none of those times due to a cause that we know.

And I never see this disease except in infants, and among all those that I have seen, it hastened their deaths; and for this reason, I think it is worth mentioning that I will divide the work into sections of treatments.
Et je vis .i. enfant de coi li chiés estoit plains d’aigue, et li chief engroissoit chescun jor tant qu’il ne lou pooit sostenir; et crut tant li moistor qu’il fut mors, et ceste moistor si est assemblee desoz l’os sus lou syphac, entre lou keur et l’os; et li ovraiges si est telz se li moistor est entre lou keur et l’os, et li apostemes est petis, que tu fendes emmi lou chief une fendure large; et soit ausi longe com .ij. nous, tant que li mostor corre; et vez ci la forme dou spatumile:	And I saw one of their children the shoulder was full of water, and the head swelled each day until it could no longer bear it; and believed so much in the moisture that he died, and this moisture is assembled around the bone in the syphac region, between the heart and the bone; and the veins are thus arranged when the moisture is between the heart and the bone, and the abscesses are small, you cut a large gash through the head until it's wide; and so long as the moisture flows; and see this shape of the syphac:

Et une autre maniere d’incision est que tu regardes ou apert li grandor de l’aposteme, et li assemblé de l’aigue; car aucune fois est elle devant; aucune fois derrier; aucune fois en destre; et aucune fois en senestre. de reume	In reference to cautery using fire, command the patient to allow hair growth until it becomes long and uniform; if they prick at their base, hold the eyes steady so they do not move until they fully grow.

dou reume des eulz	from the pus of the bones

In this manner: take two parts of the oat flower and four parts of colofon, and make plaster; then administer it on these wounds to speed up cartilage growth everywhere.
de l’estoupement des oreilles	Regarding ear piercing
Tout ceu que chiet ens oreilles est une des .iiij. choses: ou grains, ou beste, ou piere de mine ou semblans chose si com fer; ou semence, si com jaisses, feves, pois; ou chose defluans si com aigue et aisilz et semblans choses.	Everything that causes injury to the ears is one of the four things: or grains, or beast, or mine stone or similar thing like iron; or seed, like beans, peas; or flowing thing like water and oil and similar things.
Quant il chiet en l’oreille piere ou autre maniere de chose que ne s’ajoste mie a l’oreille, ne ne croist en l’oreille, si met l’oreille au solel.	When it comes to piercing the ear or any other way of doing things that do not fit with the ear or does not grow in the ear, place the ear under the sun.
Se tu vois la piere, si distille aucun poc d’oile violet ou oile de sisament, puis i amenistre extraction; et lou fai esternuer de condisi, et li estoupe les narines quant li esternuemens vient, et met entor l’oreille pieces de drapelz ou laine; et estent l’oreille au desus.	If you see the stone, if it is seeping any purple or saffron oil, then proceed with extraction; and have them sneeze with consideration, and stop their nostrils when the sneezing occurs, and insert pieces of cloth or wool inside the ear; and hold the ear upright.
Mout de fois vient fuer par ceste cure; et s’elle ne vient fuer, se li amenistre extraction as pinceures subtilz, de coi ci est li forme:	Many times it succeeds with this treatment; and if it doesn't succeed, then one performs the extraction using fine needles, which is how this is done:
S’elle saut fuer as pinceures, c’est boin; se ceu non, si amenistre extraction a l’oncine subtil de petite doubleure; et s’elle ne saut par ceu, si fai une caine d’arain et boute lou chief de la cainne ou pertuis de l’oreille fort, et estoupe ceu qui est entor la cainne de cire mole si que li vens n’i puisse entrer avec la cainne; puis le trai fuer forment, car mout de fois vient fuer si com nos avons dit; et s’elle ne vient fuer en teil maniere, si prent glut de coi en prent les oisiaus, et met en som aucun estrument qui soit a point por ceu faire, et met un poc de coton entor; puis presse le glut sus la piere ou quel chose que ce soit, et trai fuer.	If it comes out with forceps, that's good; if not, proceed with extraction using fine silk thread of small thickness; and if it doesn't come out this way, make a thimble from catgut or pull the end of the thread near the ear canal quite firmly, and stop up the space where the wick is in beeswax so that the thread cannot enter with the wax; then press the glue onto the stone or whatever it may be, and pull forcefully. And many times this brings relief; and if it doesn't bring relief in such manner, then take the glue out and replace it with a tool suitable for this, and put some cotton inside; then press the glue onto the stone or whatever it may be, and pull forcefully.
Et s’elle ne saut fuer de toutes ces choses que nos avons dit, si te haste de fendre l’oreille ainsois que aposteme chalz i veigne, et spasme; et li maniere de la fendure si est que tu faices premier sainier lou malaide de la cephalique, et estrai dou sanc selonc la mesure de sa vertu, puis fai seoir lou malaide entre tes mains et li torne l’oreille au desus, et fent une petite fendure en la racine de l’oreille a la graisse ou leu dependant; et soit li fendure ausi com une lune, tant que tu viegnes a la piere, puis l’oste selonc ton pooir, et la suce hastanment a ta bouche; et la cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if none of these things we have said cause her to jump out from all this, hurry to cut the ear in such a way that pus and blood drain away, and twitch; and the method of cutting is that you first make a surgeon's incision on the auricular muscle, remove some blood according to the measure of its strength, then let the patient sit between your hands and turn the ear upwards, and make a small cut at the root of the ear where the fat hangs down; and let the cut be as round as a crescent moon until you reach the bone, then break the bone according to your power, and suck it rapidly into your mouth; and treat it until it is healed.
Et se c’est grains qui est ens et il enfle, si aministre extraction; et si’il ne puet issir, si amenistre .i. spatumile tenve subtil selonc ceste forme:	And if it is gravel and it inflates, then administer extraction; and if it cannot come out, then administer one small spatula tool according to this shape:
et amenistre incision de celui grain.	and make an incision on that seed.
Mais ne faire mie ceu quant tu penses que li grains est moistes por la moistor de l’oreille, tant que tu en aies fait maintes pieces; puis l’estrai as pinceures subtilz et au succier, si com nos avons dit, si que li estractions soit aligie.	But do not do this if you think the seeds are moist due to ear moisture, until you have made many incisions. Then extract using fine needles and suction, just as we said, so that the extractions become easier.
En l’aigue donques que chiet en l’oreille covient que li malaides use d’esternuement de condisi premiers, et ample l’oreille de viel coton.	In water then, when a person vomits in the ear, it is required that the patient uses spitting of cold liquids first, and fully fills the ear with old cotton.
Et soit gisans sus celle oreille meisme ou li aigue est.	And let it rest on the same ear or where the water is.
s’elle saut fuer per ceu, c’est boin.	If she jumps for heaven, that's good.
se ceu non, si prent maintes pieres selonc li longesce de ton doit tenves et legieres, et les eschaufe un poc au feu; et em mette li malaides une ou pertus de son oreille, et saille sus i. de ses piez d’autre part, et fiere d’une autre piere sus la piere qui est en l’oreille; et ne cesse de faire ceu de piere em piere tant que li aigue isse toute fuer, et ensi saut elle toute fuer; et se tu vues, si prent I jonc, et boute l’un des chiés en l’oreille, et l’autre chief emprent de feu tant que li plus dou jonc soit ars; puis refai autreteil d’autres jons tant que li aigue isse toute, si com nos avons dit en la piere.	If heaven does not jump, take many stones according to their length and light ones, and warm them a bit on the fire; and place one or two of these by her ear, and let her jump from her feet while you jump from another foot, and use another stone against the stone in her ear; and keep doing this from stone to stone until all the water jumps out, and then she jumps out fully; and if you see it, take juniper, and place one of her shoulders in her ear, and the other end in fire until the hottest piece of juniper is burnt; then make another set of junipers until all the water comes out, just as we have explained with stones.
En l’estraction de la beste, s’elle est de petit cors, si com puce et semblans chose, cure la si com nos avons dit en la division; mais s’elle est de grant cors c’on la puisse sentir, si amenistre extraction de pinceures; et c’est li chose plus legiere a oster qui soit en l’oreille.	In the extraction of small beasts such as fleas and similar things, treat it in the manner we have described for removal; but if they are of large size that can be felt, then perform the pinching extraction; and this is the easier thing to remove that is found inside the ear.
En l’estraction des vers enjanrez as oreilles, quant tu lou cures si com nos avons dit en la division et ou traitier des distillations, et li cure ne profite mie, si covient que tu regardes l’oreille au soleil: s’il i apert nulz vers, si les trai as pinceures subtilz, et s’il n’aperent, si prent la cainne de coi ci est li forme:	In the extraction of worms tangled in the ears, when you are treating it as we have described for divisions and distillations, and if the cure does not help, then you must examine the ear with the sun: if there is no worm appearing, extract them using fine pincers; and if they do not appear, take this form of sugar here.
Et soit estroite desoz et large desus.	And may be narrow below and wide above.
Et boute lou plus subtil chief en l’oreille selonc la quantiteit de la soffrance dou malaide, puis succe forment a tot la caine; fai ceu sovent tant que tuit li ver issent.	And apply the most subtle oil to the ear according to the amount of pain the patient endures, then spread it throughout the entire canal; do this often until all the fluid has come out.
Et s’il n’obeissent a issir, si estoupe entor la cainne de coton si com j’ai dit en la piere; et s’il ne saillent fuer si com nos avons dit, si aministre distillations que li ancien ont esprovees en l’ocision des vers, et tu les troveras ou traitier des distillations; et si distille tes oiles et tes medicines en l’oreille a tout cest estrument, de coi ci est li forme si com tu vois:	And if they do not want to come out, then stuff the cotton into the canal as I have said in the stone; and if they do not come out like we have said, then give distillations as the old ones have proven effective in cutting worms, and you will find instructions on this in treatments for distillations; and if you distill your oils and medicines in the ear with all this instrument, as it is shown here, follow this form as you see:
Et soit d’argent ou d’arain estrois desoz a .i. petis pertuis, et desus overs por distiller; et por presser dedens la distillation a .i. estrument d’arain bien fait por ceu, et se tu vues pren .i. raseur et envoloupe entor la pointe avenanment coton; puis i giete ton oile ou ton jus, et ceu que tu vues de tes medicines en la cainne, et li caine soit en l’oreille; puis boute dedens lou raseur a tout lou coton, et presse ta main tempreement tant que li oile soit distilleit ou chevement de l’oreille; et lou sente li malaides dedens, et soit li distillations .i. poc eschaufee au feu ainsois c’on la distille en l’oreille; et garde qu’elle ne soit trop froide, car li medicine ne seroit mie si bone.	And it should be made of silver or of tin with small perforations on the bottom and top for distillation; and to press inside the distillation use a properly made tool of tin suitable for this task. Take one piece of raveling cotton wrapped around the tip part, then pour your oil or juice into it, and let it be in the ear; then fill the raveling with all the cotton and gently press your hand until the oil is distilled or until some drops come out from the ear; and listen to the patient inside, and know that after such a distillation, the medicine should not be too cold because otherwise the medicine would not be as effective.
de l’estoupement des oreilles	Regarding ear piercing
Aucun enfant naissent qui n’ont nul pertus ens oreilles; et ceste meisme chose avient as homes par estoupement de plaie, ou de char nee dedens l’oreille, et cist estoupemens vient aucune fois em parfont en l’oreille, si c’on ne lou puet veoir; et aucune fois avient .i. poc defuer lou pertus, et lou voit om bien.	No child is born without any intact parts in their ears; and this same thing happens to people due to wounds or birth in the ear, and these injuries happen inside the ear sometimes, if one cannot see them; and they happen only once inside the ear, when you can't see them. And they never occur twice, where one can see it well.
Celle donques que vient em parfont, si c’on ne la puet veoir, est de grief sanation em plusors dispositions, et en cele c’on voit covient que tu mettes l’oreille dou malaide au soleil; et regarde dedens: se tu vois l’opilation apparent, si la oevre a tot cest spatumile de coi ci est li forme:	That which happens inside and cannot be seen comes from the injury of healing in various stages, and in this situation where one can see that you should place the ear under the sun; and look inside: if you see the evident swelling, if the work has become completely filled with pus as described here:
Et soit agus et trenchans devant et derrier tout plain, si qu’il ne blece l’oreille; se li opilation est de char nee ou cors de l’oreille, si la tien as pinceures subtilz, et la cope legierement, tant que celle chars soit toute ostee.	And let it be so that you cut in front and behind completely flat, so as not to irritate the ear; if the swelling is due to newly formed flesh or a bump of the ear, then use subtle pricks on it, and gently scrape it until all the flesh is removed.
Et se li opilations est em parfont en l’oreille, si pren I raseur subtil legier et l’eschaufe un petit au feu, puis li met ou cors de l’oreille.	And if the wicks go into the ear canal, take a fine, light wax and melt it with fire for a little bit, then put it inside the ear.
Se tu sens l’opilation dont li malaides sent grieteit a l’oïr, perce legierement, et garde que tu ne grever les ners de l’oreille; puis met en l’oreille une tente selonc la largesce dou pertus, et la moille en l’oignement egyptien.	If you feel the irritation that makes the ears of the patient sensitive to touch, gently prick it and ensure not to damage the nerves of the ear; then place a tent in the ear according to its width near the entrance, and fill the ointment from the Egyptian medicine into the opening.
Fai ceu aucun jor tant que li plaie soit soudee, ou tu pren une tente et la moille en aigue rose, et poudre sus vitriole broiet; et se tu vois enflee l’oreille, si couvient que tu traies la tente et remue une autre tente moillie en cerote qui soit fait d’oile roset et de cire, tant que li enfleure soit ostee; puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	Do this every day until the wound heals or you take a plug and moisten it with rose water, and dust it with powdered vitriol. And if you see swelling in the ear, it must be that you remove the plug and put another one moistened with candle wax made from rose oil and beeswax, until the swelling is gone; then treat it until it's healthy.
Et se decorremens de sanc vient, si plonge une esponge et drapelz en aigue froide, et le met sus l’oreille, et use d’autres cures qui oste lou decorrement de sanc qui sont ou traitier des destillations.	And if bleeding occurs, immerse an sponge and soak it in cold water, then place it on the ear, and perform other treatments that stop bleeding which include remedies for distillations.
de la char des papieres	From the substance of the papers
Cist althelul que vienent em papieres des eulz quant ils sont moiste et sont sec, si covient que tu les estendes de tenailles et de pinceures, et le cope d’un spatumile de ses racines; puis met sor le leu vitriole broiet.	When handling wet and dry hairs in papers, it is necessary that you spread them using tweezers and forceps. Then, take a piece from its roots; afterwards, place sulfur on the part of the paper.
Et se sans en decort, si le cauterize dou cautere lenticulaire subtil, et li cauterizeir aprés l’incision vaut mues; et maintes fois repairent, cant aucune chose demoure de lor racines; et quant elles sont cauterizees par feu, si sont arses celles racines et ne revienent mie.	And if you don't peel it off, cauterize it with a narrow lens cautery, and after the incision, it will start to move; and many times, there are no remains from its roots. And when they are cauterized by fire, those roots burn completely and never return.
de la gresle	Regarding ice or cold treatments
Maintes fois vienent em papieres des eulz unes choses que semblent gresle en sa forme et en sa duresce, et por ceu est ceste maladie apelee «grandine», et est une assemblee de moistor grosse en la papiere desus et desoz; li ovraiges est telz: pren warde se li grandine se muet d’une part et d’autre, et c’est legiere chose a savoir; fent la donques dou large, puis l’escorche de chescune partie legierement, puis la prent as pinceures, et la cope.	Many times, papers contain things that seem to be gravel due to their shape and hardness. This illness is called "granuloma", and it's an assembly of large moisture in the paper above and below; here are the operations: take care if the granuloma moves on one or both sides, this is a simple thing to know; thus proceed by broadening it, then lightly scrape each part, then pinch them and apply treatment.
se tu ne la pues coper sens percier un poc la papiere, si ne grieve rien au malaide; et se li fendure est grans, si l’assemble a une costure, et la cure tant qu’ele soit sanee; et s’elle est petite, si n’i faire point de force, car li oignemens la restoure tantost et enjanre char.	If you cannot treat it without piercing the paper slightly, just do so without causing any pain to the patient. If the split is large and if there's a seam, cure until it heals; and when it's small, don't exert force, for the ointment will restore it quickly and promote healing tissue.
Et se li grandine est dessendans au dedens de l’oreille vers la partie desus, si enverse la papiere, et estent la grandine a unes pinceures, et la cope et presse d’une part et d’autre; et se li papiere est esloignie par l’incision, ce ne grieve rien; et quant li grandine est copee, si leive l’oil d’aigue salee, et cure le leu de ceu qui enjanre char tant que li malaides soit sanez.	And if the granuloma descends into the ear towards the upper part, turn the paper, and place the granuloma under tweezers, then remove and press from both sides; and if the paper is moved by the incision, it does not harm anything; and when the granuloma has been removed, wash with salty water, treat the area that stimulates tissue growth until the patient is healed.
de la graisse des eulz	of the fat of the lumps
Exinach est une graisse qui est enjanree en toiles des papieres desus, et ce avient plus as enfans c’a nules gens, et grieve mout a lor eulz, et li vienent li catharre as matinees, et ne pueent regardeir la lumiere dou soleil por ceu que les larmes se hastent a lor eulz; et por ceu se couchent il sor lor faices adés, et dorment sus, et sont lor papieres desoz lor sorcilz moistes que li enfleure et li apparance ont covert de l’exinach qui apert en l’oil.	Exinach is a grease that gets trapped on the papers above it, and this happens more among children than adults, causing much trouble to their eyes. And at dawn, it causes weeping (catharre), and they cannot look at the sunlight because tears rush into their eyes; thus they lie in their beds all day long, sleep on them, and have their papers wetted under their eyelids by Exinach that opens in the eye.
Et quant tu presses lou leu a tes dois et sent l’exirnach entr’ous.	And when you press on your hand with your fingers and feel exinach between them.
Et li maniere de l’ovraige si est que li malaides mette son chief en ton sain; et puis pren .i. drapeil de lin, et appareille une tente em maniere d’un cercle selonc la quantiteit que conteigne exirnach de chescune partie, puis le met sus li; et presse a tes dois d’une part et d’autre, si que li exirnach soit assemblez emmi le cercle; puis fent em mileu de la moistor au spatumile trenchant une fendure dou large, et ne soit mie plus grans que li plaie c’on fait a la sainie de voinne; et fent le cuir em parfont tant que tu veignes a l’exirnach; et em plusors dispositions vient exirnach de la fendure, selonc la forme d’une piece de graisse blainche.	And the method of the process is that the patient places their head in your hand; and then take .i. linen cloth, and set up a tent in manner of a circle according to the quantity that contains excrement from each part, then put it on; press with your fingers on both sides, so that the excrement is gathered within the circle; then cut in the midst of the moisture with a sharp knife a groove wide, and not more than the wound when you open a vein; and let the leather be tight enough until you see the excrement from the groove, according to the shape of a piece of white fat.
Estrai la donques a tout une piece de drap charpit entre tes dois au defuer, et torne ta main a destre et a senestre tant qu’il soit espars; et garde que tu n’ajoster en la fendure, que tu ne viegnes a tout le spatumile jusc’a l’oil, que tu ne le bleces.	Then remove it all in one piece of thick linen between your fingers at the front, and turn your hand to the right and left until it is dispersed; and make sure you do not mix in the groove, that you do not reach up to the whole knife until it reaches the eye, that you do not hurt it.
Et se li exirnach n’apert en l’encomencement de la fendure, si acroi un poc la fendure legierement tant qu’il apere; puis l’estrai si com nos avons dit, puis moille drapelz en aisil et en aigue, et met sus le leu, et estrain de bendelz.	And if the incision does not open at the beginning of the cut, you should gently increase the cut size; then pull it as we have said. Then soak it in moist cloths and water, place it on the wound, and strain with bandages.
Et si a de tels homes qui broient seil et mettent sus por corrompre cele moistor qui est demoree.	And if there are such people who grind salt and put it on to corrupt that moisture which has remained.
Puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	Then the treatment should continue as long as it is effective.
Et s’il vient au leu aposteme chaut, si lou cure d’emplaustres assouajant tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if it comes to the point of an abscess, then the treatment with plaster remedies until it is healed.
des poilz des papieres	of the paper hairs
Quant em papieres naissent poilz ajostez autre que li naturez, et sont enveillit, si nuisent as eulz, et font venir manieres de maladies si com larmes acostumees et mollifications des papieres et albugine, tant que c’est cause de la destruction des eulz; et est li cure selonc .iiij. manieres: ou par cautere ensamble feu, ou par medicine ague selonc ceu qu’il est devant ou chapistre de cautere, et est fais ou par incision et costure ou par caines, selonc ceu que je dirai.	When hairs grow out of place and become old, they harm the eyes, causing diseases such as habitual tears and paper softening and albugine formation. These are reasons for eye damage; and treatment should follow these four methods: either by a fire cautery, or with medicine according to what was discussed previously in the chapter on cauteries, it can be done through surgery and stitching, or sutures, depending on what I will explain next.
Il covient que tu mettes lou chief dou malaide en ton sain, puis torne la papiere de l’oil a ta main senestre; s’elle est convertie, c’est boin; se ceu non, si i boute une aguille a tout .i. fil desus; et soit ce delez la marge de la papiere ou li poil naissent delez ces poilz, et trai .i. fil au desus a tout la papiere, et la torne au raseur; puis fent en la partie desoz la papiere, desoz les poilz ajostez, a tout le spatumile copant, des le grant larmier jusc’au petit; puis estrai .i. fil, et met desoz la papiere une petite tente de couton et de drapeil, puis seigne sus la papiere une figure d’enche, si com la fuelle de mirte, et toutevoie il covient que li figure soit selonc la quantiteit que tu vues eslever la papiere qui est devisez a toz.	You must place the head of the eye in your good health, then turn the paper of the eye with your left hand; if it is turned correctly, that's fine; if not, take one thread and sew it above at each end of the paper. Then do this along the edge of the paper where hairs grow beneath these hairs, sewing a single thread above across the whole paper, then turning it flat using a razor. Afterwards, cut through the part under the paper, under the displaced hairs, all the way from the large tear to the small one; then remove that thread and place a small cotton tent on top of the paper, followed by placing an 'H' shape figure on the paper, like a bay leaf. Indeed, it must be ensured that this figure matches the size you see when lifting up the paper which is folded over everything.
Et si a teil qui a mestier c’on cope grant quantiteit de la papiere selonc ceu que li papiere est mollifie; puis fent a tout le spatumile sus les II lignes que tu as signiet, et comence des lou grant larmier jusc’a petit; et soit li une des fendures pres des poilz naturez en la groissece d’un raiz, puis boute l’oncine en l’un des II angles dou keur, puis l’escorche toute; puis assemble les II levres a une costure d’une aguille a tout I fil de laine subtil, et essue le sanc, et fai aerdre la superfluiteit des filz sus les II sorcilz a tout aucunes choses gluans, se tu vues faire ce; et se ce non, si n’en aies cure, puis laisse la costure et les filz jusc’a III jors ou IIII; puis cure la plaie sens costure de choses sechans et constrignans, car li papiere se relive au soudement de la plaie et l’assemblement de li, mais li costure est muedre (si com dirent li ancien), et c’est ovraiges sens paor; et si a une autre maniere: et est que tu seignes la papiere d’une figure qui soit ausi com li fuelle de mirte, si com nos avons conteit, a III oncines desevrez selonc la forme qui est ci:	And if there's need to use a large amount of paper according to the softness of the paper; then treat all with the application of plasters until it heals. Start from the largest part of the plaster down to smaller parts, and let one of the two incisions be close to natural hairs, around the growth size of a root, then put the thumb in one of the two angles at the corners of the mouth, then burn all around; afterward join both edges with a fine thread using a needle for about I strands of wool. Wipe out the blood and allow the excess threads to dry on both sides of the incisions, if you can perform this task; or else don't worry about it, leave the stitches until three days or four. Then treat the wound without stitches with drying and constraining substances because the paper heals with the tightness of the injury and joining them together, but the stitches degrade (as they said before), and there's no danger involved in this process; and here is another method: you mark the paper with a shape that resembles the leaf of myrtle as we described earlier, with three cuts according to the form shown here:
puis cope ceu qui sormonte as petites forces igalment selonc la forme qui est ci:	Then, cut those that are above evenly according to the shape shown here:
Et se tu n’as pooir de tenir les tenailles, et li chose n’est mie igalz, si prent une aguille ou il ait I fil, et la boute emmi la figure; et boute I autre fil delez lou grant larmier, et lou secont fil delez lou petit, et assemble entre tes dois les filz igalment; puis lieve ta main igalment, et lieve tout le cuir sus coi tu as signiet, si com nos avons conteit, puis assemble les II levres de la plaie par costure, et le cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et se aposteme vient a ton incision, si l’apaise de cerote et de semblans oignement assouajans; et aucune fois avient que li poil de la papiere sont convertit: si covient que tu uses ceu que nos avons dit de l’incision; mais li costure en l’une et en l’autre est plus artificialz.	And if you don't have the strength to hold the forceps, and things are not even, take a needle or stick with thread on it, and place one end under your thumb. Place another thread down large bone, and the second thread down small bone, then join these threads equally between your thumbs; lift your hand evenly, lifting all the skin over what you've pierced, as we have described, then stitch the two edges of the wound together, and treat until it's healed. And if pus comes out from your cut, then heal with tallow and soothing balm; and no time should pass when paper hair turns black: you must use what we have advised about cutting; but both stitching are more artificial.
Li cure des caines si est selonc ceste forme: et est que tu convertisses la papiere et la fent dedens selonc ceu que j’ai dit, et puis fai .ij. caines par art, et .ij. liiens subtilz ausi lonc com li papiere et li largesce dou spatumile est; et cope as .ij. chiés de .ij. pars ou tu tiens les filz; puis assemble l’un et l’autre subtilment sus ceu que sormonte de la papiere de l’oil, et estrain les .ij. cainnes des .ij. parties forment; et le laisse ensi aucuns jors, et li cuir qui iert estrainte morra et nercira et porrira, tant qu’il cherra par lui.	The treatment of canines follows this form: and you should convert the paper and cut inside according to what I have said, and then create four canines by art, and also two fine strings as long as the paper and as wide as the tip is; and place the tips of the two parts on either side; then assemble both finely above where the paper covers the eye, and tighten the two canine lines from each part formed; and leave it like this for a few days, and the skin that has been tightened will shrivel and turn black and spread, until it escapes by itself.

de la bowe de l’oil	By the power of the eye
Ceste maladie qui est apelee «alcunnati» nen est fuers que bowe qui est assemblee en l’oil, semblant a aigue dessendant, et ce n’est mie aigue; et li maniere de l’apparance de l’ovraige si est que tu faices seoir lou malaide sus I siege appareilliet et droit, puis prent le chief entre tes mains de II pars, et lou muef tant que tu voies la bowe venir au desus a tes eulz; puis soit ens fichie, et ne dessende et soit descombree li lumiere, et voie li malaides les choses si com il soloit; et s’elle ne dessent desoz, saiches que c’est aigue, et se li dessendemens de la bowe n’est appareilliez si com nos avons dit.	This disease called "alcunnati" only leaves behind a collection that forms in the ear, resembling descending fluid, and it is not actual fluid; and how this disease appears you should make the patient sit up straight on their apparatus and upright, then take hold of the head with both hands from two sides, and move them until you see the fluid come above to your eyes; afterwards leave it be, do not allow it to descend and disperse the light, observe the things as they were originally; and if the fluid doesn't descend immediately, know that it is a disease, and when the descent of the fluid isn't apparent in this way as we have said.

de la char sor le neis	of the flesh near the nose

de la char sor le neis	of the flesh near the nose

des sordens	Of cautering with fire, instruct the patient to allow hair growth until long and even; and if they pierce at their base, hold the eyes steady so they do not move until they grow.

When you are treating a tooth for its pain and delay the extraction as much as possible, it should not be done; because this is very rare. Many times the pain will be in the body of the patient, and one must determine if it's from tooth Saint, and extract the good tooth; yet never leave the pain with that alone until the bad tooth is removed. And remember not to act like the ignorant surgeons who break the tooth once because of their haste and boldness.
