Et soient de gros membres si qu’il ne ploient mie au traire, et soient de fer inde bien fait, et soient dentez por mues tenir.	And let them have large parts that do not bend when being pulled, and be made of very sturdy iron, and should have teeth to hold the pieces in place.
de la racine des dens	from the root of the teeth
Quant li racine demoure au traire, si covient que tu mettes sor le leu coton moilliet em burre I jor ou ij.,	When the root remains at drawing, it is necessary to place wet cotton with butter inside the wound for a day or two.
tant que li leus soit amolis, pues i boute les tenailles qui sont apelees «algefri», de coi li chiés semblet bec de soigne; et soient dedens faites ausi com une lime et c’est li forme:	As long as the thighs are soft, then grasp the tongs which are called "algefri", as the patient's thighs resemble a surgeon's scalpel; and do it inside just like a file and that is its shape:
Et se les racines ne vuellent issir a tout ces tenailles, si covient que tu descuevre la char tot entor la racine, et i met l’estrument qui est apelez «althali», c’est a savoir palainche, de coi ci est li forme:	And if the roots do not want to come out with all these forceps, it is necessary that you uncover the entire mass right up to the root, and then place an instrument known as 'althali', which is essentially an awl, as depicted here:
Et soit fors et gros si qu’il ne brise mie, et se li racine saut par ceu, c’est boin; se ceu non, si t’aide de toz les estrumens, de coi les formes vienent ci aprés:	And make it so that neither breaks and is large enough that it does not break at all, and if the root jumps out from this, it's good; if this doesn't happen, assist with all instruments you have, as their forms are shown here after:
Et si s’aide on de cest estrument qui ait .ij. rains, de coi ci est li forme:	And if assistance is taken from the instrument that has two points, as depicted here:
et d’autres ferremens qui sont devant en la rasion des dens, et de cest estrument qui semble unes grans tenailles, dont ci est li forme:	and other tools that are in front according to the size of teeth, and from this tool which seems like large forceps, as depicted here:
Et soit cist estrumens fors qu’il ne puisse brisier, et saiches que mout d’estrumens de dens sont; et ausi d’autres estrumens, qui ne sont mie contez; et li saiges maistres subtilz trueve par soi meisme son estrument, selonc ceu que ses ovraiges et li maladie li demoustre, car il i a de teilz maladies ou li ancien n’enseignerent point d’estrument por la diversiteit d’au;s et s’om brise point dou charreit ou des autres os, ou il porrit, si i cerche as estrumens qu’il i covient, que je t’ai dit, et t’aide des gestes, de coi ci est li forme:	And let this tool not be able to break it, and know that very few of the tools are made of metal; and also other tools which are not counted; and the skillful surgeons themselves find their own instrument according to what their work and illness show them, because there are parts of diseases for which old teachings do not provide a tool due to their variety. If they break anything from cartilage or from the other bones, or if they rot, so they seek out the tools that suit him, as I have told you, and help with gestures, which is what this form represents:
Et soient gros et bien tenant por tenir l’os, qu’il n’eschaipe, mais le puisse tenir et oster; et puis restoure lou leu de medicines convenant a ceu, et s’il ait en l’os porriture, et elle est petite, si la reis a tout cest estrument:	And let them be large and well suited to hold the bone so that it doesn't escape but can be held and removed; and then restore the place with medicine suitable for this, and if there is decay in the bone and it is small, if you find all this tool:
Quant li dent apperent ne mie selonc lou cors natureil, et li forme est laide, et meismement en femmes puceles, si covient que tu saiches se li dens est neis aprés lou dent, et n’est mie en droit leu, et on ne lou puet soier ne limer: adonques lou raie; et s’il est aers avec lou dent, si prent cest estrument dont ci est li forme, et est semblans a .i. petit bec, et soit de fer inde agut en som:	When the tooth appears not according to its natural form, and its shape is ugly, and especially in maiden women, you should know whether the tooth was born after it or isn't properly placed, and one can neither file nor grind it: then remove the groove; and if it's alongside the tooth, take this tool as shown here, resembling two small beaks, and let it be sharp at its tip.
Et lou cope poc et poc em mains jors por la duresce dou dent, et por ceu que tu ne mueves les autres, et s’il est apparans c’on le puisse limer, si lou lime d’une teil lime com ci est li forme:	And the hole is made small and smaller in my hands by its hardness due to tooth, and because you do not move others, and if it becomes apparent that one can shave it off, then I will shave with one piece of file as this forms:
et est ausi com li lime de coi on fait les aguilles; et en lime lou dent poc et poc em mains jors legierement, si qu’il ne se mueve tant qu’il chiece; puis la plaine en la fin a tout aucun raseur, et se li dens est trop trenchans et il blece la lengue, si covient limer l’aspreteit tant qu’il soit igalz, si qu’il ne blece la lengue ne ne corrompe la parole.	And it is also like the file used for making needles; and I gently shave in my hands slowly by tooth, so that it doesn't move until it's done; then make it completely flat with no rasp at the end. And if the edge is too sharp causing blisters on the tongue, it's necessary to shave off the roughness as much as possible, so that it doesn't blister the tongue or harm speech.
quant li dent lochent	When the tooth swells
Quant li dent devant lochent, ou par percussion ou par cheoir, et li malaides ne puet presser sus ceu qu’il menjue qu’il ne chient, et tu les as curez de medicines restrignans, et ceu ne vaut; si les covient restraindre d’un fil d’or, car li filz d’argent devient vert et porrit, mais li ors ne se mue onques; et soit li filz moiens ne trop gros ne trop menus, selonc la quantiteit de l’espaice entre les dens; et se tu vues adrecier les dens, si pren lou fil et lou boute double entre les II dens sains, puis met les chiés entre les dens meus, s’il en i a I ou plusors, tant que tu veignes saigement jusc’au dent sain d’autre part; puis rencomence la coverture jusc’a la partie ou tu encomensas, et estrains ta main subtilment et saigement, tant qu’il ne se mueve point; et soit ta lieeure a la racine dou dent si qu’il ne puist eschaper.	When the teeth are in front of the mouth, or by tapping or striking, and if the patient cannot squeeze this when they chew, that it does not matter; if you have treated them with restraining medicines, and it is not effective. So it must be restrained with a gold thread, for silver threads turn green and rot, but gold never changes. And choose the thread to be neither too thick nor too thin, according to the size of the space between the teeth. And when you see that the teeth are coming together, take the thread and the braid double between the two healthy teeth, then place the diseased teeth between the weaker teeth, if there is one or more than one, until you can feel them well on the other side; then repeat the covering to where you started, and pull your hand gently but carefully, until it does not move at all; and bind your knot at the root of the tooth so that it cannot escape.
Puis cope les chiés dou fil a unes tenailles, et les assemble, et les repont entre le dent sain, et le met ensi qu’il ne blece la lengue; et puis le laisse ensi estroit tant com il puet demorer, et s’il deslie, ou li filz ront, si l’estraint d’un autre fil; si demorrait et servira ensi tout son tens, et c’est li forme des dens et li figure de l’adrecement des II dens sains, et des II meus, si com tu vois:	Then use thread with pliers, and join them, and place them between the healthy tooth, and then position it so that it doesn't irritate the tongue; and leave it like this tightly as long as it can endure, if it comes loose or the threads slip, then hold it back in place with another thread; if it stays thus and serves like this for its entire time, and this is how teeth are placed and the arrangement of the two healthy teeth and the two middle ones looks when you see them:
Et quant li dent chiet, si lou remet on en son leu, de fres en fres, si com nos avons dit; et ne s’en entremette mie qui n’est saiges et soffrans, et aucune fois fait on la forme d’un dent d’os de vaiche, et lou met on au leu ou li defaute est, et l’estraint on si com nos avons dit, et demore et sert ensi lonc tens.	And when the tooth has shifted, should you set it back to its place, day by day as we have said; and do not interfere with anything that is not safe or endures suffering, and never make the shape of an osine's tooth, and place it in the spot where the defect exists, and bind it as we have said, so it stays there for a long time.
de coper lou liien de la lengue	To cover the tie of the tongue
Aucune fois est cist liiens qui vient desoz la lengue ou naturez, que on naist ensi; ou par accident de plaie soudee; et li ovraiges est telz que tu oevre la bouche dou malaide, et ait sa teste en ton sain, et li lieve la lengue; puis cope lou liien nervous dou large, tant que li lengue soit desloie de son tenement, et se il i a duresce ou nout, et c’est de soudement de plaie, si i boute l’uncine et cope dou large celui liement; et garde que li fendure ne soit mie trop em parfont, por l’artere qui est desoz; et quant tu as fait, si leve le leu d’aigue rose et d’aisil, ou d’aigue froide, puis met desoz la lengue une tente de lin; et la teigne li malaides chescune nuit, que li leus ne puisse soder.	None of the times does this come from under the tongue or naturez that one is born with; or by accident in a wound healed; and the operations are such that you work on the mouth for the patient, and have its head towards your healthy side, and lift up the tongue; then cut out the nerve cord as wide as possible, until the tongue is displaced from its position, and if there's any resistance or knotting, this is due to immediate healing of a wound, in which case you clip off the hook fold and cut out that cord; and remember not to let the cut be too deep down below, for there might be an artery underneath; when done, then lift up the head from the pinkish water and slight warmth or cold water, then place over the tongue a linen cloth; and every night fomentate each part of this with the patient's own urine, so that your teeth don't stick.
Et se decorremens de sanc vient, si met sor le leu vitriole broiet; et se li sans te vaint, si le cauterize au cautere lentiginout, qui est boin a ceu; puis le cure d’autre cure tant qu’il soit sanez,	And when bleeding occurs, should it start, place sulfur in the wound and bind it; and if it does not stop, then cauterize with the slow cautery, which is good for this situation; then treat it with other treatments until it stops bleeding.
et se tu lou vois de fusse color ou noir ou dur, si que li malaides ne lou sent, si n’i touchier point, car c’est chancre; et s’il est declinans a blenchor, et il i a moistor, si i giete l’oncine, et lou fent d’un spatumile subtil, et lou delivre d’une part et d’autre; et se li sans te vaint a ton ovraige, si met sus vitriole broiet tant qu’il soit estainchiez, puis revien a ton ovraige tant que tu traies tout fuer; puis leve lou leu d’aisil et de seil, et le cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if you see that it is of any other color or blackness or hardness such that the patient doesn't feel it without touching, then don't touch it as it's a sore; and if it's fading towards whitishness, and there is moisture, then apply the hook until it gets cleansed and then cleanse from both sides; and if the pus fails to drain through your procedure, then pour vinegar over it until it stops bleeding, then proceed with your task until you exhaust all the means. Then raise it up using cold water and salt, and treat further until it fully heals completely.
des apostemes de la gorge	Extractions from the throat
Aucune fois vient dedens la gorge boces qui sont apelees «godath», et les apele on proprement les II amandres, et quant tu les cures, si com nos avons dit en la division, et elles ne sont sanees, si pren garde: se c’est apostemes dur de petit sens et de fusse color, si ne lou touchier mie de fer.	None of the nodes inside the throat, called "godath", and they are properly named as the two almonds; and when you treat them, as we have said in the division, and if they are not healed; then beware: If it's hard pus-filled nodules with a thin string-like structure and a reddish color, don't touch them with metal.
Et s’il est rouges et li racine est grosse, si ne lou touchier mie de fer, ausi por lou decorrement de sanc; mais lou laisse tant qu’il soit meur, et adonques tu lou partiras, ou il rompirait par soi; et s’il est de blainche color reont, et li racine est subtilz, si aies apareilliet l’estrument por coper, mais regarde premierement se li apostemes chalz repose et est apaisiez.	And if they are red and the root is large, don't touch them with metal for fear of causing bleeding; but leave it until it heals over. Then you can remove it, or it might burst on its own; and if they're white in color, and the root is subtle, prepare your tool to grasp, but first check that the pus-filled nodule has cooled down and calmed.
Adonques fai seoir lou malaide devant lou soleil, et ses chiés soit en ton sain, et li oevre la bouche et lou preigne li serjans entre ses mains, et presse la lengue desoz a tout l’estrument, de coi ci est li forme; et soit d’argent ou d’arain subtil ausi com uns coutelz:	Therefore make the sick person sit in front of the sun, and have his limbs in their normal position, and let him open his mouth and place the surgeon's fingers between his hands, and press the tongue all over with every part of the instrument, as described; and use silver or finely made iron such as knives.
Cant tu presses la lengue a tout cest estrument, et tu vois l’aposteme, si pren l’oncine et lou fiche en l’amandre, et la trai fuer au desus plus que tu pues; et trai aucune chose des toiles avec, puis la cope a l’estrument, de coi ci est li forme, que semble unes forces; et toutevoie li chief sont corbé, et l’un endroit l’autre, et sont molt agut, et est fait de fer inde ou d’andainne:	Can't you press the tongue with all this tool? And when you see the pus lump, take the scissor and insert it into the almond, then pull strongly more than you can. Do not remove any threads, then cut using the tool; in this way it appears as a forceful process, that seems like pressing. Once the head is pressed from one place to another, it's very sharp, and made of iron or brass:
Et se tu n’as cest estrument present, si lou cope as tenailles, de coi ci est li forme:	And if you don't have this tool now, take scissors instead; in this way it is formed:
Et soit trenchans d’une part, et d’autre part nom; et quant tu as copeit l’une des amandres, si cope l’autre selonc cele meisme maniere, et aprés l’incision gargarize li malaides aigue chaude, et aigue et aisil, et se decorremens de sanc avient, si gargarize li malaides aigue, ou escorces de pomes grenates soient cuites, ou fuelles de mirte, et semblans choses, tant que li sans soit estainchiez; puis lou cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et aucune fois naissent en la gorge autres apostemes que les .ij. amandres, si les cope donques ensi com les .ij. amandres igament.	And make incisions on one side and the other; and when you have performed an incision in one of them, do the same for the other according to the same manner, and after the incision gargle the sick person with hot water, or both cold and warm water, and if there is bleeding during the recovery, then gargle them with water or pieces of cooked cherry tomatoes, or leaves of wild rosemary, and similar things, until they stop bleeding; then complete the treatment as long as the body heals; and let no other abscesses arise in the throat besides the two glands, so perform the same procedure on them accordingly.
Et je medicinai une femme d’un aposteme que li estoit neis dedens la gorge, c’est a savoir I aposteme de petit sens; et avoit jai bien pres close toute la gorge, si que li femme ne pooit expirer por le conduit qui estoit estoupez, et ne pooit ne mengier ne boivre, et fust morte s’elle demorast ensi I jor ou II.	And I treated a woman with an abscess that was inside her throat, namely the small abscess; and had well almost closed off the entire throat so that the woman could not breathe through the blocked passage, and could neither eat nor drink. She died if she had stayed like this for one or two days.
Et li apostemes estoit jai si montez qu’il avoit fuer mis II rains par les II pertuis dou neis.	And the abscesses was so high that it had forced to make two holes through both nostrils near the nose.
Je hastai donques tantost, et fichai en l’un I oncine, puis lou traï fuers, et en traï grant porcion de bowe; puis refis autreteil en l’autre pertus dou neis, et li ovrai la bouche et li pressai la lengue; aprés fichai l’oncine en ces apostemes, et en copai une partie, et n’en issit fuers que un poc de sanc; et ensi fut destoupez li conduis de la gorge la femme, et comensa maintenant a boivre aigue et puis vin, et ne cessai de taillier de cel aposteme par lonc tens; et li apostemes recroissoit adés, et remplissoit lou leu que je avoie vuidiet, tant qu’il refut mout gros; adonques je l’engignai et lou cauterizai dedens la gorge: ensi demora sens croistre; et me partis de ces parties, et ne soi que Deus fist de li aprés moi.	I quickly did this, and placed the incision in one place, then pulled out the other side, taking a large portion of the bow. Then I made another cut on the opposite side near his nose, and closed him up leaving his mouth open; after that I placed the incision within an abscess, took a part, and only a little blood came out; and thus was it done in opening her windpipe and she began to drink water and then wine, never stopping my cutting of that abscess for so long. The abscesses grew immediately filling up the space I had drained until it became quite large. Then I stitched him up and cauterized inside the throat: this way he didn't grow again; and from those parts, only God knows what happened to him after me.
de l’uve	Of the eye
Quant reume dessent a l’uve, et elle est enflee et elle est longe, si est apelee «perpendiculaire»; et s’elle est desoz grosse et reonde, si est apelee «uve».	When it descends into the uterus, and it swells and grows long, this is called "perpendicular"; and if it becomes large and round, it's called "ovum".
Quant elle est curee si com nos avons dit en la division, et li cure ne profite mie, et tu vois que li chaus apostemes est apaisiez, et elle est subtilz, si covient que tu la copes; et celle qui est reonde assemblee et n’est mie longe; et elle est sanguine ou de fusse color ou noire, si covient que tu eschues l’incision de li.	When it is treated as we have said in the division, and if the treatment doesn't help, and you see that the wound has calmed down and is subtle, then it's necessary to handle it; and for those that are roundly assembled but not long; and it is bloody or of a reddish color or black, then it's necessary to avoid making an incision in this one.
Car il i a grant peril sus lou malaide.	For there is great danger for the patient.
Il covient donques, quant tu la vois, selonc la maniere que j’ai dit, de sa blenchor et de sa longesce, que tu faices seoir le malaide devant lou soleil, et li presse la lengue a l’estrument dont nos avons fait la remembrance ci devant; puis fiche l’oncine en l’uve, et la trai desoz, et la cope a I des II estrumens que j’ai dit en l’incision des II amandres.	Therefore, when you see it, according to the manner that I have explained with regards to its location and length, you should make the patient stand in front of the sun, and press their tongue onto the tool that we described earlier. Then, insert the needle into the uterus, pull it out slightly, and then remove it using the second tool as mentioned for the incision on both kidneys.
Et covient que tu ne coper mie fuer que la superfluiteit qui est outre le termine natureil; car se tu en copes plus, si grieves a la voix, et a la parolle; et aprés l’incision, use de ceu que nos avons dit en l’incision des II amandres, et le cure tant qu’elle soit sanee.	And it must be that you remove no more than the excess which is beyond the natural boundary; for if you remove too much, you injure the voice and speech. And after incision, use what we have said about incision of the two saloons, and treat until it is healed.
Et se li malaides a paor dou coper, si covient que tu i use d’engien a la cauterization de li sens paor.	And if the patients are afraid of the cut, it is necessary for you to use remedies for the cautery of the sensitive area.
Et li maniere dou cautere si est aigue ague.	And the way of the cautery is like boiling water.
Et est que li malaides mette son chief en ton sain, et puis li presse la lengue a l’estrument que nos avons dit ou chapistre de cautere, et confis avec aigue vive chaus, si qu’elle ne soit mie trop espesse ne trop clere; et en emple le chevement de cest estrument, de coi ci est li forme:	And when the patients direct their head towards your health, then press their tongue onto the tool we mentioned or the chapter on cautery, and mix it with a lively boiling substance, so that it is neither too thick nor too clear; and apply the movement of this tool, which looks like this:
Et ait ou chief une cheveure ou om met la medecine, si com li chevemens d’une cuillier, et met l’estrument a tout la medicine sus l’uve; et li malaides soit gisans sus son costeit, si que li salive et li muscillaige corre de sa bouche de la medicine dedens, si qu’ele ne dessende a la gorge, et lou blece; puis tien ta main a tout la medicine et la presse sus l’uve, la quantiteit de la moitiet d’une houre, tant que tu la vois nercie et li mordications de la medicine soit apaisie; et se tu vues, pren coton et l’envoloupe sus aucun estrument, et moille lou coton en la medicine, et boute l’estrument a tout le couton en la cainne desus, tant que li coton s’aerde sus l’uve; et fai ceu sovent, tant que li cauteres soit parfais, puis la laisse elle seche, et chiet aprés .iiij. jors ou .v. Et se tu as mestier de rencomencier lou cautere de la medicine, si le rencomence, et aprés le cautere l’essue entor l’uve, de couton embut em burre, et mundifie ceu qui est entor de la medicine; et soit arosez d’aigue froide, et soit curez de gargarismes tant qu’il soit sanez.	And have our head with a hair or we place the medicine on it, as if with the movements of a spoon, and put the tool onto all the medicine over the eye; and that patient should lie still on their side, so that saliva and mucus flow from their mouth through the medicine inside, without reaching their throat and the wound; then hold your hand over all the medicine and press it on to the eye for half an hour, as long as you see it working and the effects of the medicine have subsided; and if you notice, take cotton and wrap it around any tool, moisten the cotton with the medicine, and place the tool onto the cotton in the wick above, so that the cotton burns on the eye; and do this often until the cautery is perfect, then let it dry, and rest for four or five days afterwards. And if you need to repeat the medicine cautery, then do so, and after the cautery clean around the eye with gauze soaked in butter, and clean off anything left of the medicine; and rinse with cold water, and gargle until healed.
Ceste cure est plus save de l’incision, ne que li cautere; s’elle est curee de fumigation selonc ceste maniere, pren calament et ysope et origanum et rue et camomille et avronne et semblans herbes, et les assemble toutes ou aucunes d’eles en .i. pot, et i met aisil, et fai bullir; et li potz soit bien gluez de fort terre, et enmi le pot ait .i. estrument cheveit selonc ceste maniere:	This cure is safer than incision, or rather the cautery; if it is treated with fumigation using this method, take valerian and sage and oregano and rue and chamomile and spinach and similar herbs, and combine all of them or some of them in one pot, and put them inside, then let it boil; and ensure that the pot is well covered with strong earth, and in the middle of the pot place two sticks according to this method:
Et soit d’argent ou d’arain, et soit li uns des chiés boutez en la bouche dou malaide tant que li vapor monte a l’uve par la caine, tant que li uve soit mortifie; aprés lou rencomence sovent, tant que li uve seche, et garde que tu ne faices ceu au comencement de l’avenement de l’aposteme chaut, car plusors choses i avienent; et ne faire mie ceu fuer que a la declination d’aposteme chaut.	And whether it is of silver or sulfur, and if one of the shoulder blades sticks in the mouth until vapor rises from the body through the nostril, until the womb has become necrotic; after that repeat often, until the womb dries out, and make sure you do not perform this at the beginning of the appearance of pus, for many things occur; and do not perform this treatment during the discharge of pus.
Et se cist estrument n’est presens, si pren une caine et met dedens lou chief une craiffe d’uef, si que li bouche au malaide n’ait mie trop chaut; car li craiffe d’uef ne lait mie la vapor grever la bouche, et c’est bone cure ensamble salut.	And if this instrument is not present, take a reed and insert an eggshell inside the mouth of the patient, so that the heat does not become too intense for him; because the eggshell does not allow steam to accumulate in the mouth, and it's a good remedy altogether for health.
Maintes fois s’aert a la gorge os ou espinee de poisson, ou aucune chose; si covient donc que tu traies ceu que tu pues veoir, et li presse la lengue au soleil a tout l’estrument, si que tu voies mues la chose; et ceu que ne t’apert mie et est reponus en la gorge, covient que tu faices vomir le malaide ainsois que li viande soit cuite en l’estomac; par aventure si istra li chose aerse par le vomissement; ou li malaides englutisse une piece d’esponge, ou une piece de navel, ou une racine de laitue, ou .i. morceil de pain sec; et lie a l’esponge .i. fil, et puis la transglutisse; et quant elle venra au leu, si s’aerdra, et puis trairas fuer; et s’elle ne vient fuer de ceu que nos avons dit, si pren .i. estrument de plonc selonc ceste forme:	Many times it occurs in the throat bone or spinal area of fish, without any specific thing; so it is good that you remove whatever you can see and press your tongue against the sun with all the tool so that you see something move. And what doesn't reveal itself and remains in the throat should be induced to vomit out the rash until the meat is cooked in the stomach; by chance if it escapes through vomiting; or if the rash ingests a piece of sponge, or a piece of navel, or a root of lettuce, or half a piece of dry bread. And tie this sponge with one thread and then swallow it again. And when she comes to you, if she ascends, and then proceed to vomit. And if what we said did not bring it out, take one tool of snuff according to this shape:
Et soit li estrumens corbés au chief si qu’il puist plus legierement entrer en la gorge, et ait le chief en haut leveit; et warde que tu ne touchier l’epiglote, que li tous ne li viegne, ne ne bouter mie l’os dedens; et mues vaut que li malaides i boute l’estrument, por ceu qu’il seit mues ou li chose est aerse; si la boute aval, ou il la traie fuer a tout l’estrument igalment, tant qu’elle soit fuer.	And make the tools curved at the tip so that they can more easily enter the throat, and have the head lifted high above it; and guard not to touch the epiglottis, making sure no part of it moves or pushes any bone inside; and move such that the patient is forced to push the tool down because movement is necessary or if something is obstructing air flow; if they swallow it, or pull it forcefully until all parts are pulled equally out of the tool, as long as force is applied.
de la sansue de la gorge	of the windpipe
Aucune fois est medicinee li sansue, si com j’ai dit en la division, par la cure de medicines; et quant ceu ne profite mie, adonques regarde en la gorge dou malaide au soleil, puis que tu li presses la lengue a l’estrument que je t’ai dit.	Never is medicine given to the veins themselves, as I have mentioned in the division by the treatment of medicines; and if this does not benefit, then look into the throat of the patient at noon, then press his tongue with the tool that I told you about.
Et se tu vois la sansue, si la trai a tout I petit uncine, ou as tenailles subtilz que valent a ceu.	And if you see the vein, guide it with all small inch, or with fine forceps that are worth this.
Et se ceu ne vaut, si pren une caine chevee, et la boute en la gorge dou malaide, puis boute ou chevement de la caine I fer chaut, et fai ce sovent.	And if that doesn't work, take a thread and apply it in the neck next to the patient's wound, then move or pull on the thread until you feel resistance, and do this frequently.
Et se teigne li malaides d’aigue toute jor.	And if you irrigate the patient with water throughout the day.
puis pren plein I voirre d’aigue froide, et oevre la bouche, et la giete ens sens englutir, et la mueve a sa main sovent; et si tost com li sansue sent l’aigue, si chiet.	Then take full glasses of cold water, and work the mouth with it, pouring it in such a way that they do not swallow immediately, and move it frequently. And as soon as the vein feels the water, they will vomit.
Et s’elle ne chiet si com nos avons dit, si subfumige lou malaide d’asefetide, a l’estrument que j’ai dit en la fumigation de l’uve; fai ceu maintes fois, car elle cherra sens targier.	And if she doesn't vomit as we have said, subfuse the patient with asafetida, using the instrument mentioned for its use in eye fumigation. Do this several times because it will expel without any disturbance.
Et li maniere de la fumigation si est que tu preignes I pot ou il ait charbons vis, et soit li pos covert d’un coverseil perciet en mileu, et en celui pertus soit li chiés de l’estrument; puis i giete ta fumigation, et li malaides mette lou chief de la cainne en sa bouche, et cloie la bouche, si que li fumee n’en isse mie, mais viegne jusc’a la sansue; et la sansue cherra maintenant, et s’elle ne chiet, si rencomence la fumigation par maintes fois; et soffre li malaides soif, et menjuce choses salees et als, et ne boive point d’aigue; et adonques li iert mestier qu’elle isse fuer par cest governement.	And the way of fumigation is that you take a pot where there are live coals inside it. And place this pot under an upside down bowl in the middle, and at its bottom put the head of the tool; then pour your fumigation into this setup, and have the patient hold a part of the herb into their mouth, seal their lips so that no smoke escapes but goes all through their throat; and now their saliva will come out, if it doesn't continue the fumigation several times. And let them suffer thirst, eat salty things and others, and do not drink water; and then it is necessary for this to be expelled forcefully by this method.
Et li forme de l’estrument a coi on trait la sansue, si est, quant on la puet veoir, semblans a tenailles corbés por mues entrer en la gorge; et ait semblance au bec de soigne, et i ait asperiteit de lime, si que ceu qu’elle prent, elle ne puet lassier; et vez ci la forme:	And the shape of the tool used to expel blood is such that when you can see it, it resembles curved scissors for cutting into the throat; and it has the appearance of a doctor's beak, and it has grinding roughness like a saw, so whatever she takes, she cannot let go. li chapistres des apostemes	The chapter on abscesses
Mout de semblances d’aposteme sont, selonc ceu que li remembrance vient ci aprés d’un et d’autre en cest livre, et sont diver en perforation et en taille; et c’est en II manieres dont l’une est en sa semblance meisme, et de ceu qu’il tient moistor.	There are descriptions of abscesses according to what memory provides from one and another in this book, they vary in perforation and shaping. And it's done in two ways; one is similar in its form itself, and regarding the presence of moisture.
Et li seconde maniere si est por les leus ou il sont au cors.	And the second way is for those limbs which are inside the body.
car li apostemes dou chief est autres que cil dou fondement, et li apostemes dou leu charnut est autres que cil qui vient en jointures, et chescuns ait son jugement en l’uevre.	For the abscesses of the head are different from those of the base, and the abscesses of the internal organs differ from those that come to joints, and each has its judgment in action.

And if with abscesses one should not pierce them until the disease is fully developed according to its completion; and if there are such that it must be pierced when they grow but do not fully develop according to their completion, like abscesses located in joints.
Car quant apostemes vient delez jointures, et on le laisse tant qu’il est porris entor, par aventure si sont corrumput li liien et li nerf de la jointure, par coi ce est cause de contraction en celui membre.	For when abscesses come from joints and they are allowed to continue until they become purulent internally, by chance, if the ligament and nerve of the joint get corrupted, this is a cause for contraction in that limb.
Ou li aposteme est delez lou membre principel, et se tu tardes la perforation tant qu’il soit meurez, si nuira au membre principeil; ou il est delez lou fondement, si le perce on ainsois qu’il soit meurs; et ne covient mie que tu perces aposteme crut sens digestion acomplie, fuers que celui qui est delez lou fondement, qu’il ne porrisse em parfont, et soit alongiez dedens, et i viegne fistule; et ne puisse saner en grant termine.	The abscess lies deep in the main limb. If you delay the puncturing until it is necrotic, it will harm the main limb. The abscess lies near the foundation, if you pierce or do so even if it's necrotic; it should not that you puncture a pus-filled abscess without completed digestion, except for when it lies near the foundation, it may have rotted through and be inside, leading to an open channel; it cannot heal in a large term.
Et covient que tu saiches l’oure de la perforation de l’aposteme qui est meur selonc l’acomplissement, et c’est quant li dolor est apaisie, et li departemens de la fievre, et l’amenuisement de la dolor et de la roujor, et dou debatement et de l’aguisement dou chief de l’aposteme, et les autres signes; et covient que tu faices seoir la perforation ou plus dependant leu de l’aposteme, et la ou il apert mues; et soit li perforation dou lonc dou cors, et se li apostemes est as mains ou as piez, ou en jointures et au ners et as arteres, et en toz leus igalz ou il n’a point de ploieure.	And you should know the time of piercing the abscess which is dead according to its completion, and this is when the pain has subsided, and the departure of fever, and the reduction of pain and redness, and the movement and sensitivity of the head of the abscess, and other signs; and you should have the piercing positioned above the abscess or as low as it opens, and where it appears; and make the piercing along the length of the body, and if the abscess is at the arms or legs, or joints and nerves and arteries, and all places where there's no fold.
En ces que ploient, par selonc celui membre.	In these cases, when they bend, according to that limb.
Et quant apostemes est en leu charnut, si vaut mues que tu laisses la perforation tant qu’il soit confermez en digestion acomplie, si com nos avons dit.	And when abscesses are in the living tissue, it is better to let the puncturing happen until digestion is fully completed, as we have said.
Car se tu lou perces devant ceu, si iert alongiez li cors dou venim de lui, et est plains de mout d’ordure; et par aventure endurcissent les levres et li parfondetez de lui.	But if you pierce it before this, then the body is filled with venom from itself and full of many dirt; and accidentally hardens the skin and the depths below him.
Et si a aucun aposteme que sont perciet selonc le large dou cors, selonc ceu que li membres en ait mestier.	And if there are no abscesses pierced straight through the center of the body as per need for each limb.
Et covient que tu amenistres em petis apostemes, petis pertus; et en grans apostemes, grans pertus, et maintes fendures selonc la semblance de la grandor de l’aposteme; et si a de tels apostemes ou il covient chever lou keur, et coper; quant il est jai devenus ausi com I drapelz, et est amortis, si covient faire ausi com on fait as bubes: et si a de telz que sont fendut en III angles, et si a de telz dont on cope ausi com la fuelle de mirte, si com apostemes des angres; et si a de telz ou on fait une reonde taille, et autres tailles et semblant copeure. Cil qui n’ont point de chief, si com aposteme souef superficial, il covient que tu lou perces plainnement; et covient quant li apostemes est gros, et il a coillit grant bowe, et tu lou perces, si ne traire mie toute la bowe en celle houre, mais en trai une partie; puis estoupe l’aposteme jusc’a l’autre jor, puis en trai aucune chose derechief; fai ceu par maintes fois de greit en greit, tant que li bowe isse toute; meismement se li malaides est de foible vertut, ou femme portans, ou petis enfes, ou viez hons decrepites.	Those who do not have a head, like superficial abscesses, it must be that you pierce them completely; and when the abscess is large, and contains a big lump, then if you drain only part of the lump at once, but remove some of it; then fill in the abscess until to the other side, then leave nothing uncovered; do this step many times progressively with increasing sizes, until the lump comes out completely; similarly, for those whose body's capability is weak, or pregnant women, or small children, or old and decrepit.
Car li esperis tressaut aucune fois avec l’issue de la bowe, que par aventure muert li malaides, et tu ne t’en persois.	For when someone tries to force it with the expulsion of blood, sometimes causing death of the patient, and you do not realize this.
Eschuez donques cest chapistre par grant cautele, et quant tu as perciet ton aposteme, si essue la plaie, et regarde se li plaie de l’aposteme est petite; et se c’est une tailleure plainne, si amenistre tentes de lin ou de viez coton; et se c’est uns grans apostemes, et il i a mout de pertus, si covient que tu boutes en chescun une tente si qu’ele viegne l’une contre l’autre; et se tu as copeit en l’aposteme une partie dou cuir, et tu l’as cheveit entor, si covient que tu l’emplisses de viel couton ou de rasure de dras de lin sens moistor, et le lie jusc’au tier jor; puis l’oste, et le cure d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez.	So avoid this chapter with great caution, and when you have incised your abscess, if there is an opening, observe if the wound from the abscess is small. And if the bleeding persists, then apply administration and treatment, and use the powders I have mentioned in this book for your hands. de squinance	"De squinance" in this context refers to treatments or procedures related to diseases or deformities of the neck and head region. This could cover a variety of topics such as injuries, infections, tumors, dislocations, and other medical conditions affecting these areas. Without more context from the specific text you're referring to, it's difficult to provide an exact translation for each line in this term. However, generally speaking, "squinance" implies a focus on neck-related ailments or surgery.
Li ancien dirent et parlerent de la tailleure de la gorge; mais je ne vis onques en nostre terre qui la feist, et c’est li escripture de lor parole.	The old ones spoke and told of the art of cutting the throat; but I never saw anyone do it in our land, and this is written down from their words.
A ces qui ont squinance, il covient que li fendure de la gorge qui est apelee «epiglote» soit eschuee; et c’on ne faice aide par ceu, por ceu que toutes les voines et li pormon dou malaide sont a ces qui ont aposteme chaut en la bouche, ou en la gorge ou en .ij. amandres.	For those with squinting vision, it is necessary that the slit of the throat known as "epiglottis" be excised; and one should not attempt this operation by oneself, because all the airways and the windpipe are in these who have phlegm either in their mouth or in their throat or between two bones.
Quant li maladie est en la chenal dou pormon, il covient coper l’epiglote por fuir la perdition qui vient de l’estranglement.	When the disease is in the channel of the windpipe, it is necessary to cover the epiglottis to prevent loss from strangulation.
Il covient donques, quant nos volons fendre l’epiglote, que nos le fendons desoz III cercles ou IIII une petite fendure dou travers, entre les II cercles ou par la quantiteit de la fendure dou syfac, ne mie en la cartillaige; et cil leus si est covenaubles a la section de l’epiglote qu’il n’i a point de char, et li vasseil sont lonc d’enqui.	Therefore, when we wish to cut through the epiglottis, we cut through three or four small slits across it between the two circles, or by the quantity of the slit towards its base, not in the cartilage; and this is advantageous for cutting the epiglottis so that there is no flesh remaining, and the vessels are long enough to reach their ends.
Et se li maistres est paourous, si covient qu’il estende le cuir de la gorge a tout l’oncine, puis fende lou keur tant qu’il viegne a la cheneil; et eschue les vasselz de sanc, se tu vois aucune chose, et puis cope lou syfac, si com nos avons dit; et est demostrez par la section dou fleume de la cheneil ki saut fuer par le leu qui est rompus, et par la defaute de la voix; et laisse la plaie overte une piece.	And if the surgeons are fearful, it is necessary that they stretch the skin of the throat to the entire inch, then cut along the keur until it reaches the chin; and avoid the vessels of blood, if you see nothing, and then shape the syfac, as we have said; and this has been demonstrated through the section of the stream of saliva in the chin which jumps out through the side where the breakage occurred, and due to loss of voice; and leave the wound open for a piece.
Et quant li houre est passee de coi on doute l’estranglement, assemble les .ij. levres de la plaie dou keur, et la cout toute soule sens la cartillaige; puis aministre medicines qui font naistre char, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when the hour has passed since one doubts strangulation, gather the two sides of the wound neatly together with care, and seal it entirely save for the cartilage; then administer medicines that cause growth to occur, until it becomes healthy.
Albucasim dist c’on ne faice ce jusc’a tant que li gorge est toute estoupee, et li malaides est jugiez a mort, et li defaut li alaine.	Albucasim insists that one should not stop this process until the throat is completely swollen and the patient is pronounced dead, and until all deficiencies are met.
Adonques cope on l’epiglote por ceu que li malaides ne puet alener, et il respire par la plaie, et ensi est gardez de mort; et por ce commanderent li anciain a laissier la plaie overte tant que li malice de la maladie soit passee, et elle est passee en III jors ou en IIII Et adonques il comanderent a coudre la plaie et curer, tant qu’elle fut curee; et je vos dirai ceu que je vis.	So shape around the epiglottis because the patient cannot breathe normally, and they inhale through the wound, thus preventing death; and in accordance with the advice of the elders, it was commanded to leave the wound open until the danger of illness passes, and this happens after three days or four. And then they were instructed to stitch up the wound and clean it, as long as it has healed; and I will tell you what I observed.
Je vis que une damoisele prist I coutel, et le ficha en sa gorge, et copa partie des chenelz dou pormon; et je fui apelez por li curer, et la trovai ausi com morte.	I witnessed that a maiden took to the knife, and stabbed it into her throat, severing part of the windpipe. And I was summoned to tend to her, finding her just as dead.
Je descovris la plaie, et trovai le sanc qui en estoit issus, et soi bien qu’elle n’avoit mie copeit voine ne conduit fuer que la gorge, et li vens issoit fuer par la plaie.	I discovered the wound and found the blood coming from it, indeed, she did not have a cut vein or artery leading there but the veins were flowing through the wound.
Je me hastai, et cousi la plaie, et la curai tant qu’elle fut sanee; et n’avint a la damoisele fuer qu’elle fut roge de voix, et revint aprés a sa disposition; por ceu di je que en la tailleure de l’epiglote n’ait mie paour.	I rushed quickly to treat the wound and healed her until she was well. And for that maiden, after her voice was strained from speaking, she returned to her usual self. That is why I say there should be no fear in cutting the epiglottis.
de la grosse gorge	From the large throat
Cist apostemes est apelez «hernie de gorge», et est uns grans apostemes en color d’une jaisse, et est molt en femmes; et est selonc II manieres: naturez, et accidens; ou natureil n’a point d’engien.	Hernias in the neck are called "throat hernias", they are large swellings of a deep red color and occur frequently in women. They can happen in two ways: naturally or accidentally. Natural hernias do not have any internal cause.
Et li accidens est selonc II manieres, de coi l’une est semblans a gras nous, et li autre maniere est semblans a aposteme qui vient de nous d’artere; et il i ait paour, et ne covient mie ovrer de feir fuers que en celi qui est petite, et le prueve et cerche a tout l’intromissoire: se tu le trueves ausi com I nout gras, et ne pent a nulle voine, si le cope, si com on cope les nous, et le trai a tout sa coife, s’il en i a point; et encerche bien tot, et le cure si com il covient, tant qu’il soit sanez parfaitement.	Accidents happen in two ways. The first is like greasy pus that comes from within us, and the second is like pus that comes out of an artery, causing fear. It's essential not to open any larger swellings except for those tiny ones. If you find one small enough to fit through without touching any veins, remove it similarly to how we would remove other pus, making sure to keep all its boundaries intact. Search thoroughly and treat according to what is necessary until it is completely healed.
des nous	after nails
Maintes manieres de nous sont, dont je dirai toutes les semblances; et or covient que je die toute la difference qui est entre nout et issue.	Many ways there are, which I will explain through their similarities; now it is fitting that I state the whole distinction between us and cause.
Je dis que issue est chalors et fievre tenans, tant que li ebulicions est passee, et est acomplie li porriture; adonques repose li fievre et li chalor.	I say that issue is characterized by heat and fever until the ebullitions have passed and putrefaction has occurred; thus, then rest ceases from the fever and heat.
Avec lou nout n’a ne chalor ne fievre ne dolor, et contient I syfac, qui est ses propres sac et est selonc la color dou cors, et encomence ausi com une jaisse, et devient gros; et sont selonc ij semblances, ou grais, ou moiste, et mout de color sont si com j’ai dit en la division.	With the original, there is no fever or inflammation, and contains pus, which is its own sac and is within the body's color, starts also like a boil, and becomes large; and are according to two appearances, greasy or moist, and most of its color is as I said in the division.
Il covient, quant tu viens a la cure dou nout, que tu esprueves et l’enquier premierement a tout l’estrument qui est apelez «entromissoire», selonc ce que sa forme venra ou chapistre qui est aprés.	When you begin the treatment for a new case, it is necessary that you first examine and inquire about all the tools which are called 'jointer', according to their shape or the chapter that follows.
Et li maniere de l’inquisicion des apostemes des nous est que tu preignes ou plus moiste leu que tu trueves en l’aposteme, et torne tes dois poc et poc, tant que tu saiches que li estrumens ait perciet le keur, puis que ce soit selonc la grandor de l’aposteme; puis estrai l’entromissoire, et pren garde en ceu que saut fuer.	And the method for the incision of pus in us is that you extract or more moist than you find in the pus, and turn your hands slowly and slowly, until you know that the instruments have pierced the body, then according to the size of the pus; then remove the center, and be careful not to jump.
Se moistor corrans cort, queil color elle ait, si le fent si com j’ai dit des autres apostemes; et se aprés l’entromissoire nen vient moistor, saiches qu’il est gras, si le fent donques en croix, et le prent as pinceures, et l’escorche legierement de chescune part et warde la cotte ou il gist que tu la traies saine avec le nout; et se tu ne la pues traire saine, si la trai par pieces si qu’il n’i demoure rien.	If moisture is removed quickly, regardless of its color, if you make the incision as I've described for other abscesses; and if after the first attempt no further moisture comes out, know that it's greasy, then cut straight through, and take hold with forceps, and lightly scrape each side, and cover the spot where it lies when you pull off the bandage safely. And if you cannot pull off the bandage safely, then remove in pieces so nothing is left behind.
Car s’il i demoure rien, si revient li nous par maintes fois; et s’il en demore un poc, et li sans te grieve, si emple la plaie d’aucunes poudres corrosives agues, et estraint la plaie, et met sus choses apaisans aposteme chaut, et le cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez; et se li nous est grans, si cout les II levres de la plaie, et le cure de ceu qui enjanre char.	For if nothing is left behind, it will recur many times; and if a little remains, without causing you grief, fill the wound with corrosive powders and dressings, then apply soothing treatments for abscesses that are hot. Continue other healing methods until it becomes clean. And if there's considerable pus, cut both sides of the wound, and treat the area around where the infection is spreading.
et se li voine batans t’est contraire ou autre si te haste et emple le leu de vitriole broiet, et lou laisse liiet .ij. jors ou .iij., tant que li plaie porrisse, et repose li ebulicion dou sanc; puis revien au coper ceu que i est demoreit dou nout.	And if the vein is thicker than expected or any other situation that requires urgency, then use the opening of vitriol and let it sit for two or three days, as long as the wound heals, and rest with blood boiling; then return to using what has been applied during the first treatment.
Vez ci les formes des estrumens entromissoires, et sont de III manieres: grans et moien et petit; et s’en i a III quarrez qui sont apelez «albaret», et I qui est apelez «breb», et s’en i a de III manieres: grant, moien, et petit, por encerchier les apostemes de fistule; et sont ausi com les aguilles dont on cout les sorceles, et sont d’arain citrin, ou de fer, ou d’argent, et mues valent cil qui sont jaune, et sont plus esprovez de plonc noir por encerchier les corbeures de fistule; et sont de III manieres: grans, moiens, et petis, selonc la quantiteit de la largesce des pertus.	Here are the forms of the surgical instruments used in cutting operations, and they come in three ways: large, medium-sized, and small. And there are three needles that are called 'albaret', and one is named 'breb'. Among these, there are also three kinds: large, medium-sized, and small, for wrapping around abscesses of fistula; and they resemble pins used in suturing wounds, made from citrine gold, iron, or silver. The yellow ones have more reputation than black nail-pins when it comes to wrapping around the bends of fistulae. They come in three forms: large, medium-sized, and small, according to the size of the openings.
Les formes des oncines sont de mout de semblances, si com tu vois ci: grans, moiens, et petis; et si a oncines qui ont II corbeures de III manieres ausi; et si a oncines qui ont III corbeures, et sont ausi de III manieres; et si a oncines qui ont II corbeures, et oncines d’une corbeure soulement, et sont de III manieres; et tuit cist sont necessaire en lor leu.	The forms of the incisions resemble sheep, as you can see here: large, medium-sized, and small. There are also two-edged incision blades with three kinds in each way; there are those that have three bends, and they come in three kinds as well; there are those with two bends and single-bend incisions, which too come in three forms; and all these are necessary according to their shape.
Li chief de ces a coi on fent sont trenchant, et de telz i a qui ne taillent mie fuer que d’une part, dont on escorche les nous, por ceu c’on ne cope la voine ne le nerf; et de ces intromissoires sont les alemeles reponues en mainches, si que li malaide ne s’en persoivent a l’overture des apostemes; et sont de III manieres: grant, petit, et moien, si com tu vois; et n’en use on mie fuer que en leu charnut, si com jambes, et bras, et mameles, et as angres, et en semblans leus; et aucune fois fait on I autre estrument petit, semblant a escorces de fistices, selonc ceste forme, a coi on estainche sanc:	The head of this one they make sharp, and there are those who don't cut with force but only from one side; in such cases they sear the flesh. This is because in these instances you do not touch the vein nor the nerve; and among these instruments, the blades are handled like scissors, so that the patient does not perceive the opening of the abscesses during its procedure. There are three ways: large, small, and medium, as you see; and one doesn't use force except in gutting meat, such as legs, arms, nipples, ribs, and similar ones; and no other small tool is used that resembles excising tools, according to this shape, on which blood clotting is done:
et le met on aucune fois au leu qui saine a copement des voines, et as arteres, et aucune fois reont selonc ceste grant forme:	And it is placed only once at the sound position of veins and arteries, and never following this large form:
Aucune fois enflent les mameles d’aucuns homes quant cil encomencent estre corrumput, tant qu’eles semblent mameles de feme; et demorent laides et enflees, et qui les vuet curer, si le covient soier selonc ceste forme des ceste ligne .b. jusques a .g.:	No time do the nipples of some men swell when they begin to be corrupted, until they seem like nipples of women; and remain ugly and swollen, and whoever wants to treat them should do it according to this method up until here:
puis escorche la graisse, et emple la plaie de medicine enjanrant char, puis assemble les II levres de la plaie a costure, et la cure tant qu’ele soit sanee; et se li mamele cline aval, et est amolie por sa grandor si com il avient as femmes, si la fent en II costelz desus, par II semblans fendures; de coi l’une soit tenans a l’autre a la fin de l’une et de l’autre, si que li plus grans ligne conteigne la menor selonc ceste forme, des ceste ligne .b. jusc’a la ligne .g.; puis escorche le cuir qui est entre les II levres, et oste la graisse, et i amenistre ceu que nos avons dit de costure et de poudres, et ceu qui est necessaire en la cure, tant qu’il soit sanez; et s’il n’est sanez, ou li incision n’est mie toute faite, por ceu que li malaides ne vuet reposer, ou por le decorrement de sanc, si covient que tu emplisses la plaie de coton moilliet en oignement corrosif; et le laisse tant qu’il menjuce le remenant et la graisse, puis le cure tant qu’il soit saneis.	Then scorch the fat, and apply medicine to the wound, then join together the two edges of the wound for stitching, and treat it until it is healed; and if the nipple hangs down and has become soft due to its size as in women, cut it into II parts above, by II similar incisions; from which one will be held onto by the other at the end of each one, so that the larger line contains the smaller according to this form, until this line .b. up to this line .g.; then scorch the skin between the two edges, remove the fat, and apply the stitching and powder instructions we have said, and what is necessary for treatment, until it is healed; and if it has not been healed or the incision was not fully made due to the inability of the patient to rest, or because of blood leakage, then you should fill the wound with wet cotton wadding in a corrosive ointment; and leave it until it starts to heal by removing the cotton stuffing and fat afterwards, then treat it until it is completely healed.
des apostemes des asselles	removal of abscesses from armpits
Cist apostemes que vienent desoz les asseles sont manieres de scrophules dures ou il ait cotes, et s’en i a que contienent moistor.	Abscesses that occur in the armpits are ways of hard scrofula or where there have been nodes, and if any contain moisture.
Cil donques qui contienent moistor covient qu’il soient copez selonc ceste forme, des la ligne .b. jusc’a la ligne .g.:	Those who contain moisture must be cut according to this form, from the line b. up until the line g:
Et quant toute li bowe qui est en l’aposteme est vuidie, si emple la plaie de viel coton, et la laisse jusc’a l’autre jor, puis oste tout le coton, et cure d’oignement avenant a ceu tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when all the pus in the abscess is drained, fill the wound with old cotton and let it stay until the next day. Then remove all the cotton and continue applying ointment until healed.
Et se li apostemes est de semblances de scrophules, si le fent si com nos avons dit en fendures des scrophules, et se li plaie rent bowe, si amenistre cautere si com nos avons dit devant.	And if the abscesses resemble scrophula sores, make incisions as we have said for cuts on scrophula sores, and if the wound is filled with pus, apply a cautery as we have said earlier.
de la routure de l’artere	regarding the rupture of an artery
Quant li artere est route, et li cuir est soudez qui est sus, si en vient maintes fois apostemes, et tout aussi avient il a la voine enflee et aposteme; et si le conoist on ensi quant c’est por l’artere, si est li apostemes lons em parfont; et quant tu le sens a tes dois, si sens I estraignement; et quant c’est por la voine, si est reons defuer aparans; et c’est folie de coper cest aposteme, et meismement quant il est desoz les asseles et as angres et ou col et em mout d’autres leus, et est mout grans.	When the artery is cut and the skin is sutured above it, there are many times when abscesses form, and this happens similarly with veins and abscesses; and if one knows that it's due to an artery, then the abscesses will be long and deep; and when you feel resistance with your fingers, you know it's a blood clot; and when it's due to a vein, there is a visible opening of skin; and it's foolishness to remove this abscess, especially when it is under joints and bones and in the neck and other parts of the body, and is very large.
Il covient donques eschuir la cure de fer, et celui qui est a chief covient eschuir ausi, et en celui qui est d’enfleure d’artere fent par desus le cuir dou lonc; puis oevre la taille as oncines, et depart bellement l’artere des toiles, tant qu’ele soit descoverte; puis boute desoz li une aguille, et la fai percier jusc’a l’autre costeit, et estraint l’artere d’un fil double en II leus, selonc ceu que je t’ai ensigniet en l’estraction des II arteres qui sont en temples; puis point le leu qui est entre les II liens d’un intromissoire tant que li sans en isse qui i est, et soit deliiez li aposteme; puis amenistre la cure que enjanre bowe, tant que li liien chient; puis cure ceu d’oignement avenant a ceu, tant qu’il soit sanez; et se li apostemes est por la taille de la voinne, si covient que tu teignes a ta main ceu que tu pues de l’aposteme a tout le cuir, puis boute l’aguille desoz le leu que tu tiens a ta main, et la fai percier, et i ait I fil double, si que tu le trais de l’autre costeit; puis lie l’aposteme, si com je t’ai dit, ou liien de l’une de II pars as II chiés dou fil; et se tu doutes que li filz n’isse fuer, si i reboute une autre aguille a tout I fil desoz tout l’aposteme a l’incision de la premiere aguille, et estraint les filz en IIII leus; puis cope l’aposteme tant que li superfluitez en isse, puis cope la superfluiteit dou keur et laisse ceu qui est liiez; puis met sus I drapeil moilliet en vin et en oile, puis li amenistre cures de tentes et d’oignemens tant qu’il soit sanez.	It is then necessary to avoid the iron cure, and that of the head should also be avoided. In the case where there is swelling due to an artery, it is done through the skin from its length; then work with the needle on the side, and detach the artery from the tissue until it's uncovered; then insert a thread under the skin for as long as possible, and pierce up to the other side of the body, then hold the artery with two threads according to what I have taught you in extracting the two arteries that are in temples. Then press the part between the two threads with an intervening tool until blood flows freely and is free; then treat the place where the cure comes into play until it heals completely; then apply ointment as long as it's intact. And if the abscess is due to vein swelling, you should color your hand with what you can of the abscess over all the skin, then insert a needle under the part you hold in your hand and pierce it, then have two threads of double thread so that you pull from the other side; then tie the abscess as I told you, or a thread between two parts by thread. And if you doubt whether the threads will pass through completely, you should reinsert another needle under all the thread across the entire abscess at the point where the first needle pierced and hold the threads in four threads; then remove the excess of the abscess as much as it comes out, then remove the excess with a pair and leave what is tied. Then place on one side a moist cloth in wine and oil, then treat with baths and ointments until it heals completely.
des apostemes des ners	from the pus of the nerves
Ausi com aposteme vienent en l’artere et en la voine, vienent aposteme as ners quant il sont ferut, ou par trop grant travail, et semblans choses.	Similarly, just like pus flows in the artery and vein, pus enters the nerves when they are cut, or by too much labor, and similar things.
Et ceu avient plus sovent as adjutoires et as dois et en toz leus ou il ait jointures, et c’est I grief apostemes, et sa color semble la color dou cors, et est em plusors dispositions sens dolor; et quant on l’estraint forment, si sent li malaides dolor, et n’est mie em parfont dou cors, mais desoz lou keur; et muet bien de toutes pars, et ne va ne avant ne arrier, ne desoz ne desus, et celui qui est en jointures ne covient mie coper par fer: par aventure i vanroit contraction; et cil qui est ou chief ou ou front, fent le cuir au spatumile.	And this occurs more often with shoulders and arms, and everywhere the joints are found, it's about abscesses, and its color seems like the color of the body, and is in many positions without pain; and when it is constrained straight, the patient feels pain from their side but not completely through their body, but on each side of the back; and moves well in all directions, neither forward nor backward, neither to the left nor right, and one who is dislocated does not fit with iron: by chance there might be constriction; and that which is at the head or forehead, makes the skin go flat.
Se li apostemes est petis, si le tien a unes tenailles, et le cope en sa racine; et s’il est grans, si le sospent a l’oncine, et l’escorche, puis l’oste et assemble la plaie a la costure, et lou cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	If the abscesses are small, and you have tweezers, grasp it at its root; and if they're large, lift them up to the wrist, and cut them, then remove the pus, after which assemble the wound along the stitch line, and continue treatment until the patient is well.
des grosses boces pendans	Of large boils hanging
Aucune fois avient en ventres et ne mie autre part thelul, et est une maladie qui est apelee «funge» par la semblance d’aus, et est li racine subtilz, et li chiez gros; et en i a de petis et de mout grans; et je vis I home qui en avoit II ou ventre qui estoient plus semblans a funges que ai autre chose, et n’i avoit point de difference, et estoient blanc, et avoient menue racine, et estoient jai fendut, et en corroit adés moistor.	No instance happens in the womb or elsewhere, and it is a disease that is called 'fungus' by its appearance, and has delicate roots and large heads; there are also smaller ones and some very large. I knew a person who had two bellies that looked more like fungi than anything else, and there was no difference, they were white, had small roots, were partly cut, and corroded with moisture immediately.
Je les copai et trovai en l’un XVIII onces pesant, et en l’autre VI З., et li ovraiges en l’incision si est que tu regardes se li malaides est moistes, et li color de l’artelul est blainche et moiste et de subtil racine; si le cope au spatumile large, et soient en ta presence li cautere au feu.	I measured and found that one was eighteen ounces in weight, and the other was six, and when you look at the incision during surgery it appears that the pus is moist, and the color of the flesh is white and moist with a delicate root; if you observe them being large pustules, then use the cautery with fire near your presence.
Car au taillier vient maintes fois trop grans decorremens de sanc, et se li sans te vaint, si te haste donques dou cauterizer; et se tu vois le malaide espoanteit et paourous de l’incision dou fer, si prent I fil de plonc bien fait, et en lie l’artelul si com nos avons dit, et le laisse II jors; et puis le restraint, et ne cesser d’estraindre lou fil de plonc tant qu’il cope l’artelul, et chiece par lui sens travail; et se les racines sont grosses, si a paour au coper meismement por le ventre, mais tu em pues bien coper la moitiet, puis le cauterize qu’il ne reviegne; puis cure la plaie, et garde que tu ne coper le thelul qui est de fuxe color et de povre sens et de lait regart.	For when a barber comes there are many times excessive bleedings, and if they don't stop, then hurry with the cautery; and if you see the patient frightened and fearful from the cut of the iron, take a well-made snail thread, tie it to the arm as we said, and leave it for two days; then hold it in place, and never cease pulling the snail thread until it comes off cleanly without pain; and if the roots are large, you fear they might pull through the belly, but you can pull half of them well, then cauterize so that they do not reappear; then treat the wound, and make sure you don't pull off the small white part which has little sensation and is sensitive to pressure.
Car c’est uns apostemes enchancrez, et je venrai a la cure de chancre ci aprés.	For this is an abscess, and I will come to the treatment of the sore afterwards.
quant li boude ist fuer	When the buttock burns, it means
Se li apparance de la boude vient par cautere de plaie ou de fendure de syfac, et est sus le ventre et en ist aucuns des bouez, si com il avient en autres routures, ou de sanc qui cort de voines ou d’arteres selonc ceu qui est devant, ou de ventositeit; et se c’est par la routure dou syfac et par l’issue dou bouel, si est li color de l’aposteme semblans a la color dou cors, et est legiere chose sens dolor, et apert de diverse issue.	The appearance of pus comes from the cautery of wound or slit in scabs, and it is on the belly and there are some in the blisters, just as it happens in other injuries, or bleeding coming from veins or arteries according to what was mentioned before, or due to windiness; and if this is by the scab injury and by the outlet of pus, then the color of the abscess resembles the color of blood, and it's a light thing without pain, opening with various discharges.
Et se c’est por l’issue de l’intestine, adonques est il plus divers, et quant on le presse a ses dois si se repont, et puis revient, et par aventure si est sarrez, et agrandist mout a l’entree dou bain et por fort travail.	And if it is due to the issue from the intestine, then it is more diverse, and when one presses on its fingers if it returns and then comes back again, and by chance if it is squeezed and expands much at the entrance of the bath and through strong labor.
Et se c’est por moistor, c’est legiere chose, et apert bien quant tu le presses a ta main, ne ne constraint mie; et se c’est por sanc, si apert par ces signes li apostemes gros et dur, et est fichiez selonc une quantiteit; et se c’est por ventositeit, si est souef au tochier, et li ovraiges si est que tu regarde se li apparance est por le sanc de l’artere, ou de la voine, ou ventositeit.	And if it's due to moisture, it's a minor matter and opens up well when you press it with your hand, not restraining it; and if it's due to blood, it opens through these symptoms - the abscesses are large and hard, spread according to quantity; and if it's due to wind, it sweats at the armpits, and in such cases look whether its appearance is due to blood from the artery, or vein, or wind.
Si covient que tu laisses la cure.	It is necessary that you leave the treatment.
Car il en a doutance et paor, si com je t’ai dit ou chapistre des apostemes, por l’artere et por la voine.	For there is doubt and fear when it comes to abscesses, as I have explained in the chapter on abscesses, concerning arteries and veins.
Et se li apparance est por l’intestine ou lou boueil, si covient que tu comandes au malaide qu’il teigne son alaine, et soit estendus tout drois, puis seigne d’enche tout entor la boude; puis le comande a gesir sovin entre tes mains, puis va entor le leu que tu as signiet a tout le spatumile, puis estent la moitiet de l’aposteme au desus a tout le grant uncine; puis le lie entor d’un fil fort, ou d’une corde de fort soie fermement, et soit li nous dou liien assolz; puis oevre la moitiet de l’aposteme estendut sus le liien, et i boute ton doit indice, et quier l’intestine; se tu le trueves pris dou liien, si le deslie, et boute l’intestine au defuer dou ventre; et se tu trueves le boueil, si le prent a l’oncine, et en cope la superfluiteit; et se li artere te fait contraire, ou li voine, si vai belement entor, puis revien a ton ovraige et pren II aguilles, et i boute II fors filz, et boute les II aguilles entor ceu que tu as fait en crois que tu feis percier; puis estrain l’aposteme en IIII leus sus les aguilles, et se tu vues, oste les aguilles, et laisse lou leu tant qu’il porrisse, et chiece li char morte par soi; ou tu la cope quant elle iert subtiliie et porrie, puis le cure de ceu qu’il covient, et cheve l’aposteme si com nos avons dit; et estrai le sanc ou la moistor que tu trueves, puis cure le leu de ceu qu’il couvient, et soude le leu.	And if its appearance is due to the intestines or the stomach, it is necessary that you have them secrete bile, and spread out completely straight. Then cut all around inside the stomach; then order them to rest somewhat in your hands, then go through as far as you marked on the body, then leave half of the abscess above all the large hook; then tie it up firmly with a strong thread or a piece of thick silk cord, and secure it tightly so that it is fully bound; then spread out half of the abscess on top of this binding, and bend your index finger, feeling for the intestine. If you find that it has been caught by the binding, remove it, and pull the intestine to the front of the abdomen; and if you find the stomach, take hold of the hook, and discard any excess fluid. And if the artery does not flow or the vein flows too much, go back to your work, take two needles, then push two separate threads, and insert the two needles at the place where you made a cross that you punctured; then pull out the abscess three times on each needle, and when you see the wound close, remove the needles, and let the body heal itself until it is soft and rotten, and discard the dead flesh. Or cut off when it has become thin and rotten, then treat the wound as appropriate, and scrape the abscess as we have said; and drain out any blood or moisture that you find, then treat the wound according to what needs to be done, and sew up the wound.
dou chancre	and the sore

de la piere	Of the stone

Car il encombre aucune fois a querir la piere.	For it clogs up one way or another when seeking the stone.

de l’aposteme des coions	regarding the discharge of testicles
