And when the abscess rests, you treat the body with ointment until it heals; and the one called "albathir" is red, resembling a hard head, if it needs to be covered as I have instructed for thylul; and then continue treating until it heals.
des apostemes de la marris	The contents of the uterus
Maintes manieres d’aposteme vienent en la marris, si com chancre et aposteme pierous et herpes et estiomenes et fistules et emorroides et aposteme chaut, et plusors autres maladies que j’ai dit en la division.	Many forms of abscess occur in the marris, such as gangrene and stone-abscesses, herpetic lesions, intestinal ulcers, fistulas, hemorrhoids, and other diseases that I have mentioned in the division.
Il covient donques que je die en cest traitier l’aposteme chaut qui vient en la marris, qui n’est mie des apostemes que coillent bowe; et se tu vues savoir l’ovraige de fer, si regarde se li apostemes est agus en l’encomencement de sa venue, et plain de chalor et de fievre, et s’il devient rouge se tu le pues veoir.	So it is necessary for me to explain in this treatise the abscess that comes from the armpit, which is not among the pus-filled abscesses; and if you wish to understand its nature, look at whether the abscess is hard at the start of its appearance, and full of heat and fever, and if it turns red when you see it.
Adonques ne te haster mie de percier, mais lou fais meurer tant que li dolor soit apaisie; et puis fai seoir lou malaide sus I siege, et ait II petis sieges ou il se cline, et apoie sus son dos et assemble ses piez as parties defuer la jambe; et soient ses cuixes espandues, et mette ses braz desoz ses genous, et les lie bien d’un boin liien; puis succe li baille devers lou destre costeit, et i amenistre l’estrument dont on oevre la bouche de la marris, de coi ci aprés vient li forme; et covient que quant tu i vues amenistrer cest estrument, que tu fiches le rait premier ens por savoir la parfondeté de la marris, si que ceu qui entre ens de l’estrument n’i viegne plus em parfont qu’il ne doit, et qu’il ne blece la malaide; et se li estrumens est plus grans, si covient covrir la parfondesce de la marris de drapelz, si que li estrumens ne li grieve; et covient qu’il mette le cornet de l’estrument au desus, et qu’il teigne l’estrument.	So do not rush to pierce immediately, but wait until the pain is relieved; and then place the patient on their seat, with two small seats behind where they lean, supporting them with their back and aligning their feet towards the front of the leg. And let their knees be spread out, and place their arms under their thighs, binding them well with a good bandage; then guide him to breathe towards his right side, and have ready the instrument used on the armpit cavity from which we will take this form; and you should check the depth of the cavity upon seeing this instrument being administered, so that what enters into the instrument does not go any further in than it should, and it doesn't hurt the patient; and if the instruments are too large, cover the depth of the cavity with cloths, so the instruments do not trouble them. And you should put the funnel of the instrument above and cut the instrument.
Et quant li apostemes apert, et on lou fent a la main mol, si le covient coper au chief, au spatumile leit; et quant li bowe est vuidie, si covient que tu mettes en la plaie tentes moillies en oile roset, ou en oile vert sec; et met la tente fuer de la plaie au parfont de la marris, et met par defuer sus la marris et sus le poignil lainne nette moillie en aigue ou malves soient cuites; puis le cure aprés II jors d’oignement avenant a ceu, tant qu’il soit sanez; et aucune fois leve on la marris et la plaie par clistere d’aigue et de miel, et puis d’aigue ou racines de lis et aristologe longe soient cuites; puis reveigne a l’oignement.	And when the abscess opens, and you treat it by hand gently, you should cover the head, the mouth of the wound; and once the pus is drained, you should apply wetted cloths in olive oil or in clear distilled oil; then place the cloth right above the mustard, and put the rest of it below the mustard and on the clean blade in water or with cooked daisy leaves and aristolochia; after that, continue the treatment for two days using an ointment suitable for this purpose until healing is complete; and each time you wash out the mustard and wound with a mixture of water and honey, then water mixed with daisy root decoctions, before resuming application of the ointment.
Et se li plaie est reponue en la marris, si covient que tu te gardes de cuire de fer, mais cure la si com nos avons dit en la division.	And if the wound is treated with mustard, you should avoid cooking it with iron, but treat it in the way we've instructed when discussing its application.
de l’enfantement	During childbirth
Mestier est premier a la baile qu’elle conoisse la figure de l’enfantement natureil, et li signes si est quant tu vois la femme apresser aval, et desire odorer l’ar: adonques se haste li enfes de fuer issir; adonc saiches que cil enfantemens est selonc la figure natureil, et est li issue soz son chief, et li secondine avec lui; et quant tu vois ces signes, si covient presser legierement son ventre, si que li enfes isse tost; car quant il dessent sus son chief, si ist li secondine avec lui, et est mondee li marris de ses superfluitez par bone mundification; et cist qui vient autrement ne vient mie naturelment.	Proficiency starts with knowing the natural birth figure and its signs. When you see a woman in labor, and she begins to push forcefully, it's then that the child wants to come out. Then you know that this birth follows the natural figure, coming from the mother's womb, accompanied by her second son. And when you notice these signs, gently press on her belly so that the child comes out quickly. For when it descends through its head and also its second son follows, it exits clean of superfluities through good cleaning; any other way does not come naturally.
Car il vient aucune fois sus ses piez, et vient fuer li cors ou li chiés, et les mains, ou il vient sus son ventre, ou sovin, et est convertis par aventure sor son col, et par autres figures malvaises; si est mestier a la baile qu’elle soit saige et subtilz en ces choses, et se warse d’error et de decevement, et je vos mostrerai toutes les figures coment on li doit aidier.	For it comes only from his joints, and moves through the body or the shoulder blades, and the hands, or it moves down through his abdomen, or belly button, being sometimes transformed by chance around his neck, and through other harmful figures; for this is necessary to a midwife that she should be wise and subtle in these matters, and be aware of error and deception. And I will show you all the figures on how one should assist in these situations.
Se li enfes vient sus son chief par issue natureil, et li femme enfante griement, et li vertus de li est foible, si la fai seoir sus une selle, ou les femmes la tienent; et arose sa nature d’oile ou fenugreic soit cuit, et puis boute li baile entre ses dois le petit spatumile dont ci est li forme:	When the child comes from his head by natural exit, and the woman is in severe labor, and her strength is weak, then make her sit on a stool, or women hold her; and let her drink out of what is cooked from fenugreek, and then have the midwife place between her fingers the small spatula described below:
et fende la secondine, et cope a son ungle tant que li moistors qui est ens corre fuers; et preint lou ventre de la femme tant que li enfes dessende, et s’il ne dessent, si covient clisterizer la femme de muscillaige de fenugrec avec oile de sisament; puis la fai preindre et esternuer de condisi, et tien sa bouche et son neis une houre: si istra maintenant l’enfes.	And divide the second part, and cut up to his nail until all moisture that is contained has escaped; and hold the woman's belly as the baby descends, and if it does not descend, then you should treat the woman with fennel seed musk oil. Then make her drink and sniff camphor water, and keep her mouth and nose closed for an hour: now the baby comes out.
Et se les II mains issent fuer, si covient que tu les ramoinne legierement poc et poc; et s’elles n’i puent entrer, si met la femme sus I siege, et li lieve les piés en haut; puis deboute le siege sus terre, et teigne on la femme, qu’elle ne chiece au deboutement; et se li mains n’i puet entrer, et li enfes muert, si li cope les mains au couteil qui est ci devant mis, et estrai l’enfant, et ramoine igalment.	And if they come out with both hands, you should gently and gradually reposition them; and if they cannot enter, place the woman on a chair, and lift her legs up; then remove the chair from under her, and shave the woman so she doesn't defecate during childbirth; and if the hands cannot enter, and the baby has died, cut off with the knife that was prepared beforehand, extract the child, and reposition them equally.
de l’issue de l’enfant sus ses piés	From the birth of the child above its feet
Quant li enfes vient sus ses piez, si lou covient bouter en haut; et puis le torne poc et poc, tant qu’il soit igalz; puis preigne I des piez et l’estende poc et poc.	When the child comes above its feet, it should be turned up; and then turn it slowly and slowly until it is even; then lift the legs and extend them slowly.
Cant il saut jusc’as cuixes, si la comande a preindre, et la fai esternuer de condisi; si saut fuer, se Deus vuet.	Can it jump up to the thighs, if you command it, and make it snort with concern; if it jumps further, may God will it.
Et s’il n’ist fuer si com nos avons dit, si le torne poc et poc, tant qu’il soit selonc la figure natureil.	And if it is not as we have said, if you gently turn it bit by bit, until it is according to the natural figure.
Car adonques ist il legierement.	And then it should be done lightly.
Et s’il ne vient fuer si com nos avons, dit si pren muscillaige de altee, et oile de sisament, et gomme fondue, et broie tout en I mortier; et met sus la nature de la femme dedens et defuer cest oignement, puis la fai seoir en aigue tede jusque desoz les costelz; et quant elle est moillifie desoz, se li fai I coliere de mirre, et li met desoz, et li laisse une houre; puis la fai seoir sus I siege, puis la fai esternuer et estraint sa bouche et son neis, et li preint le ventre legierement, car li enfes saut maintenant.	And if it doesn't jump as we described, tell to use the altitude powder and oil of frankincense, and dissolved gum, and grind everything in a mortar; then apply this ointment inside and outside her body, after that make her sit in hot water until she reaches under her ribs; and when she is well saturated, have her wear myrrh necklaces and leave them on, allowing one hour; then make her sit on a stool, make her snort and restrain her nose and mouth, gently rub her stomach, for now the child jumps.
de l’issue de l’enfant sus ses genous	from the issue of the child at its knees
Quant li enfes vient en ceste forme, si i mette li baile ses mains poc et poc; puis soit sovinee sus son col, et li pendent li piez aval, et soit gisans sor I lit; et plie ses mains poc et poc, et puis li preint les mains sus lou ventre, et li oste les cussins desoz, tant qu’elle soit appareillie aval; et se li enfes ne saut, si pren ses piez et li muef forment, puis li muef lou ventre amont, puis i boute tes mains; et ewe l’enfant poc et poc; et comande a la femme qu’elle se preigne tant que li enfes isse.	When the child comes in this form, if one places its hands little by little; then be firm on its neck, and let it hang down its legs below, and lie flat on the bed; and bend its hands a little bit, then take its hands under its belly, and lift up its buttocks until she is below; and should the child not jump, if one takes its feet and moves them forcefully, then move its head towards its belly, then I put my hands in; and pull the baby gently; and command the woman to pray as long as the child comes out.
de l’issue de l’enfant qui vient dou large une main pendant	from the birth of the child which comes with one hand wide open
I covient engignier a ramener la main: s’on ne la puet ramener, si fai lever la femme, et aler; s’elle ne puet aler, si la fai gesir sus I lit, et li deboute les jambes forment; puis amenistre lou muscillaige que j’ai conteit; et s’elle n’enfante, si la fai seoir sus I siege, puis estudie au rameneir la main; et ewe l’enfant selonc la figure natureil, et la fai esternuer, et li comande qu’elle se preigne tant que li enfes isse fuer.	It's necessary to engineer a way to bring back the hand: if one can't bring it back, make the woman stand up and move around; if she can't move, have her sit flat on the bed, and force out her legs. Then follow the massage technique I've described; and should she not give birth, make her sit on a chair, then prepare to guide back the hand; and pull the baby according to its natural form, and make her sneeze, commanding that she pray until the child is born fully.
de l’issue de l’enfant sus son col, et ait espandues ses mains, et sa faice tornee devers lou dos sa mere	From the birth of the child on its neck, and it spreads its hands, and its face turned towards the back of its mother's.
I covient que li baile teigne sa main, puis le torne poc et poc, et l’ewe legierement; et quant il est igalz, si met sus la nature muscillaige de altee et oile, si com nos avons dit, puis li comande qu’elle se mueve poc et poc; et quant tu avras ce fait, si la fai seoir sus I siege, et li comande k’elle se preigne; et la fai esternuer.	It is necessary that you cure her hand, then turn it gradually and gently, and let her move it lightly; when it becomes even, place it on the natural muscular slope of elevation and oil, as we have said, then instruct her to move it gradually; and once this is accomplished, make her sit down, and command her to pray; and have her snort.
de ceste meisme maniere a tout la secondine	In this same manner for all the second part
Quant il vient fuer en ceste maniere a tout la secondine, si cope la secondine a ton ungle, tant que li moistors soit vuidie; et se li enfes pent sus sa faice et sus son col, si la cope des la boude, qu’elle ne soit retenue, et muere li enfes; puis boute l’enfant dedens, tant que tu l’aies mis si com il covient, et comande a la femme qu’elle se preigne aucune fois: adonques si istra legierement.	When it proceeds in this manner through the entirety of the second stage, if one cuts off the second stage until under her nail, as long as the moisture is drained; and should it descend to her face and neck, cut from the belly so that it's not held back, and the child doesn't die; then expel the child inside, as you put him in such way, and make the woman pray at every moment: thus gently move her.
de l’issue des gemelz	from the issues of twins
Saiches que gemeil naissent maintes fois, et aucune fois en naissent .iij. ou .iiij.; et ceu n’est mie estrainge chose, et poc avient.	Know that twins are born many times, and sometimes three or even four; this is not an uncommon thing, it just happens.
Dui sont estrainge chose, et ne vivent mie, se poc nom; je sai ceu, qu’il soient multipliiet, et sont desevrez par lou syfac qui les devise, qui est liiez a la boude; et aucune fois issent ausi naturelment com uns tous sous, si com nos avons dit.	Two things are removed and do not live anymore, if that is what you mean; I know this much, they multiply and are expelled by the syphilitic disease which afflicts them, which is bound to the womb; and they sometimes emerge as naturally as all others together, just as we have said.
Et s’il issent griement, si la cure si com nos avons dit, et soit li baile subtilz, et faice tost et legierement ceu qu’elle fait; et faice ensi com il vaut mues a salut.	And if they come out painfully, as we have said for treatment, and the fetus is subtle, perform that action immediately and lightly as she does it; do so in such a way as to promote healing.
de plusors enfans	of many children
Aucune fois sont formez en la marris I ou II ou III ou IIII ou V ou VI ou VII, ou plusors jusc’a XV, et sont tout formeit en forme d’enfant par le mesurement dou saige glorious, et couvient que li baile saiche tout ceu, car par aventure semblans chose li avient; si faice selonc ceu qu’il covient.	They are not formed after the months I, II, III, IV, V, VI, VII or more up to XV. Instead, they all take on the form of an infant according to the measurement of their size, and it is necessary that the midwife know this, for such a thing might happen by chance; do so following what is appropriate.
de l’enfant mort	Of the dead child
Quant tu cures la femme de l’enfant mort ou ventre, si com j’ai dit en la division, et il ne vient fuers, et tu es constrains d’ovraige de mains; si covient que tu saiches se li femme est de saine vertut, et n’ait accident ou elle ait paor de mort; si covient que li femme soit sovinee sus son dos, et soit ses chiés enclins aval, et les jambes levees; et li ministre la teigne de II pars, ou elle soit liie au lit si qu’elle ne soit traite au dessendement de l’enfant; si fiche les oncines en ses eulz ou en son col ou en sa bouche ou en som palais ou desoz la barbe ou en la forcele ou pres des costez, et se li dessendemens est sus piez, se li fiche ou poignil et as costes moienes; et c’est li forme de l’oncine:	When you care for the woman with a dead fetus or in her abdomen, as I have said in division, and if it doesn't come out, and you are forced to intervene manually; then it is necessary that you know whether the woman has healthy vitality, and does not have fear of death; then it is necessary that the woman be strong on her back, and have her shoulders lowered, and her legs raised; and place the minister at half an inch from the bed if she needs to deliver the fetus there; then rub the mouth of the pregnant woman with moist oil using rosemary and fenugreek seeds and flaxseed; then smear her hands with these oils and these spices; then apply them lightly to her, then take care that the fetus is prepared for its descent through her body; if you place the spices in her belly or on her neck or in her mouth or at the back of her throat or under her beard or near her collarbone, and if it is a natural birth, place the spice near her heels; and it is necessary to cut the spice with your right hand, put the groove between her left fingers of your hand, and apply them lightly throughout your hand, and place the spice in none of these places that we have mentioned until it reaches the empty state; puis fiche encontre I autre oncine, ou le tier se tu en as mestier, si que li estractions soit igalz; et puis l’estent igalment en movant d’une part et d’autre, por mues issir, et soit li oncines dentez por mues tenir, si com ci est li forme:	Then find the second bone, or any other in your skill range, so that the extractions are equal; and then move them evenly from one side to the other, for muscles to emerge, and ensure the bones are sharp enough to hold during extraction, as this is how it should be done:
Et s’il en demoure une partie, si oigne li baile aucuns de ses dois d’oile, et les boute en celle partie, et traie l’autre partie; et s’il en i demoure point, si met cest oncine ou plus haut leu, et fai ceu tant qu’il s’en isse tout fuers.	And if any part remains, if oil is found under some of its ribs in that area, place them in this part and pull the other part; and if there's no remaining part, place this bone or higher up, and do this until it exits completely.
Et se l’une mains vient devant l’autre, et il ne puet ramener por l’estreignement, si covient que tu envoloupes sus I drapeil, tant qu’il isse tote; puis la cope en la jointure de la plante ou au coute, et ensi covient que tu faices en l’autre main, et as II piés.	And if one hand comes forward of the other, and it cannot be brought back by squeezing, you should wrap around the affected area until it exits completely; then cut in the joint at the bottom or at the ankle, and similarly do this with the other hand, and for both feet.

And if the child's head is large and it is blocked in the exit, or it has an acute chief assembled together, then you should poke through the spiny burs between your fingers, and flatten the head and remove the sharp part; or you will find it at the tool called 'almidach', from which the shape comes with the tools that follow this chapter; and in this manner make the child pass naturally with a large head. And then pull out the bones with the tongs, and if the exit twists and forces are used until the moisture is out; and if it cannot come out, you must cut it piece by piece as much as you can; and if it swells around the stomach or below the ribs, then you should pierce it up to where the moisture runs.
Et se li enfes est sus ses piez, si est li attraction legiere, et li adrecemens a la bouche de la marris est legier.	And if the child is on its feet, there's a slight pull, and the connection to the mouth of the umbilical cord is also slight.
Et s’il est estrois au ventre ou au pis, si couvient que tu l’estraies a I drapeil envoloupeit sus la main; et fent le ventre ou le pis, tant que li moistors qui i est corre; et se li autre membre sont osteit, et li chiez demoure, si boute li baile sa main em parfont de la marris, et le traie jusc’a la bouche de la marris; puis i boute I oncine ou II, et le trai fuer; et se li bouche de la marris est retrecie por aposteme chaut qui i est venus, si n’i covient mie travillier, ains covient amenistrer choses moistes et grasses; et li amenistre emplaustres, et siece en aigue mollifians et amoistans.	And if it is blocked in the belly or the udder, then you should extract it at the fold of the skin wrapped around the hand; and smooth out the belly or udder until the moisture where it resides escapes. And if another limb is osteit (a condition affecting bones) and the head remains, then grab its tail with your fingers completely covered in grease, and pull it to the mouth of the teat; then you grab the third or fourth finger, and pull it forcefully; and if the opening of the teat has narrowed due to pus that came before, then there's no need for scraping; instead, things that are moist and greasy should be administered. Et se li enfes est sus son costeit, et tu le pues mettre igal, si amenistre ceu que nos avons dit en l’enfant vif; et s’on nen ait pooir, si lou trai fuer par pieces, et n’i laissier rien de la secondine.	And if the fetus is under its ribs, and you can make it even, then apply what we have said in the live infant case; and if you cannot do that, then guide it piece by piece, and leave nothing of the second part.
Et quant tu avras ce fait, se li amenistre ceu que nos avons dit ens apostemes chaus que vienent en la marris; et se decorremens de sanc vient, si soit mise en aigue restraignant, et li amenistre autres cures.	And once you have done this, apply what we have said concerning abscesses when they occur in the groin; and if blood discharge comes, then place it under water restriction, and apply other treatments.
Et je vis une femme en cui ventre uns enfes avoit esteit mors, puis consut .i. autre sus celui, et refut mors li autres.	And I saw a woman who had borne an offspring that was dead, and then another one on him, and he revived the other.
Aprés lonc tens li vint uns apostemes en la boude, et enfla tant qu’il ovrit, et comensa a grant porreture.	After a long time, an abscess came in his belly, and it swelled so much that he opened up, and began to have severe pain.
je fui apelez a la cure, et i pensai lonc tens, et ne pot soder li plaie.	I was summoned for the treatment, and I thought for a long time, and could not accommodate the wound.
Je mis sus emplaustre de fort attraction, et en issit uns os, et aprés aucuns jors uns autres.	I place under a strong attraction, and out comes one bone, and after some days another.
Je me mervillai mout, por ceu c’ou ventre n’a point d’os.	I was greatly amazed, for this stomach has no bone.
Si pensai que c’estoit des os d’un enfant mort.	I thought it was the bones of a dead child.
Je quis la plaie, et en traï mains os, tant que li femme fut em millor point; et vesquit li femme lonc tens ensi, et issoit adés un poc de bowe dou leu; et je n’ai recordeit cest chapistre fuer que por ceu que, quant li maistres trueve une estrainge chose, qu’il i saiche mettre aide.	I wanted the wound, and in my treatment of bones, until the woman reached her best condition; and I took care of the woman for as long as this was necessary, and it was only a little later that I noticed a slight swelling around the wound. And I remember this chapter to have been taught so that when masters find an unusual thing, they know how to provide help.
dou ramener la marris a son leu	to bring the shoulder back to its place.
Ci aprés vient li forme dou pressor, a coi on ewe les livres; et a .ij. tornans as .ij. chiés des .ij. liiens.	Next comes the method of the pressure, which is described in the books; and at two turns for each of the four limbs.

et i ait une desevrance ou li ventres soit liiez, si com tu vois, et li chiez soit dedens perciez; et ait a l’un des costez II pertus, et en l’autre I; et soit li ventres ou om met les medicines d’une vessie de beste ou de parchemin, et soit perciez tout entor de menus pertus, et ait entre chescun pertus I doit d’espaice, puis boute en ces pertus I fil fort de fil crut tort en X ou enqui entor, et assemble le ventre si com est une chievre; et quant li medicine est dedens, si la lie a l’estrument devant d’un fil fort, puis clisterize; et c’est li forme dou cercle:	and if there is an obstruction in the belly so that it is intertwined, as you see, and the intestines are pierced within; then there should be two defects on one side and one on the other; and let there be a preparation for medicines of a beast's bladder or parchment, and pierce it thoroughly with small holes. There should be an equal distance of one inch between each hole, then insert one strong thread woven from raw silk into each hole in a spiral pattern up to X or even further inside, forming the belly like that of a goat; when the medicine is inside, fasten it with a sturdy string tool at the front, and then perform colostomy; this forms a circle:
Et soit li medicine ne trop chaude ne trop froide, et oint le chief dou clistere d’oile ou d’aubun d’uef, ou de semblant chose, puis le boute ens legierement; puis l’espreigne li ministres a ses II mains ensamble, tant qu’il soit toz vuis, puis estrai lou clistere, et lieve li malaides ses jambes a la paroit, et se li medicine vuet issir, si la teigne tant com il puet; et s’il dort une nuit atot, si est plus grans aide.	And let the medicine neither be too hot nor too cold, and anoint the head with oil or yolk of egg ointment or something similar, then gently rub it in. Then let the physician minister to him with his two hands together, until all is seen clearly, then remove the cyst, lift up the patient's legs at the waist, and if the medicine desires to come out, pull it out as much as possible; and if he sleeps through an entire night, that will be more significant aid.
Et se tu le clisterizes em maladie de decorrement de ventre, et li medicine se haste d’issir, si le rencomence tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if you administer it during a condition of belly obstruction, and the medicine begins to come out quickly, then continue until it's relieved.
Et se li emorroide sont ou fondement, ou aposteme, si soit li clistere ausi subtilz com por I enfant; et c’est li forme dou clistere subtil sus coi li cuir soit estraint:	And if there is bleeding or a lesion, or an abscess, even if the cyst is as delicate as that of an infant; and this is the form of a thin cyst where the skin is constrained:
des plaies	of wounds
Nos avons jai dit en la division la cure des plaies; or vos dirons les cures de mains et de medicine, selonc l’acomplissement.	We have spoken about the treatment of wounds in our previous sections; now we will discuss the treatments for hands and medicine according to their development.
Je dis que les plaies sont diverses selonc ceu qu’elles sont faites, et selonc les leus ou les plaies sont faites, et de coi elles sont faites.	I say that wounds are various depending on how they were made, and where they were made on the body, and for what reason they were made.
Les choses par coi plaies sont faites sont par gitement de piere, et taille d’espee et de couteil, ou de lance ou de fust ou de siette, ou de semblans choses; ou que sont faites selonc les leus dou cors, si com plaie que chiet sus le col, ou sus le chief, ou le peis, ou le ventre, ou le foie, et semblans membres; et je vos dirai la cure de chescune plaie, et encomencerai as plaies dou chief simples, car li remenbrance venra en son chapistre.	The things that cause injuries are due to stones, the size of a sword or knife, or spear or staff, or similar objects; or those that occur according to the parts of the body, such as a bite on the neck, or head, or breast, or abdomen, or liver, and similar organs. And I will tell you how each injury is treated, starting with simple injuries to the head, since my memory comes back in this chapter.
Je dis que quant simple plaie vient ou chief, et li os n’est brisiez, si pren garde se c’est de gitement de piere ou de semblans choses, et li cuir est toutevoie rompus et est li plaie grans, et tu doutes levement d’aposteme chaut: si le fai tantost sainier de la cephalique meismement s’il vient poc de sanc de la plaie, et soit li sainie au contraire de la partie navree; et eschuisse li malaides repletion de vin et de viandes grosses.	I state that when a simple wound appears or the head comes forward, and if there is no break in the bone, be cautious to check for stones or similar things. And let the skin remain completely ruptured and make the wound large, even when you slightly doubt the presence of pus. If only a little blood from the wound leaks out right away, then quickly apply a treatment on the cephalic side immediately if there is minimal bleeding from the wound; treat it oppositely to where the affected part is removed instead. And allow the patient's body to become full of wine and large meat.
Et s’il ne vuet sainier, si soit amenuisie sa viande, et ne boive point de vin, ne ne menjuce point de char; et met sor la plaie, se apostemes chaus i vient, coton moilliet en oile roset soulement, ou en vin stiptice; et s’il n’i a aposteme chaut, si met sus la plaie, s’elle est fresche a tout son sanc, et elle n’est muee par l’air, poudre, que je dirai un poc ci aprés; et se li ars l’ait muee, si met sus aucuns oignemens, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if he does not want to be treated, then reduce his meat intake, and do not drink wine or eat large amounts of meat; instead apply treatment directly on the wound. If pus is present in a thick form, use cotton soaked in rose oil or vinegar only; if there is no pus, treat the fresh bleeding wound by applying it, as long as it has not been thinned out by air. And if it's burnt, then apply some remedies until he heals.
Et se li plaie est grans si com de tailleure d’espee et de semblans, et les levres ne se pueent assembler par tentes, si les assemble par cousture, si com je dirai as plaies dou ventre, de la costure.	And if the wound is large like that of a sword cut and similar injuries, and the edges cannot be brought together with stitches, then bring them together by suture, as I will explain for wounds of the abdomen, through sewing.
Se li plaie est descoverte de l’os, et pent, et ne tient mais que a un poc, si le cope; puis cure la plaie de medicine, et restoure char dure en leu de cuir, et comande au malaide a mengier grosses viandes, si com testes et froment cuit, ausi com poulz, et semblans choses.	If the wound exposes bone, it will be in pain and can only hold for a short time. If surgery is performed; then treat the wound with medicine, replace tough tissue instead of skin, and instruct the patient to consume large meats, such as roosters, cooked wheat, and similar items.
Et se tu trueves ou cuir porriture, et il n’aert a l’os, si cope lou porrit tot, et giete fuer, puis le cure; et se il ait artere en la plaie ou voine, dont sans cort, et il ne puet estainchier par medicines, si quier l’artere, et se tu la trueves desloie, si la lie d’un fil; et se ceu ne profite mie, si la cauterize.	And if you find or discover gangrene, and it reaches to the bone, cut it all off, extract the pus; then treat with medication. If there is an artery in the wound or vein without a clot, and cannot be stopped by medicines, tie the artery, and if you find it dislocated, ligate it with a thread; and if this does not help, cauterize it.
Et se ces plaies sont petites et simples, si est li cure legiere: et est que tu mettes ens ceste poudre qui soude ainsois que li ars l’ait muee.	And if these wounds are small and simple, the treatment is light: and you should apply this powder that heals in such a way that the heat of fire brings it to completion.
Et li maniere de la poudre si est: pren encens une partie; sanc de dragon II parties; chalz vive III parties, et le poudre subtilment, et emple la plaie, et l’estraint forment, tant qu’elle s’aerse bien et se joigne a tout son sanc; et puis la lie bien, et la laisse sens desliier, s’elle n’enfle; car on n’oste la madicine tant qu’ele soit sanee.	And the way to make the powder is: take a part of frankincense; dragon's blood two parts; fresh ginger three parts, and finely grind them, then apply this to the wound, pressing it firmly until it dries well and joins with all its blood. Then tie it tightly, leave it undisturbed, if it doesn't swell; because you remove the medicine only when it is healed.
Et aucune fois fait on ceu de chalz soulement, quant on n’ait l’encens ne lou sanc de dragon, mais que li ars n’ait muee la plaie.	And always this is done with the charcoal alone, when one does not have the incense nor the blood of dragon, but when the art has healed the wound.
Et se li ars ait mueit la plaie, meismement en esteit, si n’i met om mie ceste poudre; mais met sus aucuns oignemens digestis, ou poulz de farine d’orge faites d’aigue et de miel, tant qu’ele giete bowe; puis le cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if the heart has healed the wound, even when it's in that state, do not apply this powder to it; but apply some digestible ointments or oat flour mixed with water and honey until it starts to heal. Then continue other treatments until it is healthy.
Et se li brisure d’os vient avec la plaie, et elle est petite, si l’estrai as pinceures subtilz; et je vos dirai ci aprés les brisures dou chief.	And if the bone fracture comes with the wound, and it is small, try to handle it with delicate forceps; and I will tell you about bone fractures below.
de la plaie dou col	from the wound around the neck.
Se plaie vient ou col et elle est simple, si n’a point de difference entre li et celi dou chief, mais se li ners dou col ou li artere est copee.	This injury occurs in or around the neck; if it is simple, there should be no distinction between this and that around the head, but if a nerve in the neck or an artery has been cut.
Se c’est li ners, si n’i a autre engien que laissier la cure, et n’i mettre nulle chose restraignant, car il nuit as ners et les fait retraire; et ne mettre sus la plaie rien froit, car li substance des ners est froide, et li continuation d’aus si est avec le cerveil, qui est li plus haus membres; mais soit li medicine souez, si com chalz lavee en aigue douce, et mellee avec oile roset, et cucie lavee ausi en aigue douce, et autres pieres de mine selonc ceste maniere, et oignemens moistes.	If it's in the nose, there is no other means but to leave the treatment alone, and not apply anything restraining; for it harms the nose and causes them to withdraw. Don't place anything cold on the wound because the substance of the nerves is cold, and this continuity is with the brain which is the highest member. But use warm medicine instead, like rose water in gentle water, mixed with olive oil and well-washed thyme leaves, and other earth minerals done similarly, and moist ointments.
Et se li plaie est grans, si la cout et lie de bendes, puis la cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if the wound is large, then sew it with bends, until it heals properly.
Et se les plaies sont parfondes et ele est chevee et pleinne de bowe, si la perce ou plus bas leu; et se li artere est copee, et decorremens de sanc en vient, si la desoivre, et la loie, et la cauterize se mestier est; et se li espinee de la gorge est copee, ou li keurs, et li conduiz est gardez, par coi la viande va, si cout le keur sus la cainne de la gorge, et ne touchier la gorge mais la remet selonc sa figure naturel; et puis l’estraint avenanment, et le laisse aucuns jors, puis le cure d’oignemens desechans tant qu’il soit sanez; et se li plaie a fait empression en l’os, si la quier; et s’il i a pieces d’os, si les trai fuers toz se tu pues, et ces que tu ne pues avoir, si laisse tant que li plaie porrisse, et soit desevree et aligie li issue; et se li plaie est fresche, si poudre sus la poudre que j’ai dit.	And if the wounds are deep and filled with blood, penetrate them or even deeper; and if an artery is severed and bleeding follows, open it, tie it off, and cauterize as needed. And if part of the spinal column is severed, or joints, keep watch on the passages where meat goes, for the meat must not touch the spine but be restored according to its natural shape; then make adjustments to fit, leave it for a few days, afterwards apply dry ointments until it heals properly; and if the wound has spread into bone, dig out whatever is possible. As for pieces of bone you cannot remove, let them alone as long as the wound heals up, and then ensure it is properly cleaned from any pus; and if the wound is fresh, apply a powder made as I have said.
Et s’il a en la plaie os et il i a fistule, si la cure ensi com j’ai dit en son chapistre.	And if there is bone in the wound and it has a fistula, treat it as described in my chapter.
de la plaie de lance ou de coutel	from the wound of a spear or a knife
Se c’est cop de lance ou de coutel, et li plaie est parfonde, si regarde se de la plaie saut ventositez cant li malaides alainne: saiches adonques que li plaie est mortelz; et s’elle n’est parfonde, et elle est fresche a tout son sanc, si n’i mettre mie a la premiere houre la poudre, ne ne la liier mie por le sanc que ne demorse em parfont, et reviegne au cuer, et ocie lou malaide; mais i met oignement atractif, et le lie II fois le jor; et se tu n’as oignement, si met en la plaie viel coton por succier fuers la moistor, et fai dormir le malaide sus la plaie III jors, ou IIII, ou plusors; si n’i venra mie spasme, ne tremor male de cuer n’estraingnemens d’alainne; et quant tu vois les bones dispositions, si saiches que li plaie est sauve.	If it's a spear or knife wound and the injury goes deep, if you observe that wind is coming out of the wound instead of blood flowing: then know that this injury is mortal. And if it doesn't go deep and it's fresh with its full blood at all times, do not apply any powder in the first hour or bind it up because blood won't flow properly throughout due to dampness, and the body will reabsorb it, giving relief to the patient; instead, put on an attractive ointment, bind it twice a day; and if you don't have ointment, place old cotton into the wound to absorb moisture. Then let the patient sleep over the wound for 3 days or more; if there are no spasms or trembling of heart or internal strain then alone, and when you see good conditions, know that the injury is saved.
Cure la donques de tentes et d’autres cures, tant qu’il soit sanez; et s’elle ne puet saner, et oevre, adés saiches que il i a fistule; si la cure si com on doit.	Heal it then with other remedies as long as there is sanity. And if she cannot heal and work, know that there is a fistula; perform the treatment accordingly.
Et se li plaie est d’incision d’espee ou de coutel, et elle est simple, ou pis ou au dos, si la cure de ceu qui est devant; s’elle est grans, de cousture; et s’elle est petite, de poudre, et s’elle est empressee en l’os, et en a copeit pieces, si quier la plaie, et les trai fuers s’il sont desevrez; et s’il ne sont desevrez, si laisse porrir la plaie, si aligera li estractions; et des autres plaies as autres membres est li jugemens si com nos avons dit.	And if the wound is an incision from a sword or knife, and it's simple, or worse, or on the back, when performing treatment for the one who is in front; if it's large, use stitches; and if it's small, use powder, and if it's contaminated within the bone, and there are pieces cut out, then handle the wound accordingly, along with removing foreign objects; and if they have been removed, allow the wound to heal naturally, which will aid in extractions; and for other wounds on other limbs, make judgments like we have said.
dou derrompement dou ventre	From the protrusion of the belly
Li derompemens dou ventre est grans et moiens et petis; de la grant plaie saut aucune fois li intestine, ou li ners des intestines, par coi li intromission d’aus; et li costure est plus malaisie, et aucune fois vaut pis li petite plaie que li grans, por ceu c’on remet plus a poinnes les intestines en, s’on ne les i remet de chaut en chaut; por ce que li intestine enflent tantost qu’il sentent le froit, si rentrent plus a poinnes, et por ceu vaut mues li moieinne plaie, por ceu c’on ramoine mues l’intestine a son leu que as autres II Et saiches que li routure dou ventre est selonc IIII manieres: les II costures communes avienent en la costure dou ventre, et li costure des autres plaies dou cors et II autres costures propres sont communes as autres plaies; et toutevoie elles sont plus propres avec la costure dou ventre, et je dirai une chescune et declairerai.	The abdominal disorders are large, medium and small; from a major wound, one might encounter the rupture of intestines, or parts of the intestines, through which foreign bodies can enter; stitching these is more troublesome and, in no case does a minor wound surpass a larger one because with larger wounds it's harder to place the intestines back properly without removing them repeatedly; because the intestines swell once they feel cold, if they're not pushed back properly, that's why smaller wounds are better than larger ones as we force the intestines into their correct position in the latter. And know that there are three ways of cutting the abdomen: The two common stitches occur at the abdominal incision and other stitches for other body parts and two other specific stitches also occur together with other types; however, they are more suitable combined with the abdominal stitch. I will mention each one separately and explain them.
Je di que quant li plaie est petite, et aucune chose de l’intestine ist fuer, et griés chose est dou remettre, ceu est par l’une des II manieres: ou por la petitece de la plaie, si com nos avons dit, ou por ce que li intestine est enflez por le froit.	I say that when the wound is small, and nothing of the intestine has been affected, and what needs to be removed can be done so easily, this can be accomplished through one of two methods: or due to the size of the wound as we have said, or because of the swelling of the intestines from cold.
Et quant il est frois, eschaufez lou en teil maniere: moillie une esponge ou I mol drapeil en aigue tede soulement, ou tu cuis en aigue squinant et cipre et spique, et arose l’intestine tant que li enfleure soit ostee; et aucune fois fait ce vins restraingnans, et est muedre que awe soule por desenfler.	And when it's cold, warm him in this way: soak a sponge or a piece of cloth with water alone, or you can cook it in water that is simmering and contains cypress and thyme, and expose the intestines until they are exposed; and do all these remedies so that this wine may be given to relieve swelling.
Et quant tu vois l’enfleure departir, si amoiste l’intestine d’aigue ou altee et malves soient cuites, car par ceu est aligie li entree a poc de chose; et s’il n’i puet entrer, si fent un poc la plaie a l’estrument de coi on cope les emorroydes; et li premiere cure est muedre que li taille, que nus n’i doit taillier sens grant necessiteit n’i ait; et c’est li estrumens por le fendre: si trenche dedens en la corbeure et defuer non, et vez ci la forme:	And when you see the swelling depart, moisten the intestines with water or broth that has been cooked well, because through this, there is a passage for very little thing; and if it cannot enter, then open up just a bit of the wound with the instrument used to cut stitches; and the first treatment is to make sure the incision isn't too large where unnecessary; and this is the tool to cut: you should cut within but not beyond the bend, and here's the shape:
Et quant li plaie est enlargie, et li intestine saut fuer, si le remet arer selonc la forme naturel en son leu propre, se tu en as pooir, car ce vaut mues.	And when the wound is enlarged, and the internal organs are displaced, if you can set it back according to its natural form in its proper place, because this counts for movement.
Quant li plaie est large, et elle est en la partie desoz lou ventre, si covient que tu faices gesir lou malaide sus son dos, et met ses jambes plus haut que son chief; et s’elle est en la partie desoz le ventre, si met le chief et le pis plus haut que les parties desoz, et ausi se li routure dou ventre est en l’une des II parties si met t’entente en ceu que li partie navree soit plus haute que li autre; et ensi covient amenistrer ceu que je dis en plaies grans et moienes.	When the wound is broad, and it's in the belly area, you should make the patient lie on their back with their legs higher than their head. And if it's in the belly area, place their head and bottom higher than the belly parts; similarly, when a ruptured stomach is divided into two halves, ensure that the part needing repair is higher than the other one; this way, you'll properly manage what I'm saying about large and medium wounds.
Es plaies petites met ceu que t’est apparilliet, puis aies entre tes mains I ministre pitous ki teigne toute la routure a sa main, et assemble les levres; et c’est la maniere commune de costures, et est que tu preignes une aguille ou plusors, selonc la quantiteit de la largesce de la plaie, puis laisse des le chief de la plaie I doi d’espaice, et i fiche une aguille ou il ait I boin fil fort; et perce les II chiés dou cuir avec les II chiés dou siphac, qui est desoz le cuir dedens, tant que tu la faices percier de celle partie, et assemble les II chief dou siphac les IIII ensamble; puis l’estrain d’un fil double entor l’aguille de II pars, puis assemble les II chiés de la plaie avenanment, et puis laisse I doi d’espaice, et i fiche une autre aguille; puis la lie dou fil si com tu as fait la premiere aguille, et ne cesser de ceu faire selonc ceu que tu as mestier des aguilles, tant que toute li plaie soit restrainte; et soient les aguilles moienes, entre subtilz et grosses, car les aguilles subtilz copent toute la char, et les trop grosses si ne pueent mie bien entrer: por ceu covient qu’elles soient moienes; et ne covient mie bouter les aguilles trop au defuer de la char et dou cuir, k’elles ne copent et oevrent la plaie devant la soudure; et puis cope les chiés des aguilles, qu’elles ne blecent lou malaide au dormir, et i met tentes ou drapelz au chiés des aguilles por mues tenir, et les laisse tant que li plaie soit soudee; et ceste maniere de costure as aguilles est plus covenauble en petites plaies, car il i soffist une aguille ou II Li seconde costure si est commune, et est que tu assemble les II chiés dou cuir et les II chiés dou syfac ensamble a une aguille ou il ait I fort fil moien; et quant tu avras perciez ces chiez toz IIII ensamble, si ramoinne l’aguille a la partie ou tu as encomenciet, en la maniere c’on cout les dras; et met d’espaice entre chescune costure la grossece d’un menor doi; ceste costure sevent li home, et je cousi une plaie c’uns hons avoit ou ventre, qui estoit navrez d’un coutel, et estoit li plaie plus d’une palme de grant, et issoit des intestines bien II palmes de grant, et estoit li plaie enmi le ventre.	For small wounds, use what is suitable for you. Have the necessary tools ready; they should cut all the way through the wound to your hand and stitch it together; this is common practice in suturing methods. Use one or more needles according to the width of the wound; leave about two inches at the start of the wound before needle; insert a needle with strong thread in that position; puncture both layers of the skin with both ends of the thread, which are inside the skin layer by layer until you've pierced through to that part, and bring together the three parts of one of the intestines; then stitch back on with a double thread through two points, then bring together the two edges of the wound, leaving about two inches, and insert another needle; then sew as you did the first needle, and continue doing so according to your need for needles until the entire wound is stitched up. The needles should be medium-sized, neither too fine nor too thick, because fine needles cut all the flesh while thicker ones don't stitch well; they shouldn't stick out from the flesh or skin much as this may prevent good sewing stitches and expose the wound before stitching. Then sew over the ends of the needles to prevent them from rubbing against the patient when sleeping; cover each needle end with cloth or bandages for proper support, and leave them until the wound has healed. This method of suturing is more suitable for small wounds as there's a second stitch made two needle lengths down the line where you bring together both skin edges and intestinal layers to one of the needles with medium thread; when you've pierced all four ends in this way, pull out the needle from where you started, just like tying knots on thread. Leave space between each stitch about an inch wide; this stitch heals the body, and I healed a wound that was made by a knife inside someone's belly; it was a large cut more than two inches long, contained several layers of intestines which were also quite big, and was located in the middle of the belly.
Je li ramenai l’intestine puis k’il ot esteit XXIIII houres fuer, et fut li plaie soudee jusc’a XV jors, et le curai, et fut sanez.	I returned his intestine to him once it had been out for twenty-four hours, and the wound was stitched up until fifteen days later. I treated it, and he recovered, and became healthy.
Et li mire l’avoient jugiet qu’il morroit, et ce fut miracle; et ne le curai mie d’oignement, car je estoie en I leu ou on n’en trovoit point, ne nule medicines; et metoie sens plus sus la plaie coton viel II fois le jor, et le lavoie d’aigue de miel tant qu’il fut sanez.	And when the doctor had judged that he was going to die, it was a miracle; and I did not treat him with ointment because there was none available in my village or any medicine. Instead, I would place old cloth on the wound twice a day and wash it with honey water until he recovered.
Or vos dirai les II propres manieres de cousture: pren l’aguille, et la boute des la partie defuers jusc’a celi dedens; quant elle a perciet le keur de droit en droit, si lai le chief dou siphac ou cousteit ou tu as bouteit l’aguille, et la fai percier d’autre part des la partie dedens jusc’a celi defuer; et li entendemens de ceste costure si est que tu cous ausi com li peletier font les pelz, et que tu laisses une fois le syfac d’une part, et le reprent d’autre, tant que li costure soit toute acomplie.	Or I will tell you two proper ways of suturing: take the needle and place it on the outer side up to inside; when it has pierced the body straight through in a straight line, place the tip near the siphon or at the point where you have inserted the needle, and make it pierce again from the inner side to that same outer part. And this method of sewing is like how the pelter sews fur, leaving one end of the siphon on one side, then picks it up on the other, until all the suturing is completed.
Li seconde maniere de costure, que Galiens dist proprement, si est si com aucun font, qui assemblent les II parties ensamble naturelment, et apploient l’un des chief dou syfac a l’autre chief, en teil maniere: fiche une aguille ou chief dou mirach prochiene, et fai percier celui leu soulement, et laisse les II chiés dou syfac; puis torne l’aguille, et la fai percier des la partie defuers jusc’a celi dedens, as II chiés dou syfac; puis fai percier l’un et l’autre des la partie defuers jusc’a celi dedens, en II autres chiés dou mirach que sont on l’autre costeit; et c’est li muedre maniere de costure et li plus commune.	The second method of suturing, as Gallien described it correctly, is such that no one does as follows: they join the two natural parts together and apply one end of silk thread to the other. The process goes like this: insert a needle or the other end of silk thread near each side; then pierce only the part above, leaving both ends of silk thread intact; afterwards turn the needle and make it pierce from below through to inside where both ends of silk thread are; then pierce both from below through to inside using two more ends of silk thread that correspond to the other sides. This is the way stitches are made in suture and the most common method.
Galiens si dist ceste parolle, et aucun le tesmoignent, c’on doit coudre le ventre a II aguilles, ou il ait fil en chescune; et doit on bouter l’une aguille d’une part, et l’autre d’autre, en la maniere de ces qui cousent corroies; et saiches que quant li routure est enmi lou ventre, si est li cousture plus griez que des autres leus dou ventre.	Galen said this word, and no one denies it, that you should stitch the abdomen with two needles or threads in each; and you must put one needle on one side and the other on the opposite side like those who sew iron. Know that when the wound is inside the abdomen, then the stitches are more painful than of others' wounds in their abdomens.
Li jugemens de la plaie si est telz com li jugemens des autres plaies: et est que quant tu trueves la plaie fresche a tout son sanc, ainsois que li ars l’ait muee, si remet arer l’intestine, et lou cout; puis met sus la poudre enjanrant char, et se li ars l’ait muee, si met sus aucun oignement que soit present, tant que li plaie bowe; et chicent li fil, et soient soudez li sifac, et li mirach; puis cure la plaie si com les autres, tant qu’il soit sanez; et se tu n’as medicines, si met sus, tantost qu’ele comance a giter bowe, coton viel, et le remue II fois le jor tant k’il soit sanez.	The judgments of the wound are such as those for other wounds: and this is that when you find the fresh wound full of blood, just like the surgeon has made it bleed, you stitch up the intestines and the cut; then apply a sealing powder on flesh. And if the surgeon has let it bleed, no ointment should be applied until the wound stops bleeding; and clean the thread, sew up the suture, and the mirror; then treat the wound like others, until it heals; and if you don't have medicines, when it starts to heal properly, use old cotton, and stir it twice a day until it is healed.
Car tu n’as mestier d’autre medicine en plusors dispositions cant les plaies sont simples; et se tu doutes que li plaie ne faice communiteit as membres principelz, si covient ke tu moilles lainne legiere en oile de tempree chalor, ou en oile roset, et la met entor les angres, et desoz les asselles; et s’il sent dolor ou porriture en bouelz, et maintes fois avient, si les clisterize de vin noir tede, et meismement se li porriture vient jusc’a l’intestine; et le perce dedens, et saiches que quant c’est li gros intestines, si est plus legier a saner que li petis.	For you do not need other medicine in various conditions if the wounds are simple; and if you doubt that the wound might cause joint issues with principal members, it is necessary for you to soak light wool in warm oil or rose oil, and place this between joints, and around the elbows. And if there is pain or gangrene in the belly areas, and such occur many times, then you should give black wine enemas several times, and especially when gangrene spreads up to the intestines; and puncture inside them, and know that when it's large intestines, it is easier to heal than small ones.
Li intestine qui est apelez «jeun» ne puet saner quant il est navrez, et c’est por la planteit des voinnes que i sont, et por la subtiliteit de tout le cors, et l’aprochement de sa nature des ners.	The intestine that is referred to as 'young' cannot heal when it's injured, and this is due to the layout of the veins around it, and the subtlety of the entire body, and its alignment with nerve nature.
Et si li zirbe saut de la plaie, si le remet arrier ausi com l’intestine, tandis qu’il est fres; et s’il est vielz et devenus vers ou noir, si covient que tu lies le leu qui est noir, que decorremens de sanc n’i viegne, car il i a voinnes et arteres; puis cope ceu qui est entre le liien, et met les II chiés pendans des la partie desoz la plaie jusque defuer por aligier l’estraction quant li zirbes chiet, et li plaie bowe.	And if the pus jumps out of the wound, then reset it back in place just like a fresh intestine would be done; and if it is old and turned towards or black, then it's necessary that you tie the dark part, so no bleeding occurs from there, because there are veins and arteries; then cut what lies between the knot, and put both ends up under the wound area until beyond for easing the extraction when the pus jumps out, and the wound heals.
de la routure dou boueil	of the rupture of the boil
Quant li intestine est rons, et li plaie est petite, si la puet on restorer en aucuns homes, por ceu que je vis que uns hons fut navrez ou ventre d’une lance; et estoit li plaie au destre de l’estomac, et fut envillie et devint fistule, et en issoit li egestion et li ventositez; je i mis cure selonc ceu que je poi, et ne cessai de subtilier tant qu’il fut sanez, et li leus soudez.	When the intestine is torn and the wound is small, it may be restored in some ways, because I witnessed that a man was wounded by a lance or in the belly; and there was the wound on the right side of the stomach, which became fistulous, causing expulsion and wind. I treated the wound according to my knowledge and continued to refine the treatment until it healed properly, and sewed up the edges.
Et quant je le vis souder, je doutai que li malaides n’eust mal en son ventre; et il n’i ot point de mal, mais demora en millors dispositions, et menjans et bevans; et dirent aucun experimentors que quant il a petite plaie en l’intestine, qu’il doit estre liiez en teil maniere: pren fremis a grans testes, puis assemble les levres de la plaie, et quant li fremis ait overte la bouche, si la met sus les II levres, si qu’elle estraigne sa bouche sus; et puis li cope la teste, et ce se tient si qu’il ne puet desliier, puis met I autre fremit aprés en celle maniere que devant, tant que li plaie soit toute porprise; et cout la plaie.	And when I saw it being sealed up, I wondered if the patient might be suffering in his belly. There was no harm, but he remained in better states, eating and drinking; and told some experimenters that when he has a small injury inside the intestine, he must be bound like this: take a large testicle, then join together the edges of the wound, and when the testicle has opened its mouth, place it between the two edges, so that she forces her mouth on it; and then pinch the head, and hold it in such a way that it cannot come undone, then put another testicle after this manner as before, until the whole wound is filled; and like this the wound.
Cil chief si s’aerdent en l’intestine, et ne vient nulle nuisance au malaide, et se puet on liier l’intestine d’un fil subtil qui est copez de l’intestine d’une beste, en teil maniere: pren le chief de cest fil d’intestine que soit mout descharnez, et puis lie au chief de cest fil I fil de lin subtil tort, puis boute le fil en l’aguille, et en cout l’intestine, et le ramoinne en la routure; et ceste maniere de costure de fremis nen est fuers que selonc la voie de fiance et d’esperance; et se li plaie est grans et large, meismement quant elle est en l’un des grailes intestines, si n’i a engien ne santeit, fuer que subtiliteit.	And if it gets into the intestine and causes no harm to the patient, one can tie the intestine with a thread that is cut from the intestine of an animal in this way: take the beginning of this intestinal thread so that most of it is uncharred, then attach the thread's thin line twist to the beginning of this thread, then insert the thread into the needle and sew through the intestine, then fasten it in the wound; and this sewing method with intestinal threads is only done according to the way of hope and expectation; and if the wound is large and wide, especially when it is in one of the larger intestines, there's no harm or disturbance because of its subtlety.
de fistule ou qu’ele soit	regarding a fistula, or if it exists
Saiches que toute plaie ou aposteme, quant il enveillist, si est apelee universement «fistule», et meismement quant elle est chevee et rent bowe.	Know that any wound or abscess, as it matures, is universally called "fistula", and even when hair grows there and the swelling recedes.
Et fistule est selonc la verteit nodation fautree dure et blainche, ou on ne sent dolor, et est ausi chevee com li penne d’un oiseil; et aucune fois en saut clere bowe, et autre fois espesse; aucune fois poc, et autre fois assez; et je en ai jai parleit en la division des plaies, que toute plaie que n’est sanee, et il n’i a char, ce n’est fuers que par une des VIIII causes: c’est a savoir, par la petitece dou sanc ou cors; ou por sa malice; ou por ceu qu’il i a char dure dedens, et sus les levres, que n’i laisse naistre char; ou il i a trop de bowe; ou li leus est porris, et li matiere est de male qualiteit; ou li medicine n’est mie bone en la cure; ou por ceu que li corruption est maniere de pestilence; ou por la proprieteit en la region est tardive li digestion, et tarde li santeit, et enflee par nature; ou il i a voinnes ou os: et j’ai ja mostreit toutes ces causes, et les signes, et les cures de medicines en la division.	And fistula is according to the genuine node hard and whitish in color, where no pain is felt, and it also grows hair like a bird's feather; sometimes with clear swelling, and at other times thick; sometimes scarce, and at other times sufficiently so. And I have spoken about this under the division of wounds, that any wound which has not healed, and there is no pus, exits only through one of the eight causes: namely, due to the smallness of blood or pus; or because of its malignancy; or because there is hard pus inside, and on the lips, which does not allow pus to emerge; or because there is too much swelling; or because the veins are dilated, and the material is of bad quality; or because the medicine was not properly administered in treatment; or due to the manner of the infection being contagious; or due to natural digestion being slow in that region, leading to delayed health improvement, and bursting out by nature; or if there are veins or bones present: and I have already shown all these causes, as well as their signs and treatments under the division.
Or covient que je te faice a savoir la cure de fistule qui est faite par oevre de mains.	So, it is necessary for me to inform you about the treatment of an abscess which is performed by manual work.
Saiches que fistule avient en tous membres dou cors; car il i a fistules que vienent as grans voines, et as arteres, et as ners, ou au syfac, ou a l’intestine, ou a la vessie, ou a aucunes des costes, ou a l’espinee dou dos, ou a aucune jointe des mains ou des piez; et si a teil que vient a la proprieteit dou membre principeil, et as semblans leus.	You should know that fistulas occur in all parts of the body; for there are fistulas that come from large veins and arteries, and nerves, or in the throat, or intestines, or bladder, or any one of the ribs, or the spine, or any joint on hands or feet. And if it happens to affect the property of the main limb, and shows their symptoms.
Et toutes les fistules que sont de ceste maniere sont de grief sanation, et n’i a fors que labour, et ignorance; et se il i a aucune fistule que ne veigne mie jusc’a leu que j’ai dit, et tu as fiance de la cure, et tu la vues conoistre, si pren une tente d’arain ou de fer, se li fistule est droite, si la quier; et se li fistule est torte, si la cerche d’une subtil tente de plonc, car li plons se ploie mues entor la tortuositeit; et se li fistule a mains pertus et tu ne la pues mie bien cerchier par tentes, si la clisterize par l’un des pertus, car la moistors si cort d’un pertus a autre, et la mundifie; puis la quier saigement a ton pooir, que tu conoisses s’il i a os ou nerf, et est chevee em parfont, et demande bien au malaide de la dolor qu’il sent au presser de ta main, et le leu ou il la sent; et quant tu savras vraiement le leu ou elle est, et s’elle est loing de jointure, ou de nerf, ou d’artere ou de voine, ou en aucuns des leus que je t’ai dit, si la cope selonc ceu que je t’ai dit, et oste fuer la fautreure et les chars corrumpues que sont dedens; et puis la cure tant qu’elle soit sanee, et se li fistule est bien parfonde de droit endroit, si covient que tu copes em parfont, tant com tu pues, puis i met tentes moillies en medicine ague, et les boute jusc’au chief de la fistule, tant que li medicine corrode la superfluiteit qui est demoree au fons; et puis i met oignemens enjanrans sainne char, tant qu’il soit sanez; et s’il n’est sanez par ceu, si le cauterize si com nos avons dit, et se li os est corrompus de la fistule, si le cope.	And all the fistulas in this manner cause dissatisfaction with healing, and there are only labor and ignorance; and if there is any fistula that does not reach as far as what I have said, and you have begun the treatment, and you understand it, then take an arachnid or iron tent. If the fistula is straight, take it; and if the fistula is bent, find a subtle plunger tent because the plungers bend according to their tortuousness; and if the fistula has lost its ends and you can't properly search for it by tents, flush it through one of the ends since moisture flows from one end to another, then cleanse. Then search wisely with your power where you know whether there is bone or nerve, and passes through completely, ask well from the patient how much pain they feel when your hand presses on it, and specify the place where they sense it; and once you truly understand where it is and that it's not near a joint, a nerve, an artery or vein, or any of the places I mentioned, if it follows as I have said, remove the pus and rotten flesh that are inside; and then continue with treatment until fully healed. If the fistula was deeply set in its correct place, it is proper to remove it completely as much as you can, then fill it with wet tents soaked in medicine, and keep them up to the root of the fistula until the medicine corrodes what remains at the bottom; and then apply healing ointments that promote new flesh growth, until it heals. If it does not heal by this means, cauterize it as we have said, and if the bone is corrupted by the fistula, remove it.
Se voinne ou ners ne te greve ou membres principelz, si com nos avons dit; et se li os est descovers, et il i a corruption et noiror, si lou reis tant que li corruption soit toute ostee, puis le cure de choses enjanrans char tant qu’il soit sanez; et s’il n’est sanez, et rent bowe si com devant, saiches que tu n’es mie alez jusc’a font: si descuevre et quier tant que tu soies au fons, et oste toute la corruption, puis restore le leu; et s’il est ensi sanez, c’est bien.	If the vein or nerves are not obstructed or the main limbs, as we have said; and if the bone is exposed, and there's decay and darkness, you should only cure until the decay has been removed in entirety. Then remove all infected flesh while it remains clean; and if it doesn't remain clean, perform surgery again as before, knowing that you must go no further than this point: keep digging out and cleaning until you reach the bottom, removing all the decay, then set the limb back into place; and if it is thus healed afterwards, it's well done.
Se ceu non, saiches que la corruption est trop en parfont, que tu n’i pues avenir; si n’i a autre engien que dou lassier a nature; et s’il i a i petit os corrumput, et tu le pues traire as tenailles, si l’estrai a I estrument covenauble a ceu, et s’il i a maint os, si les trai trestoz, ne n’en laissier nes un; et se li moistor te fait contraire, et il n’i a error ne paour, si cope et moistor et char, et delivre les os.	If it's not that way, know that the corruption has gone too far, you can't proceed any further; if there is no other choice but to let nature take its course. And if there's a small corrupted bone, and you can remove it with tongs, do so using an appropriate instrument for this task. If there are multiple bones affected, remove them all, don't leave any behind. And if moisture makes this difficult, and there is neither error nor fear, then fight against the moisture and flesh, free the bones.
Et se tu ne les pues oster a une houre, si met sus la plaie chose enjanrant porriture, et laisse tant que li leus soit porris entor les os, et adonc si avront plus legierement les os; et se c’est uns grans os, si com de jambe ou de cuisse, si reis tant soulement la corruption tant que li noiror soit toute ostee, puis restoure la plaie; et s’il en i a grant partie dou corrumput, et vient jusc’a mole de l’os; si le covient soier et coper tout jusc’a la corruption, et puis le cure tant qu’il soit soudez; et je te dirai d’une fistule qui avint I home en sa jambe, si que tu i preignes exemple et aide en ton ovraige.	And if you can't remove them within an hour, place something stimulating pus on the wound, and let it stay until the flesh is completely putrid inside the bone, and then they will break more easily; and if it's a large bone, such as from a leg or thigh, only allow the corruption until all of the blackness is removed, then heal the wound; and if there's a substantial part of the corruption reaching up to the bone; you should treat everything up to the corruption completely, and then treat it until it heals; and I will tell you about a fistula that occurred in a man's leg, so you can take this as an example and guidance for your work.
Il fut I jovencelz entor XXX ans, qui ot une dolor en sa jambe d’une cause que vint dedens le cors, tant que les matieres vinrent a la jambe, et fut enflee d’un gros aposteme, et n’ot point de cause defuer por ovrir; mais li mire par lor folie ovrerent tant sus que li apostemes ovri, et en corroient mout de matieres, et devint fistule, et i vint mout de pertus que tuit gitoient bowe et moistor dou cors; et maint mire i mirent cure entor II ans, et n’i ot nul saige en l’art de mains, tant que je i fui apelez, et vi sa jambe et les medicines dont on le curoit, et ceu que corroit par les pertus a grant cors; et devenoit rouges li cors dou jouvenceil, et avoit color citrine.	There was a young man around thirty years old, who had pain in his leg due to something coming from within the body, such that the substances reached the leg and caused an abscess. They were operated on extensively until the pus came out, and they ate away much tissue, turning into a fistula, and a great deal of pus came out causing much heat and moisture throughout the body; and many doctors operated for two years without any knowledge in the art of manual medicine, until I was called upon to see his leg and the medicines that were being used on him, and what was corroding through the pus had great heat. And became red again from youth's complexion, and had a yellowish coloration.
Je boutai une tente en l’un de ces pertus, et puis cerchai toz les pertus, et trovai que li uns venoit encontre l’autre de toutes les parties de la jambe.	I set up a tent at one of these hollows, and then searched all the hollows, finding that some came against each other from every part of the leg.
Je me hastai donques, et copai en l’un des pertus tant que je descovri une partie de l’os, et le trovai corrumput et perciet, et venoit li corruption jusc’a l’os dedens; je soiai ceu qui m’aparissoit de l’os corrumput, et cuidai qu’il n’i eust autre corruption, fuer que celi que je ostai; et comensai a restourer la plaie de medicines sodans par lonc tens, et ne pot souder; et puis rencomensai, et descovri l’os si com devant, et trovai la corruption continuee en l’os, et la soiai, et puis l’ostai, et me penai de souder le leu; mais je ne pou tant que je copai entor une palme de l’os, et le traï fuer a tout son mole, puis le restourai de medicines; et il fut sanez et soudez hastanment, et ne covint plus rencomencier l’ovraige fors por la foibleté dou malaide, qui ne pooit soffrir, et por la paour de mort que je avoie de lui.	I hurriedly proceeded and dug out a hollow until I uncovered part of the bone. I found that it was corrupted and perforated; the corruption had reached into the bone itself. It seemed to me that there was no other corruption besides what I removed, since that's all I could see from the bone. I began treating the wound with medicine for an extended period without trying to stitch it up. Then I resumed, uncovering the bone as before and found that the corruption continued within the bone. It appeared to me and then I removed it; I attempted to suture the wound but was unable to because I could only manage until a palm's breadth of bone was exposed. I operated on its entire depth afterwards, then tried to sew it up using medicine. The treatment was successful and the wound healed quickly without needing to restart the work due to my fear of death from the patient's weakness.
Car por l’evacuation sanglotoit sovent, mais il fut sanez entierement, et nasquit en leu de l’os une char dure, et fut de bone disposition et n’ot point de nuisement ne de contraire dou tout en tout, ne a l’aleir ne a venir.	For during blood evacuation, it often happens, but it was completely healed. In the place of the bone came hard flesh, and it had good consistency with no harm or opposition throughout, neither outside nor inside.
Et se li os est brisiez en aucun leu dou cors, si le covient soier en ceste maniere: pren I liien, et l’estrain au chief de l’os qui apert, et comande aucun k’il l’estende en haut; et met I autre lien de lainne plus gros dou premier liien, et le lie sus la char qui est desor l’os, et estent le chief, si que tu traies la char corrumpue au desoz, et descuevre la char sus le leu ou tu vues soier, que li soie ne blece la char; et met I tison ou une tauble desoz l’os por mues coper la char corrumpue; et covient tant soier com on puet veoir et sentir la corruption, et soier ancor autre fois.	And if the bone is broken in any part of the body, if it should be treated like this: take hold of it, and stretch out the end of the bone that is exposed, commanding it to extend upwards; and tie a thicker string than the first one with another piece of cloth on the decayed flesh around the bone, stretching the tip so that you pull away the decaying flesh underneath, revealing the healthy flesh where you want the bone to be without hurting it; put a poker or board under the bone to cover the decayed flesh; and treat until as much corruption can be seen and felt, treating again if necessary.
Et se li os est corrumpus, et n’apert mie, et li corruptions est en mileu ou en une partie, si descuevre la char toute; puis met I tison desoz, et puis soie des l’une partie a l’autre la corruption, et soit li soieure dou lonc de la corruption I poc, si com nos avons dit; et se li corruptions est en la jointure, si cope la jointure corrumpue, et soie l’os ou elle contient de l’autre part; et se li corruptions est en la continuation des II jointes, si n’i a autre angien que dou coper; et se li corruptions est ou poignil de la main, ou ou poignil dou piet, si est mout fort celle chose, mais toutevoie il covient que tu enquieres celle corrosion, coment elle t’apert; et la mundifie en toutes les manieres que tu pues, mais que li voine ou li nerf ne te faicent contraire; et saiches que li incisoire et les soies por coper ces os sont maintes, selonc l’assise des os et l’aparance d’ous, et lor grossece et lor subtiliteit, et lor grandor et lor petitece, et lor duresce; et por ceu covient il apareillier a chescune semblance d’ovraige son estrument; et saiches que l’uevre te moustrera l’estrument dont tu avras mestier, selonc la conissance de cest art, et le tesmoignaige des manieres des maladies; si porpense l’estrument dont tu as mestier selonc ceu qu’il le covient.	And if the bone is corrupted and does not open, and the corruption is in its middle or part of it, then remove all flesh; afterwards place a brand over it, and from one side to the other, let the corruption be done by heat, and make that this burning last long enough so it can consume up until the core of the corruption, as we have said; and if the corruption is at the joint, cut out the corrupted joint's bone structure, and replace with a new one on the other side; and if the corruption is in the continuation of two joints, there should be no intervening bone but to cut through both sides; and if the corruption is near the finger or toe nail tips, it will be very tough work indeed but still you must identify that corrosion, according to how it opens; then cleanse using every method possible while avoiding injuring the vein or nerve; know that cutting into bones and making cuts varies greatly based on bone structure and appearance, its size and delicacy, as well as its bulkiness and fineness, and hardness; for this reason you should have tools suited for each form of work in your arsenal; and remember that practice will show you the tools needed according to knowledge of this craft and evidence provided by diseases' symptoms; so consider which tool is necessary based on what it requires.
dou feu	with fire
Li chiés porrissent ou par cause dedens, ou par cause defuer; et quant tu avras medicinee celle corrosion par la cure des medicines, et il ne profitent mie, si covient coper celui membre jusques au leu ou li corrosion vient, si que li malaides eschaipe par ceu de la mort, ou par la malice, qui est plus grans, de la defaute dou membre; et li signes si est que li membres devient noir, si qu’il semble qu’il soit ars dou feu, et porrist aprés la noiror, pues va celle corrosions de membre em membre, et prent par tout le cors; si te haste dou coper, et se c’est par la percussion d’aucunes venimouses bestes, si com scorpion de mer et wivre et semblans, se li corrosion est au chief dou doi, si le cope, et ne li doner mie espaice de venir jusc’a la main.	The shoulder joints hurt either due to inner causes or outer reasons; and when you have treated that corrosion through medicine application but it doesn't improve, then it's necessary to cover this member until the source of corrosion comes, so that the disease escapes via death or some other greater mischief from the fault in the limb; and if any signs are present, these include the limbs turning black, as if they were burnt by fire, and afterwards there appears this corrosion spreading throughout the body, taking it over completely; so you must hasten to cover it.
