If it's due to hitting with some venomous animal such as sea scorpion, snake etc., when the corrosion is at the head of the spine, then hit it, and don't give any space for it to reach up to the hand.
Et s’elle vient jusc’a la main, si la cope a la jointe, si que la corrosion ne viegne jusc’a bras; et s’elle vient au bras, si le cope au coute; et s’elle passe le coute, c’est li mors, et n’i vaut amenistremens fuers que li quantitez de sa vertut; et tot ensi fai quant li corrosion vient ou piet: s’elle vient en la premiere jointe, si la cope aprés l’autre jointe; et s’elle vient ou piet, si cope tout le piet; et s’elle monte en la jambe, si cope a la jointure dou genoil; et s’elle vient desus le genoil, si n’i a autre engien que dou lassier le malaide a mort; et li maniere dou coper ou dou soier le membre si est que tu le lie desus et desoz, et estende uns menistres l’un des liiens aval, et uns autres ministres l’autre liien amont, et tu dessevre la char qui est entre les II liiens a I spatumile large, tant que li os soit descovers; puis le cope ou soie, et met de chescune part I drapeil de lin, si que li soie ne touche le leu sain, et viegne au malaide autre lesion et aposteme chaus.	And if it reaches up to the hand, when you cover at the joint, so that the corrosion doesn't reach up to the arm; and if it comes in the arm, when you hit on the blade; and if it passes the blade, then it's death, and only outside help remains but as much as its power has; and similarly do for whenever corrosion comes or pierces: if it comes in the first joint, after this other joint; and if it comes in any part, cover every part of that; and if it ascends to the leg, when you hit at the joint of the knee; and if it comes over the knee, there is no other way than to let the patient die; and the method of covering or curing the limb involves tying it up above and below, stretching a piece of linen on one side of the ligature down, and another piece on the other side upwards, and you cut off the flesh that lies between these two threads till the bone is exposed; then cover or cure it, and place one strip of linen from each side, so that the cure doesn't touch the healthy part, and causes no further damage or pus to spread.
Et se decorremens de sanc vient quant tu oevres, si cauterize le leu hastanment, ou tu met sus aucunes poudres restraignans; puis revien a ta medicine tant qu’elle soit acomplie, puis lie le membre navreit d’un liien covenauble, et le cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et je te conterai k’il avint a I home en som piet: il li avint une noiror qui sembloit arsure de feu, et celle corrosion vint premier en son doi dou piet, tant qu’elle porprist tout le piet; et quant li hons vit la corrosion, si se hasta de coper le piet, et fut sanez; et lonc tens aprés li revint li corrosion ou doi de la main, et il vint a moi, et je li mis sus choses repercussives aprés la mundification dou cors, et ne pot cesser li corrosions; et il vot que je li copasse la main, et je ne vou, que je avoie esperance de repercuter la matiere; et doutai ausi que se je tailloie sa main, qu’il ne morist, car li vertus de l’ome estoit foible; et il se despera toz, et revint en sa terre, et se hasta de coper sa main, et fut sanez; et je n’ai ceu conteit fuers que por ceu c’on faice autreteil, s’on en a mestier.	And when there is bleeding during your work, if you encounter a cautery, quickly cauterize the wound or apply powder to control it; then return to your medicine until its completion. Then tie the injured limb with a reliable bandage and treat it until it heals properly. And I will tell you what happened to that man: he had a blackness that seemed like a fiery sureness, and this corrosion first appeared in his heel of his foot, consuming everything down to his toe; when he saw the corrosion, he tried to protect his foot, and healed soon after. And for a long time afterwards, the corrosion returned below his hand, and came to me, and I applied things that would cause a rebound of matter after bodily purification, but could not stop the corrosion completely. He insisted that I cut off his hand, but I refused as I had hope in being able to rebound the matter; I also feared that cutting off his hand might make him bleed to death since his body's health was weak; he lost all hope and returned to his land, trying to protect his hand, and healed. This story is told only for those who might need it elsewhere.
Aucune fois vient aposteme en leu charnut, et demore si longement qu’il fait grant assemblee de bowe; et puis ront et perce, et en saut li bowe, et demoure li leus vuis, ausi com uns vasselz; et li cuir qui est desus est ausi subtilz com I drapelz deliiez, et ne corront mie jusc’a l’os, ne jusc’au nerf, et telz maladie si est apelee «sain», et n’est mie apelee «fistule»; mais s’elle est si alongie qu’elle viegne jusc’a l’os em parfont, si est apelee «fistule»; et li cuire si est que tu cope celui cuir tout entor, et meismement quant il est subtilz, ausi com uns drapelz; et ne s’aert mie por sa corruption.	No wound occurs in the meaty part and stays so long that it creates a large gathering of pus; subsequently, the pus spreads and penetrates, and then the pus jumps inside, and the meat is stuck there, like vessels; and the skin above is also as thin as silk pieces, and does not extend up to bone or nerve, and this sickness is named 'sain', it isn't called 'fistula'; but if it extends so far that it comes through completely to the bone from inside out, then it's named 'fistula'; and the skin is such that you can pinch all of that skin at once, just as silk pieces; and it doesn't swell due to its corruption.
Et se tu as fiance que li cuirs s’aerde, et li corruption n’est mie en parfont, et li cuir est espés de char, si le cure de clistere ensi: regarde se li seins est grans, et li bowe qui en ist est de puant odor, adonques le clisterize de medicine egiptiaine qui est ensi faite: prenez aisil, et oile, et litargire, igalment, et metez cuire en I vassel au feu, tant que li medicine soit rouge, et deviegne ausi espesse com miel; et puis pren de ceu selonc ta necessiteit, et le font en aigue et en miel, et en clisterize lou sein, et estraint le pertus; et laisse la medicine ens par II houres, puis l’estrai en espreignant; fai ce mout de fois, tant que li seins soit mondefiiez, et soit ostee li puor; et aucune fois est clisterizeis d’aigue de cendres, quant ceste medicine n’est presens, et est que tu preignes cendres de fust de vigne, et giete aigue desus, puis la coule, et en clisterize, tant que tu saiches que li seins est bien mondez; et se li malaides ne le puet soffrir, ne la medicine egiptiaine ne l’aigue de cendres, si le clisterize d’aigue et de miel ou il ait un poc de litargire broiet; ou tu la clistirize de miel et de vin melleit, que li mielz ait proprieteit de mundifiier et de laver, et li vins fait aerdre le sain; et quant tu as ce fait, et tu as fiance que li seins est bien mundifiiez, si le clisterize de ceu que fait naistre char en li, et est que tu preignes emplaustre diafinit, et le font avec oile roset et en vin; ou tu le clisterize d’aucunes medicines et d’oignemens, dont j’ai dit les proprietez ou traitier des oignemens; et se li pertus dou sein est petis, et li cainne dou clistere n’i puet entrer, si l’eslarge d’un fer un poc, et met ens une tente de l’oignement egiptiein, ou oignement basilicon, tant k’il soit eslargiez; et se li plaie est trop large, si la cout et i laisse tant soulement I leu ou li clistere puisse entrer, et se li pertus que giete bowe est au desus, si le cope ou plus bas leu que i est.	And if you've been contracted that the skin burns and corruption isn't at its height, and the skin is filled with flesh, then treat it this way: look to see if the glands are large, and the bowels connected with them have a rank smell; hence, use an Egyptian cathartic thus: Take aloes, oil, and litargy equally, mix them together, put them into a vessel over fire until the medicine becomes red and thick like honey. Then take it according to your need, make it into water or honey, apply it to the glands, and keep the application in for two hours; then remove this from above after straining off its impurities; repeat this process as many times as necessary till the glands are completely cleaned out and drained of pus; then use water made from ashes if there is no Egyptian medicine available, take vine wood ashes and pour hot water over them, then drain it; apply this as a cathartic until you know that the glands have been properly cleansed. If the patient can't tolerate this or cannot bear the Egyptian medicine or ash water, cathartics made from honey and wine might be used instead since honey has properties to cleanse and wash away impurities and wine makes 'sain' (health) rise; when you've done all these things, and know that the glands are properly cleansed, then use a substance containing fat to create new flesh in them, and apply it with olive oil or wine. Alternatively, you can use medicines and ointments which I have described their properties on, regarding ointments; if the gland opening is too small for your catheter to enter, enlarge it slightly using a heated iron, then insert an Egyptian ointment or basilicon balm until it reaches this size; if the wound is too wide, allow the catheter only as far as necessary and not any lower than where the catheter can enter.
Car quant li bowe est en parfont, si n’i laisse enjanrer char; et se tu ne pues coper lou sein desoz si com tu vues, si appareille en tel maniere que li bowe corre au plus bas leu que i est, car quant li bowe est parfont, si n’i laisse enjanrer char et se tu ne pues coper lou sein desoz si com tu vues, si apareille en teil maniere: que li bowe corre legierement aval, et n’i lassier rien de la bowe; et pren medicines consolidatives por mettre sor le sain, et estent sus I drapeil de lin que cuevre tout le sain; puis cope as forces endroit le pertus dou sein I poc plus large dou premier, pues estent oignement souef sus I autre drapel selonc la quantiteit dou pertus, et le met sus le pertus dou sain por aligier la bowe, et n’oster mie le grant drapeil fuers que aprés maint jor une fois; et celui qui est sor le pertus dou sein, oste sovent por oster la bowe, et saiches ceu que corra de la bowe, se c’est venin ou poc ou assez, ou digeste, ou indigeste; et pren warde se li patiens sent dolor ou nom, et s’il i a aposteme ou non, et quant ta medicine s’est en teil maniere estendue et tu vois la nature que saut sus le pertus dou sain, si saiches que li seins s’aert ja, et aproche li santez; et puis le deslie le matin, ou le tier jor, et quant tu delies la plaie, si chainge I autre drapeil, et renovele l’oignement.	For when the bowe is perfect, do not allow any pus to accumulate; and if you can't cover the breast adequately as you see fit, arrange yourself in such a manner that the bowe reaches its lowest extent possible. For when the bowe is perfect, do not allow any pus to accumulate and if you can't cover the breast adequately as you see fit, arrange yourself in such a manner: let the bowe flow slightly downwards, and don't leave anything of the bowe behind; and take consolidative medicines to put within the well-being, and place them on the linen sheet that covers all the well-being; then cover around the area somewhat larger than the original breast wound, so apply ointment of wine on the other linen sheet according to the size of the wound, and place it on the wound of the well-being to relieve the bowe, and don't remove most of the large sheet until after several days once; and that which is under the wound of the breast, often remove in order to relieve the bowe, and know how much comes from the bowe, whether it's pus or phlegm or enough, or digested, or undigested; and take care if the patient feels pain or not, and if there is an abscess or not, and when your medicine has been spread in such a manner that you see the nature rise on the wound of the well-being, know that the breast is now healing, and approaches health; and then release the wound in the morning, or on the third day, and when you release the injury, change the other sheet, and renew the ointment.
Et se li seins giete bowe indigeste aprés maint jor, saiches que li seins ne s’aert mie.	And if after many days the breasts discharge an undigested substance, know that the breasts are not healing properly.
Et se venins subtilz cort aprés lonc tens, si ne te desperer mie de la santeit, car li santez aproche.	And if delicate veins start to cut after a long time, do not despair of health, for the health approaches.
Car il i a homes cui tarde enjanremens de char en ses plaies, et de ces que font le contraire; et se bowe indigeste saut dou sein aprés maint jor, saiches que li seins ne s’aert mie; et se li seins tarde d’aerdre, et est porloigniez, si ajoste medicines sechans moistes en substance et seches en vertut, si com oignement diafinit, car il i a grant partie de vitriole, et c’est li derriene medicine; pren oignement dyafinit, et le font avec oile roset, et l’arose de viel vin igal en substance; puis le confit et en use; et ceu meisme fait mielz cuit engroissiez, quant oignemens dyafinit n’est presens, ou tu pren mirre et aloen et encens, et le broie, et le poudre sus le miel quant il est sor le feu; et puis en glue I drapel, et l’estent sor le sein, et aucune fois i aministre on aristologe longe, et racines de lis celeste, qui est ausi com farine de veces et centoire; et en use de simples ou de compostes: broie les, et en fai poudre, et met sus le miel que j’ai dit, et en use; et se li cure est alongie, et n’est curez par ceste cure, adonc saiches que la corruptions est em parfont, et fait empression en l’os, ou as membres durs, ou as liemens; si le cure de la cure de fistule, si com nos avons dit ci devant.	For there are people who take longer to heal their wounds and those who do the opposite. And if they find indigestion starting from the stomach after many days, know that the stomach is not working properly; and if digestion is delayed and is far off, adjust your medicine with dry and moist substances according to its virtue. Take ointment diafinit for example, as it has a large part of vitriol, which acts as the last remedy; take ointment diafinit, mix it with rose oil, and apply it mixed with old wine that is compatible in substance; then warm it up and use it; do the same by using cooked honey to thicken it when ointment diafinit is unavailable. Or you can take mirre, aloen, and frankincense, grind them together, and mix this paste with honey when it's heated; then apply the mixture over the chest, and do so every time you administer medicine or an aristologe (a type of medicine), along with sky lily roots which are similar to ground cloves and cinnamon; use simple medicines or combinations: grind them into a powder and mix it with the previously mentioned honey and use it. If your treatment is long-lasting but not effective, know that corruption has set in, spreading through the bones or hard parts of body tissues; if you treat fistulas (a medical condition) as we have mentioned before, do so accordingly.
de l’aposteme de l’ungle	of the abscess under the nail
Panarice est un aposteme que naist desoz l’ungle dou pouchiet de la main, ou dou piet, ou par aventure naist en autres dois; et quant il est envielliez, et on n’i prent garde, si i vient I aposteme chaus, et corront et giete bowe tant qu’elle corront la racine de l’ungle, et par aventure la corront toute; et vient li corrosions jusc’a l’os, tant qu’il i vient dolor puant, et est li chiés dou doi larges, et est li color fuxe.	Panarice is an abscess that forms under the nail of the hand's little finger or foot or sometimes on other toes; and when it grows old, if no attention is paid to it, then the abscess spreads, runs, and becomes hot as long as it reaches the root of the nail, by chance reaching all of it. And corrosion comes up to the bone, so long as it causes painful pus, and makes the toe wide and changes its color.
Quant tu le cures si com nos avons dit en la division, et li cure ne profite mie, si covient que tu copes a i. fer toute la superfluiteit qui est demoree de l’ungle, puis cauterize la plaie aprés.	When you treat it as we have instructed in the division, and if the treatment doesn't help, then you should proceed to clip all the excess that has remained from the nail. After that, cauterize the wound.
Li cauteres est mout grans aide se li os est sains, et li ungle est sainne; et se li ungle apresse la char ens, et l’encomence a poindre, et la blece, si covient que tu mettes lou rait desoz l’ungle que point la char, et la boute en haut, et cope celi char subtilment et legierement, et met sus le remenant de la char medicines ardans et corrosives por oster tout; puis le cure d’oignemens tant qu’il soit sanez.	The cautery is very helpful if the bone is healthy and the nail is healthy. If the nail presses against the flesh, starts to prick at its base, and becomes inflamed, then you should place a piece of lead under the nail where it touches the flesh, with the lead pointing upwards. Cut the thin and delicate part of this flesh gently, and apply hot and corrosive medicine over the wound so that everything can be removed. Then treat it with ointments until it heals properly.
Et se li corrosion est en l’os, si le cope, et trai fuer, car tant com li os corrumpus i est, si ne puet saner; et se tu vois le doi corrumpre, si le cope en I des nous si com il est devant dit, puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et s’il est ferus, et boutez, et il sent grant dolor, si covient que tu le sainnes premier; puis cope l’ungle dou spatumile agut en taillant de travers desus, et warde que li taille ne viegne jusc’a la char qui est desoz l’ungle, car li malaides sentiroit trop grant dolor; et s’il avient, si met chose sus qui apaise.	And if the corrosion is within the bone, you have to extract it and apply force, because as much of the bone is corrupted, it cannot heal. And if you see that the bone needs to be removed, you should do it immediately in this way as was explained previously, then treat until it is healed. If it has hardened and swelled up, and is causing great pain, you must first make it well; then cut the nail close to its sharp edge from the side, and be careful that your cut does not go through the flesh under the nail, for this would cause too much pain to the patient; if this happens, place something above where you intend to ease the pain.
la dolor dou sourdoit de la main	The pain originated from the hand
Li dois ajostez qui naist en mains d’aucuns homes par aventure est toz charnus, et par aventure i a teil ou il a osses, et aucune fois i a ungle, et aucun d’aus naissent en la racine de la jointure, ou li naissance est en aucuns nous des dois.	I must adjust what is born in the hands of some men by chance and are very muscular, and by chance there may be bones here or there where they have bones, and none of them has a nail, and no one of these are born at the root of the joint, or where birth occurs in any way.
Cil qui naist en aucune nout dou doi ne se muet, et cil qui naist a la jointure dou doi, par aventure se muet; la taille de celui qui est charnus si est legiere, en teil maniere: taille le en sa racine d’un large spatumile.	Those who are born without any new joints do not move, and those born at the joint, by chance, do move; the size of the one who is muscular thus is light in this manner: cut it down to its root with a broad spatula.
Cil qui naist en la racine de la jointure si est grief a curer: si te tien dou coper.	Those born at the root of the joint have trouble to cure: if you hold on to copper.
En celui qui naist ou doit au derrien nout, si covient que tu copes premier la char reondement jusc’a l’os, puis cope l’os a une soie convenable a ceu, puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	In the one who is born or should have at the end of the bone, it's necessary that you first cut up to the soft tissue until the bone, then cut the bone with a suitable tool for this. Then treat it as long as it remains sound.
Li soudemens que vient as dois ensamble vient par naissance, ou par soudement de plaie, ou par arsure de feu, ou par semblans choses.	The fusions that occur at the joints are due to birth, or by the welding of wounds, or by the action of fire, or by similar things.
Si couvient que tu copes celle soudeure, si que li doit repairent selonc lor formes naturelz; puis met entre dous tentes ou drapelz moilliez en oile roset, qu’il ne se soudent; ou tu met entre dous pieces de plonc subtilz, tant que li leus soit soudez, si com il covient.	It is necessary that you remove this weld, so it should be repaired according to its natural forms. Then place between two wet cloths or oil-soaked drapes, so they don't weld together; or you can place between two pieces of fine paste until the joins are welded, as it should be.
Se soudemens vient a aucun de ses dois avec la paume, si cope celle sodure si com il covient.	Welding occurs at none of his joints with the palm, if you take care of this welding just like it should be.
des vils	Of low-quality
Vis sont voinnes grosses envoloupees pleines de superfluitez melancoliouses, que vienent em plusors membres dou cors; et plus avient en jambes de ces qui vont a piet et qui travaillent et portent, que a autres.	Vessels are large, inflated conduits filled with superfluous melancholic substances, that come from many parts of the body. And more comes in legs of those who walk on foot and work, than to others.
Il covient donques que tu li aministres aucune fois espurgement de cole, et puis le saine de la basilique.	It follows therefore that you must administer one time a bloodletting procedure, and then heal it using basilica.
Li cure de fer si est selonc II manieres: l’une est c’on les cope, et traie on fuer le sanc noir; et li autre maniere si est que tu lieves la voinne, et la trai toute fuer.	The iron treatment has two methods: one is to apply pressure and extract black blood; and the other method is to open the vein and pull it all out with force.
Li taille si est selonc ceste maniere: arose li premier la jambe d’aigue chaude mout fort, tant que li gros sans soit subtiliiez, puis estrain la jambe dou malaide des desus la cuixe jusc’a la partie desoz le genoil; puis cope la voinne en I leu, ou en II ou en III, d’une taille large, puis eslieve et trair fuer le sanc noir a ta main, des l’un chief jusc’a l’autre, tant que tant de sans en isse com li vertus dou malaide puet soffrir; et puis la lie, et li comande qu’il se teigne de viandes enjanrant cole noire; et recomence l’evacuation et la sainie quant les voinnes sont plainnes, et nuist au malaide.	The procedure is as follows: first, heat the affected leg with hot water vigorously until the big vein becomes thin. Then strain the leg from the side of the wound up to above the knee; then cut open the vein on I, II or III, making a wide incision, and pull out black blood with your hand from one end to another as much as the properties of the illness can endure. And then close it again and command him to smear meat in this dark color. Then repeat evacuation and cleaning when the veins are full, causing harm to the patient.
Li alevemens de li est selonc ceste maniere: reis la jambe dou malaide, s’il i a mout de poil, puis le met ou bain, et li arose la jambe d’aigue chaude tant qu’elle deviegne rouge, et enflent les voinnes; et se tu n’as point de baing, si le chaufe au feu, et puis le cope endroit la voinne dou lonc au chief dou genoil, ou en la partie desoz a la cheville; puis aoevre le cuir a l’oncine, et escorche la voinne de chescune part, tant qu’ele apere quant on la sent; et on la voit rouge et noire, et quant elle entre ou cuir si semble ausi com une corde blainche; puis boute le rait desoz, tant qu’ele soit alevee dou cuir, et puis la pent a l’oncine legier, puis le cope en I autre leu ensus III dois; puis escorche le cuir sus la voinne tant qu’ele apere, puis la lieve au rais, si com tu as fait, et la pent a un autre uncine, si com tu as fait premiers; puis cope une autre taille, ou plusors se tu en as mestier, puis la lieve, et la cope au doi dou piet, puis la trai et lieve jusc’a la seconde taille; puis l’estrai de taille en taille, tant qu’elle isse toute fuer, puis la cope; et se tu ne la pues traire et lever, si i boute une aguille a tout I fil fort double, et la lie et la trai, et i boute desoz I rait, et torne ta main d’une part et d’autre, tant qu’il en isse; et garde qu’elle ne cope, car s’elle cope, si ne la puet on traire ne lever, et en vient nuisement au malaide; et quant tu l’as toute traite, si met sor le leu de la plaie laine moillie en vin et en oile roset; et le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	The treatment begins like this: lift the leg from the wound, if there is hair there, then immerse it in a bath. Then, keep the leg submerged in hot water until it turns red and inflamed; if you lack a bath, heat it on fire instead. Apply it over the vein along its length from thigh to knee, or in the part below the ankle bone; next, scrape the skin on that spot, and scorch the vein separately from each side, until it appears upon touch; it should appear red and black, when you can see it inside the skin as a white string; then remove the hair around it, while keeping it raised above the skin, and again place it in the hot water; then scrape the skin over the vein till it becomes visible, lift it up towards the fire like before, and then apply it on another bone from III bones onward. Then scrape the skin on top of the vein until it becomes visible, then raise it at the flame similarly to how you did, and again place it on another bone; then apply a different size or multiple sizes if needed, lifting them each time, then apply one more by pressing the heel down into the foot, pull it up and set it back onto the first bone after that; then stretch it from one size to the next, until all strength is released, then proceed. If you can't pull and lift it, sew a thick thread of double yarn straight through, bind and pull on it, and while holding it under the fire at intervals, turn your hand back and forth till it comes out; be sure not to bind it too tight as if it does, you won't be able to pull or lift it and it could cause harm to patient; when you've completed the process, place soaked cloth in wine and rose oil over the wound site. Cure until healed completely.
Et se li vis est contraite et torte et envoloupee ensamble, et ele n’est mie droite, si com nos avons dit, si covient que tu la fendes tortement, mais ne la coper mie; et la trai si com nos avons devant dit.	And if the face is tight and twisted and enclosed together, and it isn't straight, as we have said, then it should be cut viciously, but not covered; and handle it in the way that was previously mentioned.
Li forme dou fer dont on cope la vis si est corbes, et ne trenche mie, qu’il ne cope la voinne; et est de grosse corbeure, car s’il estoit subtilz, si coperoit la voine, mais soit gros si com nos avons dit, et ci est li forme:	The shape of the iron with which one cuts the thread is curved, and does not cut or nick, so as to not wound the vessel; and it has a large curvature, for if it were subtle, it would damage the vein, but being substantial, as we have said, this is the form:
de la voinne civile	of the civil vein
Ceste voinne est enjanree en jambes, en chaudes parties ou il ne naist herbes ne arbre, et en terre ou il n’a point de moistor; et par aventure naist autre part qu’en jambes, et ceu avient de la porriture que vient desoz le cuir, si com il vient dedens le cors serpens et vers, enjanrez entre cuir et char.	This vein penetrates the legs, in warm areas or where no herbs nor trees grow, and in soil without moisture; and sometimes it emerges elsewhere than on the legs, and this occurs due to corruption that originates from under the skin, just as it happens inside the body with snakes and worms, penetrating between the skin and flesh.
Et se li signes de l’encomencement de ceste voinne si est qu’il vient en la jambe une tres grans enflammation, puis se chainge li leus, et comence li voinne fors issir, ausi com une racine d’une plante.	And if the signs of this vein's beginning occur such that there is a very great inflammation in the leg, then the veins change, and the vein starts to emerge outside, like the root of a plant.
Quant li chiés apert, si covient que tu envoloupes entor une piece de plonc des une З et demi jusc’a II З., et la noe, et laisse le plonc pendant a la jambe, et totes les fois qu’il en ist point au defuer, si l’envoloupe entor le plonc, et la nowe; et s’elle est trop longe, si en cope une partie, et envoloupe le remenant, et ne la coper mie en sa racine, tant qu’elle soit toute issue; car se tu la copes, si rentre en la char, et fait venir aposteme et porriture ou leu, et male maladie; por la queil chose il covient qu’elle soit traite poc et poc jusc’a chief, et n’en remaigne rien ou cors; et est aucune fois ceste voinne quant elle est traite de V paumes de lonc, ou de X, et uns hons vint ja a moi, a cui elle issit de X paumes de long, et quant tu la copes, si boute I rais ou pertus, et la perce jusc’a fons, si que tout en isse; et soit vuidie li matiere qui est dedens, et amenistre au leu medicines enjanrans porriture aucun jor, puis le cure si com les apostemes.	And when the shoulder has been opened, it must be covered with a piece of plaster about three-quarters to two-thirds until it is completely healed; cover it and leave the plaster on the leg. And each time there's a need for restitching from the front, if you cover inside the plaster and stitch again. If it's too long, cut off some part and rewrap with covering but not in its root, until it emerges completely; because when something is covered, it can enter into the flesh, causing pus and putrefaction or an illness; so that this thing needs to be treated little by little up to half, leaving nothing behind; and there's no time during which this vein should be treated longer than five hands of length, or ten, and about two more hands from me as it comes out, and when you cover it, if there are one or two threads, pierce until the bottom so that all can pass through; and drain any matter inside, and apply medicine to prevent putrefaction each day, then treat it just like abscesses.
Et aucune fois a ceste voinne mains rains, et meismement quant elle apert en la jointure dou piet, ou ou piet, et i vient mout de pertus, et dont il saut rains; cure le donques si com nos avons dit devant.	And never in this vein apply cold hands, and especially when it opens at the bone joint or on the bone itself. There comes much loss and jumpiness; thus then treat as we have said before.
des vers qui naissent entre cuir et char	worms that come to life between skin and flesh
Ceste maladie est apelee en nostre terre «maladie de buef», por ceu qu’elle avient maintes fois as bués, et est un petis vers qui naist entre cuir et char, et va par tout le cors montant et dessendant, et le sent om bien a l’aler de membre en membre, tant qu’il desront le cuir ou il vait, et saut fuer; et est enjanrez de porriture d’aucunes humors, si com vienent vers et serpens et lumbris et ascarides ou ventre; et doute on de son malice, car quant il va par le cors, et il monte au chief, et il vient a l’oil, par aventure rentre, et destruit l’oil; et ceu avient maintes fois.	This disease is called in our land "beef illness", because it has often afflicted cattle, and it's a little worm that comes to life between the skin and flesh, and travels throughout the entire body moving up and down. Its presence can be felt from member to member until it reaches the skin where it goes, and jumps out; and it becomes infected with pus from various fluids, like worms and snakes and earthworms or in the stomach; one wonders about its mischief, because when it moves through the body, and climbs to the head, and arrives at the eye, by chance it returns and destroys the eye; this happens many times.
Quant tu le vues curer et traire, si ne puet on fuers que quant il vait: si covient donques que tu lies le leu desus et desoz d’un fort liien bien estroitement, puis cope sus et le trai fuer, et se li vers est em parfont en la char, et tu ne le trueves, si le cauterize de feu sus, tant qu’il muire; et li plus grans nuisemens que il fait, si est qu’il corront l’oil, si com nos avons dit; et se tu le vois venir ou chief pres de l’oil, si estraint desoz lui le sorcil forment, puis cope sus, et le trai fuer; et covient user le malaide de mundifiement de cors de medicines solutives por les males humors porries, et se warse de viandes enjanrans porriture.	When you see it being treated and drained, there is nothing else that can be done other than when it moves: thus, you should bind the area above and below firmly with a strong rope. Then treat it from up and down, and direct it through the flesh if possible, and if you do not find it, then cauterize it with fire until it heals; and all the worst damages that it causes are when it affects the eye as we have said; and if you see it coming close to the eye, then bind it firmly from below, treat up again, and use the aid of purification of body through medicines that dissolve, against the accumulated bodily humors, and beware of eating rotten meat which can cause putrefaction.
de la dolor qui vient de ventositeit	The pain comes from winds or windiness.
Ceste maladie est apelee en nostre terre «vakirir», et est une dolor que vient en aucuns membres, et pues se mue de membre en membre; et je vis ceu que je vos di.	This disease is called "vakirir" in our land, and it's a pain that comes to some limbs, and then moves from limb to limb; and I have seen what I am telling you.
Je fui apelez a une femme malaide, et me descovrit som bras, et vis une petite enfleure en la voinne dou brais; et I poc aprés, li vis monter ausi com un ver a l’espaule, plus tost que nulle chose, ausi com vif argent quant il cort de leu a autre; li dolor se departit de celui leu, et se ficha en l’espaule, et puis un poc aprés corrut par tout le cors, tant qu’ele vint en l’autre brais; puis me contait qu’elle tornioit adés entor le cors, si com je la vis.	I was called to a sick woman and she showed her arms to me, and I saw a small swelling in the arm vein; soon after, I noticed it rising like a worm up to her shoulder, quicker than anything else, like hot silver when cut from one person to another; the pain left that side, and settled into the shoulder, then a little later spread throughout the body until it reached the other arm; she then told me that it twisted around within her body, just as I had seen.
Je me mervillai mout coment elle se movoit ensi de membre em membre, car je n’avoie onques veut ceste maladie selonc ceste maniere.	I marveled greatly how she moved from limb to limb in this manner, for I had never seen such an illness conducted like this before.
Toutevoie, je avoie veut maint que bien avoient veut movoir dolor de leu a autre, mais je ne l’avoie mie veut, si com je le vis en la femme; et je me pensai que c’estoit por ceu que li femme avoit sec cors, et les voinnes descovertes, et por ceu apparoit celle ventositez constrainte; et n’aperent mie selonc ceste raison a ces qui sont delicious, et qui ont moistes cors et voinnes reponues.	Every way, I wanted many to move the pain from one side to another but I did not want it like what I saw in that woman; and I thought it was because of her dry body and exposed veins, and due to this constraint winds appear; yet they do not become apparent according to this reason with those who are healthy and have moist bodies and closed veins.
Et quant tu vues curer ceste maladie, et li malaides sent celle dolor, s’elle t’apert si com nos avons dit, si la lie desus et desoz hastanment, et puis cope sus tant que cele ventositez constrainte au leu isse fuer; et cauterize le leu; et se tu ne la vois a tes eulz, si le cure de ceu qui deboute les ventositez, si com pilules fetides, et pilules de serapin, et semblans autres.	And when you see to treat this illness, and the patient feels that pain, if it opens up as we have said, quickly seal it above and below, then pinch until that wind force leaves from its place; and cauterize the place. And if you do not see it at your fingers, treat those with wind disturbance, such as rotten pills, serapin pills, or similar others.
des saiettes	Of arrows
Les saiettes sont diverses, selonc lor semblances et selonc les leus dou cors ou elles chient.	Arrows are diverse, depending on their appearances and the locations where they pierce the body.
Li diversitez de lor si est qu’il i a de celles qui ont grans pointes, et petites, et chevees, et soudees; et de celles qui ont II angles, et de celz qui ont lengues, et de celles ou il a pieces; et celle qui chiet en aucun membre si chiet selonc II manieres: ou en membre principeil cheveit, si com cerveil, cuer, foie, pormon, rains, intestine, vessie, et semblans membres.	The variety of arrows is such that there are those with large points, small ones, barbed, or soldered; and those with two angles, and those with tongues, and those which have pieces. And among them, some do not discharge in any member but do so according to two ways: either in the primary members like head, heart, liver, lungs, intestines, bladder, or other similar organs.
Quant elle chiet donques en aucun leu de ces membres, et li signe de mort, que je te dirai ci aprés, t’aperent: si covient que tu te warses de l’estraction de ceste saiette, car li mors vient aprés en plusors dispositions; et quant cist mal signe ne t’aperent mie, et li saiette n’est mie em parfont, si la trai, et cure la plaie.	When the shoulder joint exits then in none of these body parts, and the signs of death, which I will tell you later, appear: so it is necessary that you know how to extract this arrow, because death comes afterwards under various circumstances; and when this bad sign does not appear and the arrow is not completely removed, if you pull it, and treat the wound.
Et li signe dou cerveil quant li saiette i chiet et perce l’os, et saut li syfac fuer qui est sus le cerveil, est quant scotomie et sode et esvertin et roujor ens eulz, et enflammation et roujor de lengue, et spasme et permixtion d’entendement, et vomissemens de cole; et per aventure ist sans fuer des narines, ou des oreilles; et par aventure pert la parole et la voix; et saut de la plaie moistor blanche semblant a poulz, et en saut ausi com bruee de char; et se cist signe t’aperent, si te tien de la cure, et trai la saiette s’elle n’est ens.	And the sign of the skull when the arrow exits and pierces the bone, and there is a blow to the brain located above the skull, is when blindness and dizziness and inversion of vision occur, as well as feverishness and redness in the eyes, inflammation and reddening of the tongue, cramps and confusion of understanding, vomiting of bile; sometimes it manifests as loss of strength from the nose or ears; and sometimes loss of speech and voice; there is a sign of dampness from the wound that looks like pus, and also burns similar to burn marks; and if this sign appears, take care in treatment, and pull out the arrow if it isn't yet.
Li signe de la siette quant elle chiet ou cuer, sont qu’elle est pres de la mamele senestre, et sent ausi com s’elle estoit fichie en chose dure, ne mie vuide; et par aventure li siette se muet ausi com li poulz, et en cort noir sanc, et vient froidor et suor froide, et sincope: saiches adonc sens doute ke li mors dessent.	The sign when it comes out or to the heart is that it's near the left nipple and feels as if it were stuck in something hard, not empty; and by chance the wart also stops like a pulse, with black blood coming out, and brings coldness and sweat that's cold, and fainting: know then without doubt death is descending.
Et li signe de la saiette que nevre lou pormon est que sans plains d’escume saut de la plaie, et li gorge enfle, et li malaides mue color, et sospire haut et quiert le froit ar.	And the sign of an arrow that never leaves its wound is that without any foam spilling from the wound, and the throat swells up, and the patient's face turns a different color, and they sigh loudly with cold chills.
Et se li saiette chiet en la coverture dou pis, si est delez les petites costes; et giete grant alainne et grant dolor et sospire; et li muevent tuit li membre des espaules.	And if the arrow stops within the thigh's cover, it hits the small bones; and causes great pain and intense agony and sighing; and all body parts from the shoulders move.
Et se li saiette chiet ou stomac, par aventure si saut de la plaie aucune chose de la viande indigeste.	And if the arrow stops in the stomach or intestine, by chance if it breaks out of the wound, there's no undigested flesh.
Et se li saiette chiet ou ventre, et en saut point de fien par l’intestine rout, si n’a point d’esperance en la cure, ne en l’estraction de la saiette.	And if the arrow stops in the belly or abdomen, and it jumps out of the wound not through the intestines, there's no hope for treatment, nor is there any hope for extracting the arrow.
Et se li saiette chiet en la vessie, et li urine en saut et vient defuer, et li malaides sent fort dolor: saiches que li plaie est mortelz.	And if the arrow stops in the bladder and causes urination to occur, and leaks out, causing great pain to the patient: you know that the wound is fatal.
Li autre membre, si com li faice et li colz et li gorge et li espaule et li adjutoire et li espinee dou dos et li forcele et li cuixe et les jambes, et li membre semblant, sont sauf selonc plusors dispositions.	The other body parts, such as the limbs and neck and throat and shoulder and shoulder blade and back spine and ribs and arms and legs, and similar seeming limbs, are safe according to various dispositions.
Quant li saiette est en lou nerf ou l’artere, et elle n’est venimouse, si com je vos dirai qu’il m’avint, por ceu que vos faciez autretel.	When the arrow is in the nerves or arteries and it's not poisonous, like what I will tell you, this happened to me because of what you were doing.
Il avint a I home c’une saiette li chut ou larmier en la racine dou neis: je la tentai, et la traï d’autre part desoz la graisse de l’oreille, et fut sanez sens nusement.	It happened to one person that an arrow struck him in the thigh near his knee: I tested it and pulled it out from another side through the fat of the ear, causing no particular pain.
Et traï a un jeu une saiette que li chut en la graisse de l’oil desoz la papiere desoz, et li saiette estoit reponue, et n’en poi ataindre que la pointe devers lou fust, et estoit li saiette grans d’un arc turcois, a tout I fer legier sens oreilles; li jeus fut sanez, et ne li vint nulz mavais accidens.	I removed an arrow from a game that had struck him in the fatty tissue near his eye beneath the paper, and the arrow was stuck, only touching the tip towards the shaft. The player was fine, and no bad accidents occurred to him.
Et traï une saiette de la gorge a un crestien, et estoit li saiette arabique a oreilles: je soiai les barbions, et subtiliai tant que je la traï, et fut sanez li crestiens.	And remove an arrow from the throat of a Christian, and the arrow was Arabic with ears: I pulled it out through my beard, pricking deeply as I drew it, and healed the Christian.
Et traï une saiette a I home, que li estoit cheue ou ventre, et pensai qu’il moroit; et puis qu’il ot passez XXX jors, si ne mua point sa disposition; je taillai sus la saiette, et l’engignai, et la traï fuer, et n’ot point de mavais accident.	And pulled an arrow from the house, that it was stuck in his back or stomach, and I thought he would die; and then after 30 days had passed, if he did not change his position; I cut into the arrow, poked it out, and pulled it free, with no adverse incident.
Et si vis I home cui une saiette chut ou dos, et fut li plaie soudee sus; et demora li saiette dedens li, et ne chainja point ses dispositions naturez, ne ne trova nuisement en aucune de ses oevres naturelz.	And if you see the house where an arrow fell or hit it, and the wound was sealed up; and stayed in the arrow inside it, and did not change its natural positions, nor found any harm in any of its natural works.
Et vis I autre homme, cui il chut une saiette en sa faice, et fut soudee li plaie; et demora ensi sens soffrir grant dolor; et mout d’autres semblans.	And look at another man, who was hit by an arrow in his face and had the wound stitched; he then endured great pain for some time; and many others like this.
Et traï une saiette a I home des princes le roi, que li estoit cheue enmi lou neiz, et estoit un poc declinans a la destre partie; et estoit li saiette toute reponue Je fui apelez a la cure aprés ceu qu’elle fut cheue III jors.	And there was an arrow shot at the king's home among the princes, which had pierced his nose and was slightly leaning to the right side; the arrow was fully in. I was called for treatment after it had been shot for three days.
Si trovai la plaie mult estroite.	I found the wound to be very tight.
Je la quis a tout une subtil tente, et ne la sentis mie; et il sentoit pointure et dolor desoz sa destre oreille.	I tried to remove it with all my skill and did not feel it at all; there was pain and discomfort spreading over his right ear.
Je pensai que c’estoit de la pointe de la saiette Je mis sus lou leu emplaustre atratifet digestif, por ceu que li leus n’enflast; et m’aparut li leus de la saiette.	I thought it was from the tip of the arrow. I placed a healing plaster on his ear, as his ears were not inflamed; and revealed the arrow's position in his ear.
Je i mis l’emplaustre mains jors, et resouda li plaie derechief, et demora ensi li malaides lonc tens, tant qu’il sentit la saiette I jor dedens son neis; et il le me dist.	I applied the plaster for several days, and resolved the wound promptly, then let the patient endure long periods, until he felt the arrow within his nose on the third day; and that is what I told him.
Je mis sus la plaie medicine ague corrosive par mains jors, tant qu’elle fut overte, et la tentai, et sentis le chief de la saiette qui s’aerdoit au leu; puis ajostai en l’overture de la plaie par celle medicine ague, tant que li chiés de la saiette m’aparut visablement; et trespassa bien li termines entor IIII mois, et puis eslarja si li plaie que je i boutai les tenailles, et le meus d’une part et d’autre, et ne pot issir; adonques ne cessai de subtiliier et d’engignier de manieres d’estrumens, tant que je la pris I jor as tenailles bien faites, selonc ceu que sa forme venra en la fin de cest chapistre, tant que je la traï, et restourai la plaie.	I placed the corrosive ague medicine on the wound for several days until it was opened, then I tried to remove it and felt the tip of the arrow near my hand. Then I adjusted within the wound opening using that same ague medicine until I could visibly see the head of the arrow; and I passed very well through the tendons up to four months, and then healed so much that I grasped both sides with forceps, and operated from one side to another, but couldn't remove it; therefore, I didn't stop refining and inventing ways for instruments until I was able on the third day using properly made forceps as described in this chapter's conclusion regarding its shape when I moved it and healed back the wound.
Et li mire jugent que li cartillaige dou nez ne puet restorer: je la restourai adonques, et fut soudee li plaie, et fut sanez li malaides entierement.	And they consider that the nose cartilage cannot be restored: I will thus restore it, and after the wound is sealed, and the patient's body has healed completely.
Or t’ai dit la qualiteit de l’estraction d’aucunes saiettes, si que tu mettes ta cure sus ceu que je ne dis mie, car li livres ne puet mie tout porprendre; mais li saiges maistres compere sus bien poc grant chose, et sus ceu que li est present et defaillant, trueve nueve oevre, et nuef estrument, au dessendement des choses estrainges qui avienent en cest art.	Or tell me the quality of the extraction of some arrows, so that you apply your cure to what I do not mention; for books cannot encompass everything. But let the wise doctors compare well on very few things, and on what is currently present and lacking, find a new work and new tool, regarding the removal of foreign substances which occur in this art.
Je dis que les saiettes n’issent des membres ou elles sont fichies fuer que selonc II manieres: ou par lou leu ou elles entrent, ou par d’autre part; et celle que saut fuer par lai ou elle entre, c’est saiette entrans en leus charnus, et saut fuer aucune fois maintenant.	I say that arrows only penetrate the limbs from where they are inserted through two ways: either through the body's natural path or from another direction; and if an arrow pierces internally or enters at a certain point, it penetrates into the flesh, and never again will this happen.
Et s’elle ne saut maintenant, si la laisse tant que li chars soit porrie entor, et soit alegie li issue; et ausi s’elle est fichie en l’os, et elle ne puet issir, si la laisse ensi aucuns jors, et la muef chescun jor; et adonques elle saut, et s’elle ne saut, si perce entor a tout I foret subtil, tant que li leus entor soit eslargiez, et puis la trai.	And if it doesn't jump now, let it grow until the skin is fully healed inside and it releases naturally; likewise, if it's stuck in the bone and can't escape, leave it that way for several days and remove a little each day; then it will jump out. If it doesn't jump out, drill straight into all the delicate passages until the inside flesh widens significantly, and then remove it.
Et se li saiette est fichie en l’os dou chief, et vait jusc’a l’un des ventres dou cerveil, et aucuns des accidens que j’ai dit apert au malaide: si ne la traire mie, mais la laisse tant qu’elle soit igalz aprés aucuns jors, car se li saiette vient jusc’a syfac, c’est li mors.	And if the arrow is stuck in the head bone and goes up to one of the brains, or any other event that I have mentioned appears to the patient: do not remove it immediately, but let it heal until it is even after several days, because if the arrow reaches this far, it means death.
Et se li saiette n’est fichie fuer qu’en l’os soulement, et ne vient jusc’a syfac, et demoure li malaides aucuns jors sens mavais accident, si l’engigne dou traire.	And if the arrow is only stuck in the bone and does not go up to the sinus, and remains without any bad event for several days, then one should use a device for extracting it.
Et s’elle est mout fichie ensi et ne puet issir fuer, si i aministre tareres entor, si com je t’ai dit; puis cure le leu tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if it is thus embedded and cannot come out like that, if you apply the arrows internally, as I have told you; then treat the wound until it heals properly.
Et se li saiette est reponue en leu dou cors si c’on ne la puisse veoir, si la quier a tout la tente; et se tu la sens, si la trai a aucun estrument covenauble; et se tu ne pues por l’estrecement de la plaie, et por la parfondesce de la saiette, et il n’i a os ne nerf ne voine, si la fens tant que li plaie soit grans; et trai la saiette se tu pues, et s’il ait en la saiette oreilles a coi elle tient, si oste la char qui est ens fichie de II pars au mues que tu pues, et puis brise ou ploie les oreilles de la saiette, tant que tu la puisses traire; et subtilie bien que tu ne brisier la saiette, que tu la trairoies plus griement.	And if the arrow is returned into its place within your body so you can't see it, then search for it thoroughly all around; and if you feel it, try to pull it with any suitable tool; and if you cannot because of the constriction of the wound or the depth of the arrow, and there are no bones, nerves, or veins, cut it as much as necessary so that the arrow is large enough; pull the arrow if you can, and if it has ears that it holds on to, remove the flesh stuck inside from both sides until you can move them, then break or bend the ears of the arrow as far as you can pull it; be very careful not to break the arrow so that you can pull it more smoothly.
Et se tu ne pues a une fois, si la lai jusque li leus entor soit porris, puis la trai, car li estraction iert alegie.	And if you cannot do it in one go, till your arm is numb from the effort, then move on, because the extraction requires endurance.
Et se li decorremens de sanc te fait contraire, si amenistre ceu que nos avons dit de la cure en son chapistre; et te warde de l’incision dou nerf et de la voinne, et met engien coment tu pues mues traire la saiette sens peril, ou tost ou tart, ou fermement ou belement; et met le malaide selonc la forme qu’il estoit quant li saiette li chut ens, car c’est li plus grans aide que i soit, et se tu ne pues, si lou met selonc ceu que li signe lou te mostrent.	And if the bleeding makes you do otherwise, then follow what we have said about treatment in this chapter; and beware of cutting near nerves and veins, and place your hands so that you can pull out the arrow without risk, quickly or slowly, firmly or gently; and position the patient according to their original form before they were hit by the arrow as that is the best for them, and if you cannot do that, then follow what the sign shows you.
Li saiette que vient fuer d’autre part, ou il apert aucune chose de li, ou li cuir est enflez endroit si c’on le voit ou sent aparamment: taille donques sus, tant que les tenailles i puissent prendre, et puis l’estrai: si saut fuer maintenant.	The arrow that comes from elsewhere, where no part of it is visible or felt bulging through the skin, or where the leather swells at the place: cut above, as long as the forceps can grasp, and then apply pressure: if it jumps now.
Et s’elle est retenue en l’os, si tornoie ta main rondement, tant qu’elle entre en l’os, et eslarge l’os, puis la trai.	And if it is held in the bone, twist your hand round as long as she enters the bone, and enlarge the bone, then pull her out.
Et s’elle ne puet issir, si la laisse encor, et puis rencomence l’estraction tant qu’elle isse fuer; et se li fust de la saiette i est, se le boute a tout le fust; et se li fust chiet, et tu vues aministrer boutement, si i aministre I estrument cheveit, si que li pointe de la saiette entre en la cheveure de l’estrument; et puis boute fuer, et se li saiette est chevee, se i boute I estrument a pointe entrant ens, por alegier l’estraction.	And if it doesn't come out, let it stay, and then start extracting again until it does; and if the arrow is inside her, hold onto the shaft completely; and if there's feces instead, when you see the need to apply pressure, if you're instructed to use a tool made of hair, make sure the tip of the arrow goes into the hair of the tool; and then apply force, and if the arrow is caught in the hair, hold onto the tool at its point entering part so as to facilitate extraction.
Et se li saiette est entouchie, si covient que tu copes toute la char entor ou li venins est, se tu pues, puis cure la plaie si com il couvient.	And if the arrow is touching, it is necessary that you remove all the flesh around where I come in, if possible, then treat the wound as is fit.
Et se li saiette chiet ou peis ou au ventre ou a la vessie ou au costeit, et elle est prochiene, et tu pues coper sus, se i cope; et te garde de coper la voinne et lou nerf, et puis l’estrai, et puis cout la plaie, se mestier est; et la cure tant qu’elle soit sanee.	And if the arrow hits or pierces the body parts such as chest, bladder, abdomen or ribs, and it's close to vital structures, you must cover carefully around it, if possible. Avoid covering the vein and nerve, then cut it, and after that treat the wound when necessary; and continue treatment until it heals.
Li forme des tenailles dont on trait les saiettes sont semblans au bec d’oiseil, et vez ci la forme:	The shape of the tongs used for extracting arrows resemble a bird's beak, and here is the form:
Et en sont mout de manieres: grans, moienes, et petites, selonc la quantitei de la saiette.	And they are made in sizes: large, medium, and small, according to the size of the arrow.

des voinnes dou cors communes	from the veins of common horns
Des voinnes dont on se saine sont XXXI, de coi il a ou chef XVI, c’est a savoir: II batans qui sont aprés les oreilles, qui sont apelees les dous «herbech»; et les II arteres qui sont en II temples apparans; et II voines que sont en II larmiers des II eulz, que sont apelees «aspires»; et li voine que est emmi le front; et li voinne que est au chief dou neis; et les II guindeges qui sont ou col; et les II voinnes que sont en levres desus de la bouche, et ce sont les voines que sont apelees «augeherich»; et II voinnes que sont desoz la lengue.	There are 31 veins which we siphon from, of which there is a head of 16, namely: Two batons located behind the ears, they are called the two "herbs"; and the two arteries that are in the two visible temples; and two veins that are inside the corners of the eyes, they are called "suction"; and the vein that runs through the forehead; and the vein that is at the root of the nose; and the two joints located around the neck; and the two veins above the lips within the mouth, these are called "augieherich"; and two veins that run along the tongue.
Les voinnes dont on saine communement sont V en chescun bras: l’une est li cephalique, et est dou senestre costeit, et l’apelent li laie gens «voinne dou chief»; et li moiene est apelee «faste», et est composte de la cephalique et de la basilique, et l’apelent li laie gens «voinne dou cuer»; et li basilique si est ou destre costeit, et l’apelent li laie gent «voinne dou ventre», et est sus le foscile, et est celle dont on saine, qui apert manifestement sus le pouchet.	The veins that are commonly treated are V in each arm: one is the cephalic vein, and it's located on the left side, and they call it by the common people "vein of the head"; and the middle one is called 'fasting', and it consists of the cephalic and basilic veins, and they call it by the common people "vein of the heart"; and the basilic so is either on the left or right side, and they call it by the common people "vein of the belly", and it's above the clavicle, and this is the one that is treated, which opens up clearly on the abdomen.
Et li salvatelle est li voine qui est entre l’auriculaire et l’anulaire, et si a II rains; et en la jambe et ou piet sont III voinnes: l’une si est desoz la corbeure dou pochet dou senestre costeit, et li seconde sophene qui est a la cheville dou destre costeit; et li voine qui est apelee «nesse», que est en la cheville de l’autre costei; et en l’autre jambe sont III voinnes desoz celles.	And the salve-telle is the vein that's between the index finger and the ring finger, and it has two parts; and in the leg and foot there are three veins: one is at the bend of the little toe on the left side, it's located near the ankle. And the second is Sophene which is at the ankle on the right side; and the vein called 'nurse' that's found at the ankle on the other side; and in the other leg are three veins beneath those.
Li sainie des voinnes que sont aprés les oreilles si aide as catharres anciens, et a emigraine; et li qualiteis dou sainier, si com je te dis, et est que tu reises lou chief dou malaide, et frote lou leu ou les voinnes sont d’un drap aspre; puis estrigne li malaides son col a une vis, tant que les II voinnes aperent derrier les oreilles en II leus dependens dou chief: quier les donques a ton doi, et ou tu sens lou poulz desoz ton doi, si seigne d’enche; puis pren la lancette, et la boute par desoz la voine jusc’a l’os, puis lieve ta main a tout la voinne amont, et cope et lou cuir et la voinne bien II dois dou traver, et fai issir dou sanc tant que tu vues; puis l’estrain et lie, tant qu’ele soit sanee; et j’ai ja dit l’incision et le cautere ou premier livre.	Surgery for veins located behind the ears helps with drainage and migraines; and discusses qualities of a surgeon as I tell you, and how to handle the wound. de la sainie des leivres	In the art of healing wounds

La qualitez de la sainie si est selonc ta pensee.	The quality of health is according to your thought.

Car il i a voinnes que fuient ausi com cordes au sainier, et si a de telz que sont plainnes de ventositeit, si que quant on met sus le flaime, si retrait a flaime, et ne puet ovrir li voinne, et ensi est on de ceus; et s’il aoevre la voinne, si est li plaie trop estroite, por ceu si covient que li sainieres soit avisez en ces choses. Et se li voine oevre la premiere fois, c’est boin; se ceu non, si rencomence ancor un poc desoz celui leu ou sus hastanment, se li leus n’est enflez. Et se li leus est enflez, et li malaides s’espoante, se li laisse I jor ou II, et ne liier mie le bras: par aventure i venra apostemes chaus; ne n’entre ou bain, puis rencomence la sainie s’elle li plait; et se li pertuis est petis, ou li sans cort subtilment et tu doutes qu’il n’isse mie tant de sanc com tu vues, si fier en celui pertuis meisme a tout le flaime droitement; et l’uevre un poc hastanment, ainsois que li leus soit enflez; car ceu avient maintes fois, quant li plaie est petite. This happens many times when the wound is small.

des sainies de ventouse	Of suction healings
