And those with a cold complexion should consume honey syrup and a moderately fragrant wine that's between old and new, and eat small pieces of food, catfish, and small birds like pheasants and chicks; on the day they are subjected to suction cup treatment, they should drink more than eat. It is fitting for some people not to consume senna or muscat before suction cup treatment or afterwards, to strengthen their main limbs; and cool down the abdomen, but it is not good for those who are hot to drink.
Les ventouses que sont mises sens ferir sont celles que sont mises sus lou foie, et sus la mice, et podagre, et sus lou ventre et la boude et les rains et la hainche, car cil membre ne soffrent mie ferir sus oulz, et ne le fait on fuer que por atraire sanc de membre em membre, si com nos mettons sus les mameles quant li neis sainne; por oster la viscositeit qui est au membre, si com nos metons ventouses sus le ventre et sus la boude por amenuisier le membre; et oste la dolor, quant il i a opilation ou piere, si oste par sa vertu atractive par aventure l’opilation, ou desaert la piere de son leu; et ensi fait ele quant on le met sus lou foie et sus la mice quant il i a ventositeit retenue, et ces ventouses sont aministrees vuides por sucier tant soulement; et aucune fois sont aministrees ensamble feu, et aucunes fois plainnes d’aigue tede, si com em maladies dou pleuresin, et en tel maniere c’on emplisse la ventouse d’aigue chaude soule, ou d’aigue ou il ait cuit herbes covenaubles a ceu.	The suction cups meant to cause injury are those placed on the liver, on the spleen, and in podagra (gout), on the belly and kidneys and hip; because this limb cannot tolerate being injured by needles, and one does not do it forcefully only to draw blood from member to member, like we place them on the nipples when the newborn cries; to remove the viscosity that is in the member, we place suction cups on the belly and on the nostril for diminution of the member; and relieves pain where there's obstruction or stone, or removes by its attractive power any obstruction, or empties the stone from its place; and so it does when one places them on the liver and spleen where there's retained viscosity, and these suction cups are administered empty only to suck just that much; they are never given together with fire, and sometimes filled with water, as in diseases of pleurisy, and in such manner we fill a suction cup with hot water or water into which herbs useful for this have been cooked.
Li forme de la ventouse aministré a feu si est ci:	The shape of the suction cup administered with fire is as follows:
Et ait II dois de large et demi palme de parfont, et ait ou costeit entor lou mileu I petit pertus, ausi com por bouter une aguille, et soit d’arain, souef devant si qu’ele ne blece lou malaide au mettre sus lou membre; et ait em mileu une verge de travers d’arain ou de fer, por mettre une chandoile emprise, et en soient et grans et petites selonc les maladies et l’eaige de ces qui les prenent; car les ventouses des enfans sont autres que des vielz, et des maigres que des gras.	And there are two handles each half a palm wide at the widest point. These are placed such that they meet in the middle and are slightly pointed like a needle's hole, for driving an awl through; made of brass or iron, with a candle holder in the middle that allows large or small candles depending on the disease and season of those using them; because children's suckers differ from adults', and from skinny to fatty ones.
Et doit on ensi mettre ceste ventouse sus lou membre: empren la chandoile de cire ou I linement, et le met emmi la ventouse au traver de la verge qui est emmi la ventouse, si que li clartez soit au fons de la ventouse qu’elle ne brule le malaide; et puis la met sus lou membre, et tes dois soit sus lou pertus que nos avons dit, si que quant on vuet, si en va li vapor, et oste on la ventouse; et emprent on le linement si com devant, et le rencomence sovent, se tu as mestier.	And one should place this suction cup thus onto the body: take the candle or wick and put it through the hole in the suction cup that is placed inside the suction cup, ensuring the flame is at the bottom of the suction cup to prevent burning the skin; then place it onto the body, hold the handles against the tip as we've described, so when needed, if heat escapes, remove the suction cup; and reapply the wick as before, repeating often, should you need to.
En la ventouse donques qui est aministree em maladie de pleuresin, a tout aigue, n’a point de verge ne de pertus, et n’est amenistree fuer que quant ele est plaine d’aigue, et est mise sus lou membre tant soulement; et c’est li forme:	In the suction device therefore that is administered in pleurisy illness, during all stages of fever, there should not be any pain or itching, and it is only given strength when it is full of water, and placed on the body only; this is its form.
Sansues ne sont amenistrees fuer que en membres ou on ne puet mettre ventouses por lour petitece, si com levres et gencives, et semblans leus; et en leus desnuez de char, si com doi ou neis, et autres semblans; et li qualitez de l’user si est que quant tu trueves sansues que sont en aigues douces nettes sens porreture, si les pren; et les met une nut en aigue douce, tant qu’elles soient famillouses, et n’aient rien en ventres; et puis soit sainiez de voinne et de ventouse, puis frote le membre tant k’il soit rouges, et met sus les sansues; et quant elles seront plainnes, et cherront, se c’est leu ou on puisse mettre ventouse, se li met, car ce vaut mout aprés.	Without sutures are only used in limbs where suction cannot be applied due to their small size like lips and gums, and similar ones; and when the body is free of pus, such as for a knee or nose, and others similarly. And regarding the quality of the operation is that if you find without sutures that are in gentle water without inflammation, take them, and place them in gentle water until they are used to it and have nothing in their stomachs; then cleanse with bloodletting and suction, then rub the body until it turns red, and place the without sutures on it; and when they become full and drain, if there is a part where a suction can be placed, then place it, because this works not too much afterwards.
Se ceu non, si leve le leu d’aisil, et puis d’aigue, mout bien, et puis l’espreint; et se li leus saine trop aprés lou cors des sansues, si moille I drapel de lin en aigue froide, et met sus, tant que li sans soit estenchiés; et se li sans est multipliez, si met sus vitriole broié, ou gales, et semblans choses, tant qu’il soit estenchiez; ou tu met sor le leu moitiez de feves pelees, et les laisse tant qu’elles s’aerdent au leu, si estanchera maintenant; et se tu en as de plus mestier, si pren autres sansues.	If not that way, then raise the arm in water, quite well, and then apply cold water; and if the arm heals too soon after the surgery of blood removal, wet it with linen dipped in cold water, and place it on top, until the wound is healed. And if there are many wounds following the surgery, put ground vitriol or gall on them, until they heal; or you might fill half the arm with peeled pea skins, leave them there until they burn off at the arm, which will stop bleeding now; and if you need more, take other wounds.
Et se les sansues ne se vuellent prendre, si frote le leu de sanc fres, ou tu i fiche une aguille tant que li sans en isse, et puis les met sus, et tantost com elles sentent lou sanc, si s’aerdent; et quant tu vues qu’elles chieent, si poudre sus un poc d’aloen et de seil broiet, ou de cendre, si cherront maintenant.	And if the wounds do not heal naturally, then rub the arm with fresh blood, or you could stick a needle in them until blood comes out, and then place it there, just as soon as they sense the blood, which will stop bleeding; and when you see that they are bleeding, then powder some aloes and ground sesame on a little, or ash, which will heal now.
Ci comence li livre des brisures	Here begins the book on fractures
Cist chapistres est maintes fois necessaires en l’art de medicine, et est restorement de brisure et de desaluement.	This chapter is often necessary in the art of medicine, and it deals with the restoration and healing of fractures.
Saichiez, chier fil, que li fol mire se gietent de cest chapistre, qu’il ne virent onques nul des anciens livres, ne lettre n’en lurent; et por ceste cause est estraingie li science en nostre terre, car je n’en trovai onques nul boin; et n’en sai nient, fuer que par la science des anciens livres, ou j’ai tant estudiiet que je en ai traite la science, et par experiment, et par l’acostumance de ma vie; et je vos ai jai descrit en cest chapistre ceu qui est contenut, et l’ai abregié en la fin, et ai mostreit clerement les formes des estrumens que sont amenistrez, si com j’ai fait en ces II chapistres ci devant.	Know, dear son, that the knowledge about this chapter is hidden from present times; it was not found in any old books or read out loud; because of this reason, we have separated it from our lands as I never encountered anything beneficial; and about this subject I know nothing at all. This is due to studying ancient texts, which I've done extensively enough to treat their knowledge within my field, through experiments, and with the experience of my life. And in this chapter, I have described what's contained here clearly, summarized it towards the end, and shown you the clear forms of instruments used; similarly as I did in these two previous chapters.
Il covient donques que nos disons ou prologue de cest livre les sommes de la parole et les chapistres ou li saiges met son entendement, et demore sus la verteit, si que cil qui sont esproveit saichent et aprenent cest art noble, et l’aprenent a autrui.	Therefore, it is necessary for us to outline the essence of this book in its introduction and prologue, and highlight the chapters where wise minds apply their intellect. We should adhere to truth, so that those who have been taught can understand and learn this noble art, and teach it to others as well.
Je dis que quant brisure ou dislocation ou torsions ou quasseure vient a aucun, si covient que tu te hastes de sainier lou malaide d’une part et d’autre, s’aucune chose ne lou te tot, si com foiblece de cors, ou enfes, ou viellars; ou se li tens n’est tres chaus, ou trop frois; et menjuce cholz frois, c’est a savoir froides joutes, et char d’oiseil et de chevril, et ne boive point de vin, ne menjuce nules grasses chars, et ne s’emplisse mie trop de viandes qui remplissent les voinnes de sanc, tant que tu n’aies doute d’aposteme chaut, ne d’espandement de matiere au membre; si reviegne li malaides a som premerain governement k’il a useit.	I say that when there is fracture or dislocation or twists or stiffness in any part of the body, it's necessary for you to quickly cleanse the patient from one side and another, without leaving anything undone. Consider factors like weakness, children, elderly people; if the patient's tension isn't too tight, or they're overly cold; or if there are cold joints, such as ice jousts, horse droppings, and not drinking wine, nor eating fatty meats; don't let them fill up with meat that fills the veins with blood until you have no doubt about a pus formation or spreading of material in the body. If you can bring relief to the patient at their first treatment until it aligns again according to its original governance as it was used before.
Et quant li os brisiés comence a restourer, si covient que on norrisse le malaide de viandes que font gros norrissement, ou il ait viscositeit, si com froment cuit en aigue, et ris, et testes, et piez, et pance de vaiche, et oefz, et poissons fres, et gros vin, et semblans chose.	And when the broken bones begin to heal, it is necessary to nourish the patient with foods that cause heavy digestion or are viscous, such as cooked wheat in water, and onions, and leeks, and peas, and cow liver, and eggs, and fresh fish, and heavy wine, and similar items.
Car a teil norrissement se reprent mues et plus tost li brisure.	For at any time of loosening they are moved more quickly and quicker is the breakage.
Et saichiez que li os brisiez des vielz et des decrepites ne se pueent mie bien reprendre ne souder selonc lor nature por la sechor des membres, ne cil ausi qui sont trop tendre, si com os de petis enfans; mais n’a cure, ramoinne sus l’os brisiet I gros tenrons qui s’aert et joint le membre ensamble, tant qu’il enforce si com il fut devant; et ne li tot point de son oevre, et por ceu le covient norrir de grosses viandes, si com nos avons dit.	And know that a broken bone in old or decrepit people cannot be mended properly or joined according to their nature due to the dryness of limbs, nor is it suitable for those who are too tender like the bones of young children; but treat the wound, set the broken bone gently over the protruding ends and join the limb together, as strong as before; do not rush with your work, and following this manner, feed them on large meats as we have said.
Et saiches que les briseures sont diverses em maintes manieres.	And know that fractures are varied in many ways.
Car li brisure dou chief est autre que li brisure dou pis, ou de la jambe, et je vos dirai en cest chapistre toutes manieres de brisure.	For the breakage of the head is different from the breakage of the foot, or of the leg, and I will tell you all manners of breaking in this chapter.
Car il i a brisure que vait a arvol, et autre en aguisant, si com li taille d’une penne por escrire.	For there are breaks that go to the elbow, and others through prodding, such as the size of a feather for writing.
Et si a brisure avec plaie, et brisure a tout une petite fendure.	And if it's a broken bone with an injury, or a break resulting in a small crack.
Et a chescune maniere ait son engien, et son estrument propre en la restauration, selonc ceu que li remembrance vient en son leu; et est conue li brisure de l’os par ceu que li leus est tors, et apert bien par defuer, et sone au presseir de la main; et quant il n’i a tortuositeit ne son au tochier, et li malaides ne sent mie grant dolor, se n’i a point de brisure; mais il puet bien avoir tortuositeit, ou fendure, ou petite brisure.	And each way has its own tool and proper instrument in the restoration, according to what memory brings to his mind; and is known that bone fracture happens through bending of the limb, showing an opening well exposed from outside, or due to manual pressure; and when there's no twisting nor swelling around, and if the patient doesn't feel much pain, it means there's no bone breakage; but one can have a twist, or a crack, or small breakage.
Si ne covient mie que tu lou mueves a la main, mais met sus medicines que vienent ci aprés, et puis l’estraint maintenant subtilment.	If it doesn't suit you to move it with your hand, but apply the remedies that follow, and then gently strain it now.
Et saiches que li brisure que vait en arvol, et sont les II parties desjointes, il les covient maintenant mettre a point igalment, ainsois que apostemes chaus i viegne; et se apostemes chaulz i vient, si lou laisse aucun jor, tant que li apostemes soit apaisiez; puis le met igal au mues que tu pues legierement et saigement, et saiches que li restauration de li est plus legiere que li restaurations de celi ou il ait pieces; puis l’estraint, si com il covient ci aprés.	And know that when the break occurred in the journey, and the two parts were disjointed, they should now put them on an equal point, as if they were to incise an artery or vein; and if pus comes out, you must leave no more than one day, until the pus subsides; then place it evenly according to your ability to move it lightly and wisely, and know that their restoration will be easier than in those with pieces. Then constrict it as we shall explain later.
Et se en l’os a piéces brisies, si l’estent de II pars, se c’est mains ou piet, ou a ta main se c’est uns petis membres, ou a II cordes, ou a une corde et a ta main; et met le membre selonc sa figure natureil, si que quant les parties dou membre brisiet sont desevrees, si ramoinne par toz engiens les additions en lor leus au mues que tu pues, et garde que par ton ovraige ne viegne au malaide lesion ne doulor; et ajoste bien les II chiés des os selonc les millors formes.	And if there are pieces broken in the bone, should it be divided into two parts, whether they're arms or legs, or with your hand if it's a small limb, or divided into two tendons, or one tendon and your hand; then place the limb according to its natural shape, so when the body parts have healed, pull them off using all means in their natural positions as you are able, and take care not to cause injury or pain to the patient; and adjust both ends of the bones according to the best forms.
Et le sent bien a la main s’il te semble k’il ne soit mie bien: si la dresce bellement, et ne l’estraindre mie trop, ne presser si com font cil qui i font venir par lor ovraige aposteme chaut et contraction au membre, si com nos avons veut maintes fois.	And feel well with your hand if you think it's not quite right: if it feels good to the touch, and don't strain it too much, don't press like those who bring about abscess drainage and muscle tension in the body as we have many times wanted.
Et quant li membres est a point, si chastie bien lou malaide qu’il ne lou mueve, ne en veillant ne en dormant, ne en tornant, ne en autre maniere; et warde bien que li membres soit si asseurez qu’il ne sente nule dolor.	And when the limbs are in place, chastise well the patient so they do not move them, neither while awake nor asleep, neither upon turning or in any other manner; and ensure that the limbs are securely set so that no pain is felt.
Car quant il sent nulle dolor, si n’est mie a point, et le covient mettre en teil disposition qu’il ne sent nule dolor; et te garde k’il soit mis droitement, que tortuositez n’i veigne quant il iert restorez; et li qualitez dou membre brisiet est selonc ceu que je te dis.	And when the person does not feel any pain, it is not properly set and one should arrange them in such a way that no pain is felt. Ensure they are placed correctly so that there is no twist upon restoration; and the quality of the injured member heals according to what I am telling you.
Saiches que li membre brisiet sont divers em petitece et en grandor et en forme.	Know that limbs broken vary in size and extent, and in shape.
Car il i a petis membres, si com brais et dois et semblans: si covient envoloupeir drapelz de lin molz et subtilz; et cil qui sont gros, si com cuixe et jambe: si covient envoloupeir d’un liien large et dur, car li larges liiens embraice tout le grant membre, et l’estraint de toutes pars igalment, si qu’il n’i a nule taiche; puis lie entor estoupes legieres, III tours ou IIII selonc lou membre, et estraint ta main un poc a tout le liien, puis vai au desus de la brisure et l’estraint moins, que la brisure puis esloigne un poc la brisure; et mollifie lou liien poc et poc, tant que tu preignes grant partie dou leu sain, puis repren I autre liien, et torne entor derechief sus lou leu brisiet; puis revai a la partie desoz de la brisure, et l’estraint moienement, ne mie trop fort ne trop molement, si com nos avons dit en la premiere lieure desus; puis met entre les liiens estoupes de lin ou drapelz, tant qu’il soit toz igalz, puis lie tout par desus I bendeil, et puis met tes esteles bien faites sus, s’il n’i a aposteme ou enfleure.	And for small limbs, such as wrists and ankles, it is suitable to wrap them in soft, fine linen; and for larger parts like calves and thighs: they should be wrapped with wide, firm bandages because the wider bands hug the entire large limb uniformly from all sides so that there are no wrinkles. Wrap around by placing light wraps, three or four times according to the limb's size, then gently hold your hand on each of these bandages, after which move upwards beyond the break and tighten less where the break occurs, allowing it to slightly recede from the break; gradually soften the bandage as you can touch a significant portion of the healthy part. Then start with another bandage, apply tight wraps around the broken limb in circles, then return slightly above the break site and partially constrict it not too tightly or too loosely as we instructed earlier. Continue placing between these linen wraps until all parts are uniform, cover everything with an upper layer, then set your well-made fasteners on top without any pus or swelling occurring.
Et s’il i a enfleure ou aposteme, si met sus chose apaisant aposteme chaut, et qui oste l’enfleure, et le laisse ensi aucuns jors; puis estrain sus tes esteles, et soient de moitiet d’une large cainne rese saigement, ou de fust dont on fait les clives, ou de rains de palme, et soient selonc ceste figure:	And if there is swelling or an abscess, one should apply something that soothes the abscess, and relieves the swelling. Let it stay like this for a few days; then tighten around your stars (likely referring to some medical procedure or body parts), and have them be half the width of a smooth cane, or from the shafts used in making arrows, or from palm fronds, arranged according to this diagram:
mais il covient que li estele que om met sus la brisure soit un poc plus grosse et plus large que les autres; et soit ausi longe com il covient au membre de petitece ou de grandor; puis estraint sus les esteles ausi com tu as fait a la premiere lieure, puis lie desus un fil avenanment, si com en la premiere lieure sus la briseure; plus estroit est ensus, adés moins; et covient que li fil soient moien, ne trop gros ne trop menus, et soient de lin mol; car se li fil sont gros, si com j’ai veut des oevres des folz qui font lor lieures des cordes de linement tort, et c’est grant error, car li lieure ne puet estre igal s’il est trop subtilz, et ne covient mie qu’il ait entre chescune estele moins dou doi d’espaice.	But it is necessary that the stars that one puts on the fracture be slightly larger and wider than the others; and they should also be as long as what's suitable for the size of the limb whether small or large. Then tighten them around the stars like you did in the first step, then put an extension cord above them just as you did with the first step under the strapping; more tightly here at the start, less later on; and it is necessary that the string be neither too thick nor too thin, but of soft linen. For if the string is too thick, as in works done by people who make their string from twisted linen cord, this is a great mistake, for the strapping cannot be uniform if it's too delicate, and it doesn't suit that there should be less than two finger-widths between each star.
Et se li malaides est navrez par les chiés des esteles aprés l’estrignement en leus sains, si met desoz elles estoupes de lin, ou lainne charpie, si qu’il ne se blece.	And if the patients are sore from the nails of the stakes after the tightening at their healthy parts, then put patches of linen or shoddy wool on them, so they do not blister.
Quant li plaie est avec la briseure, et li keurs est rompus, je en dirai la cure ci aprés.	When the wound is inflamed and the joints are broken, I will describe the treatment below.
Et saiches qu’il ne covient mie estraindre d’esteles toz les membres brisiez le premier jor.	And know that it is not right to constrain all limbs broken on the first day.
Car quant li membres est grans, se n’i covient mie mettre esteles fuer que aprés V jors ou VII, ou plus selonc ta seurteit d’aposteme chaut sorvenant; et vez ci la maniere des emplaustres anciiens por restorer brisure, dislocation, et torsion: et est que tu pren de la farine que se tient as parois dou molin, et la confis avec abun d’uef, et met ceste confection, ne trop clere ne trop espesse, et en use, et c’est li commune maniere de l’emplaustre restorant la brisure a plusors dispositions, et meismement as femmes et as petis enfans, car il n’est mie ne trop chas ne trop frois.	For when the limbs are large, it is not suitable to insert these splints immediately after three or five days, or more depending on the severity of the abscess that occurs; and here is the method of the ancient plaster for restoring breaks, dislocations, and twists: you take flour from the mill walls and mix it with plenty of egg, creating a mixture neither too thin nor too thick. Use this concoction in moderation, which is the common way of applying plaster to restore breaks in several orientations, as well as on women and young children because it is neither too hot nor too cold.
Autre maniere d’emplastre restorans la brisure et la dislocation et la torsion: pren З abareis et ladani et enule et asefetide et gomme arabique et mugat, ana .x. З.; mirre et aloes, ana .v. З.; alechil .viiij. З.; et en fai poudre, et les melle avec aubun d’uef; se li complexion de l’ome est chaude, si use de cest emplaustre, car il est de bone composition, et restoure les os brisiés hastanment, et vaut a plusors homes.	Another method for the plastering that restores fractures and dislocations: take three parts of saffron, nine parts of cardamom, eight parts of rue, and one part of asafetida and gum Arabic, in a ratio of .x.3; add myrrh and aloes in the amount of .v.3; mix seven parts of vinegar with this concoction; if the mixture is warm, use this plaster, for it has good composition and heals broken bones quickly, and is beneficial to many people.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre que vaut a torsion: pren mugat et vismalve, ana X З.; mirre et aloes, ana VIIII З.; acaice VI З.; bolic armenic X З., et broie bien, et confit avec aigue ou abun d’uef, et l’aministre.	Another plaster method suitable for twists: take mastic and valerian root, each in 15 parts; myrrh and aloes each in 9 parts; acacia in 6 parts; boric acid from Armenia in 10 parts, grind well and mix with water or plenty of egg. Then administer it.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre a jointes et as os desevrez de lor leus, et apaise la dolor sorvenant, et le taille usent de l’os, et la briseure: pren lainne novele, et la moille en aisil et en oile cuit, et met sus lou leu.	Another way of plastering for joints and bones that have moved out of their places, and to alleviate the pain that arises, and the sawing uses bone, and the heating: take new wool, and render it soft in oil and heat, and place it upon its place.
Cist emplastres ne restoure mie, mais il est boins por apaisier d’aposteme chaut, et oste proprement les dolors.	Plastering does not heal completely, but it is better for soothing abscesses and properly treats bone pains.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre qui restoure les os brisiez: pren foilles de figuier seches, et foilles de pavol terrestre, et broie ensamble, et fai emplaustre.	Another method for dressing broken bones that heals them: take dried fig leaves and land beech leaves, grind them together, and make a plaster.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre a la restoration de la brisure de l’os et por amenusier lou remenant de l’aposteme.	Another method of plastering for the restoration of bone breakage and to soothe the removal of pus.
Pren racine de vismalve, camomille, flors de violettes, farine de veces, de chescune une partie; et broie, et confis avec vin, et se li membres est eschaufez, se le confis avec aigue de coriandre moiste, ou d’aigue, et en use.	Take root of valerian, chamomile, violet flowers, flour of comfrey, from each take one part; and grind it, mix with wine, and if the limbs are warm, mix with moist coriander water, or plain water, and use it.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre plus fors que li premier, quant aposteme dur vient a la restauration dou membre.	Another method of plastering more firmly than the first when an abscess is returning to the restoration of the limb.
Pren racines de vismalve, et semence de lin, balauste, mellilote, et sansuce, et flors de violetes et de camomille, de toutes ana une partie; et broie, et confit avec aigue de salz, ou aigue douce, ou avec vin, selonc la chalor du membre, et son repos.	Take roots of vismalve, and sesame seed, balsa wood, melilot, and soapwort, and flowers of violet and chamomile, from all these take a portion; and grind it with salt water, or sweet water, or with wine, according to the heat of the limb and its rest.
Ypocras dist en son livre c’on ne mette sus lou membre brisiet por restorer fuer que cerote fait de cire et d’oile, et nulle autre chose plus, et dist qu’il soit entre dous ne trop molz ne trop durs.	In his book, Hippocrates states that to restore strength in a fractured limb one should apply a salve made of beeswax and oil, and nothing else more. He says it should be between two layers neither too soft nor too hard.
Et il semble galien c’on doit mettre sus lou membre brisiet, por restoreir, choses seches un poc chaudes, si com mirre et aloes et encens et semblans choses, si com nos avons dit.	And it seems to Galen that we should place upon the broken limb for restoration, things slightly moistened but somewhat warm, such as mirr (mastic), aloe, incense and similar things, just as we have said.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre que vaut a lesion et a dolor: pren mugath et chevolz d’omes decopez, ou pennes d’oiseil, et vismalve, et seil igalment, et les broie, et en fai emplaustre et lou lie.	Another method for dressing injuries and pain: take the fat and feathers from cooked sheep or goose carcasses, or bird feathers, and ground coriander seeds equally with them. Grind all these ingredients together to create a poultice which you apply to the wound.
Et puis lou deslie un poc aprés, et pren garde se li malaides ne sent nule dolor, ne ne s’est meus li os de son leu; si ne lou deslie par mains jors Et se dolor vient au leu, ou prurite, sens repos ou enfleure, si te haste, et le deslie, et oste l’emplaustre maintenant; et pren drapeil legier, et esponge de mer moiste, et plonge en aigue, et en leve lou leu, tant que li prurite cesse, et soit apaisie li dolor; puis laisse reposer lou membre une houre, puis met sus lainne seche, moillie en aigue ou en oile roset, et lie sus une nut, tant que tu soies seur d’aposteme chaut; et repose li enflammation dou membre, et soit ostee li dolor, puis rencomence la lieure subtil, et un poc d’emplaustre, et ne l’estraindre mie si fort com devant; et subtilie tant qu’il soit sanez.	Then let the plaster off a little later on, and take care that the patient does not feel any pain or discomfort in their limb or that the bone is not moving from its place; if you let it off manually without haste. If pain begins to occur in the limb, or itching, restlessness or swelling appears, then do it quickly and remove the plaster now; take a light cover and a moistened sea sponge, dip them into water, and soak up the limb until the itching stops and any pain is relieved; then leave the member to rest for an hour, then put on dry hay soaked in water or oil, binding it with a bandage until you are sure that the abscess has drained properly; and allow the inflammation of the limb to subside and the pain to stop before resuming gentle reapplication of the plaster, just a little bit at a time, and do not apply pressure as you did before; continue with this gentle method until they are healed.
Et se tu vois que aposteme chaus et roujor et dolor et enfleure sont jai osteit dou tout, et tu as mestier d’emplaustre et de liien, si le rencomence, si com tu a fait premier igalment.	And if you notice that pus and redness, pain and swelling are subsiding, indicating the injury has healed throughout, then you need plaster and bandaging; start again as you did initially.
Et s’il ne vient au membre nient de ceu que nos avons dit, si ne le desliier fuer que aprés III jors ou IIII ou V ou VII; et aucune fois le laisse XX jors, selonc ce c’on voit, tant que li briseure s’aert, et aproche li ajostement de la char sus; adonques lou restraint plus que premier, et li engroisse sa viande, si com j’ai dit devant; et se tu vois lou leu sechier plus que mestier n’est, saiches que norrissemens n’i puet venir; arose lou donques d’aigue chaude tede, toutes les fois que tu lou deslies, et ce soit chescun tier jor, et eslaiche un poc la lieure; par cest ovraige donques cort li norrissemens au membre, et esmende hastanment ceu que font li fol mire, que restourent le membre tortement: c’est malvais, et si est ovraiges paourous, et je n’i voi autre chose que dou lassier et de l’ovrer droitement.	And if no change occurs in the limb as we have described, or if the dislocation requires to be reset only after three days or four or five or seven; and leave it undisturbed for twenty days, according to what you see, until the pain subsides, and approaches the adjustment of flesh above; then tighten your restraint more than at first, let its muscle grow bigger as I have mentioned before; and if you notice that the limb has dried excessively, know that injuries cannot occur; take a hot water bath each time you reset it, every third day, clean some of the wound; with this action cut out any remaining inflammation in the limb, hasten the process that the blind surgeons are unable to do properly: this is wrong, and such actions are careless, and I see no other way than letting it heal straight.
des diverses manieres de brisure	Through various methods of breaking up
Maintes manieres de brisures sont, et diverses figures, et les causes sont destintees; car il a brisures que sont faites de percussion d’espee, et li colz oste tout l’os jusc’a syfac qui est desoz l’os, si com fait haiche ou fust; et por ceu est apelee ceste maniere de briseure «haichure».	Many methods of fractures exist, and various shapes occur. The causes are specific; for there are fractures that come from the impact of a sword, and the collar bone breaks all the way up to the shoulder joint, just below the bone, like when hit by a spear or cudgel. Because of this, it's called this type of fracture "shattering".
Ou li espee cope l’os par desus sens percier, et est apelee ceste maniere de brisure «absolue»; et est li plaie de ces .ij. brisures grans ou petite.	Or when the sword penetrates the bone from above without passing through, this type of breakage is called "absolute"; and both large and small wounds result from these two kinds of breaks.
Et s’il i a percussion emboee, ou fendure ou de colz de piere, ou de cheoir sus piere, ou d’autres semblans.	And if there is sequential impact, or crack in the bone, or injury from stone, or impact on stone, or other similar occurrences.
Et s’il a brisure persant, qui aproiche jusc’a la toile qui est desoz l’os, ou elle est sus l’os, et est ceste plaie ou grans ou petite.	And if there is a break that approaches until it reaches the tissue beneath the bone, or above the bone, and this wound can be large or small.
Et si a plaie qui est reponue en l’os ausi subtil com uns chevous, et est li fendure petite, et por ceu est apelee ceste brisure «capillaire»; et si la plaie qui est faite ou par ferir de piere, ou par cheoir, ou par semblant chose, et fait entrer la piece de l’os aval, et est li leus chevez si com font li chaudelier quant il fierent sus les chaudieres; si entre li piere dedens.	And if there's a wound that heals within the bone as thin as hair, and has small cracks, and this type of fracture is called "hairline"; and if a wound is made or caused by hitting with stone, falling, or any similar thing, causing the piece of bone to enter from below, and sits between the bones just like candle makers work when making candles on them; so there's an inside the rock.
Et ceu avient plus a sous qui ont ou chief moistes os, si com chief d’enfant; et avient a toutes ces manieres de brisure que pieces menues en sont desevrees si com esteles; et je em parlerai en son leu.	This happens more often in those with wet bones below the head, such as in children's heads; and occurs through all these types of fracture where small fragments are broken off, like in cases of cracking. And I will speak about this when it comes to its place.
Et conoissons toutes manieres de briseures par la detraction sus elles, et l’inquisition a tentes, et par la char corrumpue qui est sus.	And let us know all the ways of breakages through the diminishment above them, and the examination at stakes, and by the corrupt flesh which is upon.
Li semblance capillaire est conue par ceu que quant on a descovert l’os, et on frote enche sus, si apert li brisure noire.	The appearance of hair can be recognized when one has exposed the bone and rubs it inside, revealing the black breakage.
En la cure de la brisure, pren garde as accidens dou malaide, et se tu vois nul malvais accident, si com vomissement de cole, et amission d’entendement, et estension, et paumeson, et fievre ague, et les eulz issir fuer et rougir, et autres semblans em plusors dispositions, si ne puet saner sens doute.	In treating breakage, beware of adverse effects due to malaise, and if you do not encounter any bad side effects such as vomiting bile, loss of consciousness, stretching, pallor, fever ague, and other symptoms appearing in various conditions, it cannot be cured without doubt.
Et se tu ne vois accident espoantauble, et tu esperes salut, si comence la cure.	And if you do not see an alarming mishap, and you hope for salvation, then begin the treatment.
Et quant li navrez vient premier a toi, et c’est en yver, si covient oster l’os devant lou quatorzime jor au mues que tu pues.	And when winter comes first to you, and if it is winter, then it's necessary to remove the bone before the fourteenth day of the month that you can.
Et se c’est en esteit, si te haste d’oster l’os devant lou septime jor, ainsois que li toile desoz l’os soit corrumpue, et vienent li accident que nos avons dit.	And if it is spring, then you should hurry to remove the bone before the seventh day, in such a way that the pus around the bone is rotten, and accidents occur as we have said.
Et se li brisure de l’os vient jusc’a la toile que cuevre lou cerveil, si covient que tu fendes la partie fendue ensi: et est que tu preignes lou chief dou malaide navreit, et descuevre sus l’os en toutes les manieres que tu pues, et sus la figure de la plaie plus souef que tu pues, et se decorrement de sanc vient au descovrir l’os, ou aposteme chaus, se li aide de ceu qu’il covient, et est que tu emplisses lou leu de drapelz moilliez en oile roset; et fai reposer la plaie tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez, et soies asseurez de decorrement de sanc; puis comence entor l’os a oster, et c’est fait selonc II manieres d’ovraige: l’une manieres si est que tu copes au taillement estroit devant, et c’est li forme:	And if breaking of the bone reaches to the membrane that covers the brain, then it is necessary that you cut through the broken part like this: and that you take hold of the forehead of the patient without harming them, and expose on the bone in every way possible, and concerning the figure of the wound as much as possible, and if blood comes out upon exposure of the bone, or an abscess develops, then assist with whatever is appropriate, and ensure that you fill the gap with wet cloths in oil. And let the wound rest until the abscesses disappear and are assured of no further bleeding; then start to remove through the bone from within, this should be done according to two ways of work: one method is that you cut at a narrow angle forward, and this is the form:
Et puis i boute .i. autre taillement plus grant que lou premier.	And then make another cut larger than the first one.
Et li seconde maniere si est que tu aies nombre de taillemens divers, les uns estrois et les autres larges, et soient a pointe, et soient de fer inde; et en oevre legierement, que tu ne bleces le chief.	And the second method is that you have various sizes of knives, some narrow and others wide, and they should be pointed, and made of hard iron; and you use them lightly in your work so as not to injure the head.
Et se li os est fors et durs, si covient que tu lou perces entor, ainsois que tu i aministres taillemens avec tareres, ne mie parfont qu’il ne percent outre l’os dou test, et doit avoir desus la pointe une marge ou .i. cercle, que ne laisse passer la pointe outre l’os; et t’en covient avoir plusors, si que chescuns viegne en son leu de l’espés de l’os, si que tu aies tareres por toz test; et c’est li forme des .iij. manieres de tareres:	And if the bone is too hard, you should drill it internally, so as to apply cuts with awls without going through the soft tissue beyond the bone, and there must be a margin or a circle of about one inch above the point that does not allow the point to go beyond the bone; and you need more than one, so that each goes into its place of the thickness of the bone, so that you have awls for all sides; and this is the shape of the three types of awl cuts.
Li qualitez por percier entor l’os brisiet est que tu mettes .i. tarere sus l’os, et torne a tes dois tant que tu saiches que li os est perciez; puis remet lou tarere autre part un poc aprés, et ensi fai tout entor, puis cope as incisoires l’espaice de l’os qui est entre les pertu, et fai ceu plus subtilment que tu pues, et legierement, si com nos avons dit, tant que tu en traies l’os a ta main, ou a aucun des estrumens que tu as si com tenailles, pinceures; et garde que tu ne touchier au cerveil ne au syfac.	The quality for drilling through the bone is to place an awl on the bone and twist with your fingers until you know that the bone is pierced. Then remove the awl a little further, and do this all around, then cut out the space between the fractures of the bone, and do it as finely and gently as possible, while still using light force, as we have said, either by hand or any tool you have such as tweezers; make sure not to touch the brain or the spinal cord.
Et quant tu avras l’os perciet, et trait, si couvient que tu reses l’apreteit qui est demoree de l’os a tout I autre estrument semblant a un incisoire, mais il covient qu’il soit plus tenves et plus subtilz que li autre incisoire; et s’il demore rien des petis os, ne nulles escailles, si les oste legierement a I des estrumens; puis cure la plaie de tentes et d’oignemens que nos avons dit.	And when you have pierced and treated the bone, it is necessary that you reapply the preparation which has remained from the bone to all other instruments similar to an incisor. But it must be thicker and more delicate than any other incisor; and if there remains nothing of the small bones or no scales, then scrape with light tools; then treat the wound with ointments and remedies as we have said.
Et li autre maniere d’ovraige si est cil que Galiiens dist, qui est plus saus; et le loa molt fort, et c’est sa parole.	And another way of treatment is this, as Galien stated, which is more sparing; and it uses a strong knife, and that is his word.
Il covient premier que tu descuevres une partie de l’os, lai ou li brisure apert mues, si que quant tu avras descovert celle partie, si metras desoz lou chief de cest incisoire lenticulaire, de coi ci est li forme:	It is necessary first to uncover a part of the bone where the fracture opens and moves. So when you have uncovered that part, place underneath the tip of this ophthalmic incisor, as described here:
Et ne trenche mie d’une part, et est li partie ague en II costez, si que li trenchans est devers l’os; puis fier d’un petit maillet sus, si que tu copes legierement l’os tout entor, et te done bien en garde de la toile que est desoz; s’elle est aerse a l’os, si l’oste legierement, car on l’oste bien sens nuisement, et sens paor.	And do not cut from one side alone, and make the cut go towards two sides so that you are cutting against the bone; then strike with a small hammer in such a way that you lightly touch the entire bone, and be careful of the cloth underneath it. If there is flesh under the bone, cut it lightly as well because the bone feels painlessly and without fear.
Et se li brisure de l’os ne perce jusc’a la toile, et li os est copez tant soulement par desus, et il i a petites pieces, si couvient rere celle asperiteit, et oster les escailles au raseur subtil dont tu dois avoir diverses quantitez, por amenistrer en chescun leu le plus covenauble, selonc l’ovraige et la figure de la brisure.	And if the bone break does not pierce until the cloth and only cuts through from above, with small pieces remaining, then after that roughness, use a fine razor to remove the scales. You must have various quantities of this tool in order to administer the most suitable treatment for each location according to the manual and the appearance of the break.
Si reis devant de grant raseurs, et aprés de plus subtilz, et ne cesser de ceu faire tant k’il soit bien.	If you stand before great razors, and after finer ones, and do not stop doing this until it is well done.
En chescune des autres tailleures capillaires et brisure subtil, covient que tu amenistres cause selonc son adrecement; et c’est chose que n’est mie reponue a celui qui a mis son estude en cest art.	In every other hair cutting and delicate breakage, you must adjust your actions according to their direction; this is something that cannot be done by someone who has devoted their study to this craft.
Et se li syfac est descovers, si covient que tu preignes I drapeil de lin, selonc la quantiteit de la plaie, et le moille en oile roset, et le mete sus la plaie; puis pren I autre drapeil doublé en II ou en III, et le moille en vin et en oile roset, et le met sus le premier drapeil; et fai ceu plus legierement que tu pues, que tu ne grever lou syfac, puis aministre par desus I autre liien, et ne l’estraindre mie fuer que tant k’il teigne la plaie soulement; et le laisse ensi I jor ou II, tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez, puis le deslie, et i aministre medicines si com racines de lis, et farine de veces, et poudre d’encens, et aristologe, et semblans choses; et de ces choses fai poudre, et met sus la plaie, et i aministre adés medicines mondefians sens mordication; et warde que li plaie soit adés nette, que tu n’i laissier mie l’oignement, ne n’i laissier mie assembler bowe, car quant bowe s’asemble sus la toile dou cerveil, si la corront et porrist, et avient au malaide grans malice; car quant on met sus lou syfac chose mordant, si nercist par desus.	And if it is discovered that the dislocation is external, then you should take a linen bandage according to the size of the wound, soak it in olive oil and apply it to the wound; afterwards take another double layer bandage, soaked in wine and olive oil, and place it on top of the first bandage; do this with as little force as possible so that you don't burden the dislocation, then administer another layer above it without pulling too hard until it touches only the wound; keep this way for one or two days, until the abscess subsides, then release the dislocation and administer medicines such as lily roots, corn flour, incense powder, and various other things; from these ingredients make a powder and apply it to the wound, then begin administering foreign medicines without causing irritation; be sure that the wound is cleaned properly, do not leave any ointment on it, nor allow it to stick together, for when paste sticks onto the cloth covering the brain, it will spread and cause great harm to the patient; because when one applies something irritating to the dislocation, it becomes irritated from above.
Pren warde donques, se nulz mavais accidens vient au malaide, si com nos avons dit, si est doutable sens doute.	Take care then, so that no harmful events occur to the patient as we have said, in case there is doubt without doubt.
Et se noiror n’i vient fuers que por la medicine c’on a mise sus, que teil vertu ait, si covient que tu preignes une partie de miel, et III parties d’oile roset et en glue I drapel, et lou met sus lou syfac; puis lou cure de manieres de cures qu’il couvient, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if the smell does not come out only because of the medicine we have applied there, and it has that power, then you should take a part of honey, and three parts of rose oil, and one spoonful of glue, and put them on the wound; then treat as proper treatment should be done until it heals.
Saiches que aucune fois sont brisies les .ij. parties dou neis desus, ou li une par li soulement, car ce sont .ij. os; et cil desoz est cartillaginous, et ne brise mie, si ne fait fuer k’enbower ou tordre, et puis saine.	Know that neither of the two parts above the nose are broken, or only one if necessary, as these consist of two bones; and the one below is cartilaginous, it does not break, nor will it allow bending or twisting once healed.
Et se l’une des II parties est brisie, si covient que tu boutes ton petit doi ou pertus dou neis, et met igal cele brisure dedens a ton doi indice, et au pouchet par defuer, tant que li neis reveigne selonc sa figure natureil; et fai ce legierement, et warde que li malaides ne sente dolor par ton ovraige.	And if one of the two parts is broken, it should be that you pinch your little finger or the back of your nose, and place an equal break inside your index finger, and through the nostril outwardly, until the nose revives according to its natural shape; do this gently, and be careful not to allow the patient to feel pain through your action.
Et se li brisure est en la partie desus lou neis, et ne puet venir li dois au leu, si couvient que tu lou mettes igal au chief d’un rait un poc gros.	And if the break is above the nose part and cannot reach to its place at the head, then it is necessary that you make it equal to the tip of a stick somewhat thick.
Et se li brisure est de II pars, si refai autretel, et te haste de restorer lou premier jor, se tu pues; se ce non, aprés lou septime ou le disime, quant li apostemes chaus est apaisiez, puis bouthe au chief dou neis tentes de drapelz de lin, se li brisure est en une partie.	And if the break is of two parts, redo that procedure and hurry to restore it on the first day if you can; should this not be possible, after the seventh or eighth day when the abscess has subsided, then pinch at the base of your nose with a linen cloth square, if the break is in one part.
Ou tu boutes .i. autre d’autre part, se li brisure i est; et soient les tentes si grosses qu’eles emplissent les pertus dou neis.	When you pull one to another on the other side, if breaking occurs; and make sure they are as large as they fill the cavities in the nose.
Et dirent aucun restorour c’on doit moillier les tentes em burre, et muer chescun jor.	And they say no healer should grease the nipples with butter, and change each day.
Il ne me semble mie que ce soit bien, mais covient qu’elles soient moillies en confection d’aubun d’uef, et de poudre de molin; puis laisse la tente, tant que li os soit fers, et li cartilaiges endurcis.	I believe it might not be correct, but they need to be greased during the preparation of a hen's egg mixture, and with powder from grinding; then leave the nipple until the bone becomes hard, and the cartilage is toughened.
Et aucune fois boute on ou neis pennes d’oie en leu de tentes, et si a .i. souef drapeil entor, et se tient la briseure, et soffle li malaides parmi; or fai lou kel ke tu vues.	And every time you pull out the original or nose feathers in place of the tents, and if it's one egg with an inner layer of skin, and keeps the wound intact, and lets the air pass through; do as you see fit.
Et se apostemes chaus vient au neis tandis com tu i oevres, si i met cerote ou coton moilliet en oile roset, ou en .i. poc de dyaquilon.	And if abscesses come to the nose in the same way as you are doing it, then put a poultice or wet cotton in oil mixed with it, or in one corner of a spoonful of snail juice.
Et se apostemes chaus n’i vient, si met emplastre par defuer, de farine de sisament, et de poudre d’encens, confites avec aubun d’uef, puis met sus estoupes legieres, et ne liier mie lou neis; et se li brisure dou neis est petite, et il est brisiés em menues pieces, si l’estrai as estrumens covenables a ceu, puis cout la fendure, et la cure de choses enjanrans char, et soudant, si com emplastres et oignemens covenables a ceu; et s’il n’a dedens lou neis nule plaie, si lou cure de tentes, et i met cainnes de plonc, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if the abscesses leak out, then apply a plaster outside, of corn flour and incense powder, mixed with egg yolk. Then place them on light bandages without tying them tightly; and when the bandage pieces break down into small parts, and are broken into small fragments, you should remove them using instruments suitable for this purpose; then cut along the wound, and cleanse everything in a process of heating and soldering like plasters and ointments suitable for this task; and if there is no injury under the bandage, treat it as usual, and you should apply pieces of opium until it heals.
de la routure de la mandibule	Of the rupture of the jawbone
Quant li mandibule est route desoz, et il n’i a point de plaie defuer, et li brisure est defuer tant soulement, et n’est mie brisiez en dous, fuer que corbelz dedens, si le conoist on legierement.	When the jawbone is broken externally, and there's no wound outwardly, only the fracture is external. It isn't broken into two halves completely; rather it breaks internally as well, which can be discerned lightly.
Il covient, se li brisure est en la destre partie, que tu boutes ton doi indice en la bouche dou malaide; et se li brisure est en la mandibule senestre, si boute ton doi indice de la main destre, et boute la brisure dedens legierement, et l’afaite a l’autre main par defuer, et met igal.	It is necessary, should the break occur in the right part of the jawbone, to press your index finger into the mouth at the site where the patient is suffering; and if the break occurs in the left mandibular part, you must use your index finger from the right hand, press gently on the break internally, and then proceed with the operation by making an incision externally with the other hand.
Et se li brisure de la mandibule est desevree en .ij., si covient que tu aministres extension de .ij. pars, tant qu’il soit igalz.	And if there is a break in both parts of the jawbone, it must be treated with extension of half parts, until they are equal.
Et se commovemens des dens avient, ou routure, si les estrain d’un fil d’or ou d’argent ou de soie, puis met sus la mandibule brisie cerote, et met sus .i. drapel double; et met sus lou drapel une grant estele bien faite, ou une piece de cuir igal, longe et large selonc la mandibule, et la lie sus au mues que tu pues, et comande a malaide qu’il se repose, et menjuce viandes legieres.	And if tooth movements occur, or rupture, then hold them with a thread of gold, silver or silk. Then place wax on the broken jaw, and place two pieces of cloth on top; and place one large pad well made under this cloth piece, or a leather piece equal to it in length and width according to the jaw size, and tie it on as much as you can. Command the patient to rest, and have light meals.
Et se tu vois que li figure se chainge, si le deslie au tier jor, et puis remet a point ceu que c’est chaingiet; et met emplaustre sus, de la poudre dou moulin avec abun d’uef ou farine de sisament, aprés ceu que tu as osteit lou cerote; et met sus l’emplaustre lainne legiere, et se li emplaustres s’aert, et li disposition dou malaide ne se chainge, laisse le tant k’il soit sanez; maintes fois est sanez en .iij. semainnes.	And if you notice that the figure changes, then reposition it on the third day and thereafter put back into place whatever has shifted; apply plaster to this area, mix powdered chalk with abundant egg or sesame flour after removing the wax; cover the plaster with fine wool, and when the plaster hardens and the patient's position does not change anymore, let them be like that until they are healed; many times it is healed in three weeks.
Et se apostemes chaus vient, si amenistre ceu que nos avons dit maintes fois.	And if pus-filled ulcers come about, then apply what we have repeatedly instructed.
Et s’il i a brisure et plaie ensamble, rewarde se nule piece de l’os en est ostee; si subtilie de l’oster as estrumens covenaubles a ceu.	And if there is a fracture combined with a wound together, reward nothing of the bone has been removed; so much skill in extracting tools needed for this task is required.
Et se li plaie est estroite, si l’eslarge a flaime selonc ta necessiteit.	And if the wound is narrow, widen it with fire according to your need.
Et quant tu avras ostees toutes ces pieces, et il n’i demore nule, si cout la plaie, s’ele est large, et met sus .i. des emplaustres covenaubles a ceu, por enjanrer char, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when you have removed all these pieces and there is nothing left, if the wound is wide, place one plaster over it suitable for this purpose to promote healing until it heals.
de la forcele	with strength
Li forcele brise plusors fois devant, devers l’espaule, et li brisure si est selonc .iij. manieres: ou elle est brisie et desevree en .ij., et i a pieces, et est li plus legiere a restorer; ou il i a brisure avec plaie.	The force breaks many times before reaching the shoulder, and each break occurs in three ways: it may break completely and be separated into two parts, leaving fragments that are easier to restore; or there might be a break accompanied by an injury.
Et li ovraiges si est quant li brisure est sens plaie, que tu aies .ij. ministres, si que li uns teigne l’ajutoire que sent la forcele brisie; et li autres estende lou col vers la partie; puis met igal la brisure a tes dois, si que li forme soit si com il covient, et n’i ait ne apparance ne chevement.	And in the cases where there is a break accompanied by an injury, if you have two helpers, so that one marks the shoulder where the force breaks; and the other extends their hand towards the affected part. Then align the break with your fingers, ensuring the shape matches how it should be, without any appearance or movement of the break.
Et se tu a mestier de plus estendre, si met desoz l’espaule au malaide une spere reonde de drap, ou de lainne, et soit grosse selonc ta necessiteit; et estent et lieve la forcele, et estraint le spere a ta main, si que tu mettes igal la brisure, si com il covient.	And if you need to extend further, place a round sponge of cloth or wool under the shoulder and side, with its size according to your needs; stretch out and lift the force (meaning pressure), while restraining the sponge in your hand so that you can align the break correctly, as it should be.
Et se tu ne pues traire le chief de la forcele au defuer, por ceu qu’elle vient em parfont, si covient que li malaides gise sovin sus son hatereil, et met desoz l’espaule .i. oreillier moien, et boute li ministres l’espaule aval, tant que li os de la forcele soit levez.	And if you cannot draw the head from the strength's force behind it, because it comes forward, then the patient must lie with their head resting on their pillow, and place one of the shoulder's cushions under both shoulders. Have the attendants press the shoulder downwards until the bone of the strength rises.
Et puis adrece la brisure a tes dois, et se tu lou trueves debrisiet, si covient que tu fendes sus; et trai fuer les pieces legierement, et se li os ne puet joindre por aucun sormontement, si le cope a l’un des incisoires que tu as; mais que tu mettes desoz la forcele cest estrument, por warder lou syfac:	And then strike the break with your fingers, and if you find fragments, it is necessary to cut there; and pull gently on the pieces. If the bone cannot join at all pressures, then use one of the incisors that you have; but place this instrument against the strength, to guide this surgery:
et semble une cuiller, et n’est mie chevez, et soit ausi large com il lou covient, selonc la grandor de l’os et la possance de l’uevre; et ait II chiés, si com tu vois, et soit li uns larges, et li autres estrois, si com est li routure de la plaie que tu as fait quant tu as trait les os; et quant tu es asseurez d’aposteme chaut, si cout la plaie, et se li routure est petite, ou tu doutes aposteme chaut, si emple la plaie de drapelz et de tentes, selonc sa quantiteit.	And seems like a spoon, and isn't there anywhere, and is as wide as it should be, according to the size of the bone and the power of the operation; and has two heads, as you see, and one is broad, and the other narrow, just like the wound you have made when treating bones; and when you are sure about an abscess each time, if you cover the wound, and if the wound is small, or if you doubt there's an abscess each time, if you cover the wound with bandages and tents, according to its quantity.
Et se apostemes chaus i vient, si moille .i. drapel en oile roset et en aisil et en vin, et met sus.	And when the abscesses are drained, if it is moist, soak bandages in oil rose and in sweat and wine, and place them on top.
Li estrignement de l’os, quant il est sens plaies et sens tailleure, est que tu mettes sus l’os l’enplaustre de la poudre dou molin et d’aubun d’uef, et met estoupes legieres sus, et met une spere desoz l’assele, se tu en as mestier; puis pren une tres grant bende d’une palme de large, puis met I drapeil double sus estoupes, et l’emplaustre; puis pren une estele subtil de III dois de large et de lonc, et l’envoloupe entor celui bendeil, si que li chief dou bendeil soient pendant; et met l’estele sus la briseure, et torne le bendeil sus lou col, et desoz l’asselle sainne, et desoz l’asselle malaide; et la ramoinne de chescune partie, et quant tu vois ke li lieure tient la briseure avenanment, et tu vois clerement que li estele ne se muet desus l’os brisiet, si le rewarde chescun jor, et quant li liiens eslaiche, si lou restraint; et fai gesir lou malaide sus son dos, et li met quant il dort I petit orillier desoz l’assele, por lever l’ajutoire en haut; si aligera li brisure de la forcele par l’aligement de l’espaule, ou tu li lie lou bras au col, et ne lou desliier se malvais accidens n’i vient, jusc’a XX jors; puis rencomence l’emplaustre, se tu vois qu’il en ait mestier, et l’estraint et le laisse ensi, tant qu’il soit restorez; et elle est restoree au plus en XXVIII jors, et en moins a aucuns homes.	The grinding of bone, when it is in the presence of wounds and measurement, is that you place on the bone the plaster made from powder ground in the mill and egg yolk. Place light spoons over it, and if needed put a nail under it; then take a very large band about a palm wide, then place double cloth on top of the spoons, and plaster it. Then take a subtle strap about three finger widths wide and long, wrap it around that band, so that the ends are hanging down, and place this strap over the wound, and twist the band up to the neck, and under the healthy side, and under the sick side; and apply pressure from each part, and when you see that the ligament holds the wound in place well, and you clearly see that the strap is not moving above the broken bone, then you relieve it every day, and once the stitches are removed, then you keep holding it. Make sure the illness leaves on its backside, and while he sleeps, place a small pillow under the side, to lift up the shoulder; if this relieves the strain of the force by aligning the shoulder joint, or you tie his arm around his neck, not letting him move in case of any bad incidents occur, for at most 20 days; then restart the plastering if necessary and keep it bound like that until he is restored. And she/he is fully restored within 28 days, and less time in some cases.
de la brisure de l’espaule	From the breaking of the shoulder
Poc avient que li espaule brise ou large leu ne em mileu, et ne lou seit on fuers que par lou touchement; si l’apareille selonc la figure de la brisure, et la ramoinne selonc sa forme natureil, en toutes les manieres que tu pues; puis met sor le leu poudre dou molin avec abun d’uef, et estoupes legieres, et met sus I drapeil double; puis met sus une estele large et subtil, un poc plus large de l’espaule, et se desoz l’estele est chevemens en aucun leu de l’espaule, si emple celle cheveure d’estoupes de lin, si que li estele siece igalment; et puis l’estraint a tout une grant bende fermement, si que li estele ne se mueve de son leu, et regarde le liien chescun jor; et toutes les fois k’il amolist, si l’estraint, et met igal l’estele s’elle est fuer de son leu, et gise li malaides sus son costeit; et li espaule est restouree en XX jors ou en xxv, Et quant cist nombres est acomplis, si le deslie, et soies seur, car ce n’est mie os qui se mette fuer legierement.	A fracture affects either the top or middle of the shoulder, and not just from an external source; it is determined based on the shape of the break, treated according to its natural form, in any way you can. Then apply a powder made with mill-ground flour along with raw eggs, and light compresses, then place two layers of cloth over it. Next, lay a broad but subtle stick slightly wider than the shoulder, such that there are no parts of the shoulder under this stick; cover these areas with linseed wadding so that the stick sits evenly; and then secure everything tightly into one large bandage firmly, ensuring the stick does not move from its place. Check each day's healing process; and every time it loosens, you tighten again until the wadding is in equilibrium if it has moved off its place, placing the patient on their side; and the shoulder remains healed after twenty to twenty-five days. And once this number of days is completed, remove the dislocation, and be sure, because it's not bone that quickly settles into position.
Et se une piece de l’os tent avant, et point desoz lou keur, si fent sus, et l’oste, et fai ceu que nos avons dit en la brisure de la forcele d’apaisier aposteme chaut. de la brisure dou pis	of the breaking of the foot

Saiches que li briseure des costes ne vient fuer que en leus gros aprés le dos, et au chief dedens, et ne ploient fuer que por ceu qu’eles sont glairouses; et le sent om bien a l’inquisition as dois. de la brisure dou col	Of the breaking of the neck

de la brisure de l’ajutoire	Regarding the breaking of the shoulder.

Si l’adrece, si com nos avons dit.	If the address, as we have said.
Et se nulz telz accidens n’i vient, si ne lou desliier fuer que aprés III jors ou plus, et dorme li malaides sus son dos, et ait ses mains sus son stomac; et met desoz l’ajutoire I cussin plain de laine igalment, et regarde chescune houre dou jor ou de la nut, que li figure dou membre brisiet ne se mueve, ou ne soit amollis li liiens; si l’adrece par la vertu de medicine, et li done la viande que nos avons devant mis, en teil maniere que li viande soit au premier subtilz; et quant il comance a reprendre, si soit grosse.	And if no such events come about, nor the healing is only after three days or more, and the patient sleeps on his back, with his hands on his stomach; and place underneath the shoulder one inch of wool evenly, and observe each hour of that day or night, so that the figure of the broken limb doesn't move or become softened by the ligament; if the address through the virtue of medicine, and gives it the meat that we have placed in front, in such a manner that the meat is at first subtle; and when it begins to heal, it becomes large.

Et se li estricture est laide et emboee, si demore a desliier L jors ou II mois.	And if the constriction is ugly and tangled, it should be left for loosening for one or two months.
de la brisure du bras	of the breaking of the arm
Li bras est compos de .ij. os, qui sont apelez li dui «foscile», de coi li uns est petis, et est cil qui enseut le pouchet; et li autres est grans, et est cil qui est desoz, devers lou petit doi; par aventure brise li grans foscile soulement, ou li petis, et par aventure andui ensamble.	The arm is made up of two bones, which are called the 'fosciles'. One bone is smaller, and it is this one that protects the elbow; while the other bone is larger, and it is this one that lies beneath the small head. Sometimes only the large foscile breaks or both might break together.
Quant li petis fosciles est brisiez, li restaurations est legiere, et li sanations; et quant li grans est brisiez, si est li sanation male, et plus griés que quant il sont brisiez andui ensamble.	When the small pieces break off, the restoration is light, and the healing. And when the large ones break, the healing is bad, and more painful than when they broke together.
Se c’est li petis foscile qui est brisiez soulement, si le covient poc estendre legierement, et mettre igal.	If only the small bone breaks off, it should be gently extended and made equal.
Et se c’est li grans foscile, si le covient estraindre plus fort; et l’estende sus I cussin, et teigne le pouchet de la main plus haut des autres, et li petis dois plus bas des autres dois, et soit li malaides croisiez sus lui meisme, et I cussin devant lui plus haut, que li malaides ne soffre nule labor; puis estende li ministres som bras a la partie desoz a sa main, ou a I liien, et uns autres ministres a I autre au desus.	And if it's the large bone that breaks off, you should pull harder. Extend it to one foot above, and pinch the hand's pouch higher than the others, and the small fingers lower than the other fingers. And let the bones cross themselves against themselves, with one foot in front of him slightly higher so that the bones don't suffer any strain; then extend your assistants' arms at this part below his hand, or elbow, and another assistant above the other.
Et puis le mette li mires igal, selonc sa millor forme.	And then place the eyes evenly, according to their best form.

And if during the breaking into pieces, you place each back in its original position, and if none of them is broken to be grasped by the hand, and you cannot restore it to its original position, then you do work on and the bone, as we said before.
Et se avec la briseure a plaie, je en ai parleit au chapistre singuler; si pren la cure.	And if during the wound caused by the breakage, which I have discussed in the single chapter; take the treatment.
Et se en l’encomencement dou restorement sorvient apostemes chaus, si glue I drapeil de cerote fait d’oile roset et de cire blainche, que ne soit mie ne trop durs ne trop molz; et lie I drapeil par sus subtilment, tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez.	And if during the beginning of reattachment abscesses appear, then apply a bandage made of ointment from rosin and white beeswax, so that it is neither too hard nor too soft; and place the bandage finely downwards, until the abscesses are alleviated.
Et puis oste lou cerote, et i met l’emplaustre de la poudre dou molin avec abun d’uef, pues met les esteles, et soit li estele de la briseure adés plus fors, et un poc plus large que les autres; et saiches que il doit avoir VI esteles ou bras em plusors dispositions: soit que li briseure soit en l’un des os, soit en II; et estraint plus sus la briseure que autre part, et toz jors moins en aloignant, si com j’ai dit au comencement dou chapistre; et soient li drapelz que sont sus la briseure molz et moistes, et ne soient mie dur ne aspres; et soit li filz, dont il est estrains, de lin, ne trop gros ne trop menus, si com nos avons dit.	And then apply the rosin, and place the plaster made from the mill powder mixed with plenty of egg, put the splints in, and ensure that the splint against inflammation is more exposed to the air than others, and slightly larger than the rest. Know that there should be six or more splints arranged in various ways: either where the inflammation is within one bone, or within two; and hold it closer near the inflammation than elsewhere, as I mentioned at the beginning of this chapter; and keep the bandages that cover the inflammation soft and moist, so they are neither hard nor abrasive; and use the threads made from linen that are neither too thick nor too thin, as we have said.
Et rewarde lou membre et lou liien aprés aucuns jors.	And reward the limb and the connection after some days.
Et se aucuns mavais accidens vient au membre, si com prurite ki vient au membre, si covient que tu aroses lou membre d’aigue chaude, tant que cil prurites soit apaisiez; et laisse le membre ne mie estroit reposer.	And if any bad incidents occur to the limb, such as itching that comes to the limb, it is necessary that you immerse the limb in hot water until that itch subsides; and leave the limb not allowed to rest.
Et puis rencomence l’estrignement, et se li liiens est amolis et li os desevrez, et semblant chose, si l’adresce.	And then continue the reduction, and if the ligaments have been torn and the bones exposed, and resembling a thing, perform it.
Et se pren warde se li norrissemens ne puet venir au membre, por ceu qu’il est trop estrois, si covient que tu l’amollisses .i. poc, et laisse ensi aucuns jors, tant que li norrissemens i corre, et puis l’estraint.	And if precaution is taken so that no distresses cannot come to the limb because it is too constricted, it should be that you soften it with pox (a kind of compress or poultice), and leave it in this manner for a few days, until the distresses have passed, and then you should tighten.
Et se nules de ces choses que nos avons dit ne vient au malaide, si ne lou desliier jusc’a XX jors.	And if none of these things we have said come to the patient, or the release does not happen until after twenty days.
ou enqui entor, puis li pent les mains a son col, et soit ses cols igalz, et se warde de movement et de degitement, et dorme sus son dos; et saiches que ceste briseure est restoree en XXX jors ou en XXXV, et par aventure en XX jors, selonc les compositions et les complexions des vertus. de la brisure de la main	Of the breaking of the hand
Saiches que au dos de la main et as nous des dois avient poc de briseures, et n’i vient mais que ploieure maintes fois.	Know that on the back of the hand and around our thumbs there are few breaks, and only bending happens many times.
Et quant li plante de la main est brisie ou ploie, si covient que li malaides siece croisiet, et siet droitement devant lui igalement; puis met sa main sus la toie estendue, et estende li ministres les os brisiez, et les mete igalz li mires, tant qu’il soient bien joint; et met l’emplastre et les estoupes, se apostemes n’i vient, puis i met une estele selonc la quantiteit dou leu; et soit envoloupee en .i. drapeil de lin.	And when the sole of the hand is broken or bent, it should be treated so that the parts heal in a straight line and directly in front of him equally; then place his hand on an extended surface, and extend the fingers with the broken bones, placing them evenly under each eye, until they are properly aligned; then apply the bandage and splints if no abscess forms, and then place an elevation according to the size of his bed; and wrap it in one layer of linen.
Et se li briseure est au pardedens entor lou ventre de la plante, si fai une spere de drapelz, et comande au malaide qu’il l’estrigne a sa plante brisie; et puis l’estrain d’un lonc drapeil, et soit li estele de keur souef ausi grans com li plante de la main, et l’estraint, si com il covient.
