Et se li briseure vient a aucun des nous des dois, se c’est li pouchés, si le met igal, si com il covient; et l’estraint avec la plante, et se tu vues si met une estele droite petite por lever la briseure, et ne se mueve; et se li brisure est as autres dois, si com en l’indice ou l’un des autres, si le met igal, et lou lie avec lou doi sain qui est aprés; ou tu les lie toz en .i. tenant, que mues vaut, ou tu met sus une estele, si com ou pouchet; et pren warde en la restauration et en la disposition d’aposteme chaut, et secor ceu qui i vient, si com j’ai dit.	And if the breakage affects neither of my fingers, it's the thumb case, and you should place them equally, as is appropriate; and apply pressure with the sole, and if you see fit to use a small right electrode to lift the breakage, and keep it still; and if the breakage occurs on one of the other fingers like in the index or any other, then you should place them equally, and tie them with a healthy finger that follows; or you can tie all together, considering each's position, or you put an electrode here like you would for the thumb; take care in maintaining and arranging the treatment at each stage, and help those who are coming up against problems, as I have explained.
de la cuixe brisie	Of the broken kneecap
Li os de la cuixe est maintes fois brisiez, et bien le voit on quant elle torne devant et derrier; et li restauration si est c’on lie .i. liien desus la briseure, et .i. autre desoz.	The bone of the elbow is often broken, and one can see it when it turns in front and behind; and the restoration happens as follows: first, one ties a bandage above the break, and secondly underneath it.
Et li malaides gise sus sa faice, puis estende chescuns ministres son lien a sa part igalment; et c’est quant li brisure est emmi l’os.	And the wounds lie on their face, then stretch each of their joints to their equal parts; and this is when the break has reached into the bone.
Et se li brisure est prochiene a la racine de la cuixe, si soit li uns des liiens devers lou poignil, et li autres liiens desoz la briseure.	And if the break is close to the root of the arm, then one end should be tied towards the hand, and the other end away from the break.
Et ausi s’elle est prochiene au genoil, et adonques soit li liens delez lou genoil, et soit li extension aval; puis mette li mires l’os igal a ses II mains, tant qu’il soit selonc sa figure natureil, et puis met l’emplaustre, et lou lie, se apostemes chaz n’i vient.	And if it is close to the elbow, then place one end of the bandage around the elbow, and the other end at the lower part; then position your eyes on the bone equally with both hands until it matches its natural shape, and then apply the plaster and tie it up, should an abscess not appear.
Et s’il i a aposteme chaut, si le laisse apaisier puis revien a ton ovraige et a ta cure; li lieure est faite en teil maniere.	And if there is an abscess to deal with, let it heal first before returning to your work and treatment; the incision is made in such a manner.
Il covient que tu envoloupes sus la briseure I bendeil dur doublé en II ou III, et en demoure li superfluitez, puis torne la jambe tant que li talons veigne a la racine de la naige, et boute I fil lonc entre la cuixe et la jambe, delez lou genoil desoz, et veignent li chief dou fil au desus; puis torne sus la jambe et sus la cuixe le bendeil, puis met sus la briseure esteles, et met une estele sus l’os de la jambe; puis emple le leu vuit entre la jambe et la cuixe de drapelz souef por mettre igal l’estrignement, puis comence a liier forment III tors ou IIII sus la briseure; et quant plus vas en sus de la briseure, et moins l’estraint; puis enten as II chiés dou fil que tu as bouteit entre la jambe et la cuixe, et en lie III esteles que sont desus, puis revai au desoz au chief dou fil, tant que tu veignes delez le piet; et l’estraint, si qu’il ne se mueve de son leu, puis le laisse ensi, puis k’il n’i vient ne aposteme ne enfleure n’autre semblant.	It is necessary that you wrap around the break with two or three doubled bands of hard cloth, leaving excess material. Then turn your leg until the heels reach the root of the knee, and secure the thread lengthwise between the arm and leg, from below the elbow downwards; then guide the tip of the thread above. After this, loop back up to the leg and arm with the bandage again, then place a marker on the break area, and another on the bone of the leg; then distribute eight layers of drapery cloth between the leg and arm to ensure even pressure. Then begin binding in three or four turns around the break. When moving beyond the break point, you should tighten less, then secure with two threads that you've inserted between the leg and arm, fastening them three times from above, then return below the tip of your thread until it's covered by the skin; and finally tighten so it doesn't move from its place, then leave it like this until no further swelling or signs appear.
Et s’il i avient, si le deslie, et adresce ceu que i vient, si com nos avons dit maintes fois; et se il i a pieces de l’os que poigne, si le covient ewer, s’om puet; et s’on ne puet, si covient fendre le leu, et traire fuer; et le cure si com nos avons dit, tant k’il soit sanez.	And if it happens that it dislocates again, reposition as what we have said many times; and if there are pieces of bone that catch, it is necessary to extract them if possible; and if you cannot, then it is necessary to cut through the wound, and drain the fluid; and treat in the way we have said, until it heals.

de la brisure de la jambe	of the fracture of the leg
Saiches que en la jambe ait II os, de coi li uns est apelez par droit non «mustelz», et li autres est apelez «foscile»; et avient tout auteil briseure com il vient au bras, et por ceu est li restauracion si com celle dou bras igalment, et li ovraiges est tout i. Et se li dui os sont brisiet ensamble, si torne li jambe de toutes pars.	Know that in the leg are two bones, of which one is named "mustelz" by its proper name and the other is named "foscile"; and you can suffer from any kind of breakage as you would with an arm. Therefore, restoration works similarly to what we do for a broken arm, and the procedures are just like that for the arm in every way. And if both bones are broken together, then the leg turns in all directions.
Et se li os subtilz est brisiez, si torne devant.	And if the delicate bones are broken, then turn in front.
Et se li gros os est brisiez, si sent on grant dolor, et le voit on bien; et torne desoz.	And if the large bone is broken, one feels great pain and sees it very clearly; then the leg twists around.

So apply stretching, and make it even, and tie the joints evenly; but still, when there is malformation, or there are more than several pieces, that stretching should be less and lighter. And when you have accomplished your task, take two ropes of hawser that bind the leg on both sides and are as long as the leg from the knee down to there; then wrap them twice around each of the two large ligaments above and below, tying them in the middle so that the leg cannot move either right or left. And thus it is well done; and no one should treat with a single rope of this length made of hawser, and they put the leg to rest from movement, doing this properly at the break where there is an injury; and move the leg every day to see if any abscess forms or any other incident occurs; heal it as long as it is sound.
de la brisure des os dou piet	From the breaking of bones at the knee
A la cheville ne vient point de brisure, mais as os dou piet vient aucune fois brisure et as dois poc, et n’i avient fuer que quassure em plusor dispositions. And if breaking occurs at the bones of the knee, and you see these bones press one against another, place those bones in the ground like they wanted to go, just as it would with them trying to move. Et quant .iij. jors ou .iiij. seront passez, si deslie lou liien, car tu troveras les os igalz, soient brisiez, soient desaluez.	And once three or four days have passed, you'll find that the ligaments are equal; whether they were broken or dislocated.

And you must not forget the other things I have said about other injuries, once we've discussed them; and attend to each incident according to how it should be.
de la brisure de l’os dou poignil	of the breaking of the hand bone
Quant li os de la nature la femme est brisiez, si la fai seoir enlargie, puis l’encline a la partie dou dos, et soit tenue par derrier; puis emplisse li baile la nature de la malaide de couton, et en i mette ausi gros com I sto; puis deboute la femme, et lieve lou dos poc et poc, et adonques saut li coton, tant qu’il vient a l’entree de la nature, et revient li os avec lou sto; et quant elle vuet pissier, si oste lou coton, et quant elle a pissiet, se li remette, et ensi faice VII jors ou entor: si sera restoree li brisure, et se tu vues, pren une vessie de berbis, et lie au pertus une cainne, et boute toute la vessie en la nature; puis soffle en la cainne forment, tant que li vessie soit enflee dedens: la nature si revenra li brisure; puis soit emplie de coton, et le laisse ensi aucuns jors, tant qu’il soit sanez.	When the bones of nature are broken in a woman, if she is allowed to swell and then laid on her back towards the part of the spine, held at the buttocks; then fill the gap with the padding of nature's own wound, and put it also as full as possible. Then stand up the woman, lift the back little by little, and then jump out the cotton until it reaches the entrance of nature, returning the bone with the same action. And when she wants to urinate, remove the cotton, and when she has urinated, put her back again and do this for seven or more days: the break will be restored; if you see fit, take a bladder of goat's skin, tie it at one end with a stick, and fill the entire bladder into nature; then blow air into the stick until the bladder is inflated internally. Nature will return to restore the break, then fill it with cotton and leave in that manner for some days until healed.
Et quant li os dou poignil de l’ome est brisiez, ou de la femme, si le restoure ensi com nos avons dit en l’os de la hainche; et ne sont mie occultees ces briseures prochienes a celui qui i met son estude et son us, et entent mon livre.	And when the bone of the hand in the body is broken, or in woman, if it is restored in such a way as we have said in the hip bone; and these nearby fractures are not hidden from him who devotes his study and use to it, and hear my book.
Car li brisure li signifie em plusors dispositions la droite voie de la restauration: enten le donques.	For the breaking means in many positions the right way of restoration: so understand it then.
En la verge, quant elle est brisie, pren une gorge d’oie et i boute la verge; puis envoloupe drapelz entor, et le laisse .iij. jors ou enqui entor, et il sera sanez hastanment.	In the case of a broken penis, take an oyster shell and fill it with the penis; then wrap it securely in cloth, and leave it for three days or as long as needed, and it will heal quickly.
de brisure avec plaie	of fracture with wound
Il covient a celui qui a brisure avec plaie, meismement s’elle est grans, si com li os de la cuixe ou de l’ajutoire ou semblant, qu’il soit sainiez maintenant, si que les sainies que nos avons dit le tesmoignent.	It is necessary for the one who has a fracture with wound, even if it's large, like in the case of a rib or shoulder blade or similar, that it be treated surgically now, so that the surgeries we have mentioned can attest to this.
Et se li plaie saine, si la restainche de vitriole, se tu n’as autre chose, puis rencomence a restorer la briseure en cele meisme houre, ou celui jor, se apostemes chaus n’i vient.	And if the wound is healing well, one may use vinegar to do so, should you have nothing else; then proceed to heal the fracture in that same hour or day. If abscesses form and remain there, however, then start again on the treatment of the fracture at that point.
Et se apostemes chaus i vient, si laisse la restauration jusc’a nuevime jor, tant que li apostemes soit apaisiez, et n’i touchier ne au tier jor ne au quart, car tu i feroies venir malvais accident.	And should abscesses continue to form and remain there, let the healing process continue for a new day, until the abscesses are subdued. Don't touch them on the third or fourth day, as you would cause unwanted complications.
Et se li os brisiez est aparans sus lou keur descovert, si covient que tu lou mettes a point legierement a tes mains, a extension petite.	And if the bone is broken and visible under the uncovered part of your body, you should place it lightly with your hands, in a small extension.
Et se li extensions ne t’est apareillie por mettre igal a tes mains, si le ramoine a cest estrument qui est de fer, qui a .vij. dois ou .viij. de lonc, et li largesce est selonc la quantiteit de la plaie; et por ceu est mestier au mire qu’il empreigne .iii. ou iiij., selonc ceu qu’il en ait mestier en chescune cure de briseure; et soit rons et un poc gros, k’il ne ploie mie a la compression sus lou membre a ton ovraige, et soit agus devant, et gros des le mileu en avant, ensi:	And if the extension does not appear for you to place it evenly with your hands, then take this tool made of iron which is .vij. or .viij. inches long, and its width corresponds to the size of the wound; and in each case of a broken bone, the surgeon must insert three or four (depending on his needs), according to what he requires for each treatment of fracture; it should be round and slightly thick so that it does not bend under compression against your limb when working, and it should be sharp at both ends, and thick at the middle towards the front.
Et est apelez «palainche», por coi il covient que li chiés corbes soit mis sus lou chief de l’os apparent; et le boute a une fois, tant k’il reviegne, et soit igalz l’un encontre l’autre.	And it is called 'palainche' because it must be that the curved heads are placed on the tip of the apparent bone; and it should be hit once, until it heals, and should be even against each other.
Et se li brisure est subtilz, et li estrumens ne puet bien prendre l’os, si covient que tu copes lou chief de l’os, tant que li estrumens en ait possance.	And if the break is subtle and the instruments cannot take hold of the bone well, it must be that you catch the tip of the bone as long as the instruments have power.
Et se tu ne pues ramener l’os, si com nos avons dit, si lou cope d’un estrument covenable a ceu, ou incisoire ou soieure, a ton pooir; puis reis ceu qui est demorez en l’os d’aspreteit et de menues escorces.	And if you cannot bring back the bone, as we have said, if you have a suitable tool for this purpose, such as an incisor or awl, use your strength; then remove what is left in the bone of roughness and small flakes.
Et quant li os est ramenez, et li malaides sent grant dolor aprés, saiches qu’il n’est mie en son leu natureil.	And when the bone is returned, and after the patients feel great pain, know that it has not been placed in its natural position.
Si fai tant qu’il soit en son leu, puis moille I drapeil en vin stiptique noir, et proprement se c’est en esteit; et ne mettre mie sus la plaie cerote ne autre chose ou il ait oile, qu’il n’i faice venir porriture et corruption; puis aministre esteles quant tu as restoreit l’os, et laisse la plaie descoverte, et cope la coverture tout entor, selonc la quantiteit de la plaie, et te done bien en garde que li plaie ne soit estrainte avec la brisure; et maintes fois ont ce fait li fol mire, et ont fait venir sus le malaide ou mort ou corrodent aucune fois; et soit li estrignemens plus molz et plus souef des autres brisures.	If you do as such that it is in its place, then moisten the dressing with a black and clean wine, and if it is in health; and don't put wax or any other thing containing oil near the wound, for fear of causing corruption or rot; instead administer these remedies after restoring the bone, leave the wound open, and cover the whole body with a covering according to the size of the wound, and take great care that the wound is not restrained by breaking. Many have done this wrong way, causing death or decay in the patient on numerous occasions; and if the compresses are softer and more forgiving than other breaks.
Et se li plaie est male ou grans, et tu doutes que mavais accidens n’i veigne, si com nos avons dit, et tu trueves dolor au leu, si n’i covient mie mettre sus esteles; mais envoloupe entor, en leu d’esteles, drapelz durs, et les lie.	And if the wound is bad or large, and you doubt that harmful incidents have occurred within it, as we have said, and you find pain in the limb, if there is no need to place bandages; but envelop it internally, instead of bandages, with hard cloths, and tie them.
Et quant tu vois aprés I jor ou II enjanrer bowe a la plaie, si oste ceu que tu as mis sus a tout vin, et i met oignement sanant plaies, si com oignement tetrafarmaçon et semblans.	And when you see after one day or two days that the wound begins to heal, remove what you have placed with all kinds of vinegar, and apply healing ointment for wounds, such as tetrarmofarm and similar.
Et covient que tu deslies lou membre .ij. fois le jor, lou matin et au vespre, tant qu’il soit soudez et sanez.	And it must be that you dislocate the limb twice a day, in the morning and at vespers, until it is joined and healed.
Et covient que li membres soit aparilliez en teil maniere que li bowe corre aval legierement.	And it should be that the limb is placed so that the bone goes back up slightly gently.
Et se maint jor trespassent, et il ne puet souder mais rent adés bowe, saiches k’il i a petites pieces d’os, por coi il covient que tu quieres la plaie avec tente, et oste toutes ces pieces desevrees que font venir celle dolor.	And if this continues for several days, and it can't join at all back to its place, know that there are small pieces of bone, so you should treat the wound with a plaster bandage, and remove all these pieces that cause pain.
Et se fistule vient au leu, ou autre maniere de corruption, si covient que tu le cures, selonc ceu qu’il dist en son chapistre ci devant.	And if there is a fistula at the wound or some other form of infection, it is necessary that you treat it according to what he explained in his previous chapter.
Et quant li os est brisiez, et apert sus lou membre, si com li os de la cuixe ou de l’ajutoire, et autres semblans des grans membres, si ne le traire mie, car maintes fois en vient li mors, mais le laisse tant qu’il porrisse; par aventure cherra par lui aprés XX jors ou XXX, puis cure la plaie, se tu pues; et se tu ne pues, si la laisse.	And when the bone is broken and open in the limb, such as the bones of the foot or shoulder, or others like the large bones, do not treat it immediately because many die from it, but leave it until it heals; by chance it will heal after 20 or 30 days. Then if you can, cure the wound, and if you cannot, let it be.
des brus qui vienent sor la sodure	The burns that come from sweat
Nous vienent maintes fois aprés la santeit de la briseure, meismement quant c’est pres de la jointure, et laide chose est a veoir li figure dou membre; et par aventure ne puet faire li membres ses ovraiges naturelz.	We often see burns after rubbing the skin by the breeze, especially near joints. An ugly thing to see is how the member's figure becomes; and by chance cannot perform its natural actions on the body.
Pren warde donques se li nous est fres: si li aministre medicines stiptiques, si com aloes, encens, et mirre, et sarcocolle, acaice, et semblans autres, ensi que tu preignes aucune de ces choses, ou toutes ensamble, et les confit avec vin stiptique ou avec abun d’uef ou avec aisil; et les met sus le nout en estoupes, et l’estraint bien, et ne la desliier en mains jors; et puis la desloie, et rencomence une autre, tant que li nodations soit ostee; ou tu estrain sus une piece de plonc bien faite; car li proprietez dou plonc si est qu’il oste toutes les enfleures desus les membres; et se li nodation est ja convertie en durteit ausi com piere, et il est besoing de l’oster, si la cope desus, et fent la superfluiteit apparent; ou tu la reis a aucun raseur, tant qu’ele soit ostee, et la cure tant qu’ele soit sanee.	Take caution then when it is fresh: if you administer any stictch medicines such as aloes, frankincense, and myrrh, sarsagall, aniseed, and similar others, do so according to your preference for any of these things or all together, and mix them with a stichtic wine or with plenty of egg or with vinegar; then apply it on the skin in poultices, squeeze well, and do not remove by hand; afterwards remove it, and start another application until all the lumps are removed. Or you apply on a well-made piece of plaster; for the properties of the plaster so are that it removes all swellings above the limbs; and if the lump has turned into hardness like stone and needs to be removed, then cover it from below, and let the excess show clearly; or take it away with any knife until it is completely removed, and continue treating until it heals.
dou membre qui est foibles aprés la garison	Of the member which becomes weak after garrisoning
Quant li brisure de l’os est restoree, et demoure aprés li membres foibles et subtilz, si avient por mout de causes: de coi l’une est por ceu qu’il fut liiez trop estroit, et ne fut mie liiez si com il covenoit; ou por ceu qu’il i ot trop de liiens, et ne pooit venir li norrissemens au membre; ou por multitude d’arosement; ou por trop grans movements, ne mie en son houre; ou por ceu qu’il a poc de sanc en son cors, si est foibles.	When the breaking of the bone has been restored and afterwards, the limbs are weak and subtle, this happens due to various reasons: because it was tied too tightly and not as it should be; or because there were too many bindings, and no relief could come to the limb; or due to an excessive amount of swelling; or due to large movements that did not occur in their time; or because he has little blood in his body, being weak.
Et li cure si est que tu faices mengier le malaide, et faire le cors tendre, tant que li sans soit multipliiez en lui; et li aministre bain, et li done joie et liesce; puis met poix sus le membre, si que li poix atraie a li grant norrissement, et l’arose sovent d’aigue tede, tant que li norrissement corre au membre; et reviegne a sa figure natureil.	And the treatment is that you must eat the disease for him, and make his body soft, until the abscess multiplies within him; then give him baths, and make him happy and relaxed. Then put ointment on the limb, so that the ointment attracts to the large swelling, and washes it with cold water frequently, until the swelling aligns with the limb; and restore its natural shape.
dou membre tort aprés la santeit	If the member is bent after illness
Quant li membres est tors aprés la restauration, et li os brisiez apert, et li forme dou membre est laide, toutevoie ne pert mie son ovraige natureil: si ne croire mie les folz qui dient c’on doit brisier lou membre tout de noveil, et maint fol mire ont ce fait en nostre terre; et cist ovraiges est blamez, et en vient grans malz, et par aventure li mors; toutevoie, se li nodations et li torture sont fres, si covient k’il soient arosez d’aigue chaude, ou herbes mollifians soient cuites, si com foilles de vismalve, et racines, et mellilote, et semblans choses; et li fai .i. emplaustre mollificatif, si com dyaquilon bien fait, et tu pren le muscillaige de vismalve, et la confit avec graisse de geline ou oile de sisament, et fai emplaustre sus; ou tu pren figues graisses, et les broie avec fien de colon, et semblans medicines que amenuisent le soudement.	When the limbs are twisted after restoration, and if the bones were broken apart during this process, even though the shape of the limb becomes ugly afterward; yet it does not lose its natural function. Do not believe in those who say one must break the limb anew entirely; many people have followed this advice in our land; these procedures are criticized and lead to great harms and even death. Nonetheless, if the swellings and pains from the injury are still fresh, they should be treated with hot water applications or with boiled soothing herbs like leaves of fennel, roots, and melilot, among other such remedies. And apply one part of a moisturizing plaster; take figs in oil, grind them with cumin seeds, and similar medicinal substances that soften the wound. Prepare this with oil from sesame or grease, then apply as a plaster on top; alternatively, you can gather fatty figs, crush them together with flour from cumin, and other such medicines that reduce inflammation, mix it with fat from lard or oil from safflower, and apply it as a plaster.
Et aucune fois est ostee li nodacion por froter continuelment et longement a mains moistes.	And never is removed the operation of rubbing constantly and for a long time with wet hands.
Et soit amenistrez movement au membre chescune houre.	And let there be a movement to the member every hour.
Et se li tortuositez est enveillie et endurcie, ausi com piere, et besoins est de l’oster au fer, si la covient coper jusc’a l’os, a l’incisoire subtil legierement; et mettre cusenson et estude en la cure.	And if the twists are aged and hardened, like bone, and it requires being treated with fire, then cover up to the bone, incising subtly lightly; and apply consideration and study in the treatment.
Ci encomence li livres des dislocations	This begins the book on dislocations
Dislocations est issue d’aucune jointe de son leu, por coi il ne se puet muevre, et est li membres mal figurez, et sent li malaides grant dolor et grant lesion.	Dislocation occurs when a joint moves out of its place, which prevents it from moving, and the limb is misaligned, causing great pain and injury to the patient.
Quant dislocation vient a aucun, si le covient maintenant ramener sens targier.	When dislocation affects any part, if the situation requires it now, you should attempt to reduce or reset it without delay.
Car s’on tarde, si enfle li leus, et par aventure si le remet on a poines au leu; por ceu ne covient mie c’on le mueve a l’oure k’il est enflez: maintes fois fait venir spame et autres dolors; toutevoie, quant ce avenra, si fai sainier lou malaide, puis le laisse, tant que li apostemes chas soit apaisiez; puis arose le membre d’aigue chaude et d’oile, puis le ramoinne legierement, et cure chescun membre si com li cure venra en son leu.	For if you delay, the limbs will swell, and by chance they will move into positions at their joints; this should never happen when the limb is swollen: many times it brings pus and other pains; however, whenever this happens, get a surgeon for the patient, then leave them alone until the abscess subsides; then immerse the limb in hot water and oil, then gently manipulate it, and treat each limb as the treatment would occur at their joints.
Et j’ai ordenez les chapistres des dislocations des lou chief jusc’a piez.	And I have arranged the chapters on shoulder dislocations up until this point.
des mandibules	of the jaw
Poc avient que les mandibules soient desaluees andous, et li dislocations d’ambedous est selonc .ij. manieres: ou elles sont un poc ostees de lor leus, et mollifies un poc; ou elles sont desaluees entierement, et pendent vers lou pis, et cort li salive de la bouche qu’il ne la puet tenir, ne ne puet clore sa bouche, et envoloupe sa langue avec la parole.	It happens that the jaws are dislocated downwards, and the dislocations of both jaws occur in two ways: either they are somewhat bone-like at their roots and somewhat softened; or they are completely dislocated and hang down towards the bottom, and expel saliva from the mouth so that they cannot hold it, nor can they close their mouths, and wrap their tongue with their speech.
Quant li dislocations est petite, si revient par li em plusors disposicions.	When the dislocation is small, it can return through various positions.
Et s’elle est entiere et acomplie, si covient que tu la ramoinne hastanment, et ne targier mie; et en tel maniere que li ministres teigne le chief dou malaide, et boute li mires som pochet de l’une de ses mains en la racine de la dislocation de la mandibule dedens la bouche, se li dislocations est de II pars; et li autre doi des mains soient defuer, por mettre igal; et comande au malaide qu’il les amollisse, ses mandibules, et les mueve de toutes pars.	And when it is complete and accomplished, you should quickly manipulate it without hesitation; and in such a way that the assistants cut near the patient's head, and place a mirror inside their mouth at the root of the dislocated jawbone if the dislocation involves two parts. And for those with one part of the dislocation, have their hands rest outward to ensure they are even. Command the patient to soften, their jaws, and move them in all directions.
Et li mires la mete igal, tant qu’elle reveigne en son leu.	And keep the fingers steady until they return to their place.
Et se li ramener est griés, meismement se ce sont les .ij. mandibules ensamble, si les arose d’aigue chaude et d’oile, tant que les ramoinnes legierement; ne ne targier mie dou ramener, si com nos avons dit.	And if bringing it back causes pain, similarly when the two jaws are together, if they come from hot water and oil, as long as you gently bring them back; do not burn during the attempt to return them, as we have said.
Et quant elles sont ramenees igalment, et li bouche dou malaide clot bien sens mollifiier, si met sus drapelz moilliez en cerote fait d’oile roset et de cire, puis le lie legierement de molz liiens; et dorme li malaides sus son dos, et ses chiés soit estans entre II cussins, si qu’il ne lou mueve ne a destre ne a senestre, ne ne s’efforce mie de maixier, mais preigne legiere viande, tant que les dolors soient ostees, et soient noees les mandibules; et puis menjuce ce qu’il vuet legierement, et ne se travaille mie d’ovrir la bouche au mengier et au boivre, tant que li mandibule soit bien noee et sanee.	And when they are brought back evenly, and the mouth of the sick person is properly closed and softened, place moist cloths in a poultice made from rose oil and wax, then bind them loosely with wool threads; let the patient lie on their back, and keep their limbs between two cushions so that they do not move to either side nor try to stretch, but should eat light food until the pains subside and the jaws are healed. Then offer them what they want lightly, without working to open their mouth when eating or drinking, until the jaw is well healed and recovered.
Et se les .ij. mandibules ne pueent estre remises a point a une houre, et ne sont mie converties a lor leus, si en vient fievres et sode acostumees, et par aventure solution de ventre, et par aventure vomist cole pure.	And if the two lower jaws cannot be properly aligned within an hour and are not turned back to their original position, fever and chronic fatigue will result, and in some cases, abdominal pain or vomiting will occur.
Et quant tu verras ceu, adonc saiches que c’est perdicions; et maintes fois muert cil cui il avient, en .viiij. jors.	And when you see this, then know that it is a loss; and many times, death befalls the one who undergoes this within eight days.
de la forcelle	from the lever (referring to mechanics or possibly medical tools)
Li forcele ne puet desaluer dou costeit dedens la continuation de li et dou pis, et est desaluee aucune fois au defuer, et bien le sent on.	The forces cannot displace from within along the middle of the chest and the back; it is displaced only outward, and one feels this clearly.
Et li restauration si est que li malaides gise sovin sor son dos, et estende ses bras; et puis presse le leu forment a ta palme, et elle revenra; puis met sus l’emplaustre et lou bendeil, et l’estraint; et li chiez qui est devers lou coute ne puet desaluer; se poc non, et se il desalue aucune fois, si le ramoinne a son leu, si com nos avons dit; puis met sus l’emplaustre et le bendeil, et l’estraint, et coumande au malaide qu’il se repose tant qu’il soit sanez; et ensi meisme est ramenez li chiés de l’espale, quant il est desevrez de son leu.	And the restoration is such that the sick person lies down on their back, and extends their arms; then press your hand into the shape of his torso, and he will return to normal. And thus similarly, the shoulder blades of the back are brought back when he is returned to health.
de la dislocation de l’espaule	On the dislocation of the shoulder
Saiches que li espaule n’est desaluee fuer que selonc III manieres: de coi l’une est qu’ele desalue a la partie de l’assele au desoz; et li seconde est a la partie dou pis; et par aventure desalue a la partie desus, et ceu avient poc; et ne desalue mie derrier por l’espaule, et ne desalue mie dedens por les ners; et plusors fois desalue desoz vers l’assele, meismement a ces qui ont poc de char, car a ces saut ele fuer hastanment; a ces qui ont assez char, saut ele a poines, et rentre a poines.	Know that the shoulder is dislocated according to three ways: where one way is when it is dislocated from the part of the scapula to the side; and the second is at the part near the elbow; and sometimes dislocated from the part above, this happens rarely; and does not dislocate behind for the shoulder, nor inside for nerves; and multiple times dislocated downwards towards the scapula, similarly with those who have little flesh, because in these cases it goes quickly; to those who have enough flesh, it jumps and enters through points.
Et par aventure avient a aucuns homes percussion ou casseure, et enfle li espaule d’un aposteme chaut, et cuide qu’elle est desaluee par ceu.	By chance, it happens to some men from a blow or dislocation, and the shoulder swells with an abscess filled with heat, and they think that she is dislocated because of this.
Il covient donques que tu l’esprueves, tant que tu en soies certains; et adonques encomence la cure.	So you must verify this thoroughly until you are certain; then you can start the treatment.
Et est conue li dislocations quant il est aval vers l’assele, et met difference entre l’espaule malade et la saine, et tu troveras entre lor diversiteit manifeste; et troveras au chief de l’espaule une fosse, et desoz l’assele au tochier le chief de l’espaule, ausi com se ce soit uns oes; et ne puet li malaides ramener sa main a son neis, ne movoir de nulz movemens; et ausi, s’elle est desaluee en haut, si n’est mie occultee, car tu le trueves manifestement au tochier; et ceste maniere de dislocation n’est mie fors a ramener, quant elle est novele, ou se li enfes est malaides.	And know about dislocations when it goes towards the scapula, and you will see differences between the sick shoulder and the healthy one, and you will find various clear manifestations between them; and you will find a depression at the top of the shoulder, and from the scapula to the spine, as if it were an eye; and the patient cannot bring their hand back to their nose, nor move in any movement; and similarly, if it is dislocated upwards, it is not hidden either, for you will clearly find it at the spine; and this type of dislocation can only be corrected when it's new, or when the baby is born.
Et li maniere est que li ministres lieve la main dou malaide en haut, puis met tes peuchas desoz l’assele, et lieve la jointure a force en haut au leu; et li ministres lieve la main, et l’estende en haut, pues le mette desoz; si venra hastanment.	And the method is that the ministers lift their hand from the disease up, then place their thumbs under the joint, and lift the joint to its full height at the top of its position; and the ministers lift their hand and extend it upwards, putting it underneath; if it comes quickly.
Et s’elle ne vient si com nos avons dit em mains jors aprés, si covient ke li malaides soit baigniez en aigue chaude; et li amenistre arosement mollifiant et assouajant, si com decoction de altee et de fenugrec et de mellilote en aigue, et soit amenistree; puis soit sovinez li malaides sus son dos, et mette on desoz l’assele un sto de lainne igal, ne trop mol ne trop dur, puis mette li mires son talon sus le sto, et lieve le chief de l’espaule vertuousement, et traie la main dou malaide; et uns autres ministres teigne lou chief dou malaide, si qu’il ne se mueve aval; celle espaule revient tout maintenant, et se tu vues si le ramoinne selonc ceste maniere: et est que tu faices estre present I home qui soit plus grans que li malaides; et soit drois devers lou costeit, et boute s’espaule desoz l’assele dou malaide, et lieve l’assele en haut, si que li malaides pende en l’ar; et uns autres ministres traie la main dou malaide aval devers lou ventre.	And if she doesn't come like we have said in a few days after, it is necessary that the patient should be bathed in hot water; and treat him with gentle soothing and calming methods, such as decoction of garlic, fenugreek, and fennel in warm water, then administer this treatment. Then wrap the patient's back with cloth that is medium in softness, not too hard or too soft, after that place a pad on the buttocks, and under it put a piece of fabric evenly soft, not too hard or too soft; then place the hand under the fabric on the buttocks, and lift the shoulder's head up firmly, pull out the affected arm, and guide the hand toward the patient gently; and another attendant should sharpen the hand by the affected area so that it doesn't move down. This shoulder has returned completely now, if you see that you have successfully reset it in this manner: and someone bigger than the patient should be present at home; stand straight towards your side, place the shoulder under the fabric of the attendant, lift the attendant up high so that the affected person hangs downwardly; and another attendant should pull their hand backward towards their abdomen from the affected area.
Et se li malaides est trop legiers, si pent avec lui aucune chose pesant, et li dislocation revient maintenant.	And if the body is too light, it can carry nothing heavy, and the dislocation returns immediately.
Et le ramoinne on ausi en autre maniere: et est c’on fiche I lonc tison en terre, dont li chiés soit ausi reons com I pistal, et ne soit ne trop gros ne trop graile; puis soit mis desoz lou malaide, mais k’il ait drapelz souef sus, et li malaides soit estans dou lonc dou fust; puis soit estendue sa main aval d’autre part forment, et li jointure revenra en son leu hastanment; et s’elle ne vuet revenir por toutes ces choses que nos avons dit, si fai ceste cure: pren I tison de II bras de grant et IIII dois de large, qui ait le chief reont por mues entrer em parfont desoz l’assele, selonc ceste forme:	And to reset it can also be done in other ways: and one sticks the long stick into the ground, so that the shoulder is also held like a pistol, and neither too large nor too slippery; then place it under the body, but with something hard underneath, and the body remains in contact for the length of the stick; then extend their hand down on the other side in formation, and the joint will return to its place quickly; and if it does not return using all these things that we have said, then do this cure: take a stick two hands wide and four feet long, which has a taper suitable for entering at both ends under the skin, according to this shape.
puis lie sus le chief dou fust drapelz souez, que li fust ne blece lou malaide, puis le met desoz l’assele dou malaide; et estende som bras sus le fust dou lonc, et lie l’ajutoire sus le fust, et lou bras au chief de la main, puis met le bras sus .i. eschillon d’une eschiele dou large, et soit estendue li mains aval, et soit laissiez li cors pendans d’autre part: li jointure reva ens maintenant.	then tie the staff with a shield underneath so it doesn't hurt the patient, then place the staff under the wound on the patient; and extend your arms along the staff as long as needed, and tie the brace onto the staff, and the arm at the hand's head, then put the arm on one of the pegs of the same size from below, and keep the hands down, and leave the body hanging on the other side: the joint will return to its place now.

And when the dislocation is in front, it should be stretched out as quickly as possible, and according to what I have said; and place the patient's pain on the diseased side, then press with the other hand, and stretch down towards the knee.
Et se li dislocations est au defuer, si ne covient pas estendre le malaide aval, ne lever sus la terre, ains covient qu’il soit ausi com se li hainche estoit desaluee au defuer, si com nos avons dit dou couchement sus les II hainches; et soit sus sa faice, et li lien estendut si com nos avons dit ci devant, et doit om presser sus la jointure a la table; et sera a point quant li malaides estendra ses jambes, et elles seront igalz; adonques ajoste les cuixes, et met l’emplaustre, et l’estrain d’un bendeil, si que li hainche ne se mueve; et se repose III jors ou IIII, puis le deslie, et met l’emplaustre sus; et se tu vois qu’elles soient igalz, si l’estrain, si com devant, et le laisse III jors; puis le deslie, et lou fai aler belement, tant que li membres soit confortez.	And if the dislocation is at the front, and it doesn't allow for extending the patient's lower part backwards, or lifting them onto their feet, instead they should stay in a position like when they were dislocated at the back, as we explained about lying on both hips; and they should lie on their stomach, with their arms stretched out just as we said before, and they should press against the joint while lying on the table; it will be correct when the patient extends their legs and they are even; then adjust their hips, apply the plaster, tie a bandage tight enough so that neither hip moves, and let them rest for three or four days. Then release them from this position and apply the plaster again; and if you see that their limbs are now even, reapply the bandage as before, and leave it on for another three days; then release them and ensure they walk properly until their limbs are fully recovered.
de la dislocation dou genoil	Of the shoulder joint dislocation
Li genous est desaluez selonc .iij. manieres: c’est a savoir, dedens et defuer, et derrier; et ne desalue point devant.	The shoulder joint can be dislocated in three ways: to understand this is as follows, either internally or externally, and behind; and it does not dislocate forward.
Et li signes si est que tu comande au malaide qu’il plie sa jambe a sa cuixe, et s’ele ne s’aert a sa cuixe, saiches qu’il est desaluez; et li restauration de toutes si est que tu faices seoir le malaide droit, et estende sa jambe s’il puet, et li met ton dos sus sa faice, et met son piet sus tes piez; puis pren son genoil a tes paumes, et retrai entre tes dois, puis plie les II costez dou genoil forment; et uns autres ministres estende son piet, tant que li genous reviegne a son leu, et li signes est qu’il aert bien sa jambe a sa cuixe legierement; et met l’emplastre sus, et fai aerdre la jambe a la cuixe, et les loie ensamble fort III jors ou IIII, puis le deslie; et ne se travaille mie li malaides d’aler, tant que li membres soit confortez.	And the signs are that you instruct the patient to bend his leg at his knee. If he cannot touch his knee, know that it is dislocated; and the restoration of all this is that you make the patient stand straight, extend his leg if he can, place his back against your buttocks, and put his foot on yours; then take his knee with your palms, pull between your fingers, then bend the two sides from the knee inward; and another attendant extends his foot until the knees return to their position, and the signs are that he bends well his leg slightly at his knee; and apply the plaster, let the leg cool to the knee, bind them tightly for three or four days, then release him; do not trouble the patient in walking until the limbs are strengthened.
Et se li membres n’est a point, si aministre estendement fort, si com nos avons dit en la cure de la hainche, tant qu’il soit sanez	And if the limb is not present, apply strong extension, as we have said in the treatment of the hip, until it returns to its normal state.
de la dislocation dou talon	Of the dislocation of the heel
Li talons est aucune fois esmeus, et aucune fois desaluez plenement, et dedens et defuer.	The heels are never completely dislocated and neither fully out of place, both inwards and outwards.
Et li signes si est que li cheville est enflee, et tent avant a la partie ou elle est desaluee: li ramenemens si est legier, et le doit on estendre legierement a ses mains quant il est esmeus soulement.	And the signs are that the ankle swells and bends forward towards the part where it is dislocated; the reset should be gentle, and one must gently extend it with their hands when it has been realigned just slightly.
Et quant il est desaluez dou tot, si covient que tu faices seoir le malaide droit, et le tigne I ministres fors par la jambe, desus la cheville; puis trai le piet a toi a ta main destre, et puis a la senestre II fois, puis l’estent en haut, et boute bellement lou piet en haut; et fai ce II fois, si com nos avons dit, em boutant et en traiant lou piet; s’elle revient, c’est bien; se ce non, si rencomence l’ovraige, car il revient; et s’il ne puet revenir ensi, si fai gesir lou malaide sor son dos sus terre, et fiche I passeil fermement en terre entre ses cuixes, et lie drapelz entor, qu’il ne blece lou malaide; puis teigne li ministres la cuixe, et uns autres ministres estende lou piet a ses mains ou a I liien, k’il lie sus le col dou piet; puis estende chescuns ministres igalment, et li passelz soit adés entre les cuixes dou malaide por retenir le malaide quant on l’estent; puis mette li mires igal la dislocation a ses mains, et uns autres ministres teigne la jambe sainne au desoz, et li dislocation revenra hastanment.	And when it is realigned immediately, you should have the patient lie straight, and guide their feet out from under them by lifting the calf; then pull the leg towards yourself with your right hand, and then do so twice with your left. Next, extend it upwards, and firmly hold the foot up; repeat this two times while pulling and guiding the foot. If it returns in place, that's good; if not, continue with the procedure because it will return; if it still cannot come back like that, you should let the patient lie on their back on the ground, firmly plant one leg into the ground between their buttocks, and tie cloths around them to prevent bruising. Then lift the feet by their owners' hands or at the ankle and tie them onto the neck of the foot; extend each foot evenly, placing the shoe firmly under the buttocks so that they hold the foot in place when it is extended. Lastly, adjust the dislocation slightly with your hands, and have another person cut the healthy leg just below the knee, and the dislocation will return quickly.
Et quant elle iert a point, si met l’emplastre et estoupes sus, et l’estrain forment, et lie lou piet a la jambe, et warde les ners qui sont sus la cheville derrier, que li liiens ne soit trop estrois; puis le laisse II jors ou III, et se li liiens amolist, si l’estrain; puis le deslie au tier jor ou au quart, et deffent a aler lou malaide par IIII jors; et s’il va devant cel termine, ce n’est mie seurtez qu’il ne desalue encor.	And when it is at the right point, apply the plaster and bind with a strip, keep it tight, and attach the foot to the leg, make sure not to tie too tightly any nerves located behind the ankle. Leave it for two or three days, if it unties itself then release it; after that, release in a third or quarter day, allow walking by four days; and if it progresses past this stage, there is no assurance it will not dislocate again.
Et se apostemes chaus i vient, si covient que tu l’apaises, si com nos avons dit autre part, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if pus comes out at the incision site, it is necessary that you soothe it, just as we have said in other places, while it remains clean.
des dois	Of the cautery made with fire, command the patient to let the hairs grow long and even; if they prick at their base, hold the eyes steady so they do not move until they grow.
Quant li doi sont desaluez, si les covient bellement estendre sens travail, et c’est legiere chose.	When the shoulders are dislocated, if they can be properly stretched like in manual work, it's a simple task.
Et se li dislocations est en aucun nout dou dos dou piet, si covient que tu faices seoir le malaide sus I leu plain ou sus .ie. table tot droit, et met ton piet sus ce qui apert de ces jointures, puis presse a ton piet forment, tant qu’il reviegne; et quant il est igalz, et il n’i apert nient, si met desoz la plante dou piet une table a II chiés, puis l’estrain forment, et le laisse III jors, puis le deslie; et le fai reposer, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if the dislocation is at no point in the back or bottom of the foot, it is necessary that you have the patient sit straight up on I his full height or on a table entirely upright, and place your foot against the opening of these joints. Push with your foot as long as he resists; and when it's equal and there is nothing left to open, put under the sole of the foot a board for two shoulders, then press the ankles in place, and leave him for three days, then release him; and make him rest until he has recovered.
de plaie et de dislocation ensamble	regarding injuries and dislocations together
Quant plaie vient avec la dislocation, et on la vuet restorer, maintes fois avient que li malaides muert: si ne soies mie presumptuous en la cure, se tu n’es saiges en l’art et tu ne l’as useit longement, et se tu n’es pitous et misericors et tardis, ne mie hardis; et use au comencement de choses apaisans aposteme chaut, et laisse le malaide en la main Deu, se tu n’i vois esperance de santeit; et quant tu i vois esperance, si ramoinne maintenant le membre au leu, ainsois que li apostemes chaus i viegne; et quant li membres est a leu, si aministre choses apaisans aposteme chaut, et cure la plaie, si com il covient, d’oignemens desiccatis; et se avec la dislocation a brisure, et os menus desevrez, si les oste, et fai ce que nos avons dit en maladies simples; et te garde d’entrer en voie de paour, selonc ce que j’ai dit, car ce te vaut mues selonc ton Creator, et por la saveteit de t’arme et de ton cors.	When injury comes with dislocation and you want to restore it, many times the patient dies: if not being presumptuous in treatment, if you are not skilled in this art and have not used it for a long time, and if you are not pitiful and merciful but rather rash; do not be rash at the beginning with calming remedies against abscesses. Leave the patient in God's hands if you do not see hope of healing; and when you see hope, now apply to set back the member into its place, as if the abscesses are gone; and once the member is set into place, apply calming remedies against abscesses, treat the wound accordingly with desiccating ointments. And should there be fracture along with dislocation, and small bones broken, mend them, do as we have said in simple diseases; and protect yourself from entering a path of fear, according to what I have said, for this will lead you to behave according to your Creator, and through knowledge about yourself and your body.
